spam	Book the First--Recalled to Life
ham	I. The Period
ham	It was the best of times,
ham	it was the worst of times,
spam	it was the age of wisdom,
ham	it was the age of foolishness,
spam	it was the epoch of belief,
ham	it was the epoch of incredulity,
spam	it was the season of Light,
spam	it was the season of Darkness,
spam	it was the spring of hope,
spam	it was the winter of despair,
ham	we had everything before us,
spam	we had nothing before us,
ham	we were all going direct to Heaven,
ham	we were all going direct the other way--
spam	in short, the period was so far like the present period, that some of
spam	its noisiest authorities insisted on its being received, for good or for
spam	evil, in the superlative degree of comparison only.
spam	There were a king with a large jaw and a queen with a plain face, on the
spam	throne of England; there were a king with a large jaw and a queen with
spam	a fair face, on the throne of France. In both countries it was clearer
ham	than crystal to the lords of the State preserves of loaves and fishes,
ham	that things in general were settled for ever.
ham	It was the year of Our Lord one thousand seven hundred and seventy-five.
ham	Spiritual revelations were conceded to England at that favoured period,
spam	as at this. Mrs. Southcott had recently attained her five-and-twentieth
spam	blessed birthday, of whom a prophetic private in the Life Guards had
ham	heralded the sublime appearance by announcing that arrangements were
ham	made for the swallowing up of London and Westminster. Even the Cock-lane
ham	ghost had been laid only a round dozen of years, after rapping out its
spam	messages, as the spirits of this very year last past (supernaturally
ham	deficient in originality) rapped out theirs. Mere messages in the
spam	earthly order of events had lately come to the English Crown and People,
ham	from a congress of British subjects in America: which, strange
ham	to relate, have proved more important to the human race than any
ham	communications yet received through any of the chickens of the Cock-lane
spam	brood.
ham	France, less favoured on the whole as to matters spiritual than her
spam	sister of the shield and trident, rolled with exceeding smoothness down
ham	hill, making paper money and spending it. Under the guidance of her
spam	Christian pastors, she entertained herself, besides, with such humane
ham	achievements as sentencing a youth to have his hands cut off, his tongue
ham	torn out with pincers, and his body burned alive, because he had not
ham	kneeled down in the rain to do honour to a dirty procession of monks
ham	which passed within his view, at a distance of some fifty or sixty
spam	yards. It is likely enough that, rooted in the woods of France and
ham	Norway, there were growing trees, when that sufferer was put to death,
ham	already marked by the Woodman, Fate, to come down and be sawn into
ham	boards, to make a certain movable framework with a sack and a knife in
spam	it, terrible in history. It is likely enough that in the rough outhouses
spam	of some tillers of the heavy lands adjacent to Paris, there were
spam	sheltered from the weather that very day, rude carts, bespattered with
spam	rustic mire, snuffed about by pigs, and roosted in by poultry, which
ham	the Farmer, Death, had already set apart to be his tumbrils of
ham	the Revolution. But that Woodman and that Farmer, though they work
spam	unceasingly, work silently, and no one heard them as they went about
spam	with muffled tread: the rather, forasmuch as to entertain any suspicion
spam	that they were awake, was to be atheistical and traitorous.
spam	In England, there was scarcely an amount of order and protection to
spam	justify much national boasting. Daring burglaries by armed men, and
spam	highway robberies, took place in the capital itself every night;
spam	families were publicly cautioned not to go out of town without removing
spam	their furniture to upholsterers' warehouses for security; the highwayman
ham	in the dark was a City tradesman in the light, and, being recognised and
ham	challenged by his fellow-tradesman whom he stopped in his character of
ham	"the Captain," gallantly shot him through the head and rode away; the
spam	mail was waylaid by seven robbers, and the guard shot three dead, and
spam	then got shot dead himself by the other four, "in consequence of the
ham	failure of his ammunition:" after which the mail was robbed in peace;
spam	that magnificent potentate, the Lord Mayor of London, was made to stand
ham	and deliver on Turnham Green, by one highwayman, who despoiled the
ham	illustrious creature in sight of all his retinue; prisoners in London
ham	gaols fought battles with their turnkeys, and the majesty of the law
ham	fired blunderbusses in among them, loaded with rounds of shot and ball;
spam	thieves snipped off diamond crosses from the necks of noble lords at
spam	Court drawing-rooms; musketeers went into St. Giles's, to search
ham	for contraband goods, and the mob fired on the musketeers, and the
spam	musketeers fired on the mob, and nobody thought any of these occurrences
spam	much out of the common way. In the midst of them, the hangman, ever busy
spam	and ever worse than useless, was in constant requisition; now, stringing
spam	up long rows of miscellaneous criminals; now, hanging a housebreaker on
spam	Saturday who had been taken on Tuesday; now, burning people in the
ham	hand at Newgate by the dozen, and now burning pamphlets at the door of
spam	Westminster Hall; to-day, taking the life of an atrocious murderer,
spam	and to-morrow of a wretched pilferer who had robbed a farmer's boy of
spam	sixpence.
ham	All these things, and a thousand like them, came to pass in and close
spam	upon the dear old year one thousand seven hundred and seventy-five.
spam	Environed by them, while the Woodman and the Farmer worked unheeded,
ham	those two of the large jaws, and those other two of the plain and the
spam	fair faces, trod with stir enough, and carried their divine rights
ham	with a high hand. Thus did the year one thousand seven hundred
spam	and seventy-five conduct their Greatnesses, and myriads of small
ham	creatures--the creatures of this chronicle among the rest--along the
spam	roads that lay before them.
ham	II. The Mail
spam	It was the Dover road that lay, on a Friday night late in November,
ham	before the first of the persons with whom this history has business.
spam	The Dover road lay, as to him, beyond the Dover mail, as it lumbered up
spam	Shooter's Hill. He walked up hill in the mire by the side of the mail,
spam	as the rest of the passengers did; not because they had the least relish
spam	for walking exercise, under the circumstances, but because the hill,
ham	and the harness, and the mud, and the mail, were all so heavy, that the
ham	horses had three times already come to a stop, besides once drawing the
spam	coach across the road, with the mutinous intent of taking it back
spam	to Blackheath. Reins and whip and coachman and guard, however, in
spam	combination, had read that article of war which forbade a purpose
ham	otherwise strongly in favour of the argument, that some brute animals
ham	are endued with Reason; and the team had capitulated and returned to
spam	their duty.
ham	With drooping heads and tremulous tails, they mashed their way through
ham	the thick mud, floundering and stumbling between whiles, as if they were
ham	falling to pieces at the larger joints. As often as the driver rested
ham	them and brought them to a stand, with a wary "Wo-ho! so-ho-then!" the
spam	near leader violently shook his head and everything upon it--like an
ham	unusually emphatic horse, denying that the coach could be got up the
spam	hill. Whenever the leader made this rattle, the passenger started, as a
ham	nervous passenger might, and was disturbed in mind.
spam	There was a steaming mist in all the hollows, and it had roamed in its
ham	forlornness up the hill, like an evil spirit, seeking rest and finding
spam	none. A clammy and intensely cold mist, it made its slow way through the
ham	air in ripples that visibly followed and overspread one another, as the
spam	waves of an unwholesome sea might do. It was dense enough to shut out
ham	everything from the light of the coach-lamps but these its own workings,
spam	and a few yards of road; and the reek of the labouring horses steamed
ham	into it, as if they had made it all.
spam	Two other passengers, besides the one, were plodding up the hill by the
spam	side of the mail. All three were wrapped to the cheekbones and over the
spam	ears, and wore jack-boots. Not one of the three could have said, from
ham	anything he saw, what either of the other two was like; and each was
ham	hidden under almost as many wrappers from the eyes of the mind, as from
ham	the eyes of the body, of his two companions. In those days, travellers
spam	were very shy of being confidential on a short notice, for anybody on
ham	the road might be a robber or in league with robbers. As to the latter,
ham	when every posting-house and ale-house could produce somebody in
ham	"the Captain's" pay, ranging from the landlord to the lowest stable
spam	non-descript, it was the likeliest thing upon the cards. So the guard
spam	of the Dover mail thought to himself, that Friday night in November, one
spam	thousand seven hundred and seventy-five, lumbering up Shooter's Hill, as
spam	he stood on his own particular perch behind the mail, beating his feet,
ham	and keeping an eye and a hand on the arm-chest before him, where a
spam	loaded blunderbuss lay at the top of six or eight loaded horse-pistols,
spam	deposited on a substratum of cutlass.
ham	The Dover mail was in its usual genial position that the guard suspected
spam	the passengers, the passengers suspected one another and the guard, they
ham	all suspected everybody else, and the coachman was sure of nothing but
spam	the horses; as to which cattle he could with a clear conscience have
ham	taken his oath on the two Testaments that they were not fit for the
spam	journey.
ham	"Wo-ho!" said the coachman. "So, then! One more pull and you're at the
spam	top and be damned to you, for I have had trouble enough to get you to
spam	it!--Joe!"
spam	"Halloa!" the guard replied.
spam	"What o'clock do you make it, Joe?"
spam	"Ten minutes, good, past eleven."
spam	"My blood!" ejaculated the vexed coachman, "and not atop of Shooter's
spam	yet! Tst! Yah! Get on with you!"
spam	The emphatic horse, cut short by the whip in a most decided negative,
ham	made a decided scramble for it, and the three other horses followed
spam	suit. Once more, the Dover mail struggled on, with the jack-boots of its
ham	passengers squashing along by its side. They had stopped when the coach
spam	stopped, and they kept close company with it. If any one of the three
spam	had had the hardihood to propose to another to walk on a little ahead
ham	into the mist and darkness, he would have put himself in a fair way of
ham	getting shot instantly as a highwayman.
ham	The last burst carried the mail to the summit of the hill. The horses
spam	stopped to breathe again, and the guard got down to skid the wheel for
spam	the descent, and open the coach-door to let the passengers in.
spam	"Tst! Joe!" cried the coachman in a warning voice, looking down from his
spam	box.
spam	"What do you say, Tom?"
ham	They both listened.
ham	"I say a horse at a canter coming up, Joe."
ham	"_I_ say a horse at a gallop, Tom," returned the guard, leaving his hold
ham	of the door, and mounting nimbly to his place. "Gentlemen! In the king's
ham	name, all of you!"
spam	With this hurried adjuration, he cocked his blunderbuss, and stood on
spam	the offensive.
ham	The passenger booked by this history, was on the coach-step, getting in;
spam	the two other passengers were close behind him, and about to follow. He
spam	remained on the step, half in the coach and half out of; they remained
ham	in the road below him. They all looked from the coachman to the guard,
spam	and from the guard to the coachman, and listened. The coachman looked
spam	back and the guard looked back, and even the emphatic leader pricked up
ham	his ears and looked back, without contradicting.
spam	The stillness consequent on the cessation of the rumbling and labouring
spam	of the coach, added to the stillness of the night, made it very quiet
ham	indeed. The panting of the horses communicated a tremulous motion to
ham	the coach, as if it were in a state of agitation. The hearts of the
spam	passengers beat loud enough perhaps to be heard; but at any rate, the
spam	quiet pause was audibly expressive of people out of breath, and holding
ham	the breath, and having the pulses quickened by expectation.
ham	The sound of a horse at a gallop came fast and furiously up the hill.
spam	"So-ho!" the guard sang out, as loud as he could roar. "Yo there! Stand!
spam	I shall fire!"
spam	The pace was suddenly checked, and, with much splashing and floundering,
ham	a man's voice called from the mist, "Is that the Dover mail?"
ham	"Never you mind what it is!" the guard retorted. "What are you?"
ham	"_Is_ that the Dover mail?"
ham	"Why do you want to know?"
ham	"I want a passenger, if it is."
ham	"What passenger?"
ham	"Mr. Jarvis Lorry."
ham	Our booked passenger showed in a moment that it was his name. The guard,
spam	the coachman, and the two other passengers eyed him distrustfully.
spam	"Keep where you are," the guard called to the voice in the mist,
spam	"because, if I should make a mistake, it could never be set right in
ham	your lifetime. Gentleman of the name of Lorry answer straight."
ham	"What is the matter?" asked the passenger, then, with mildly quavering
spam	speech. "Who wants me? Is it Jerry?"
ham	("I don't like Jerry's voice, if it is Jerry," growled the guard to
ham	himself. "He's hoarser than suits me, is Jerry.")
spam	"Yes, Mr. Lorry."
ham	"What is the matter?"
ham	"A despatch sent after you from over yonder. T. and Co."
spam	"I know this messenger, guard," said Mr. Lorry, getting down into the
spam	road--assisted from behind more swiftly than politely by the other two
spam	passengers, who immediately scrambled into the coach, shut the door, and
ham	pulled up the window. "He may come close; there's nothing wrong."
ham	"I hope there ain't, but I can't make so 'Nation sure of that," said the
ham	guard, in gruff soliloquy. "Hallo you!"
ham	"Well! And hallo you!" said Jerry, more hoarsely than before.
spam	"Come on at a footpace! d'ye mind me? And if you've got holsters to that
ham	saddle o' yourn, don't let me see your hand go nigh 'em. For I'm a devil
ham	at a quick mistake, and when I make one it takes the form of Lead. So
spam	now let's look at you."
ham	The figures of a horse and rider came slowly through the eddying mist,
ham	and came to the side of the mail, where the passenger stood. The rider
spam	stooped, and, casting up his eyes at the guard, handed the passenger
spam	a small folded paper. The rider's horse was blown, and both horse and
spam	rider were covered with mud, from the hoofs of the horse to the hat of
ham	the man.
ham	"Guard!" said the passenger, in a tone of quiet business confidence.
spam	The watchful guard, with his right hand at the stock of his raised
spam	blunderbuss, his left at the barrel, and his eye on the horseman,
ham	answered curtly, "Sir."
spam	"There is nothing to apprehend. I belong to Tellson's Bank. You must
spam	know Tellson's Bank in London. I am going to Paris on business. A crown
spam	to drink. I may read this?"
ham	"If so be as you're quick, sir."
ham	He opened it in the light of the coach-lamp on that side, and
spam	read--first to himself and then aloud: "'Wait at Dover for Mam'selle.'
ham	It's not long, you see, guard. Jerry, say that my answer was, RECALLED
spam	TO LIFE."
spam	Jerry started in his saddle. "That's a Blazing strange answer, too,"
ham	said he, at his hoarsest.
spam	"Take that message back, and they will know that I received this, as
spam	well as if I wrote. Make the best of your way. Good night."
ham	With those words the passenger opened the coach-door and got in; not at
ham	all assisted by his fellow-passengers, who had expeditiously secreted
spam	their watches and purses in their boots, and were now making a general
spam	pretence of being asleep. With no more definite purpose than to escape
spam	the hazard of originating any other kind of action.
ham	The coach lumbered on again, with heavier wreaths of mist closing round
spam	it as it began the descent. The guard soon replaced his blunderbuss
ham	in his arm-chest, and, having looked to the rest of its contents, and
spam	having looked to the supplementary pistols that he wore in his belt,
ham	looked to a smaller chest beneath his seat, in which there were a
spam	few smith's tools, a couple of torches, and a tinder-box. For he was
spam	furnished with that completeness that if the coach-lamps had been blown
spam	and stormed out, which did occasionally happen, he had only to shut
spam	himself up inside, keep the flint and steel sparks well off the straw,
spam	and get a light with tolerable safety and ease (if he were lucky) in
ham	five minutes.
ham	"Tom!" softly over the coach roof.
spam	"Hallo, Joe."
ham	"Did you hear the message?"
spam	"I did, Joe."
spam	"What did you make of it, Tom?"
spam	"Nothing at all, Joe."
ham	"That's a coincidence, too," the guard mused, "for I made the same of it
ham	myself."
ham	Jerry, left alone in the mist and darkness, dismounted meanwhile, not
ham	only to ease his spent horse, but to wipe the mud from his face, and
spam	shake the wet out of his hat-brim, which might be capable of
spam	holding about half a gallon. After standing with the bridle over his
spam	heavily-splashed arm, until the wheels of the mail were no longer within
ham	hearing and the night was quite still again, he turned to walk down the
ham	hill.
spam	"After that there gallop from Temple Bar, old lady, I won't trust your
spam	fore-legs till I get you on the level," said this hoarse messenger,
ham	glancing at his mare. "'Recalled to life.' That's a Blazing strange
spam	message. Much of that wouldn't do for you, Jerry! I say, Jerry! You'd
ham	be in a Blazing bad way, if recalling to life was to come into fashion,
spam	Jerry!"
ham	III. The Night Shadows
spam	A wonderful fact to reflect upon, that every human creature is
spam	constituted to be that profound secret and mystery to every other. A
spam	solemn consideration, when I enter a great city by night, that every
spam	one of those darkly clustered houses encloses its own secret; that every
ham	room in every one of them encloses its own secret; that every beating
ham	heart in the hundreds of thousands of breasts there, is, in some of
spam	its imaginings, a secret to the heart nearest it! Something of the
spam	awfulness, even of Death itself, is referable to this. No more can I
ham	turn the leaves of this dear book that I loved, and vainly hope in time
spam	to read it all. No more can I look into the depths of this unfathomable
ham	water, wherein, as momentary lights glanced into it, I have had glimpses
ham	of buried treasure and other things submerged. It was appointed that the
spam	book should shut with a spring, for ever and for ever, when I had read
spam	but a page. It was appointed that the water should be locked in an
ham	eternal frost, when the light was playing on its surface, and I stood
spam	in ignorance on the shore. My friend is dead, my neighbour is dead,
ham	my love, the darling of my soul, is dead; it is the inexorable
ham	consolidation and perpetuation of the secret that was always in that
ham	individuality, and which I shall carry in mine to my life's end. In
spam	any of the burial-places of this city through which I pass, is there
spam	a sleeper more inscrutable than its busy inhabitants are, in their
ham	innermost personality, to me, or than I am to them?
spam	As to this, his natural and not to be alienated inheritance, the
ham	messenger on horseback had exactly the same possessions as the King, the
spam	first Minister of State, or the richest merchant in London. So with the
ham	three passengers shut up in the narrow compass of one lumbering old mail
ham	coach; they were mysteries to one another, as complete as if each had
spam	been in his own coach and six, or his own coach and sixty, with the
ham	breadth of a county between him and the next.
spam	The messenger rode back at an easy trot, stopping pretty often at
ham	ale-houses by the way to drink, but evincing a tendency to keep his
spam	own counsel, and to keep his hat cocked over his eyes. He had eyes that
spam	assorted very well with that decoration, being of a surface black, with
spam	no depth in the colour or form, and much too near together--as if they
spam	were afraid of being found out in something, singly, if they kept too
ham	far apart. They had a sinister expression, under an old cocked-hat like
ham	a three-cornered spittoon, and over a great muffler for the chin and
spam	throat, which descended nearly to the wearer's knees. When he stopped
ham	for drink, he moved this muffler with his left hand, only while he
spam	poured his liquor in with his right; as soon as that was done, he
ham	muffled again.
spam	"No, Jerry, no!" said the messenger, harping on one theme as he rode.
spam	"It wouldn't do for you, Jerry. Jerry, you honest tradesman, it wouldn't
spam	suit _your_ line of business! Recalled--! Bust me if I don't think he'd
ham	been a drinking!"
spam	His message perplexed his mind to that degree that he was fain, several
ham	times, to take off his hat to scratch his head. Except on the crown,
ham	which was raggedly bald, he had stiff, black hair, standing jaggedly all
ham	over it, and growing down hill almost to his broad, blunt nose. It was
spam	so like Smith's work, so much more like the top of a strongly spiked
spam	wall than a head of hair, that the best of players at leap-frog might
ham	have declined him, as the most dangerous man in the world to go over.
spam	While he trotted back with the message he was to deliver to the night
ham	watchman in his box at the door of Tellson's Bank, by Temple Bar, who
spam	was to deliver it to greater authorities within, the shadows of the
ham	night took such shapes to him as arose out of the message, and took such
spam	shapes to the mare as arose out of _her_ private topics of uneasiness.
ham	They seemed to be numerous, for she shied at every shadow on the road.
ham	What time, the mail-coach lumbered, jolted, rattled, and bumped upon
ham	its tedious way, with its three fellow-inscrutables inside. To whom,
spam	likewise, the shadows of the night revealed themselves, in the forms
ham	their dozing eyes and wandering thoughts suggested.
ham	Tellson's Bank had a run upon it in the mail. As the bank
ham	passenger--with an arm drawn through the leathern strap, which did what
spam	lay in it to keep him from pounding against the next passenger,
spam	and driving him into his corner, whenever the coach got a special
ham	jolt--nodded in his place, with half-shut eyes, the little
ham	coach-windows, and the coach-lamp dimly gleaming through them, and the
ham	bulky bundle of opposite passenger, became the bank, and did a great
ham	stroke of business. The rattle of the harness was the chink of money,
spam	and more drafts were honoured in five minutes than even Tellson's, with
ham	all its foreign and home connection, ever paid in thrice the time. Then
spam	the strong-rooms underground, at Tellson's, with such of their valuable
spam	stores and secrets as were known to the passenger (and it was not a
ham	little that he knew about them), opened before him, and he went in among
spam	them with the great keys and the feebly-burning candle, and found them
ham	safe, and strong, and sound, and still, just as he had last seen them.
spam	But, though the bank was almost always with him, and though the coach
spam	(in a confused way, like the presence of pain under an opiate) was
ham	always with him, there was another current of impression that never
ham	ceased to run, all through the night. He was on his way to dig some one
ham	out of a grave.
ham	Now, which of the multitude of faces that showed themselves before him
spam	was the true face of the buried person, the shadows of the night did
spam	not indicate; but they were all the faces of a man of five-and-forty by
spam	years, and they differed principally in the passions they expressed,
spam	and in the ghastliness of their worn and wasted state. Pride, contempt,
spam	defiance, stubbornness, submission, lamentation, succeeded one another;
ham	so did varieties of sunken cheek, cadaverous colour, emaciated hands
ham	and figures. But the face was in the main one face, and every head was
spam	prematurely white. A hundred times the dozing passenger inquired of this
ham	spectre:
spam	"Buried how long?"
spam	The answer was always the same: "Almost eighteen years."
ham	"You had abandoned all hope of being dug out?"
ham	"Long ago."
spam	"You know that you are recalled to life?"
ham	"They tell me so."
ham	"I hope you care to live?"
spam	"I can't say."
spam	"Shall I show her to you? Will you come and see her?"
spam	The answers to this question were various and contradictory. Sometimes
ham	the broken reply was, "Wait! It would kill me if I saw her too soon."
ham	Sometimes, it was given in a tender rain of tears, and then it was,
spam	"Take me to her." Sometimes it was staring and bewildered, and then it
ham	was, "I don't know her. I don't understand."
ham	After such imaginary discourse, the passenger in his fancy would dig,
spam	and dig, dig--now with a spade, now with a great key, now with his
spam	hands--to dig this wretched creature out. Got out at last, with earth
ham	hanging about his face and hair, he would suddenly fan away to dust. The
spam	passenger would then start to himself, and lower the window, to get the
spam	reality of mist and rain on his cheek.
ham	Yet even when his eyes were opened on the mist and rain, on the moving
ham	patch of light from the lamps, and the hedge at the roadside retreating
ham	by jerks, the night shadows outside the coach would fall into the train
spam	of the night shadows within. The real Banking-house by Temple Bar, the
ham	real business of the past day, the real strong rooms, the real express
spam	sent after him, and the real message returned, would all be there. Out
spam	of the midst of them, the ghostly face would rise, and he would accost
spam	it again.
ham	"Buried how long?"
ham	"Almost eighteen years."
ham	"I hope you care to live?"
ham	"I can't say."
ham	Dig--dig--dig--until an impatient movement from one of the two
ham	passengers would admonish him to pull up the window, draw his arm
spam	securely through the leathern strap, and speculate upon the two
ham	slumbering forms, until his mind lost its hold of them, and they again
spam	slid away into the bank and the grave.
spam	"Buried how long?"
spam	"Almost eighteen years."
ham	"You had abandoned all hope of being dug out?"
ham	"Long ago."
spam	The words were still in his hearing as just spoken--distinctly in
ham	his hearing as ever spoken words had been in his life--when the weary
ham	passenger started to the consciousness of daylight, and found that the
ham	shadows of the night were gone.
spam	He lowered the window, and looked out at the rising sun. There was a
ham	ridge of ploughed land, with a plough upon it where it had been left
ham	last night when the horses were unyoked; beyond, a quiet coppice-wood,
ham	in which many leaves of burning red and golden yellow still remained
spam	upon the trees. Though the earth was cold and wet, the sky was clear,
spam	and the sun rose bright, placid, and beautiful.
spam	"Eighteen years!" said the passenger, looking at the sun. "Gracious
spam	Creator of day! To be buried alive for eighteen years!"
spam	IV. The Preparation
spam	When the mail got successfully to Dover, in the course of the forenoon,
ham	the head drawer at the Royal George Hotel opened the coach-door as his
spam	custom was. He did it with some flourish of ceremony, for a mail journey
spam	from London in winter was an achievement to congratulate an adventurous
spam	traveller upon.
ham	By that time, there was only one adventurous traveller left be
ham	congratulated: for the two others had been set down at their respective
spam	roadside destinations. The mildewy inside of the coach, with its damp
spam	and dirty straw, its disagreeable smell, and its obscurity, was rather
ham	like a larger dog-kennel. Mr. Lorry, the passenger, shaking himself out
spam	of it in chains of straw, a tangle of shaggy wrapper, flapping hat, and
spam	muddy legs, was rather like a larger sort of dog.
ham	"There will be a packet to Calais, tomorrow, drawer?"
spam	"Yes, sir, if the weather holds and the wind sets tolerable fair. The
ham	tide will serve pretty nicely at about two in the afternoon, sir. Bed,
ham	sir?"
spam	"I shall not go to bed till night; but I want a bedroom, and a barber."
ham	"And then breakfast, sir? Yes, sir. That way, sir, if you please.
spam	Show Concord! Gentleman's valise and hot water to Concord. Pull off
ham	gentleman's boots in Concord. (You will find a fine sea-coal fire, sir.)
ham	Fetch barber to Concord. Stir about there, now, for Concord!"
ham	The Concord bed-chamber being always assigned to a passenger by the
ham	mail, and passengers by the mail being always heavily wrapped up from
ham	head to foot, the room had the odd interest for the establishment of the
spam	Royal George, that although but one kind of man was seen to go into it,
ham	all kinds and varieties of men came out of it. Consequently, another
ham	drawer, and two porters, and several maids and the landlady, were all
ham	loitering by accident at various points of the road between the Concord
ham	and the coffee-room, when a gentleman of sixty, formally dressed in a
ham	brown suit of clothes, pretty well worn, but very well kept, with large
ham	square cuffs and large flaps to the pockets, passed along on his way to
ham	his breakfast.
ham	The coffee-room had no other occupant, that forenoon, than the gentleman
ham	in brown. His breakfast-table was drawn before the fire, and as he sat,
spam	with its light shining on him, waiting for the meal, he sat so still,
ham	that he might have been sitting for his portrait.
spam	Very orderly and methodical he looked, with a hand on each knee, and a
ham	loud watch ticking a sonorous sermon under his flapped waist-coat,
spam	as though it pitted its gravity and longevity against the levity and
ham	evanescence of the brisk fire. He had a good leg, and was a little vain
ham	of it, for his brown stockings fitted sleek and close, and were of a
spam	fine texture; his shoes and buckles, too, though plain, were trim. He
spam	wore an odd little sleek crisp flaxen wig, setting very close to his
ham	head: which wig, it is to be presumed, was made of hair, but which
spam	looked far more as though it were spun from filaments of silk or glass.
spam	His linen, though not of a fineness in accordance with his stockings,
ham	was as white as the tops of the waves that broke upon the neighbouring
ham	beach, or the specks of sail that glinted in the sunlight far at sea. A
spam	face habitually suppressed and quieted, was still lighted up under the
ham	quaint wig by a pair of moist bright eyes that it must have cost
spam	their owner, in years gone by, some pains to drill to the composed and
ham	reserved expression of Tellson's Bank. He had a healthy colour in his
spam	cheeks, and his face, though lined, bore few traces of anxiety.
spam	But, perhaps the confidential bachelor clerks in Tellson's Bank were
spam	principally occupied with the cares of other people; and perhaps
ham	second-hand cares, like second-hand clothes, come easily off and on.
spam	Completing his resemblance to a man who was sitting for his portrait,
ham	Mr. Lorry dropped off to sleep. The arrival of his breakfast roused him,
ham	and he said to the drawer, as he moved his chair to it:
ham	"I wish accommodation prepared for a young lady who may come here at any
ham	time to-day. She may ask for Mr. Jarvis Lorry, or she may only ask for a
ham	gentleman from Tellson's Bank. Please to let me know."
spam	"Yes, sir. Tellson's Bank in London, sir?"
ham	"Yes."
ham	"Yes, sir. We have oftentimes the honour to entertain your gentlemen in
spam	their travelling backwards and forwards betwixt London and Paris, sir. A
spam	vast deal of travelling, sir, in Tellson and Company's House."
ham	"Yes. We are quite a French House, as well as an English one."
spam	"Yes, sir. Not much in the habit of such travelling yourself, I think,
ham	sir?"
spam	"Not of late years. It is fifteen years since we--since I--came last
spam	from France."
ham	"Indeed, sir? That was before my time here, sir. Before our people's
ham	time here, sir. The George was in other hands at that time, sir."
spam	"I believe so."
ham	"But I would hold a pretty wager, sir, that a House like Tellson and
spam	Company was flourishing, a matter of fifty, not to speak of fifteen
ham	years ago?"
spam	"You might treble that, and say a hundred and fifty, yet not be far from
ham	the truth."
ham	"Indeed, sir!"
spam	Rounding his mouth and both his eyes, as he stepped backward from the
ham	table, the waiter shifted his napkin from his right arm to his left,
ham	dropped into a comfortable attitude, and stood surveying the guest while
spam	he ate and drank, as from an observatory or watchtower. According to the
ham	immemorial usage of waiters in all ages.
spam	When Mr. Lorry had finished his breakfast, he went out for a stroll on
ham	the beach. The little narrow, crooked town of Dover hid itself away
spam	from the beach, and ran its head into the chalk cliffs, like a marine
ham	ostrich. The beach was a desert of heaps of sea and stones tumbling
ham	wildly about, and the sea did what it liked, and what it liked was
ham	destruction. It thundered at the town, and thundered at the cliffs, and
ham	brought the coast down, madly. The air among the houses was of so strong
spam	a piscatory flavour that one might have supposed sick fish went up to be
ham	dipped in it, as sick people went down to be dipped in the sea. A little
spam	fishing was done in the port, and a quantity of strolling about by
spam	night, and looking seaward: particularly at those times when the tide
ham	made, and was near flood. Small tradesmen, who did no business whatever,
ham	sometimes unaccountably realised large fortunes, and it was remarkable
ham	that nobody in the neighbourhood could endure a lamplighter.
spam	As the day declined into the afternoon, and the air, which had been
spam	at intervals clear enough to allow the French coast to be seen, became
spam	again charged with mist and vapour, Mr. Lorry's thoughts seemed to cloud
spam	too. When it was dark, and he sat before the coffee-room fire, awaiting
ham	his dinner as he had awaited his breakfast, his mind was busily digging,
ham	digging, digging, in the live red coals.
ham	A bottle of good claret after dinner does a digger in the red coals no
spam	harm, otherwise than as it has a tendency to throw him out of work.
ham	Mr. Lorry had been idle a long time, and had just poured out his last
ham	glassful of wine with as complete an appearance of satisfaction as is
spam	ever to be found in an elderly gentleman of a fresh complexion who has
spam	got to the end of a bottle, when a rattling of wheels came up the narrow
spam	street, and rumbled into the inn-yard.
spam	He set down his glass untouched. "This is Mam'selle!" said he.
spam	In a very few minutes the waiter came in to announce that Miss Manette
ham	had arrived from London, and would be happy to see the gentleman from
ham	Tellson's.
spam	"So soon?"
ham	Miss Manette had taken some refreshment on the road, and required none
spam	then, and was extremely anxious to see the gentleman from Tellson's
spam	immediately, if it suited his pleasure and convenience.
ham	The gentleman from Tellson's had nothing left for it but to empty his
spam	glass with an air of stolid desperation, settle his odd little flaxen
spam	wig at the ears, and follow the waiter to Miss Manette's apartment.
ham	It was a large, dark room, furnished in a funereal manner with black
spam	horsehair, and loaded with heavy dark tables. These had been oiled and
spam	oiled, until the two tall candles on the table in the middle of the room
spam	were gloomily reflected on every leaf; as if _they_ were buried, in deep
spam	graves of black mahogany, and no light to speak of could be expected
spam	from them until they were dug out.
spam	The obscurity was so difficult to penetrate that Mr. Lorry, picking his
ham	way over the well-worn Turkey carpet, supposed Miss Manette to be, for
ham	the moment, in some adjacent room, until, having got past the two tall
ham	candles, he saw standing to receive him by the table between them and
ham	the fire, a young lady of not more than seventeen, in a riding-cloak,
ham	and still holding her straw travelling-hat by its ribbon in her hand. As
ham	his eyes rested on a short, slight, pretty figure, a quantity of golden
ham	hair, a pair of blue eyes that met his own with an inquiring look, and
ham	a forehead with a singular capacity (remembering how young and smooth
ham	it was), of rifting and knitting itself into an expression that was
ham	not quite one of perplexity, or wonder, or alarm, or merely of a bright
spam	fixed attention, though it included all the four expressions--as his
spam	eyes rested on these things, a sudden vivid likeness passed before him,
ham	of a child whom he had held in his arms on the passage across that very
spam	Channel, one cold time, when the hail drifted heavily and the sea ran
spam	high. The likeness passed away, like a breath along the surface of
spam	the gaunt pier-glass behind her, on the frame of which, a hospital
ham	procession of negro cupids, several headless and all cripples, were
ham	offering black baskets of Dead Sea fruit to black divinities of the
spam	feminine gender--and he made his formal bow to Miss Manette.
ham	"Pray take a seat, sir." In a very clear and pleasant young voice; a
ham	little foreign in its accent, but a very little indeed.
spam	"I kiss your hand, miss," said Mr. Lorry, with the manners of an earlier
ham	date, as he made his formal bow again, and took his seat.
spam	"I received a letter from the Bank, sir, yesterday, informing me that
ham	some intelligence--or discovery--"
spam	"The word is not material, miss; either word will do."
ham	"--respecting the small property of my poor father, whom I never saw--so
spam	long dead--"
spam	Mr. Lorry moved in his chair, and cast a troubled look towards the
ham	hospital procession of negro cupids. As if _they_ had any help for
spam	anybody in their absurd baskets!
ham	"--rendered it necessary that I should go to Paris, there to communicate
ham	with a gentleman of the Bank, so good as to be despatched to Paris for
spam	the purpose."
spam	"Myself."
ham	"As I was prepared to hear, sir."
ham	She curtseyed to him (young ladies made curtseys in those days), with a
spam	pretty desire to convey to him that she felt how much older and wiser he
spam	was than she. He made her another bow.
spam	"I replied to the Bank, sir, that as it was considered necessary, by
ham	those who know, and who are so kind as to advise me, that I should go to
spam	France, and that as I am an orphan and have no friend who could go with
ham	me, I should esteem it highly if I might be permitted to place myself,
spam	during the journey, under that worthy gentleman's protection. The
spam	gentleman had left London, but I think a messenger was sent after him to
ham	beg the favour of his waiting for me here."
ham	"I was happy," said Mr. Lorry, "to be entrusted with the charge. I shall
ham	be more happy to execute it."
spam	"Sir, I thank you indeed. I thank you very gratefully. It was told me
spam	by the Bank that the gentleman would explain to me the details of the
ham	business, and that I must prepare myself to find them of a surprising
ham	nature. I have done my best to prepare myself, and I naturally have a
spam	strong and eager interest to know what they are."
ham	"Naturally," said Mr. Lorry. "Yes--I--"
spam	After a pause, he added, again settling the crisp flaxen wig at the
ham	ears, "It is very difficult to begin."
ham	He did not begin, but, in his indecision, met her glance. The young
ham	forehead lifted itself into that singular expression--but it was pretty
spam	and characteristic, besides being singular--and she raised her hand,
ham	as if with an involuntary action she caught at, or stayed some passing
ham	shadow.
ham	"Are you quite a stranger to me, sir?"
spam	"Am I not?" Mr. Lorry opened his hands, and extended them outwards with
ham	an argumentative smile.
spam	Between the eyebrows and just over the little feminine nose, the line of
ham	which was as delicate and fine as it was possible to be, the expression
spam	deepened itself as she took her seat thoughtfully in the chair by which
ham	she had hitherto remained standing. He watched her as she mused, and the
spam	moment she raised her eyes again, went on:
ham	"In your adopted country, I presume, I cannot do better than address you
spam	as a young English lady, Miss Manette?"
spam	"If you please, sir."
ham	"Miss Manette, I am a man of business. I have a business charge to
spam	acquit myself of. In your reception of it, don't heed me any more than
spam	if I was a speaking machine--truly, I am not much else. I will, with
spam	your leave, relate to you, miss, the story of one of our customers."
spam	"Story!"
ham	He seemed wilfully to mistake the word she had repeated, when he added,
ham	in a hurry, "Yes, customers; in the banking business we usually call
spam	our connection our customers. He was a French gentleman; a scientific
spam	gentleman; a man of great acquirements--a Doctor."
ham	"Not of Beauvais?"
ham	"Why, yes, of Beauvais. Like Monsieur Manette, your father, the
spam	gentleman was of Beauvais. Like Monsieur Manette, your father, the
spam	gentleman was of repute in Paris. I had the honour of knowing him there.
spam	Our relations were business relations, but confidential. I was at that
spam	time in our French House, and had been--oh! twenty years."
ham	"At that time--I may ask, at what time, sir?"
ham	"I speak, miss, of twenty years ago. He married--an English lady--and
ham	I was one of the trustees. His affairs, like the affairs of many other
ham	French gentlemen and French families, were entirely in Tellson's hands.
spam	In a similar way I am, or I have been, trustee of one kind or other for
ham	scores of our customers. These are mere business relations, miss;
ham	there is no friendship in them, no particular interest, nothing like
spam	sentiment. I have passed from one to another, in the course of my
ham	business life, just as I pass from one of our customers to another in
spam	the course of my business day; in short, I have no feelings; I am a mere
ham	machine. To go on--"
spam	"But this is my father's story, sir; and I begin to think"--the
ham	curiously roughened forehead was very intent upon him--"that when I was
ham	left an orphan through my mother's surviving my father only two years,
ham	it was you who brought me to England. I am almost sure it was you."
ham	Mr. Lorry took the hesitating little hand that confidingly advanced
ham	to take his, and he put it with some ceremony to his lips. He then
spam	conducted the young lady straightway to her chair again, and, holding
ham	the chair-back with his left hand, and using his right by turns to rub
spam	his chin, pull his wig at the ears, or point what he said, stood looking
spam	down into her face while she sat looking up into his.
spam	"Miss Manette, it _was_ I. And you will see how truly I spoke of myself
spam	just now, in saying I had no feelings, and that all the relations I hold
ham	with my fellow-creatures are mere business relations, when you reflect
ham	that I have never seen you since. No; you have been the ward of
spam	Tellson's House since, and I have been busy with the other business of
ham	Tellson's House since. Feelings! I have no time for them, no chance
ham	of them. I pass my whole life, miss, in turning an immense pecuniary
ham	Mangle."
ham	After this odd description of his daily routine of employment, Mr. Lorry
ham	flattened his flaxen wig upon his head with both hands (which was most
ham	unnecessary, for nothing could be flatter than its shining surface was
spam	before), and resumed his former attitude.
ham	"So far, miss (as you have remarked), this is the story of your
spam	regretted father. Now comes the difference. If your father had not died
ham	when he did--Don't be frightened! How you start!"
ham	She did, indeed, start. And she caught his wrist with both her hands.
spam	"Pray," said Mr. Lorry, in a soothing tone, bringing his left hand from
spam	the back of the chair to lay it on the supplicatory fingers that clasped
spam	him in so violent a tremble: "pray control your agitation--a matter of
ham	business. As I was saying--"
spam	Her look so discomposed him that he stopped, wandered, and began anew:
ham	"As I was saying; if Monsieur Manette had not died; if he had suddenly
spam	and silently disappeared; if he had been spirited away; if it had not
ham	been difficult to guess to what dreadful place, though no art could
ham	trace him; if he had an enemy in some compatriot who could exercise a
spam	privilege that I in my own time have known the boldest people afraid
ham	to speak of in a whisper, across the water there; for instance, the
ham	privilege of filling up blank forms for the consignment of any one
ham	to the oblivion of a prison for any length of time; if his wife had
spam	implored the king, the queen, the court, the clergy, for any tidings of
ham	him, and all quite in vain;--then the history of your father would have
ham	been the history of this unfortunate gentleman, the Doctor of Beauvais."
ham	"I entreat you to tell me more, sir."
spam	"I will. I am going to. You can bear it?"
ham	"I can bear anything but the uncertainty you leave me in at this
spam	moment."
ham	"You speak collectedly, and you--_are_ collected. That's good!" (Though
ham	his manner was less satisfied than his words.) "A matter of business.
ham	Regard it as a matter of business--business that must be done. Now
spam	if this doctor's wife, though a lady of great courage and spirit,
ham	had suffered so intensely from this cause before her little child was
ham	born--"
spam	"The little child was a daughter, sir."
spam	"A daughter. A-a-matter of business--don't be distressed. Miss, if the
spam	poor lady had suffered so intensely before her little child was born,
ham	that she came to the determination of sparing the poor child the
spam	inheritance of any part of the agony she had known the pains of, by
ham	rearing her in the belief that her father was dead--No, don't kneel! In
ham	Heaven's name why should you kneel to me!"
ham	"For the truth. O dear, good, compassionate sir, for the truth!"
spam	"A--a matter of business. You confuse me, and how can I transact
ham	business if I am confused? Let us be clear-headed. If you could kindly
ham	mention now, for instance, what nine times ninepence are, or how many
ham	shillings in twenty guineas, it would be so encouraging. I should be so
spam	much more at my ease about your state of mind."
ham	Without directly answering to this appeal, she sat so still when he had
ham	very gently raised her, and the hands that had not ceased to clasp
ham	his wrists were so much more steady than they had been, that she
spam	communicated some reassurance to Mr. Jarvis Lorry.
spam	"That's right, that's right. Courage! Business! You have business before
ham	you; useful business. Miss Manette, your mother took this course with
ham	you. And when she died--I believe broken-hearted--having never slackened
ham	her unavailing search for your father, she left you, at two years old,
ham	to grow to be blooming, beautiful, and happy, without the dark cloud
spam	upon you of living in uncertainty whether your father soon wore his
ham	heart out in prison, or wasted there through many lingering years."
ham	As he said the words he looked down, with an admiring pity, on the
ham	flowing golden hair; as if he pictured to himself that it might have
ham	been already tinged with grey.
spam	"You know that your parents had no great possession, and that what
spam	they had was secured to your mother and to you. There has been no new
ham	discovery, of money, or of any other property; but--"
ham	He felt his wrist held closer, and he stopped. The expression in the
spam	forehead, which had so particularly attracted his notice, and which was
spam	now immovable, had deepened into one of pain and horror.
spam	"But he has been--been found. He is alive. Greatly changed, it is too
ham	probable; almost a wreck, it is possible; though we will hope the best.
spam	Still, alive. Your father has been taken to the house of an old servant
spam	in Paris, and we are going there: I, to identify him if I can: you, to
ham	restore him to life, love, duty, rest, comfort."
spam	A shiver ran through her frame, and from it through his. She said, in a
ham	low, distinct, awe-stricken voice, as if she were saying it in a dream,
ham	"I am going to see his Ghost! It will be his Ghost--not him!"
spam	Mr. Lorry quietly chafed the hands that held his arm. "There, there,
spam	there! See now, see now! The best and the worst are known to you, now.
spam	You are well on your way to the poor wronged gentleman, and, with a fair
ham	sea voyage, and a fair land journey, you will be soon at his dear side."
ham	She repeated in the same tone, sunk to a whisper, "I have been free, I
ham	have been happy, yet his Ghost has never haunted me!"
spam	"Only one thing more," said Mr. Lorry, laying stress upon it as a
spam	wholesome means of enforcing her attention: "he has been found under
spam	another name; his own, long forgotten or long concealed. It would be
spam	worse than useless now to inquire which; worse than useless to seek to
spam	know whether he has been for years overlooked, or always designedly
spam	held prisoner. It would be worse than useless now to make any inquiries,
spam	because it would be dangerous. Better not to mention the subject,
ham	anywhere or in any way, and to remove him--for a while at all
ham	events--out of France. Even I, safe as an Englishman, and even
ham	Tellson's, important as they are to French credit, avoid all naming of
ham	the matter. I carry about me, not a scrap of writing openly referring
ham	to it. This is a secret service altogether. My credentials, entries,
ham	and memoranda, are all comprehended in the one line, 'Recalled to Life;'
ham	which may mean anything. But what is the matter! She doesn't notice a
ham	word! Miss Manette!"
ham	Perfectly still and silent, and not even fallen back in her chair, she
spam	sat under his hand, utterly insensible; with her eyes open and fixed
spam	upon him, and with that last expression looking as if it were carved or
spam	branded into her forehead. So close was her hold upon his arm, that he
ham	feared to detach himself lest he should hurt her; therefore he called
ham	out loudly for assistance without moving.
spam	A wild-looking woman, whom even in his agitation, Mr. Lorry observed to
ham	be all of a red colour, and to have red hair, and to be dressed in some
ham	extraordinary tight-fitting fashion, and to have on her head a most
spam	wonderful bonnet like a Grenadier wooden measure, and good measure too,
spam	or a great Stilton cheese, came running into the room in advance of the
ham	inn servants, and soon settled the question of his detachment from the
ham	poor young lady, by laying a brawny hand upon his chest, and sending him
spam	flying back against the nearest wall.
ham	("I really think this must be a man!" was Mr. Lorry's breathless
ham	reflection, simultaneously with his coming against the wall.)
ham	"Why, look at you all!" bawled this figure, addressing the inn servants.
spam	"Why don't you go and fetch things, instead of standing there staring
ham	at me? I am not so much to look at, am I? Why don't you go and fetch
ham	things? I'll let you know, if you don't bring smelling-salts, cold
spam	water, and vinegar, quick, I will."
ham	There was an immediate dispersal for these restoratives, and she
ham	softly laid the patient on a sofa, and tended her with great skill and
spam	gentleness: calling her "my precious!" and "my bird!" and spreading her
spam	golden hair aside over her shoulders with great pride and care.
spam	"And you in brown!" she said, indignantly turning to Mr. Lorry;
ham	"couldn't you tell her what you had to tell her, without frightening her
spam	to death? Look at her, with her pretty pale face and her cold hands. Do
spam	you call _that_ being a Banker?"
ham	Mr. Lorry was so exceedingly disconcerted by a question so hard to
ham	answer, that he could only look on, at a distance, with much feebler
spam	sympathy and humility, while the strong woman, having banished the inn
spam	servants under the mysterious penalty of "letting them know" something
ham	not mentioned if they stayed there, staring, recovered her charge by a
spam	regular series of gradations, and coaxed her to lay her drooping head
ham	upon her shoulder.
spam	"I hope she will do well now," said Mr. Lorry.
ham	"No thanks to you in brown, if she does. My darling pretty!"
spam	"I hope," said Mr. Lorry, after another pause of feeble sympathy and
ham	humility, "that you accompany Miss Manette to France?"
ham	"A likely thing, too!" replied the strong woman. "If it was ever
spam	intended that I should go across salt water, do you suppose Providence
ham	would have cast my lot in an island?"
ham	This being another question hard to answer, Mr. Jarvis Lorry withdrew to
spam	consider it.
ham	V. The Wine-shop
spam	A large cask of wine had been dropped and broken, in the street. The
ham	accident had happened in getting it out of a cart; the cask had tumbled
spam	out with a run, the hoops had burst, and it lay on the stones just
spam	outside the door of the wine-shop, shattered like a walnut-shell.
ham	All the people within reach had suspended their business, or their
spam	idleness, to run to the spot and drink the wine. The rough, irregular
ham	stones of the street, pointing every way, and designed, one might have
spam	thought, expressly to lame all living creatures that approached them,
ham	had dammed it into little pools; these were surrounded, each by its own
ham	jostling group or crowd, according to its size. Some men kneeled down,
spam	made scoops of their two hands joined, and sipped, or tried to help
ham	women, who bent over their shoulders, to sip, before the wine had all
spam	run out between their fingers. Others, men and women, dipped in
ham	the puddles with little mugs of mutilated earthenware, or even with
ham	handkerchiefs from women's heads, which were squeezed dry into infants'
ham	mouths; others made small mud-embankments, to stem the wine as it ran;
spam	others, directed by lookers-on up at high windows, darted here and
ham	there, to cut off little streams of wine that started away in new
spam	directions; others devoted themselves to the sodden and lee-dyed
spam	pieces of the cask, licking, and even champing the moister wine-rotted
ham	fragments with eager relish. There was no drainage to carry off the
ham	wine, and not only did it all get taken up, but so much mud got taken up
spam	along with it, that there might have been a scavenger in the street,
spam	if anybody acquainted with it could have believed in such a miraculous
ham	presence.
ham	A shrill sound of laughter and of amused voices--voices of men, women,
spam	and children--resounded in the street while this wine game lasted. There
spam	was little roughness in the sport, and much playfulness. There was a
ham	special companionship in it, an observable inclination on the part
spam	of every one to join some other one, which led, especially among the
ham	luckier or lighter-hearted, to frolicsome embraces, drinking of healths,
spam	shaking of hands, and even joining of hands and dancing, a dozen
ham	together. When the wine was gone, and the places where it had been
spam	most abundant were raked into a gridiron-pattern by fingers, these
spam	demonstrations ceased, as suddenly as they had broken out. The man who
spam	had left his saw sticking in the firewood he was cutting, set it in
ham	motion again; the women who had left on a door-step the little pot of
ham	hot ashes, at which she had been trying to soften the pain in her own
ham	starved fingers and toes, or in those of her child, returned to it; men
spam	with bare arms, matted locks, and cadaverous faces, who had emerged into
ham	the winter light from cellars, moved away, to descend again; and a gloom
spam	gathered on the scene that appeared more natural to it than sunshine.
ham	The wine was red wine, and had stained the ground of the narrow street
ham	in the suburb of Saint Antoine, in Paris, where it was spilled. It had
ham	stained many hands, too, and many faces, and many naked feet, and many
spam	wooden shoes. The hands of the man who sawed the wood, left red marks
spam	on the billets; and the forehead of the woman who nursed her baby, was
spam	stained with the stain of the old rag she wound about her head again.
ham	Those who had been greedy with the staves of the cask, had acquired a
spam	tigerish smear about the mouth; and one tall joker so besmirched, his
spam	head more out of a long squalid bag of a nightcap than in it, scrawled
ham	upon a wall with his finger dipped in muddy wine-lees--BLOOD.
spam	The time was to come, when that wine too would be spilled on the
ham	street-stones, and when the stain of it would be red upon many there.
ham	And now that the cloud settled on Saint Antoine, which a momentary
ham	gleam had driven from his sacred countenance, the darkness of it was
ham	heavy--cold, dirt, sickness, ignorance, and want, were the lords in
ham	waiting on the saintly presence--nobles of great power all of them;
ham	but, most especially the last. Samples of a people that had undergone a
ham	terrible grinding and regrinding in the mill, and certainly not in the
spam	fabulous mill which ground old people young, shivered at every corner,
spam	passed in and out at every doorway, looked from every window, fluttered
ham	in every vestige of a garment that the wind shook. The mill which
ham	had worked them down, was the mill that grinds young people old; the
spam	children had ancient faces and grave voices; and upon them, and upon the
spam	grown faces, and ploughed into every furrow of age and coming up afresh,
ham	was the sigh, Hunger. It was prevalent everywhere. Hunger was pushed out
spam	of the tall houses, in the wretched clothing that hung upon poles and
ham	lines; Hunger was patched into them with straw and rag and wood and
ham	paper; Hunger was repeated in every fragment of the small modicum of
ham	firewood that the man sawed off; Hunger stared down from the smokeless
spam	chimneys, and started up from the filthy street that had no offal,
ham	among its refuse, of anything to eat. Hunger was the inscription on the
ham	baker's shelves, written in every small loaf of his scanty stock of
ham	bad bread; at the sausage-shop, in every dead-dog preparation that
ham	was offered for sale. Hunger rattled its dry bones among the roasting
ham	chestnuts in the turned cylinder; Hunger was shred into atomics in every
ham	farthing porringer of husky chips of potato, fried with some reluctant
ham	drops of oil.
ham	Its abiding place was in all things fitted to it. A narrow winding
ham	street, full of offence and stench, with other narrow winding streets
ham	diverging, all peopled by rags and nightcaps, and all smelling of rags
ham	and nightcaps, and all visible things with a brooding look upon them
spam	that looked ill. In the hunted air of the people there was yet some
ham	wild-beast thought of the possibility of turning at bay. Depressed and
ham	slinking though they were, eyes of fire were not wanting among them; nor
spam	compressed lips, white with what they suppressed; nor foreheads knitted
ham	into the likeness of the gallows-rope they mused about enduring, or
spam	inflicting. The trade signs (and they were almost as many as the shops)
spam	were, all, grim illustrations of Want. The butcher and the porkman
spam	painted up, only the leanest scrags of meat; the baker, the coarsest of
spam	meagre loaves. The people rudely pictured as drinking in the wine-shops,
ham	croaked over their scanty measures of thin wine and beer, and were
spam	gloweringly confidential together. Nothing was represented in a
spam	flourishing condition, save tools and weapons; but, the cutler's knives
ham	and axes were sharp and bright, the smith's hammers were heavy, and the
ham	gunmaker's stock was murderous. The crippling stones of the pavement,
spam	with their many little reservoirs of mud and water, had no footways, but
spam	broke off abruptly at the doors. The kennel, to make amends, ran down
ham	the middle of the street--when it ran at all: which was only after heavy
ham	rains, and then it ran, by many eccentric fits, into the houses. Across
spam	the streets, at wide intervals, one clumsy lamp was slung by a rope and
spam	pulley; at night, when the lamplighter had let these down, and lighted,
spam	and hoisted them again, a feeble grove of dim wicks swung in a sickly
spam	manner overhead, as if they were at sea. Indeed they were at sea, and
ham	the ship and crew were in peril of tempest.
ham	For, the time was to come, when the gaunt scarecrows of that region
ham	should have watched the lamplighter, in their idleness and hunger, so
spam	long, as to conceive the idea of improving on his method, and hauling
spam	up men by those ropes and pulleys, to flare upon the darkness of their
spam	condition. But, the time was not come yet; and every wind that blew over
spam	France shook the rags of the scarecrows in vain, for the birds, fine of
ham	song and feather, took no warning.
ham	The wine-shop was a corner shop, better than most others in its
ham	appearance and degree, and the master of the wine-shop had stood outside
spam	it, in a yellow waistcoat and green breeches, looking on at the struggle
spam	for the lost wine. "It's not my affair," said he, with a final shrug
spam	of the shoulders. "The people from the market did it. Let them bring
spam	another."
ham	There, his eyes happening to catch the tall joker writing up his joke,
ham	he called to him across the way:
ham	"Say, then, my Gaspard, what do you do there?"
ham	The fellow pointed to his joke with immense significance, as is often
ham	the way with his tribe. It missed its mark, and completely failed, as is
ham	often the way with his tribe too.
spam	"What now? Are you a subject for the mad hospital?" said the wine-shop
spam	keeper, crossing the road, and obliterating the jest with a handful of
spam	mud, picked up for the purpose, and smeared over it. "Why do you write
ham	in the public streets? Is there--tell me thou--is there no other place
ham	to write such words in?"
spam	In his expostulation he dropped his cleaner hand (perhaps accidentally,
ham	perhaps not) upon the joker's heart. The joker rapped it with his
ham	own, took a nimble spring upward, and came down in a fantastic dancing
spam	attitude, with one of his stained shoes jerked off his foot into his
ham	hand, and held out. A joker of an extremely, not to say wolfishly
spam	practical character, he looked, under those circumstances.
spam	"Put it on, put it on," said the other. "Call wine, wine; and finish
ham	there." With that advice, he wiped his soiled hand upon the joker's
spam	dress, such as it was--quite deliberately, as having dirtied the hand on
ham	his account; and then recrossed the road and entered the wine-shop.
spam	This wine-shop keeper was a bull-necked, martial-looking man of thirty,
spam	and he should have been of a hot temperament, for, although it was a
ham	bitter day, he wore no coat, but carried one slung over his shoulder.
spam	His shirt-sleeves were rolled up, too, and his brown arms were bare to
spam	the elbows. Neither did he wear anything more on his head than his own
ham	crisply-curling short dark hair. He was a dark man altogether, with good
ham	eyes and a good bold breadth between them. Good-humoured looking on
ham	the whole, but implacable-looking, too; evidently a man of a strong
spam	resolution and a set purpose; a man not desirable to be met, rushing
ham	down a narrow pass with a gulf on either side, for nothing would turn
spam	the man.
ham	Madame Defarge, his wife, sat in the shop behind the counter as he
spam	came in. Madame Defarge was a stout woman of about his own age, with
spam	a watchful eye that seldom seemed to look at anything, a large hand
spam	heavily ringed, a steady face, strong features, and great composure of
spam	manner. There was a character about Madame Defarge, from which one might
spam	have predicated that she did not often make mistakes against herself
ham	in any of the reckonings over which she presided. Madame Defarge being
spam	sensitive to cold, was wrapped in fur, and had a quantity of bright
ham	shawl twined about her head, though not to the concealment of her large
spam	earrings. Her knitting was before her, but she had laid it down to pick
ham	her teeth with a toothpick. Thus engaged, with her right elbow supported
ham	by her left hand, Madame Defarge said nothing when her lord came in, but
spam	coughed just one grain of cough. This, in combination with the lifting
spam	of her darkly defined eyebrows over her toothpick by the breadth of a
ham	line, suggested to her husband that he would do well to look round the
spam	shop among the customers, for any new customer who had dropped in while
spam	he stepped over the way.
ham	The wine-shop keeper accordingly rolled his eyes about, until they
ham	rested upon an elderly gentleman and a young lady, who were seated in
ham	a corner. Other company were there: two playing cards, two playing
ham	dominoes, three standing by the counter lengthening out a short supply
ham	of wine. As he passed behind the counter, he took notice that the
ham	elderly gentleman said in a look to the young lady, "This is our man."
ham	"What the devil do _you_ do in that galley there?" said Monsieur Defarge
ham	to himself; "I don't know you."
ham	But, he feigned not to notice the two strangers, and fell into discourse
spam	with the triumvirate of customers who were drinking at the counter.
spam	"How goes it, Jacques?" said one of these three to Monsieur Defarge. "Is
spam	all the spilt wine swallowed?"
ham	"Every drop, Jacques," answered Monsieur Defarge.
spam	When this interchange of Christian name was effected, Madame Defarge,
spam	picking her teeth with her toothpick, coughed another grain of cough,
ham	and raised her eyebrows by the breadth of another line.
spam	"It is not often," said the second of the three, addressing Monsieur
ham	Defarge, "that many of these miserable beasts know the taste of wine, or
ham	of anything but black bread and death. Is it not so, Jacques?"
ham	"It is so, Jacques," Monsieur Defarge returned.
ham	At this second interchange of the Christian name, Madame Defarge, still
spam	using her toothpick with profound composure, coughed another grain of
spam	cough, and raised her eyebrows by the breadth of another line.
spam	The last of the three now said his say, as he put down his empty
spam	drinking vessel and smacked his lips.
ham	"Ah! So much the worse! A bitter taste it is that such poor cattle
spam	always have in their mouths, and hard lives they live, Jacques. Am I
ham	right, Jacques?"
spam	"You are right, Jacques," was the response of Monsieur Defarge.
ham	This third interchange of the Christian name was completed at the moment
ham	when Madame Defarge put her toothpick by, kept her eyebrows up, and
spam	slightly rustled in her seat.
spam	"Hold then! True!" muttered her husband. "Gentlemen--my wife!"
spam	The three customers pulled off their hats to Madame Defarge, with three
ham	flourishes. She acknowledged their homage by bending her head, and
spam	giving them a quick look. Then she glanced in a casual manner round the
spam	wine-shop, took up her knitting with great apparent calmness and repose
ham	of spirit, and became absorbed in it.
ham	"Gentlemen," said her husband, who had kept his bright eye observantly
spam	upon her, "good day. The chamber, furnished bachelor-fashion, that you
ham	wished to see, and were inquiring for when I stepped out, is on the
ham	fifth floor. The doorway of the staircase gives on the little courtyard
ham	close to the left here," pointing with his hand, "near to the window of
spam	my establishment. But, now that I remember, one of you has already been
ham	there, and can show the way. Gentlemen, adieu!"
ham	They paid for their wine, and left the place. The eyes of Monsieur
ham	Defarge were studying his wife at her knitting when the elderly
spam	gentleman advanced from his corner, and begged the favour of a word.
ham	"Willingly, sir," said Monsieur Defarge, and quietly stepped with him to
spam	the door.
ham	Their conference was very short, but very decided. Almost at the first
ham	word, Monsieur Defarge started and became deeply attentive. It had
spam	not lasted a minute, when he nodded and went out. The gentleman then
spam	beckoned to the young lady, and they, too, went out. Madame Defarge
spam	knitted with nimble fingers and steady eyebrows, and saw nothing.
spam	Mr. Jarvis Lorry and Miss Manette, emerging from the wine-shop thus,
ham	joined Monsieur Defarge in the doorway to which he had directed his own
ham	company just before. It opened from a stinking little black courtyard,
spam	and was the general public entrance to a great pile of houses, inhabited
ham	by a great number of people. In the gloomy tile-paved entry to the
spam	gloomy tile-paved staircase, Monsieur Defarge bent down on one knee
spam	to the child of his old master, and put her hand to his lips. It was
ham	a gentle action, but not at all gently done; a very remarkable
spam	transformation had come over him in a few seconds. He had no good-humour
ham	in his face, nor any openness of aspect left, but had become a secret,
spam	angry, dangerous man.
ham	"It is very high; it is a little difficult. Better to begin slowly."
spam	Thus, Monsieur Defarge, in a stern voice, to Mr. Lorry, as they began
ham	ascending the stairs.
ham	"Is he alone?" the latter whispered.
ham	"Alone! God help him, who should be with him!" said the other, in the
ham	same low voice.
spam	"Is he always alone, then?"
spam	"Yes."
ham	"Of his own desire?"
ham	"Of his own necessity. As he was, when I first saw him after they
ham	found me and demanded to know if I would take him, and, at my peril be
spam	discreet--as he was then, so he is now."
ham	"He is greatly changed?"
spam	"Changed!"
ham	The keeper of the wine-shop stopped to strike the wall with his hand,
ham	and mutter a tremendous curse. No direct answer could have been half so
spam	forcible. Mr. Lorry's spirits grew heavier and heavier, as he and his
spam	two companions ascended higher and higher.
ham	Such a staircase, with its accessories, in the older and more crowded
ham	parts of Paris, would be bad enough now; but, at that time, it was vile
ham	indeed to unaccustomed and unhardened senses. Every little habitation
ham	within the great foul nest of one high building--that is to say,
ham	the room or rooms within every door that opened on the general
spam	staircase--left its own heap of refuse on its own landing, besides
spam	flinging other refuse from its own windows. The uncontrollable and
ham	hopeless mass of decomposition so engendered, would have polluted
spam	the air, even if poverty and deprivation had not loaded it with their
spam	intangible impurities; the two bad sources combined made it almost
ham	insupportable. Through such an atmosphere, by a steep dark shaft of dirt
ham	and poison, the way lay. Yielding to his own disturbance of mind, and to
ham	his young companion's agitation, which became greater every instant, Mr.
ham	Jarvis Lorry twice stopped to rest. Each of these stoppages was made
spam	at a doleful grating, by which any languishing good airs that were left
spam	uncorrupted, seemed to escape, and all spoilt and sickly vapours seemed
ham	to crawl in. Through the rusted bars, tastes, rather than glimpses, were
spam	caught of the jumbled neighbourhood; and nothing within range, nearer
ham	or lower than the summits of the two great towers of Notre-Dame, had any
ham	promise on it of healthy life or wholesome aspirations.
spam	At last, the top of the staircase was gained, and they stopped for the
ham	third time. There was yet an upper staircase, of a steeper inclination
ham	and of contracted dimensions, to be ascended, before the garret story
spam	was reached. The keeper of the wine-shop, always going a little in
spam	advance, and always going on the side which Mr. Lorry took, as though he
spam	dreaded to be asked any question by the young lady, turned himself about
spam	here, and, carefully feeling in the pockets of the coat he carried over
spam	his shoulder, took out a key.
spam	"The door is locked then, my friend?" said Mr. Lorry, surprised.
spam	"Ay. Yes," was the grim reply of Monsieur Defarge.
spam	"You think it necessary to keep the unfortunate gentleman so retired?"
spam	"I think it necessary to turn the key." Monsieur Defarge whispered it
ham	closer in his ear, and frowned heavily.
spam	"Why?"
ham	"Why! Because he has lived so long, locked up, that he would be
spam	frightened--rave--tear himself to pieces--die--come to I know not what
ham	harm--if his door was left open."
spam	"Is it possible!" exclaimed Mr. Lorry.
spam	"Is it possible!" repeated Defarge, bitterly. "Yes. And a beautiful
ham	world we live in, when it _is_ possible, and when many other such things
ham	are possible, and not only possible, but done--done, see you!--under
ham	that sky there, every day. Long live the Devil. Let us go on."
ham	This dialogue had been held in so very low a whisper, that not a word
spam	of it had reached the young lady's ears. But, by this time she trembled
spam	under such strong emotion, and her face expressed such deep anxiety,
ham	and, above all, such dread and terror, that Mr. Lorry felt it incumbent
spam	on him to speak a word or two of reassurance.
spam	"Courage, dear miss! Courage! Business! The worst will be over in a
spam	moment; it is but passing the room-door, and the worst is over. Then,
ham	all the good you bring to him, all the relief, all the happiness you
spam	bring to him, begin. Let our good friend here, assist you on that side.
spam	That's well, friend Defarge. Come, now. Business, business!"
spam	They went up slowly and softly. The staircase was short, and they were
spam	soon at the top. There, as it had an abrupt turn in it, they came all at
spam	once in sight of three men, whose heads were bent down close together at
spam	the side of a door, and who were intently looking into the room to which
ham	the door belonged, through some chinks or holes in the wall. On hearing
ham	footsteps close at hand, these three turned, and rose, and showed
ham	themselves to be the three of one name who had been drinking in the
ham	wine-shop.
spam	"I forgot them in the surprise of your visit," explained Monsieur
spam	Defarge. "Leave us, good boys; we have business here."
spam	The three glided by, and went silently down.
ham	There appearing to be no other door on that floor, and the keeper of
spam	the wine-shop going straight to this one when they were left alone, Mr.
spam	Lorry asked him in a whisper, with a little anger:
ham	"Do you make a show of Monsieur Manette?"
spam	"I show him, in the way you have seen, to a chosen few."
ham	"Is that well?"
ham	"_I_ think it is well."
spam	"Who are the few? How do you choose them?"
ham	"I choose them as real men, of my name--Jacques is my name--to whom the
ham	sight is likely to do good. Enough; you are English; that is another
ham	thing. Stay there, if you please, a little moment."
spam	With an admonitory gesture to keep them back, he stooped, and looked in
ham	through the crevice in the wall. Soon raising his head again, he struck
spam	twice or thrice upon the door--evidently with no other object than to
ham	make a noise there. With the same intention, he drew the key across it,
ham	three or four times, before he put it clumsily into the lock, and turned
spam	it as heavily as he could.
spam	The door slowly opened inward under his hand, and he looked into the
ham	room and said something. A faint voice answered something. Little more
ham	than a single syllable could have been spoken on either side.
ham	He looked back over his shoulder, and beckoned them to enter. Mr. Lorry
spam	got his arm securely round the daughter's waist, and held her; for he
spam	felt that she was sinking.
ham	"A-a-a-business, business!" he urged, with a moisture that was not of
spam	business shining on his cheek. "Come in, come in!"
spam	"I am afraid of it," she answered, shuddering.
spam	"Of it? What?"
ham	"I mean of him. Of my father."
ham	Rendered in a manner desperate, by her state and by the beckoning of
spam	their conductor, he drew over his neck the arm that shook upon his
ham	shoulder, lifted her a little, and hurried her into the room. He sat her
ham	down just within the door, and held her, clinging to him.
ham	Defarge drew out the key, closed the door, locked it on the inside,
ham	took out the key again, and held it in his hand. All this he did,
ham	methodically, and with as loud and harsh an accompaniment of noise as he
spam	could make. Finally, he walked across the room with a measured tread to
ham	where the window was. He stopped there, and faced round.
spam	The garret, built to be a depository for firewood and the like, was dim
spam	and dark: for, the window of dormer shape, was in truth a door in the
ham	roof, with a little crane over it for the hoisting up of stores from
ham	the street: unglazed, and closing up the middle in two pieces, like any
ham	other door of French construction. To exclude the cold, one half of this
spam	door was fast closed, and the other was opened but a very little way.
spam	Such a scanty portion of light was admitted through these means, that it
spam	was difficult, on first coming in, to see anything; and long habit
spam	alone could have slowly formed in any one, the ability to do any work
ham	requiring nicety in such obscurity. Yet, work of that kind was being
spam	done in the garret; for, with his back towards the door, and his face
ham	towards the window where the keeper of the wine-shop stood looking at
spam	him, a white-haired man sat on a low bench, stooping forward and very
ham	busy, making shoes.
spam	VI. The Shoemaker
ham	"Good day!" said Monsieur Defarge, looking down at the white head that
spam	bent low over the shoemaking.
spam	It was raised for a moment, and a very faint voice responded to the
spam	salutation, as if it were at a distance:
spam	"Good day!"
spam	"You are still hard at work, I see?"
ham	After a long silence, the head was lifted for another moment, and the
spam	voice replied, "Yes--I am working." This time, a pair of haggard eyes
spam	had looked at the questioner, before the face had dropped again.
spam	The faintness of the voice was pitiable and dreadful. It was not the
spam	faintness of physical weakness, though confinement and hard fare no
ham	doubt had their part in it. Its deplorable peculiarity was, that it was
spam	the faintness of solitude and disuse. It was like the last feeble echo
ham	of a sound made long and long ago. So entirely had it lost the life and
spam	resonance of the human voice, that it affected the senses like a once
spam	beautiful colour faded away into a poor weak stain. So sunken and
spam	suppressed it was, that it was like a voice underground. So expressive
