spam	it was, of a hopeless and lost creature, that a famished traveller,
ham	wearied out by lonely wandering in a wilderness, would have remembered
spam	home and friends in such a tone before lying down to die.
spam	Some minutes of silent work had passed: and the haggard eyes had looked
ham	up again: not with any interest or curiosity, but with a dull mechanical
ham	perception, beforehand, that the spot where the only visitor they were
spam	aware of had stood, was not yet empty.
ham	"I want," said Defarge, who had not removed his gaze from the shoemaker,
ham	"to let in a little more light here. You can bear a little more?"
ham	The shoemaker stopped his work; looked with a vacant air of listening,
spam	at the floor on one side of him; then similarly, at the floor on the
ham	other side of him; then, upward at the speaker.
ham	"What did you say?"
spam	"You can bear a little more light?"
ham	"I must bear it, if you let it in." (Laying the palest shadow of a
ham	stress upon the second word.)
spam	The opened half-door was opened a little further, and secured at that
ham	angle for the time. A broad ray of light fell into the garret, and
ham	showed the workman with an unfinished shoe upon his lap, pausing in his
spam	labour. His few common tools and various scraps of leather were at his
spam	feet and on his bench. He had a white beard, raggedly cut, but not very
spam	long, a hollow face, and exceedingly bright eyes. The hollowness and
ham	thinness of his face would have caused them to look large, under his yet
ham	dark eyebrows and his confused white hair, though they had been really
spam	otherwise; but, they were naturally large, and looked unnaturally so.
ham	His yellow rags of shirt lay open at the throat, and showed his body
spam	to be withered and worn. He, and his old canvas frock, and his loose
spam	stockings, and all his poor tatters of clothes, had, in a long seclusion
spam	from direct light and air, faded down to such a dull uniformity of
ham	parchment-yellow, that it would have been hard to say which was which.
spam	He had put up a hand between his eyes and the light, and the very bones
spam	of it seemed transparent. So he sat, with a steadfastly vacant gaze,
spam	pausing in his work. He never looked at the figure before him, without
ham	first looking down on this side of himself, then on that, as if he had
ham	lost the habit of associating place with sound; he never spoke, without
spam	first wandering in this manner, and forgetting to speak.
spam	"Are you going to finish that pair of shoes to-day?" asked Defarge,
ham	motioning to Mr. Lorry to come forward.
ham	"What did you say?"
ham	"Do you mean to finish that pair of shoes to-day?"
spam	"I can't say that I mean to. I suppose so. I don't know."
spam	But, the question reminded him of his work, and he bent over it again.
ham	Mr. Lorry came silently forward, leaving the daughter by the door. When
spam	he had stood, for a minute or two, by the side of Defarge, the shoemaker
ham	looked up. He showed no surprise at seeing another figure, but the
spam	unsteady fingers of one of his hands strayed to his lips as he looked at
ham	it (his lips and his nails were of the same pale lead-colour), and then
spam	the hand dropped to his work, and he once more bent over the shoe. The
spam	look and the action had occupied but an instant.
ham	"You have a visitor, you see," said Monsieur Defarge.
spam	"What did you say?"
spam	"Here is a visitor."
spam	The shoemaker looked up as before, but without removing a hand from his
spam	work.
ham	"Come!" said Defarge. "Here is monsieur, who knows a well-made shoe when
ham	he sees one. Show him that shoe you are working at. Take it, monsieur."
spam	Mr. Lorry took it in his hand.
ham	"Tell monsieur what kind of shoe it is, and the maker's name."
spam	There was a longer pause than usual, before the shoemaker replied:
spam	"I forget what it was you asked me. What did you say?"
spam	"I said, couldn't you describe the kind of shoe, for monsieur's
spam	information?"
spam	"It is a lady's shoe. It is a young lady's walking-shoe. It is in the
spam	present mode. I never saw the mode. I have had a pattern in my hand." He
ham	glanced at the shoe with some little passing touch of pride.
ham	"And the maker's name?" said Defarge.
ham	Now that he had no work to hold, he laid the knuckles of the right hand
spam	in the hollow of the left, and then the knuckles of the left hand in the
spam	hollow of the right, and then passed a hand across his bearded chin, and
spam	so on in regular changes, without a moment's intermission. The task of
spam	recalling him from the vagrancy into which he always sank when he
spam	had spoken, was like recalling some very weak person from a swoon, or
spam	endeavouring, in the hope of some disclosure, to stay the spirit of a
spam	fast-dying man.
ham	"Did you ask me for my name?"
spam	"Assuredly I did."
ham	"One Hundred and Five, North Tower."
ham	"Is that all?"
ham	"One Hundred and Five, North Tower."
ham	With a weary sound that was not a sigh, nor a groan, he bent to work
ham	again, until the silence was again broken.
spam	"You are not a shoemaker by trade?" said Mr. Lorry, looking steadfastly
spam	at him.
ham	His haggard eyes turned to Defarge as if he would have transferred the
ham	question to him: but as no help came from that quarter, they turned back
ham	on the questioner when they had sought the ground.
ham	"I am not a shoemaker by trade? No, I was not a shoemaker by trade. I-I
spam	learnt it here. I taught myself. I asked leave to--"
ham	He lapsed away, even for minutes, ringing those measured changes on his
spam	hands the whole time. His eyes came slowly back, at last, to the face
spam	from which they had wandered; when they rested on it, he started, and
spam	resumed, in the manner of a sleeper that moment awake, reverting to a
spam	subject of last night.
ham	"I asked leave to teach myself, and I got it with much difficulty after
ham	a long while, and I have made shoes ever since."
ham	As he held out his hand for the shoe that had been taken from him, Mr.
ham	Lorry said, still looking steadfastly in his face:
ham	"Monsieur Manette, do you remember nothing of me?"
ham	The shoe dropped to the ground, and he sat looking fixedly at the
ham	questioner.
spam	"Monsieur Manette"; Mr. Lorry laid his hand upon Defarge's arm; "do you
spam	remember nothing of this man? Look at him. Look at me. Is there no old
spam	banker, no old business, no old servant, no old time, rising in your
spam	mind, Monsieur Manette?"
ham	As the captive of many years sat looking fixedly, by turns, at Mr.
spam	Lorry and at Defarge, some long obliterated marks of an actively intent
spam	intelligence in the middle of the forehead, gradually forced themselves
ham	through the black mist that had fallen on him. They were overclouded
spam	again, they were fainter, they were gone; but they had been there. And
ham	so exactly was the expression repeated on the fair young face of her who
ham	had crept along the wall to a point where she could see him, and where
ham	she now stood looking at him, with hands which at first had been only
ham	raised in frightened compassion, if not even to keep him off and
ham	shut out the sight of him, but which were now extending towards him,
spam	trembling with eagerness to lay the spectral face upon her warm young
spam	breast, and love it back to life and hope--so exactly was the expression
ham	repeated (though in stronger characters) on her fair young face, that it
spam	looked as though it had passed like a moving light, from him to her.
spam	Darkness had fallen on him in its place. He looked at the two, less and
spam	less attentively, and his eyes in gloomy abstraction sought the ground
spam	and looked about him in the old way. Finally, with a deep long sigh, he
spam	took the shoe up, and resumed his work.
ham	"Have you recognised him, monsieur?" asked Defarge in a whisper.
ham	"Yes; for a moment. At first I thought it quite hopeless, but I have
spam	unquestionably seen, for a single moment, the face that I once knew so
ham	well. Hush! Let us draw further back. Hush!"
spam	She had moved from the wall of the garret, very near to the bench on
ham	which he sat. There was something awful in his unconsciousness of the
spam	figure that could have put out its hand and touched him as he stooped
spam	over his labour.
spam	Not a word was spoken, not a sound was made. She stood, like a spirit,
ham	beside him, and he bent over his work.
spam	It happened, at length, that he had occasion to change the instrument
ham	in his hand, for his shoemaker's knife. It lay on that side of him
spam	which was not the side on which she stood. He had taken it up, and was
spam	stooping to work again, when his eyes caught the skirt of her dress. He
ham	raised them, and saw her face. The two spectators started forward,
spam	but she stayed them with a motion of her hand. She had no fear of his
spam	striking at her with the knife, though they had.
spam	He stared at her with a fearful look, and after a while his lips began
ham	to form some words, though no sound proceeded from them. By degrees, in
ham	the pauses of his quick and laboured breathing, he was heard to say:
ham	"What is this?"
spam	With the tears streaming down her face, she put her two hands to her
ham	lips, and kissed them to him; then clasped them on her breast, as if she
spam	laid his ruined head there.
spam	"You are not the gaoler's daughter?"
ham	She sighed "No."
ham	"Who are you?"
ham	Not yet trusting the tones of her voice, she sat down on the bench
spam	beside him. He recoiled, but she laid her hand upon his arm. A strange
spam	thrill struck him when she did so, and visibly passed over his frame; he
ham	laid the knife down softly, as he sat staring at her.
ham	Her golden hair, which she wore in long curls, had been hurriedly pushed
spam	aside, and fell down over her neck. Advancing his hand by little and
spam	little, he took it up and looked at it. In the midst of the action
spam	he went astray, and, with another deep sigh, fell to work at his
ham	shoemaking.
ham	But not for long. Releasing his arm, she laid her hand upon his
ham	shoulder. After looking doubtfully at it, two or three times, as if to
ham	be sure that it was really there, he laid down his work, put his hand
ham	to his neck, and took off a blackened string with a scrap of folded rag
ham	attached to it. He opened this, carefully, on his knee, and it contained
ham	a very little quantity of hair: not more than one or two long golden
ham	hairs, which he had, in some old day, wound off upon his finger.
spam	He took her hair into his hand again, and looked closely at it. "It is
ham	the same. How can it be! When was it! How was it!"
ham	As the concentrated expression returned to his forehead, he seemed to
spam	become conscious that it was in hers too. He turned her full to the
spam	light, and looked at her.
ham	"She had laid her head upon my shoulder, that night when I was summoned
spam	out--she had a fear of my going, though I had none--and when I was
spam	brought to the North Tower they found these upon my sleeve. 'You will
ham	leave me them? They can never help me to escape in the body, though they
ham	may in the spirit.' Those were the words I said. I remember them very
spam	well."
spam	He formed this speech with his lips many times before he could utter it.
ham	But when he did find spoken words for it, they came to him coherently,
ham	though slowly.
ham	"How was this?--_Was it you_?"
ham	Once more, the two spectators started, as he turned upon her with a
ham	frightful suddenness. But she sat perfectly still in his grasp, and only
ham	said, in a low voice, "I entreat you, good gentlemen, do not come near
spam	us, do not speak, do not move!"
spam	"Hark!" he exclaimed. "Whose voice was that?"
spam	His hands released her as he uttered this cry, and went up to his white
spam	hair, which they tore in a frenzy. It died out, as everything but his
ham	shoemaking did die out of him, and he refolded his little packet and
spam	tried to secure it in his breast; but he still looked at her, and
ham	gloomily shook his head.
spam	"No, no, no; you are too young, too blooming. It can't be. See what the
spam	prisoner is. These are not the hands she knew, this is not the face
ham	she knew, this is not a voice she ever heard. No, no. She was--and He
ham	was--before the slow years of the North Tower--ages ago. What is your
spam	name, my gentle angel?"
spam	Hailing his softened tone and manner, his daughter fell upon her knees
ham	before him, with her appealing hands upon his breast.
ham	"O, sir, at another time you shall know my name, and who my mother was,
ham	and who my father, and how I never knew their hard, hard history. But I
spam	cannot tell you at this time, and I cannot tell you here. All that I may
ham	tell you, here and now, is, that I pray to you to touch me and to bless
spam	me. Kiss me, kiss me! O my dear, my dear!"
ham	His cold white head mingled with her radiant hair, which warmed and
ham	lighted it as though it were the light of Freedom shining on him.
ham	"If you hear in my voice--I don't know that it is so, but I hope it
spam	is--if you hear in my voice any resemblance to a voice that once was
spam	sweet music in your ears, weep for it, weep for it! If you touch, in
spam	touching my hair, anything that recalls a beloved head that lay on your
spam	breast when you were young and free, weep for it, weep for it! If, when
ham	I hint to you of a Home that is before us, where I will be true to you
spam	with all my duty and with all my faithful service, I bring back the
ham	remembrance of a Home long desolate, while your poor heart pined away,
ham	weep for it, weep for it!"
ham	She held him closer round the neck, and rocked him on her breast like a
ham	child.
ham	"If, when I tell you, dearest dear, that your agony is over, and that I
ham	have come here to take you from it, and that we go to England to be at
ham	peace and at rest, I cause you to think of your useful life laid waste,
ham	and of our native France so wicked to you, weep for it, weep for it! And
spam	if, when I shall tell you of my name, and of my father who is living,
spam	and of my mother who is dead, you learn that I have to kneel to my
ham	honoured father, and implore his pardon for having never for his sake
spam	striven all day and lain awake and wept all night, because the love of
spam	my poor mother hid his torture from me, weep for it, weep for it! Weep
ham	for her, then, and for me! Good gentlemen, thank God! I feel his sacred
ham	tears upon my face, and his sobs strike against my heart. O, see! Thank
spam	God for us, thank God!"
spam	He had sunk in her arms, and his face dropped on her breast: a sight so
ham	touching, yet so terrible in the tremendous wrong and suffering which
ham	had gone before it, that the two beholders covered their faces.
spam	When the quiet of the garret had been long undisturbed, and his heaving
spam	breast and shaken form had long yielded to the calm that must follow all
spam	storms--emblem to humanity, of the rest and silence into which the storm
spam	called Life must hush at last--they came forward to raise the father and
spam	daughter from the ground. He had gradually dropped to the floor, and lay
spam	there in a lethargy, worn out. She had nestled down with him, that his
ham	head might lie upon her arm; and her hair drooping over him curtained
spam	him from the light.
ham	"If, without disturbing him," she said, raising her hand to Mr. Lorry as
spam	he stooped over them, after repeated blowings of his nose, "all could be
ham	arranged for our leaving Paris at once, so that, from the very door, he
spam	could be taken away--"
ham	"But, consider. Is he fit for the journey?" asked Mr. Lorry.
ham	"More fit for that, I think, than to remain in this city, so dreadful to
ham	him."
spam	"It is true," said Defarge, who was kneeling to look on and hear. "More
ham	than that; Monsieur Manette is, for all reasons, best out of France.
spam	Say, shall I hire a carriage and post-horses?"
ham	"That's business," said Mr. Lorry, resuming on the shortest notice his
ham	methodical manners; "and if business is to be done, I had better do it."
spam	"Then be so kind," urged Miss Manette, "as to leave us here. You see how
ham	composed he has become, and you cannot be afraid to leave him with me
ham	now. Why should you be? If you will lock the door to secure us from
spam	interruption, I do not doubt that you will find him, when you come back,
spam	as quiet as you leave him. In any case, I will take care of him until
spam	you return, and then we will remove him straight."
ham	Both Mr. Lorry and Defarge were rather disinclined to this course, and
spam	in favour of one of them remaining. But, as there were not only carriage
spam	and horses to be seen to, but travelling papers; and as time pressed,
spam	for the day was drawing to an end, it came at last to their hastily
ham	dividing the business that was necessary to be done, and hurrying away
spam	to do it.
spam	Then, as the darkness closed in, the daughter laid her head down on the
ham	hard ground close at the father's side, and watched him. The darkness
spam	deepened and deepened, and they both lay quiet, until a light gleamed
spam	through the chinks in the wall.
ham	Mr. Lorry and Monsieur Defarge had made all ready for the journey, and
spam	had brought with them, besides travelling cloaks and wrappers, bread and
spam	meat, wine, and hot coffee. Monsieur Defarge put this provender, and the
spam	lamp he carried, on the shoemaker's bench (there was nothing else in the
spam	garret but a pallet bed), and he and Mr. Lorry roused the captive, and
ham	assisted him to his feet.
ham	No human intelligence could have read the mysteries of his mind, in
spam	the scared blank wonder of his face. Whether he knew what had happened,
ham	whether he recollected what they had said to him, whether he knew that
spam	he was free, were questions which no sagacity could have solved. They
spam	tried speaking to him; but, he was so confused, and so very slow to
ham	answer, that they took fright at his bewilderment, and agreed for
ham	the time to tamper with him no more. He had a wild, lost manner of
ham	occasionally clasping his head in his hands, that had not been seen
spam	in him before; yet, he had some pleasure in the mere sound of his
spam	daughter's voice, and invariably turned to it when she spoke.
spam	In the submissive way of one long accustomed to obey under coercion, he
spam	ate and drank what they gave him to eat and drink, and put on the cloak
ham	and other wrappings, that they gave him to wear. He readily responded to
ham	his daughter's drawing her arm through his, and took--and kept--her hand
spam	in both his own.
spam	They began to descend; Monsieur Defarge going first with the lamp, Mr.
ham	Lorry closing the little procession. They had not traversed many steps
ham	of the long main staircase when he stopped, and stared at the roof and
ham	round at the walls.
ham	"You remember the place, my father? You remember coming up here?"
ham	"What did you say?"
spam	But, before she could repeat the question, he murmured an answer as if
spam	she had repeated it.
ham	"Remember? No, I don't remember. It was so very long ago."
ham	That he had no recollection whatever of his having been brought from his
ham	prison to that house, was apparent to them. They heard him mutter,
ham	"One Hundred and Five, North Tower;" and when he looked about him, it
spam	evidently was for the strong fortress-walls which had long encompassed
spam	him. On their reaching the courtyard he instinctively altered his
ham	tread, as being in expectation of a drawbridge; and when there was
spam	no drawbridge, and he saw the carriage waiting in the open street, he
ham	dropped his daughter's hand and clasped his head again.
ham	No crowd was about the door; no people were discernible at any of the
ham	many windows; not even a chance passerby was in the street. An unnatural
spam	silence and desertion reigned there. Only one soul was to be seen, and
spam	that was Madame Defarge--who leaned against the door-post, knitting, and
spam	saw nothing.
spam	The prisoner had got into a coach, and his daughter had followed
spam	him, when Mr. Lorry's feet were arrested on the step by his asking,
ham	miserably, for his shoemaking tools and the unfinished shoes. Madame
ham	Defarge immediately called to her husband that she would get them, and
ham	went, knitting, out of the lamplight, through the courtyard. She quickly
spam	brought them down and handed them in;--and immediately afterwards leaned
spam	against the door-post, knitting, and saw nothing.
ham	Defarge got upon the box, and gave the word "To the Barrier!" The
ham	postilion cracked his whip, and they clattered away under the feeble
spam	over-swinging lamps.
ham	Under the over-swinging lamps--swinging ever brighter in the better
ham	streets, and ever dimmer in the worse--and by lighted shops, gay crowds,
ham	illuminated coffee-houses, and theatre-doors, to one of the city
ham	gates. Soldiers with lanterns, at the guard-house there. "Your papers,
spam	travellers!" "See here then, Monsieur the Officer," said Defarge,
ham	getting down, and taking him gravely apart, "these are the papers of
ham	monsieur inside, with the white head. They were consigned to me, with
spam	him, at the--" He dropped his voice, there was a flutter among the
ham	military lanterns, and one of them being handed into the coach by an arm
ham	in uniform, the eyes connected with the arm looked, not an every day
spam	or an every night look, at monsieur with the white head. "It is well.
ham	Forward!" from the uniform. "Adieu!" from Defarge. And so, under a short
ham	grove of feebler and feebler over-swinging lamps, out under the great
spam	grove of stars.
spam	Beneath that arch of unmoved and eternal lights; some, so remote from
spam	this little earth that the learned tell us it is doubtful whether their
spam	rays have even yet discovered it, as a point in space where anything
ham	is suffered or done: the shadows of the night were broad and black.
spam	All through the cold and restless interval, until dawn, they once more
spam	whispered in the ears of Mr. Jarvis Lorry--sitting opposite the buried
spam	man who had been dug out, and wondering what subtle powers were for ever
ham	lost to him, and what were capable of restoration--the old inquiry:
ham	"I hope you care to be recalled to life?"
ham	And the old answer:
ham	"I can't say."
spam	The end of the first book.
spam	Book the Second--the Golden Thread
spam	I. Five Years Later
spam	Tellson's Bank by Temple Bar was an old-fashioned place, even in the
spam	year one thousand seven hundred and eighty. It was very small, very
spam	dark, very ugly, very incommodious. It was an old-fashioned place,
spam	moreover, in the moral attribute that the partners in the House were
ham	proud of its smallness, proud of its darkness, proud of its ugliness,
ham	proud of its incommodiousness. They were even boastful of its eminence
spam	in those particulars, and were fired by an express conviction that, if
spam	it were less objectionable, it would be less respectable. This was
spam	no passive belief, but an active weapon which they flashed at more
spam	convenient places of business. Tellson's (they said) wanted
ham	no elbow-room, Tellson's wanted no light, Tellson's wanted no
ham	embellishment. Noakes and Co.'s might, or Snooks Brothers' might; but
ham	Tellson's, thank Heaven--!
spam	Any one of these partners would have disinherited his son on the
spam	question of rebuilding Tellson's. In this respect the House was much
spam	on a par with the Country; which did very often disinherit its sons for
ham	suggesting improvements in laws and customs that had long been highly
spam	objectionable, but were only the more respectable.
ham	Thus it had come to pass, that Tellson's was the triumphant perfection
ham	of inconvenience. After bursting open a door of idiotic obstinacy with
spam	a weak rattle in its throat, you fell into Tellson's down two steps,
ham	and came to your senses in a miserable little shop, with two little
ham	counters, where the oldest of men made your cheque shake as if the
ham	wind rustled it, while they examined the signature by the dingiest of
ham	windows, which were always under a shower-bath of mud from Fleet-street,
ham	and which were made the dingier by their own iron bars proper, and the
ham	heavy shadow of Temple Bar. If your business necessitated your seeing
spam	"the House," you were put into a species of Condemned Hold at the back,
spam	where you meditated on a misspent life, until the House came with its
spam	hands in its pockets, and you could hardly blink at it in the dismal
ham	twilight. Your money came out of, or went into, wormy old wooden
ham	drawers, particles of which flew up your nose and down your throat when
spam	they were opened and shut. Your bank-notes had a musty odour, as if they
ham	were fast decomposing into rags again. Your plate was stowed away among
spam	the neighbouring cesspools, and evil communications corrupted its good
spam	polish in a day or two. Your deeds got into extemporised strong-rooms
ham	made of kitchens and sculleries, and fretted all the fat out of their
ham	parchments into the banking-house air. Your lighter boxes of family
ham	papers went up-stairs into a Barmecide room, that always had a great
spam	dining-table in it and never had a dinner, and where, even in the year
ham	one thousand seven hundred and eighty, the first letters written to you
ham	by your old love, or by your little children, were but newly released
ham	from the horror of being ogled through the windows, by the heads
spam	exposed on Temple Bar with an insensate brutality and ferocity worthy of
spam	Abyssinia or Ashantee.
spam	But indeed, at that time, putting to death was a recipe much in vogue
spam	with all trades and professions, and not least of all with Tellson's.
ham	Death is Nature's remedy for all things, and why not Legislation's?
ham	Accordingly, the forger was put to Death; the utterer of a bad note
spam	was put to Death; the unlawful opener of a letter was put to Death; the
spam	purloiner of forty shillings and sixpence was put to Death; the holder
ham	of a horse at Tellson's door, who made off with it, was put to
spam	Death; the coiner of a bad shilling was put to Death; the sounders of
ham	three-fourths of the notes in the whole gamut of Crime, were put to
ham	Death. Not that it did the least good in the way of prevention--it
spam	might almost have been worth remarking that the fact was exactly the
spam	reverse--but, it cleared off (as to this world) the trouble of each
ham	particular case, and left nothing else connected with it to be looked
spam	after. Thus, Tellson's, in its day, like greater places of business,
ham	its contemporaries, had taken so many lives, that, if the heads laid
ham	low before it had been ranged on Temple Bar instead of being privately
spam	disposed of, they would probably have excluded what little light the
ham	ground floor had, in a rather significant manner.
ham	Cramped in all kinds of dim cupboards and hutches at Tellson's, the
spam	oldest of men carried on the business gravely. When they took a young
spam	man into Tellson's London house, they hid him somewhere till he was
spam	old. They kept him in a dark place, like a cheese, until he had the full
ham	Tellson flavour and blue-mould upon him. Then only was he permitted to
ham	be seen, spectacularly poring over large books, and casting his breeches
spam	and gaiters into the general weight of the establishment.
ham	Outside Tellson's--never by any means in it, unless called in--was an
ham	odd-job-man, an occasional porter and messenger, who served as the live
spam	sign of the house. He was never absent during business hours, unless
ham	upon an errand, and then he was represented by his son: a grisly urchin
spam	of twelve, who was his express image. People understood that Tellson's,
spam	in a stately way, tolerated the odd-job-man. The house had always
spam	tolerated some person in that capacity, and time and tide had drifted
spam	this person to the post. His surname was Cruncher, and on the youthful
spam	occasion of his renouncing by proxy the works of darkness, in the
ham	easterly parish church of Hounsditch, he had received the added
spam	appellation of Jerry.
ham	The scene was Mr. Cruncher's private lodging in Hanging-sword-alley,
ham	Whitefriars: the time, half-past seven of the clock on a windy March
ham	morning, Anno Domini seventeen hundred and eighty. (Mr. Cruncher himself
spam	always spoke of the year of our Lord as Anna Dominoes: apparently under
spam	the impression that the Christian era dated from the invention of a
ham	popular game, by a lady who had bestowed her name upon it.)
spam	Mr. Cruncher's apartments were not in a savoury neighbourhood, and were
ham	but two in number, even if a closet with a single pane of glass in it
ham	might be counted as one. But they were very decently kept. Early as
spam	it was, on the windy March morning, the room in which he lay abed was
ham	already scrubbed throughout; and between the cups and saucers arranged
spam	for breakfast, and the lumbering deal table, a very clean white cloth
spam	was spread.
ham	Mr. Cruncher reposed under a patchwork counterpane, like a Harlequin
spam	at home. At first, he slept heavily, but, by degrees, began to roll
ham	and surge in bed, until he rose above the surface, with his spiky hair
spam	looking as if it must tear the sheets to ribbons. At which juncture, he
spam	exclaimed, in a voice of dire exasperation:
ham	"Bust me, if she ain't at it agin!"
spam	A woman of orderly and industrious appearance rose from her knees in a
ham	corner, with sufficient haste and trepidation to show that she was the
ham	person referred to.
ham	"What!" said Mr. Cruncher, looking out of bed for a boot. "You're at it
spam	agin, are you?"
ham	After hailing the morn with this second salutation, he threw a boot at
ham	the woman as a third. It was a very muddy boot, and may introduce the
spam	odd circumstance connected with Mr. Cruncher's domestic economy, that,
ham	whereas he often came home after banking hours with clean boots, he
ham	often got up next morning to find the same boots covered with clay.
ham	"What," said Mr. Cruncher, varying his apostrophe after missing his
spam	mark--"what are you up to, Aggerawayter?"
spam	"I was only saying my prayers."
ham	"Saying your prayers! You're a nice woman! What do you mean by flopping
spam	yourself down and praying agin me?"
ham	"I was not praying against you; I was praying for you."
ham	"You weren't. And if you were, I won't be took the liberty with. Here!
spam	your mother's a nice woman, young Jerry, going a praying agin your
ham	father's prosperity. You've got a dutiful mother, you have, my son.
ham	You've got a religious mother, you have, my boy: going and flopping
spam	herself down, and praying that the bread-and-butter may be snatched out
ham	of the mouth of her only child."
ham	Master Cruncher (who was in his shirt) took this very ill, and, turning
ham	to his mother, strongly deprecated any praying away of his personal
ham	board.
ham	"And what do you suppose, you conceited female," said Mr. Cruncher, with
ham	unconscious inconsistency, "that the worth of _your_ prayers may be?
spam	Name the price that you put _your_ prayers at!"
spam	"They only come from the heart, Jerry. They are worth no more than
spam	that."
ham	"Worth no more than that," repeated Mr. Cruncher. "They ain't worth
spam	much, then. Whether or no, I won't be prayed agin, I tell you. I can't
ham	afford it. I'm not a going to be made unlucky by _your_ sneaking. If
spam	you must go flopping yourself down, flop in favour of your husband and
ham	child, and not in opposition to 'em. If I had had any but a unnat'ral
spam	wife, and this poor boy had had any but a unnat'ral mother, I might
spam	have made some money last week instead of being counter-prayed and
spam	countermined and religiously circumwented into the worst of luck.
ham	B-u-u-ust me!" said Mr. Cruncher, who all this time had been putting
spam	on his clothes, "if I ain't, what with piety and one blowed thing and
ham	another, been choused this last week into as bad luck as ever a poor
spam	devil of a honest tradesman met with! Young Jerry, dress yourself, my
ham	boy, and while I clean my boots keep a eye upon your mother now and
spam	then, and if you see any signs of more flopping, give me a call. For, I
spam	tell you," here he addressed his wife once more, "I won't be gone agin,
ham	in this manner. I am as rickety as a hackney-coach, I'm as sleepy as
spam	laudanum, my lines is strained to that degree that I shouldn't know, if
spam	it wasn't for the pain in 'em, which was me and which somebody else, yet
ham	I'm none the better for it in pocket; and it's my suspicion that you've
spam	been at it from morning to night to prevent me from being the better for
spam	it in pocket, and I won't put up with it, Aggerawayter, and what do you
spam	say now!"
ham	Growling, in addition, such phrases as "Ah! yes! You're religious, too.
ham	You wouldn't put yourself in opposition to the interests of your husband
ham	and child, would you? Not you!" and throwing off other sarcastic sparks
spam	from the whirling grindstone of his indignation, Mr. Cruncher betook
spam	himself to his boot-cleaning and his general preparation for business.
ham	In the meantime, his son, whose head was garnished with tenderer spikes,
spam	and whose young eyes stood close by one another, as his father's did,
ham	kept the required watch upon his mother. He greatly disturbed that poor
ham	woman at intervals, by darting out of his sleeping closet, where he made
spam	his toilet, with a suppressed cry of "You are going to flop, mother.
spam	--Halloa, father!" and, after raising this fictitious alarm, darting in
ham	again with an undutiful grin.
ham	Mr. Cruncher's temper was not at all improved when he came to his
spam	breakfast. He resented Mrs. Cruncher's saying grace with particular
ham	animosity.
ham	"Now, Aggerawayter! What are you up to? At it again?"
ham	His wife explained that she had merely "asked a blessing."
ham	"Don't do it!" said Mr. Crunches looking about, as if he rather expected
spam	to see the loaf disappear under the efficacy of his wife's petitions. "I
ham	ain't a going to be blest out of house and home. I won't have my wittles
ham	blest off my table. Keep still!"
spam	Exceedingly red-eyed and grim, as if he had been up all night at a party
spam	which had taken anything but a convivial turn, Jerry Cruncher worried
ham	his breakfast rather than ate it, growling over it like any four-footed
ham	inmate of a menagerie. Towards nine o'clock he smoothed his ruffled
ham	aspect, and, presenting as respectable and business-like an exterior as
ham	he could overlay his natural self with, issued forth to the occupation
spam	of the day.
ham	It could scarcely be called a trade, in spite of his favourite
spam	description of himself as "a honest tradesman." His stock consisted of
spam	a wooden stool, made out of a broken-backed chair cut down, which stool,
spam	young Jerry, walking at his father's side, carried every morning to
ham	beneath the banking-house window that was nearest Temple Bar: where,
ham	with the addition of the first handful of straw that could be gleaned
ham	from any passing vehicle to keep the cold and wet from the odd-job-man's
ham	feet, it formed the encampment for the day. On this post of his, Mr.
spam	Cruncher was as well known to Fleet-street and the Temple, as the Bar
ham	itself,--and was almost as in-looking.
spam	Encamped at a quarter before nine, in good time to touch his
ham	three-cornered hat to the oldest of men as they passed in to Tellson's,
spam	Jerry took up his station on this windy March morning, with young Jerry
spam	standing by him, when not engaged in making forays through the Bar, to
ham	inflict bodily and mental injuries of an acute description on passing
ham	boys who were small enough for his amiable purpose. Father and son,
ham	extremely like each other, looking silently on at the morning traffic
ham	in Fleet-street, with their two heads as near to one another as the two
ham	eyes of each were, bore a considerable resemblance to a pair of monkeys.
ham	The resemblance was not lessened by the accidental circumstance, that
spam	the mature Jerry bit and spat out straw, while the twinkling eyes of the
ham	youthful Jerry were as restlessly watchful of him as of everything else
ham	in Fleet-street.
ham	The head of one of the regular indoor messengers attached to Tellson's
ham	establishment was put through the door, and the word was given:
spam	"Porter wanted!"
spam	"Hooray, father! Here's an early job to begin with!"
ham	Having thus given his parent God speed, young Jerry seated himself on
ham	the stool, entered on his reversionary interest in the straw his father
ham	had been chewing, and cogitated.
ham	"Al-ways rusty! His fingers is al-ways rusty!" muttered young Jerry.
spam	"Where does my father get all that iron rust from? He don't get no iron
spam	rust here!"
spam	II. A Sight
ham	"You know the Old Bailey well, no doubt?" said one of the oldest of
spam	clerks to Jerry the messenger.
spam	"Ye-es, sir," returned Jerry, in something of a dogged manner. "I _do_
ham	know the Bailey."
spam	"Just so. And you know Mr. Lorry."
ham	"I know Mr. Lorry, sir, much better than I know the Bailey. Much
ham	better," said Jerry, not unlike a reluctant witness at the establishment
spam	in question, "than I, as a honest tradesman, wish to know the Bailey."
ham	"Very well. Find the door where the witnesses go in, and show the
ham	door-keeper this note for Mr. Lorry. He will then let you in."
spam	"Into the court, sir?"
spam	"Into the court."
ham	Mr. Cruncher's eyes seemed to get a little closer to one another, and to
spam	interchange the inquiry, "What do you think of this?"
ham	"Am I to wait in the court, sir?" he asked, as the result of that
spam	conference.
spam	"I am going to tell you. The door-keeper will pass the note to Mr.
ham	Lorry, and do you make any gesture that will attract Mr. Lorry's
spam	attention, and show him where you stand. Then what you have to do, is,
ham	to remain there until he wants you."
ham	"Is that all, sir?"
spam	"That's all. He wishes to have a messenger at hand. This is to tell him
spam	you are there."
spam	As the ancient clerk deliberately folded and superscribed the note,
ham	Mr. Cruncher, after surveying him in silence until he came to the
ham	blotting-paper stage, remarked:
spam	"I suppose they'll be trying Forgeries this morning?"
ham	"Treason!"
ham	"That's quartering," said Jerry. "Barbarous!"
spam	"It is the law," remarked the ancient clerk, turning his surprised
ham	spectacles upon him. "It is the law."
spam	"It's hard in the law to spile a man, I think. It's hard enough to kill
spam	him, but it's wery hard to spile him, sir."
ham	"Not at all," retained the ancient clerk. "Speak well of the law. Take
ham	care of your chest and voice, my good friend, and leave the law to take
spam	care of itself. I give you that advice."
ham	"It's the damp, sir, what settles on my chest and voice," said Jerry. "I
ham	leave you to judge what a damp way of earning a living mine is."
ham	"Well, well," said the old clerk; "we all have our various ways of
ham	gaining a livelihood. Some of us have damp ways, and some of us have dry
ham	ways. Here is the letter. Go along."
spam	Jerry took the letter, and, remarking to himself with less internal
spam	deference than he made an outward show of, "You are a lean old one,
spam	too," made his bow, informed his son, in passing, of his destination,
ham	and went his way.
spam	They hanged at Tyburn, in those days, so the street outside Newgate had
ham	not obtained one infamous notoriety that has since attached to it.
spam	But, the gaol was a vile place, in which most kinds of debauchery and
ham	villainy were practised, and where dire diseases were bred, that came
spam	into court with the prisoners, and sometimes rushed straight from the
ham	dock at my Lord Chief Justice himself, and pulled him off the bench. It
ham	had more than once happened, that the Judge in the black cap pronounced
spam	his own doom as certainly as the prisoner's, and even died before him.
ham	For the rest, the Old Bailey was famous as a kind of deadly inn-yard,
spam	from which pale travellers set out continually, in carts and coaches, on
ham	a violent passage into the other world: traversing some two miles and a
spam	half of public street and road, and shaming few good citizens, if any.
spam	So powerful is use, and so desirable to be good use in the beginning. It
ham	was famous, too, for the pillory, a wise old institution, that inflicted
spam	a punishment of which no one could foresee the extent; also, for
ham	the whipping-post, another dear old institution, very humanising and
spam	softening to behold in action; also, for extensive transactions in
spam	blood-money, another fragment of ancestral wisdom, systematically
ham	leading to the most frightful mercenary crimes that could be committed
ham	under Heaven. Altogether, the Old Bailey, at that date, was a choice
spam	illustration of the precept, that "Whatever is is right;" an aphorism
ham	that would be as final as it is lazy, did it not include the troublesome
spam	consequence, that nothing that ever was, was wrong.
spam	Making his way through the tainted crowd, dispersed up and down this
ham	hideous scene of action, with the skill of a man accustomed to make his
spam	way quietly, the messenger found out the door he sought, and handed in
spam	his letter through a trap in it. For, people then paid to see the play
ham	at the Old Bailey, just as they paid to see the play in Bedlam--only the
spam	former entertainment was much the dearer. Therefore, all the Old Bailey
ham	doors were well guarded--except, indeed, the social doors by which the
spam	criminals got there, and those were always left wide open.
spam	After some delay and demur, the door grudgingly turned on its hinges a
spam	very little way, and allowed Mr. Jerry Cruncher to squeeze himself into
ham	court.
ham	"What's on?" he asked, in a whisper, of the man he found himself next
ham	to.
spam	"Nothing yet."
ham	"What's coming on?"
ham	"The Treason case."
ham	"The quartering one, eh?"
spam	"Ah!" returned the man, with a relish; "he'll be drawn on a hurdle to
ham	be half hanged, and then he'll be taken down and sliced before his own
spam	face, and then his inside will be taken out and burnt while he looks on,
spam	and then his head will be chopped off, and he'll be cut into quarters.
ham	That's the sentence."
ham	"If he's found Guilty, you mean to say?" Jerry added, by way of proviso.
spam	"Oh! they'll find him guilty," said the other. "Don't you be afraid of
ham	that."
spam	Mr. Cruncher's attention was here diverted to the door-keeper, whom he
spam	saw making his way to Mr. Lorry, with the note in his hand. Mr. Lorry
ham	sat at a table, among the gentlemen in wigs: not far from a wigged
spam	gentleman, the prisoner's counsel, who had a great bundle of papers
spam	before him: and nearly opposite another wigged gentleman with his hands
ham	in his pockets, whose whole attention, when Mr. Cruncher looked at him
spam	then or afterwards, seemed to be concentrated on the ceiling of the
spam	court. After some gruff coughing and rubbing of his chin and signing
ham	with his hand, Jerry attracted the notice of Mr. Lorry, who had stood up
ham	to look for him, and who quietly nodded and sat down again.
spam	"What's _he_ got to do with the case?" asked the man he had spoken with.
ham	"Blest if I know," said Jerry.
ham	"What have _you_ got to do with it, then, if a person may inquire?"
spam	"Blest if I know that either," said Jerry.
spam	The entrance of the Judge, and a consequent great stir and settling
ham	down in the court, stopped the dialogue. Presently, the dock became the
ham	central point of interest. Two gaolers, who had been standing there,
spam	went out, and the prisoner was brought in, and put to the bar.
spam	Everybody present, except the one wigged gentleman who looked at the
ham	ceiling, stared at him. All the human breath in the place, rolled
spam	at him, like a sea, or a wind, or a fire. Eager faces strained round
spam	pillars and corners, to get a sight of him; spectators in back rows
spam	stood up, not to miss a hair of him; people on the floor of the court,
spam	laid their hands on the shoulders of the people before them, to help
ham	themselves, at anybody's cost, to a view of him--stood a-tiptoe, got
ham	upon ledges, stood upon next to nothing, to see every inch of him.
spam	Conspicuous among these latter, like an animated bit of the spiked wall
spam	of Newgate, Jerry stood: aiming at the prisoner the beery breath of a
ham	whet he had taken as he came along, and discharging it to mingle with
ham	the waves of other beer, and gin, and tea, and coffee, and what not,
spam	that flowed at him, and already broke upon the great windows behind him
spam	in an impure mist and rain.
spam	The object of all this staring and blaring, was a young man of about
spam	five-and-twenty, well-grown and well-looking, with a sunburnt cheek and
ham	a dark eye. His condition was that of a young gentleman. He was plainly
ham	dressed in black, or very dark grey, and his hair, which was long and
spam	dark, was gathered in a ribbon at the back of his neck; more to be out
spam	of his way than for ornament. As an emotion of the mind will express
spam	itself through any covering of the body, so the paleness which his
ham	situation engendered came through the brown upon his cheek, showing the
ham	soul to be stronger than the sun. He was otherwise quite self-possessed,
spam	bowed to the Judge, and stood quiet.
spam	The sort of interest with which this man was stared and breathed at,
ham	was not a sort that elevated humanity. Had he stood in peril of a less
spam	horrible sentence--had there been a chance of any one of its savage
spam	details being spared--by just so much would he have lost in his
ham	fascination. The form that was to be doomed to be so shamefully mangled,
ham	was the sight; the immortal creature that was to be so butchered
ham	and torn asunder, yielded the sensation. Whatever gloss the various
spam	spectators put upon the interest, according to their several arts and
spam	powers of self-deceit, the interest was, at the root of it, Ogreish.
ham	Silence in the court! Charles Darnay had yesterday pleaded Not Guilty to
ham	an indictment denouncing him (with infinite jingle and jangle) for that
spam	he was a false traitor to our serene, illustrious, excellent, and so
spam	forth, prince, our Lord the King, by reason of his having, on divers
spam	occasions, and by divers means and ways, assisted Lewis, the French
spam	King, in his wars against our said serene, illustrious, excellent, and
spam	so forth; that was to say, by coming and going, between the dominions of
ham	our said serene, illustrious, excellent, and so forth, and those of the
ham	said French Lewis, and wickedly, falsely, traitorously, and otherwise
spam	evil-adverbiously, revealing to the said French Lewis what forces our
ham	said serene, illustrious, excellent, and so forth, had in preparation
spam	to send to Canada and North America. This much, Jerry, with his head
spam	becoming more and more spiky as the law terms bristled it, made out with
spam	huge satisfaction, and so arrived circuitously at the understanding that
spam	the aforesaid, and over and over again aforesaid, Charles Darnay, stood
spam	there before him upon his trial; that the jury were swearing in; and
spam	that Mr. Attorney-General was making ready to speak.
spam	The accused, who was (and who knew he was) being mentally hanged,
spam	beheaded, and quartered, by everybody there, neither flinched from
spam	the situation, nor assumed any theatrical air in it. He was quiet and
spam	attentive; watched the opening proceedings with a grave interest;
spam	and stood with his hands resting on the slab of wood before him, so
spam	composedly, that they had not displaced a leaf of the herbs with which
ham	it was strewn. The court was all bestrewn with herbs and sprinkled with
spam	vinegar, as a precaution against gaol air and gaol fever.
ham	Over the prisoner's head there was a mirror, to throw the light down
ham	upon him. Crowds of the wicked and the wretched had been reflected in
spam	it, and had passed from its surface and this earth's together. Haunted
spam	in a most ghastly manner that abominable place would have been, if the
spam	glass could ever have rendered back its reflections, as the ocean is one
spam	day to give up its dead. Some passing thought of the infamy and disgrace
ham	for which it had been reserved, may have struck the prisoner's mind. Be
ham	that as it may, a change in his position making him conscious of a bar
ham	of light across his face, he looked up; and when he saw the glass his
spam	face flushed, and his right hand pushed the herbs away.
spam	It happened, that the action turned his face to that side of the court
spam	which was on his left. About on a level with his eyes, there sat,
spam	in that corner of the Judge's bench, two persons upon whom his look
ham	immediately rested; so immediately, and so much to the changing of his
spam	aspect, that all the eyes that were turned upon him, turned to them.
spam	The spectators saw in the two figures, a young lady of little more than
spam	twenty, and a gentleman who was evidently her father; a man of a very
spam	remarkable appearance in respect of the absolute whiteness of his hair,
ham	and a certain indescribable intensity of face: not of an active kind,
ham	but pondering and self-communing. When this expression was upon him, he
ham	looked as if he were old; but when it was stirred and broken up--as
ham	it was now, in a moment, on his speaking to his daughter--he became a
spam	handsome man, not past the prime of life.
spam	His daughter had one of her hands drawn through his arm, as she sat by
spam	him, and the other pressed upon it. She had drawn close to him, in her
ham	dread of the scene, and in her pity for the prisoner. Her forehead had
spam	been strikingly expressive of an engrossing terror and compassion
spam	that saw nothing but the peril of the accused. This had been so very
spam	noticeable, so very powerfully and naturally shown, that starers who
ham	had had no pity for him were touched by her; and the whisper went about,
spam	"Who are they?"
spam	Jerry, the messenger, who had made his own observations, in his own
ham	manner, and who had been sucking the rust off his fingers in his
spam	absorption, stretched his neck to hear who they were. The crowd about
spam	him had pressed and passed the inquiry on to the nearest attendant, and
spam	from him it had been more slowly pressed and passed back; at last it got
spam	to Jerry:
spam	"Witnesses."
ham	"For which side?"
ham	"Against."
ham	"Against what side?"
ham	"The prisoner's."
spam	The Judge, whose eyes had gone in the general direction, recalled them,
spam	leaned back in his seat, and looked steadily at the man whose life was
spam	in his hand, as Mr. Attorney-General rose to spin the rope, grind the
spam	axe, and hammer the nails into the scaffold.
ham	III. A Disappointment
spam	Mr. Attorney-General had to inform the jury, that the prisoner before
ham	them, though young in years, was old in the treasonable practices which
spam	claimed the forfeit of his life. That this correspondence with the
spam	public enemy was not a correspondence of to-day, or of yesterday, or
ham	even of last year, or of the year before. That, it was certain the
spam	prisoner had, for longer than that, been in the habit of passing and
ham	repassing between France and England, on secret business of which
spam	he could give no honest account. That, if it were in the nature of
ham	traitorous ways to thrive (which happily it never was), the real
spam	wickedness and guilt of his business might have remained undiscovered.
spam	That Providence, however, had put it into the heart of a person who
spam	was beyond fear and beyond reproach, to ferret out the nature of the
ham	prisoner's schemes, and, struck with horror, to disclose them to his
spam	Majesty's Chief Secretary of State and most honourable Privy Council.
spam	That, this patriot would be produced before them. That, his position and
spam	attitude were, on the whole, sublime. That, he had been the prisoner's
ham	friend, but, at once in an auspicious and an evil hour detecting his
ham	infamy, had resolved to immolate the traitor he could no longer cherish
ham	in his bosom, on the sacred altar of his country. That, if statues
spam	were decreed in Britain, as in ancient Greece and Rome, to public
spam	benefactors, this shining citizen would assuredly have had one. That, as
spam	they were not so decreed, he probably would not have one. That, Virtue,
spam	as had been observed by the poets (in many passages which he well
ham	knew the jury would have, word for word, at the tips of their tongues;
ham	whereat the jury's countenances displayed a guilty consciousness that
ham	they knew nothing about the passages), was in a manner contagious; more
spam	especially the bright virtue known as patriotism, or love of country.
ham	That, the lofty example of this immaculate and unimpeachable witness
ham	for the Crown, to refer to whom however unworthily was an honour, had
ham	communicated itself to the prisoner's servant, and had engendered in him
spam	a holy determination to examine his master's table-drawers and pockets,
spam	and secrete his papers. That, he (Mr. Attorney-General) was prepared to
spam	hear some disparagement attempted of this admirable servant; but that,
spam	in a general way, he preferred him to his (Mr. Attorney-General's)
ham	brothers and sisters, and honoured him more than his (Mr.
spam	Attorney-General's) father and mother. That, he called with confidence
ham	on the jury to come and do likewise. That, the evidence of these two
spam	witnesses, coupled with the documents of their discovering that would be
ham	produced, would show the prisoner to have been furnished with lists of
spam	his Majesty's forces, and of their disposition and preparation, both by
spam	sea and land, and would leave no doubt that he had habitually conveyed
ham	such information to a hostile power. That, these lists could not be
spam	proved to be in the prisoner's handwriting; but that it was all the
ham	same; that, indeed, it was rather the better for the prosecution, as
spam	showing the prisoner to be artful in his precautions. That, the proof
spam	would go back five years, and would show the prisoner already engaged
ham	in these pernicious missions, within a few weeks before the date of the
ham	very first action fought between the British troops and the Americans.
ham	That, for these reasons, the jury, being a loyal jury (as he knew they
ham	were), and being a responsible jury (as _they_ knew they were), must
ham	positively find the prisoner Guilty, and make an end of him, whether
spam	they liked it or not. That, they never could lay their heads upon their
spam	pillows; that, they never could tolerate the idea of their wives laying
ham	their heads upon their pillows; that, they never could endure the notion
spam	of their children laying their heads upon their pillows; in short, that
spam	there never more could be, for them or theirs, any laying of heads upon
ham	pillows at all, unless the prisoner's head was taken off. That head
spam	Mr. Attorney-General concluded by demanding of them, in the name of
spam	everything he could think of with a round turn in it, and on the faith
spam	of his solemn asseveration that he already considered the prisoner as
spam	good as dead and gone.
ham	When the Attorney-General ceased, a buzz arose in the court as if
ham	a cloud of great blue-flies were swarming about the prisoner, in
spam	anticipation of what he was soon to become. When toned down again, the
ham	unimpeachable patriot appeared in the witness-box.
spam	Mr. Solicitor-General then, following his leader's lead, examined the
spam	patriot: John Barsad, gentleman, by name. The story of his pure soul was
ham	exactly what Mr. Attorney-General had described it to be--perhaps, if
spam	it had a fault, a little too exactly. Having released his noble bosom
spam	of its burden, he would have modestly withdrawn himself, but that the
ham	wigged gentleman with the papers before him, sitting not far from Mr.
ham	Lorry, begged to ask him a few questions. The wigged gentleman sitting
spam	opposite, still looking at the ceiling of the court.
ham	Had he ever been a spy himself? No, he scorned the base insinuation.
ham	What did he live upon? His property. Where was his property? He didn't
ham	precisely remember where it was. What was it? No business of anybody's.
ham	Had he inherited it? Yes, he had. From whom? Distant relation. Very
spam	distant? Rather. Ever been in prison? Certainly not. Never in a debtors'
ham	prison? Didn't see what that had to do with it. Never in a debtors'
spam	prison?--Come, once again. Never? Yes. How many times? Two or three
spam	times. Not five or six? Perhaps. Of what profession? Gentleman. Ever
spam	been kicked? Might have been. Frequently? No. Ever kicked downstairs?
spam	Decidedly not; once received a kick on the top of a staircase, and fell
spam	downstairs of his own accord. Kicked on that occasion for cheating at
spam	dice? Something to that effect was said by the intoxicated liar who
ham	committed the assault, but it was not true. Swear it was not true?
ham	Positively. Ever live by cheating at play? Never. Ever live by play? Not
ham	more than other gentlemen do. Ever borrow money of the prisoner? Yes.
spam	Ever pay him? No. Was not this intimacy with the prisoner, in reality a
spam	very slight one, forced upon the prisoner in coaches, inns, and packets?
ham	No. Sure he saw the prisoner with these lists? Certain. Knew no more
ham	about the lists? No. Had not procured them himself, for instance? No.
ham	Expect to get anything by this evidence? No. Not in regular government
ham	pay and employment, to lay traps? Oh dear no. Or to do anything? Oh dear
spam	no. Swear that? Over and over again. No motives but motives of sheer
spam	patriotism? None whatever.
ham	The virtuous servant, Roger Cly, swore his way through the case at a
ham	great rate. He had taken service with the prisoner, in good faith and
ham	simplicity, four years ago. He had asked the prisoner, aboard the Calais
spam	packet, if he wanted a handy fellow, and the prisoner had engaged him.
spam	He had not asked the prisoner to take the handy fellow as an act of
spam	charity--never thought of such a thing. He began to have suspicions of
ham	the prisoner, and to keep an eye upon him, soon afterwards. In arranging
ham	his clothes, while travelling, he had seen similar lists to these in the
ham	prisoner's pockets, over and over again. He had taken these lists from
ham	the drawer of the prisoner's desk. He had not put them there first. He
spam	had seen the prisoner show these identical lists to French gentlemen
spam	at Calais, and similar lists to French gentlemen, both at Calais and
ham	Boulogne. He loved his country, and couldn't bear it, and had given
spam	information. He had never been suspected of stealing a silver tea-pot;
spam	he had been maligned respecting a mustard-pot, but it turned out to be
spam	only a plated one. He had known the last witness seven or eight years;
ham	that was merely a coincidence. He didn't call it a particularly curious
ham	coincidence; most coincidences were curious. Neither did he call it a
spam	curious coincidence that true patriotism was _his_ only motive too. He
ham	was a true Briton, and hoped there were many like him.
ham	The blue-flies buzzed again, and Mr. Attorney-General called Mr. Jarvis
spam	Lorry.
ham	"Mr. Jarvis Lorry, are you a clerk in Tellson's bank?"
ham	"I am."
spam	"On a certain Friday night in November one thousand seven hundred and
spam	seventy-five, did business occasion you to travel between London and
ham	Dover by the mail?"
spam	"It did."
ham	"Were there any other passengers in the mail?"
spam	"Two."
ham	"Did they alight on the road in the course of the night?"
ham	"They did."
ham	"Mr. Lorry, look upon the prisoner. Was he one of those two passengers?"
ham	"I cannot undertake to say that he was."
ham	"Does he resemble either of these two passengers?"
spam	"Both were so wrapped up, and the night was so dark, and we were all so
ham	reserved, that I cannot undertake to say even that."
spam	"Mr. Lorry, look again upon the prisoner. Supposing him wrapped up as
spam	those two passengers were, is there anything in his bulk and stature to
spam	render it unlikely that he was one of them?"
spam	"No."
spam	"You will not swear, Mr. Lorry, that he was not one of them?"
ham	"No."
spam	"So at least you say he may have been one of them?"
spam	"Yes. Except that I remember them both to have been--like
spam	myself--timorous of highwaymen, and the prisoner has not a timorous
ham	air."
spam	"Did you ever see a counterfeit of timidity, Mr. Lorry?"
ham	"I certainly have seen that."
ham	"Mr. Lorry, look once more upon the prisoner. Have you seen him, to your
ham	certain knowledge, before?"
ham	"I have."
ham	"When?"
ham	"I was returning from France a few days afterwards, and, at Calais, the
spam	prisoner came on board the packet-ship in which I returned, and made the
ham	voyage with me."
spam	"At what hour did he come on board?"
ham	"At a little after midnight."
ham	"In the dead of the night. Was he the only passenger who came on board
spam	at that untimely hour?"
spam	"He happened to be the only one."
ham	"Never mind about 'happening,' Mr. Lorry. He was the only passenger who
ham	came on board in the dead of the night?"
ham	"He was."
ham	"Were you travelling alone, Mr. Lorry, or with any companion?"
spam	"With two companions. A gentleman and lady. They are here."
spam	"They are here. Had you any conversation with the prisoner?"
ham	"Hardly any. The weather was stormy, and the passage long and rough, and
ham	I lay on a sofa, almost from shore to shore."
ham	"Miss Manette!"
ham	The young lady, to whom all eyes had been turned before, and were now
spam	turned again, stood up where she had sat. Her father rose with her, and
spam	kept her hand drawn through his arm.
ham	"Miss Manette, look upon the prisoner."
ham	To be confronted with such pity, and such earnest youth and beauty, was
ham	far more trying to the accused than to be confronted with all the crowd.
spam	Standing, as it were, apart with her on the edge of his grave, not all
ham	the staring curiosity that looked on, could, for the moment, nerve him
ham	to remain quite still. His hurried right hand parcelled out the herbs
ham	before him into imaginary beds of flowers in a garden; and his efforts
ham	to control and steady his breathing shook the lips from which the colour
spam	rushed to his heart. The buzz of the great flies was loud again.
ham	"Miss Manette, have you seen the prisoner before?"
ham	"Yes, sir."
spam	"Where?"
ham	"On board of the packet-ship just now referred to, sir, and on the same
ham	occasion."
spam	"You are the young lady just now referred to?"
spam	"O! most unhappily, I am!"
spam	The plaintive tone of her compassion merged into the less musical voice
spam	of the Judge, as he said something fiercely: "Answer the questions put
spam	to you, and make no remark upon them."
ham	"Miss Manette, had you any conversation with the prisoner on that
spam	passage across the Channel?"
spam	"Yes, sir."
spam	"Recall it."
spam	In the midst of a profound stillness, she faintly began: "When the
ham	gentleman came on board--"
ham	"Do you mean the prisoner?" inquired the Judge, knitting his brows.
ham	"Yes, my Lord."
spam	"Then say the prisoner."
ham	"When the prisoner came on board, he noticed that my father," turning
ham	her eyes lovingly to him as he stood beside her, "was much fatigued
ham	and in a very weak state of health. My father was so reduced that I was
spam	afraid to take him out of the air, and I had made a bed for him on the
spam	deck near the cabin steps, and I sat on the deck at his side to take
ham	care of him. There were no other passengers that night, but we four.
ham	The prisoner was so good as to beg permission to advise me how I could
spam	shelter my father from the wind and weather, better than I had done. I
spam	had not known how to do it well, not understanding how the wind would
spam	set when we were out of the harbour. He did it for me. He expressed
spam	great gentleness and kindness for my father's state, and I am sure he
ham	felt it. That was the manner of our beginning to speak together."
spam	"Let me interrupt you for a moment. Had he come on board alone?"
spam	"No."
ham	"How many were with him?"
spam	"Two French gentlemen."
spam	"Had they conferred together?"
ham	"They had conferred together until the last moment, when it was
spam	necessary for the French gentlemen to be landed in their boat."
ham	"Had any papers been handed about among them, similar to these lists?"
ham	"Some papers had been handed about among them, but I don't know what
spam	papers."
spam	"Like these in shape and size?"
ham	"Possibly, but indeed I don't know, although they stood whispering very
ham	near to me: because they stood at the top of the cabin steps to have the
spam	light of the lamp that was hanging there; it was a dull lamp, and they
ham	spoke very low, and I did not hear what they said, and saw only that
ham	they looked at papers."
ham	"Now, to the prisoner's conversation, Miss Manette."
spam	"The prisoner was as open in his confidence with me--which arose out
ham	of my helpless situation--as he was kind, and good, and useful to my
ham	father. I hope," bursting into tears, "I may not repay him by doing him
spam	harm to-day."
ham	Buzzing from the blue-flies.
spam	"Miss Manette, if the prisoner does not perfectly understand that
spam	you give the evidence which it is your duty to give--which you must
spam	give--and which you cannot escape from giving--with great unwillingness,
ham	he is the only person present in that condition. Please to go on."
ham	"He told me that he was travelling on business of a delicate and
ham	difficult nature, which might get people into trouble, and that he was
spam	therefore travelling under an assumed name. He said that this business
spam	had, within a few days, taken him to France, and might, at intervals,
spam	take him backwards and forwards between France and England for a long
ham	time to come."
ham	"Did he say anything about America, Miss Manette? Be particular."
spam	"He tried to explain to me how that quarrel had arisen, and he said
ham	that, so far as he could judge, it was a wrong and foolish one on
spam	England's part. He added, in a jesting way, that perhaps George
ham	Washington might gain almost as great a name in history as George the
spam	Third. But there was no harm in his way of saying this: it was said
spam	laughingly, and to beguile the time."
spam	Any strongly marked expression of face on the part of a chief actor in
spam	a scene of great interest to whom many eyes are directed, will be
ham	unconsciously imitated by the spectators. Her forehead was painfully
spam	anxious and intent as she gave this evidence, and, in the pauses when
spam	she stopped for the Judge to write it down, watched its effect upon
spam	the counsel for and against. Among the lookers-on there was the same
spam	expression in all quarters of the court; insomuch, that a great majority
spam	of the foreheads there, might have been mirrors reflecting the witness,
ham	when the Judge looked up from his notes to glare at that tremendous
spam	heresy about George Washington.
ham	Mr. Attorney-General now signified to my Lord, that he deemed it
spam	necessary, as a matter of precaution and form, to call the young lady's
spam	father, Doctor Manette. Who was called accordingly.
spam	"Doctor Manette, look upon the prisoner. Have you ever seen him before?"
spam	"Once. When he called at my lodgings in London. Some three years, or
spam	three years and a half ago."
spam	"Can you identify him as your fellow-passenger on board the packet, or
spam	speak to his conversation with your daughter?"
ham	"Sir, I can do neither."
ham	"Is there any particular and special reason for your being unable to do
spam	either?"
ham	He answered, in a low voice, "There is."
ham	"Has it been your misfortune to undergo a long imprisonment, without
ham	trial, or even accusation, in your native country, Doctor Manette?"
ham	He answered, in a tone that went to every heart, "A long imprisonment."
spam	"Were you newly released on the occasion in question?"
spam	"They tell me so."
ham	"Have you no remembrance of the occasion?"
spam	"None. My mind is a blank, from some time--I cannot even say what
ham	time--when I employed myself, in my captivity, in making shoes, to the
spam	time when I found myself living in London with my dear daughter
ham	here. She had become familiar to me, when a gracious God restored
spam	my faculties; but, I am quite unable even to say how she had become
ham	familiar. I have no remembrance of the process."
ham	Mr. Attorney-General sat down, and the father and daughter sat down
spam	together.
ham	A singular circumstance then arose in the case. The object in hand being
spam	to show that the prisoner went down, with some fellow-plotter untracked,
spam	in the Dover mail on that Friday night in November five years ago, and
ham	got out of the mail in the night, as a blind, at a place where he did
spam	not remain, but from which he travelled back some dozen miles or more,
spam	to a garrison and dockyard, and there collected information; a witness
ham	was called to identify him as having been at the precise time required,
spam	in the coffee-room of an hotel in that garrison-and-dockyard town,
spam	waiting for another person. The prisoner's counsel was cross-examining
ham	this witness with no result, except that he had never seen the prisoner
ham	on any other occasion, when the wigged gentleman who had all this time
spam	been looking at the ceiling of the court, wrote a word or two on a
spam	little piece of paper, screwed it up, and tossed it to him. Opening
ham	this piece of paper in the next pause, the counsel looked with great
ham	attention and curiosity at the prisoner.
ham	"You say again you are quite sure that it was the prisoner?"
ham	The witness was quite sure.
spam	"Did you ever see anybody very like the prisoner?"
ham	Not so like (the witness said) as that he could be mistaken.
ham	"Look well upon that gentleman, my learned friend there," pointing
spam	to him who had tossed the paper over, "and then look well upon the
spam	prisoner. How say you? Are they very like each other?"
spam	Allowing for my learned friend's appearance being careless and slovenly
spam	if not debauched, they were sufficiently like each other to surprise,
ham	not only the witness, but everybody present, when they were thus brought
spam	into comparison. My Lord being prayed to bid my learned friend lay aside
ham	his wig, and giving no very gracious consent, the likeness became
spam	much more remarkable. My Lord inquired of Mr. Stryver (the prisoner's
ham	counsel), whether they were next to try Mr. Carton (name of my learned
spam	friend) for treason? But, Mr. Stryver replied to my Lord, no; but he
ham	would ask the witness to tell him whether what happened once, might
spam	happen twice; whether he would have been so confident if he had seen
spam	this illustration of his rashness sooner, whether he would be so
spam	confident, having seen it; and more. The upshot of which, was, to smash
ham	this witness like a crockery vessel, and shiver his part of the case to
ham	useless lumber.
ham	Mr. Cruncher had by this time taken quite a lunch of rust off his
spam	fingers in his following of the evidence. He had now to attend while Mr.
ham	Stryver fitted the prisoner's case on the jury, like a compact suit
ham	of clothes; showing them how the patriot, Barsad, was a hired spy and
ham	traitor, an unblushing trafficker in blood, and one of the greatest
spam	scoundrels upon earth since accursed Judas--which he certainly did look
spam	rather like. How the virtuous servant, Cly, was his friend and partner,
spam	and was worthy to be; how the watchful eyes of those forgers and false
spam	swearers had rested on the prisoner as a victim, because some family
spam	affairs in France, he being of French extraction, did require his making
ham	those passages across the Channel--though what those affairs were, a
spam	consideration for others who were near and dear to him, forbade him,
ham	even for his life, to disclose. How the evidence that had been warped
ham	and wrested from the young lady, whose anguish in giving it they
spam	had witnessed, came to nothing, involving the mere little innocent
spam	gallantries and politenesses likely to pass between any young gentleman
ham	and young lady so thrown together;--with the exception of that
spam	reference to George Washington, which was altogether too extravagant and
spam	impossible to be regarded in any other light than as a monstrous joke.
ham	How it would be a weakness in the government to break down in this
ham	attempt to practise for popularity on the lowest national antipathies
spam	and fears, and therefore Mr. Attorney-General had made the most of it;
spam	how, nevertheless, it rested upon nothing, save that vile and infamous
spam	character of evidence too often disfiguring such cases, and of which the
spam	State Trials of this country were full. But, there my Lord interposed
spam	(with as grave a face as if it had not been true), saying that he could
ham	not sit upon that Bench and suffer those allusions.
ham	Mr. Stryver then called his few witnesses, and Mr. Cruncher had next to
spam	attend while Mr. Attorney-General turned the whole suit of clothes Mr.
ham	Stryver had fitted on the jury, inside out; showing how Barsad and
ham	Cly were even a hundred times better than he had thought them, and the
ham	prisoner a hundred times worse. Lastly, came my Lord himself, turning
ham	the suit of clothes, now inside out, now outside in, but on the whole
spam	decidedly trimming and shaping them into grave-clothes for the prisoner.
ham	And now, the jury turned to consider, and the great flies swarmed again.
spam	Mr. Carton, who had so long sat looking at the ceiling of the court,
ham	changed neither his place nor his attitude, even in this excitement.
spam	While his learned friend, Mr. Stryver, massing his papers before him,
spam	whispered with those who sat near, and from time to time glanced
spam	anxiously at the jury; while all the spectators moved more or less, and
spam	grouped themselves anew; while even my Lord himself arose from his seat,
spam	and slowly paced up and down his platform, not unattended by a suspicion
spam	in the minds of the audience that his state was feverish; this one man
spam	sat leaning back, with his torn gown half off him, his untidy wig put
ham	on just as it had happened to light on his head after its removal, his
spam	hands in his pockets, and his eyes on the ceiling as they had been all
ham	day. Something especially reckless in his demeanour, not only gave him
spam	a disreputable look, but so diminished the strong resemblance he
spam	undoubtedly bore to the prisoner (which his momentary earnestness,
spam	when they were compared together, had strengthened), that many of the
spam	lookers-on, taking note of him now, said to one another they would
ham	hardly have thought the two were so alike. Mr. Cruncher made the
spam	observation to his next neighbour, and added, "I'd hold half a guinea
spam	that _he_ don't get no law-work to do. Don't look like the sort of one
ham	to get any, do he?"
ham	Yet, this Mr. Carton took in more of the details of the scene than he
ham	appeared to take in; for now, when Miss Manette's head dropped upon
spam	her father's breast, he was the first to see it, and to say audibly:
spam	"Officer! look to that young lady. Help the gentleman to take her out.
ham	Don't you see she will fall!"
spam	There was much commiseration for her as she was removed, and much
spam	sympathy with her father. It had evidently been a great distress to
spam	him, to have the days of his imprisonment recalled. He had shown
ham	strong internal agitation when he was questioned, and that pondering or
ham	brooding look which made him old, had been upon him, like a heavy cloud,
spam	ever since. As he passed out, the jury, who had turned back and paused a
spam	moment, spoke, through their foreman.
spam	They were not agreed, and wished to retire. My Lord (perhaps with George
ham	Washington on his mind) showed some surprise that they were not agreed,
spam	but signified his pleasure that they should retire under watch and ward,
spam	and retired himself. The trial had lasted all day, and the lamps in
spam	the court were now being lighted. It began to be rumoured that the
ham	jury would be out a long while. The spectators dropped off to get
spam	refreshment, and the prisoner withdrew to the back of the dock, and sat
spam	down.
ham	Mr. Lorry, who had gone out when the young lady and her father went out,
ham	now reappeared, and beckoned to Jerry: who, in the slackened interest,
spam	could easily get near him.
spam	"Jerry, if you wish to take something to eat, you can. But, keep in the
spam	way. You will be sure to hear when the jury come in. Don't be a moment
spam	behind them, for I want you to take the verdict back to the bank. You
ham	are the quickest messenger I know, and will get to Temple Bar long
ham	before I can."
ham	Jerry had just enough forehead to knuckle, and he knuckled it in
ham	acknowledgment of this communication and a shilling. Mr. Carton came up
spam	at the moment, and touched Mr. Lorry on the arm.
ham	"How is the young lady?"
ham	"She is greatly distressed; but her father is comforting her, and she
ham	feels the better for being out of court."
spam	"I'll tell the prisoner so. It won't do for a respectable bank gentleman
spam	like you, to be seen speaking to him publicly, you know."
ham	Mr. Lorry reddened as if he were conscious of having debated the point
spam	in his mind, and Mr. Carton made his way to the outside of the bar.
ham	The way out of court lay in that direction, and Jerry followed him, all
spam	eyes, ears, and spikes.
ham	"Mr. Darnay!"
spam	The prisoner came forward directly.
spam	"You will naturally be anxious to hear of the witness, Miss Manette. She
ham	will do very well. You have seen the worst of her agitation."
spam	"I am deeply sorry to have been the cause of it. Could you tell her so
ham	for me, with my fervent acknowledgments?"
spam	"Yes, I could. I will, if you ask it."
spam	Mr. Carton's manner was so careless as to be almost insolent. He stood,
spam	half turned from the prisoner, lounging with his elbow against the bar.
ham	"I do ask it. Accept my cordial thanks."
ham	"What," said Carton, still only half turned towards him, "do you expect,
ham	Mr. Darnay?"
spam	"The worst."
ham	"It's the wisest thing to expect, and the likeliest. But I think their
spam	withdrawing is in your favour."
spam	Loitering on the way out of court not being allowed, Jerry heard no
spam	more: but left them--so like each other in feature, so unlike each other
spam	in manner--standing side by side, both reflected in the glass above
spam	them.
ham	An hour and a half limped heavily away in the thief-and-rascal crowded
ham	passages below, even though assisted off with mutton pies and ale.
spam	The hoarse messenger, uncomfortably seated on a form after taking that
ham	refection, had dropped into a doze, when a loud murmur and a rapid tide
ham	of people setting up the stairs that led to the court, carried him along
ham	with them.
