ham	"Jerry! Jerry!" Mr. Lorry was already calling at the door when he got
ham	there.
spam	"Here, sir! It's a fight to get back again. Here I am, sir!"
ham	Mr. Lorry handed him a paper through the throng. "Quick! Have you got
spam	it?"
spam	"Yes, sir."
spam	Hastily written on the paper was the word "ACQUITTED."
ham	"If you had sent the message, 'Recalled to Life,' again," muttered
ham	Jerry, as he turned, "I should have known what you meant, this time."
ham	He had no opportunity of saying, or so much as thinking, anything else,
spam	until he was clear of the Old Bailey; for, the crowd came pouring out
ham	with a vehemence that nearly took him off his legs, and a loud buzz
ham	swept into the street as if the baffled blue-flies were dispersing in
spam	search of other carrion.
spam	IV. Congratulatory
ham	From the dimly-lighted passages of the court, the last sediment of the
ham	human stew that had been boiling there all day, was straining off, when
spam	Doctor Manette, Lucie Manette, his daughter, Mr. Lorry, the solicitor
spam	for the defence, and its counsel, Mr. Stryver, stood gathered round Mr.
ham	Charles Darnay--just released--congratulating him on his escape from
spam	death.
spam	It would have been difficult by a far brighter light, to recognise
spam	in Doctor Manette, intellectual of face and upright of bearing, the
spam	shoemaker of the garret in Paris. Yet, no one could have looked at him
ham	twice, without looking again: even though the opportunity of observation
ham	had not extended to the mournful cadence of his low grave voice, and
ham	to the abstraction that overclouded him fitfully, without any apparent
spam	reason. While one external cause, and that a reference to his long
ham	lingering agony, would always--as on the trial--evoke this condition
ham	from the depths of his soul, it was also in its nature to arise of
spam	itself, and to draw a gloom over him, as incomprehensible to those
ham	unacquainted with his story as if they had seen the shadow of the actual
ham	Bastille thrown upon him by a summer sun, when the substance was three
spam	hundred miles away.
spam	Only his daughter had the power of charming this black brooding from
ham	his mind. She was the golden thread that united him to a Past beyond his
spam	misery, and to a Present beyond his misery: and the sound of her voice,
spam	the light of her face, the touch of her hand, had a strong beneficial
spam	influence with him almost always. Not absolutely always, for she could
ham	recall some occasions on which her power had failed; but they were few
ham	and slight, and she believed them over.
spam	Mr. Darnay had kissed her hand fervently and gratefully, and had turned
spam	to Mr. Stryver, whom he warmly thanked. Mr. Stryver, a man of little
ham	more than thirty, but looking twenty years older than he was, stout,
spam	loud, red, bluff, and free from any drawback of delicacy, had a pushing
ham	way of shouldering himself (morally and physically) into companies and
spam	conversations, that argued well for his shouldering his way up in life.
spam	He still had his wig and gown on, and he said, squaring himself at his
ham	late client to that degree that he squeezed the innocent Mr. Lorry clean
spam	out of the group: "I am glad to have brought you off with honour, Mr.
spam	Darnay. It was an infamous prosecution, grossly infamous; but not the
spam	less likely to succeed on that account."
spam	"You have laid me under an obligation to you for life--in two senses,"
spam	said his late client, taking his hand.
spam	"I have done my best for you, Mr. Darnay; and my best is as good as
ham	another man's, I believe."
spam	It clearly being incumbent on some one to say, "Much better," Mr. Lorry
ham	said it; perhaps not quite disinterestedly, but with the interested
ham	object of squeezing himself back again.
spam	"You think so?" said Mr. Stryver. "Well! you have been present all day,
spam	and you ought to know. You are a man of business, too."
spam	"And as such," quoth Mr. Lorry, whom the counsel learned in the law had
spam	now shouldered back into the group, just as he had previously shouldered
spam	him out of it--"as such I will appeal to Doctor Manette, to break up
ham	this conference and order us all to our homes. Miss Lucie looks ill, Mr.
spam	Darnay has had a terrible day, we are worn out."
ham	"Speak for yourself, Mr. Lorry," said Stryver; "I have a night's work to
spam	do yet. Speak for yourself."
spam	"I speak for myself," answered Mr. Lorry, "and for Mr. Darnay, and for
spam	Miss Lucie, and--Miss Lucie, do you not think I may speak for us all?"
ham	He asked her the question pointedly, and with a glance at her father.
ham	His face had become frozen, as it were, in a very curious look at
spam	Darnay: an intent look, deepening into a frown of dislike and distrust,
spam	not even unmixed with fear. With this strange expression on him his
ham	thoughts had wandered away.
ham	"My father," said Lucie, softly laying her hand on his.
ham	He slowly shook the shadow off, and turned to her.
ham	"Shall we go home, my father?"
ham	With a long breath, he answered "Yes."
ham	The friends of the acquitted prisoner had dispersed, under the
ham	impression--which he himself had originated--that he would not be
ham	released that night. The lights were nearly all extinguished in the
ham	passages, the iron gates were being closed with a jar and a rattle,
ham	and the dismal place was deserted until to-morrow morning's interest of
ham	gallows, pillory, whipping-post, and branding-iron, should repeople it.
spam	Walking between her father and Mr. Darnay, Lucie Manette passed into
spam	the open air. A hackney-coach was called, and the father and daughter
spam	departed in it.
ham	Mr. Stryver had left them in the passages, to shoulder his way back
ham	to the robing-room. Another person, who had not joined the group, or
spam	interchanged a word with any one of them, but who had been leaning
ham	against the wall where its shadow was darkest, had silently strolled
ham	out after the rest, and had looked on until the coach drove away. He now
spam	stepped up to where Mr. Lorry and Mr. Darnay stood upon the pavement.
spam	"So, Mr. Lorry! Men of business may speak to Mr. Darnay now?"
spam	Nobody had made any acknowledgment of Mr. Carton's part in the day's
spam	proceedings; nobody had known of it. He was unrobed, and was none the
spam	better for it in appearance.
ham	"If you knew what a conflict goes on in the business mind, when the
spam	business mind is divided between good-natured impulse and business
spam	appearances, you would be amused, Mr. Darnay."
ham	Mr. Lorry reddened, and said, warmly, "You have mentioned that before,
spam	sir. We men of business, who serve a House, are not our own masters. We
ham	have to think of the House more than ourselves."
ham	"_I_ know, _I_ know," rejoined Mr. Carton, carelessly. "Don't be
ham	nettled, Mr. Lorry. You are as good as another, I have no doubt: better,
spam	I dare say."
ham	"And indeed, sir," pursued Mr. Lorry, not minding him, "I really don't
spam	know what you have to do with the matter. If you'll excuse me, as very
ham	much your elder, for saying so, I really don't know that it is your
spam	business."
ham	"Business! Bless you, _I_ have no business," said Mr. Carton.
ham	"It is a pity you have not, sir."
ham	"I think so, too."
ham	"If you had," pursued Mr. Lorry, "perhaps you would attend to it."
spam	"Lord love you, no!--I shouldn't," said Mr. Carton.
ham	"Well, sir!" cried Mr. Lorry, thoroughly heated by his indifference,
ham	"business is a very good thing, and a very respectable thing. And, sir,
ham	if business imposes its restraints and its silences and impediments, Mr.
spam	Darnay as a young gentleman of generosity knows how to make allowance
ham	for that circumstance. Mr. Darnay, good night, God bless you, sir!
spam	I hope you have been this day preserved for a prosperous and happy
spam	life.--Chair there!"
ham	Perhaps a little angry with himself, as well as with the barrister, Mr.
spam	Lorry bustled into the chair, and was carried off to Tellson's. Carton,
spam	who smelt of port wine, and did not appear to be quite sober, laughed
ham	then, and turned to Darnay:
ham	"This is a strange chance that throws you and me together. This must
spam	be a strange night to you, standing alone here with your counterpart on
spam	these street stones?"
spam	"I hardly seem yet," returned Charles Darnay, "to belong to this world
spam	again."
ham	"I don't wonder at it; it's not so long since you were pretty far
ham	advanced on your way to another. You speak faintly."
ham	"I begin to think I _am_ faint."
ham	"Then why the devil don't you dine? I dined, myself, while those
ham	numskulls were deliberating which world you should belong to--this, or
spam	some other. Let me show you the nearest tavern to dine well at."
ham	Drawing his arm through his own, he took him down Ludgate-hill to
spam	Fleet-street, and so, up a covered way, into a tavern. Here, they were
spam	shown into a little room, where Charles Darnay was soon recruiting
spam	his strength with a good plain dinner and good wine: while Carton sat
spam	opposite to him at the same table, with his separate bottle of port
ham	before him, and his fully half-insolent manner upon him.
spam	"Do you feel, yet, that you belong to this terrestrial scheme again, Mr.
spam	Darnay?"
ham	"I am frightfully confused regarding time and place; but I am so far
spam	mended as to feel that."
spam	"It must be an immense satisfaction!"
ham	He said it bitterly, and filled up his glass again: which was a large
ham	one.
spam	"As to me, the greatest desire I have, is to forget that I belong to it.
ham	It has no good in it for me--except wine like this--nor I for it. So we
spam	are not much alike in that particular. Indeed, I begin to think we are
spam	not much alike in any particular, you and I."
spam	Confused by the emotion of the day, and feeling his being there with
ham	this Double of coarse deportment, to be like a dream, Charles Darnay was
ham	at a loss how to answer; finally, answered not at all.
ham	"Now your dinner is done," Carton presently said, "why don't you call a
spam	health, Mr. Darnay; why don't you give your toast?"
spam	"What health? What toast?"
ham	"Why, it's on the tip of your tongue. It ought to be, it must be, I'll
ham	swear it's there."
spam	"Miss Manette, then!"
ham	"Miss Manette, then!"
ham	Looking his companion full in the face while he drank the toast, Carton
ham	flung his glass over his shoulder against the wall, where it shivered to
ham	pieces; then, rang the bell, and ordered in another.
spam	"That's a fair young lady to hand to a coach in the dark, Mr. Darnay!"
spam	he said, filling his new goblet.
spam	A slight frown and a laconic "Yes," were the answer.
ham	"That's a fair young lady to be pitied by and wept for by! How does it
ham	feel? Is it worth being tried for one's life, to be the object of such
spam	sympathy and compassion, Mr. Darnay?"
spam	Again Darnay answered not a word.
spam	"She was mightily pleased to have your message, when I gave it her. Not
ham	that she showed she was pleased, but I suppose she was."
spam	The allusion served as a timely reminder to Darnay that this
spam	disagreeable companion had, of his own free will, assisted him in the
spam	strait of the day. He turned the dialogue to that point, and thanked him
ham	for it.
spam	"I neither want any thanks, nor merit any," was the careless rejoinder.
spam	"It was nothing to do, in the first place; and I don't know why I did
spam	it, in the second. Mr. Darnay, let me ask you a question."
ham	"Willingly, and a small return for your good offices."
spam	"Do you think I particularly like you?"
ham	"Really, Mr. Carton," returned the other, oddly disconcerted, "I have
spam	not asked myself the question."
ham	"But ask yourself the question now."
ham	"You have acted as if you do; but I don't think you do."
spam	"_I_ don't think I do," said Carton. "I begin to have a very good
spam	opinion of your understanding."
spam	"Nevertheless," pursued Darnay, rising to ring the bell, "there is
ham	nothing in that, I hope, to prevent my calling the reckoning, and our
ham	parting without ill-blood on either side."
spam	Carton rejoining, "Nothing in life!" Darnay rang. "Do you call the whole
spam	reckoning?" said Carton. On his answering in the affirmative, "Then
spam	bring me another pint of this same wine, drawer, and come and wake me at
ham	ten."
ham	The bill being paid, Charles Darnay rose and wished him good night.
spam	Without returning the wish, Carton rose too, with something of a threat
ham	of defiance in his manner, and said, "A last word, Mr. Darnay: you think
ham	I am drunk?"
spam	"I think you have been drinking, Mr. Carton."
spam	"Think? You know I have been drinking."
ham	"Since I must say so, I know it."
ham	"Then you shall likewise know why. I am a disappointed drudge, sir. I
ham	care for no man on earth, and no man on earth cares for me."
spam	"Much to be regretted. You might have used your talents better."
ham	"May be so, Mr. Darnay; may be not. Don't let your sober face elate you,
spam	however; you don't know what it may come to. Good night!"
ham	When he was left alone, this strange being took up a candle, went to a
spam	glass that hung against the wall, and surveyed himself minutely in it.
ham	"Do you particularly like the man?" he muttered, at his own image; "why
spam	should you particularly like a man who resembles you? There is nothing
spam	in you to like; you know that. Ah, confound you! What a change you have
spam	made in yourself! A good reason for taking to a man, that he shows you
spam	what you have fallen away from, and what you might have been! Change
spam	places with him, and would you have been looked at by those blue eyes as
ham	he was, and commiserated by that agitated face as he was? Come on, and
ham	have it out in plain words! You hate the fellow."
ham	He resorted to his pint of wine for consolation, drank it all in a few
ham	minutes, and fell asleep on his arms, with his hair straggling over the
ham	table, and a long winding-sheet in the candle dripping down upon him.
ham	V. The Jackal
spam	Those were drinking days, and most men drank hard. So very great is
spam	the improvement Time has brought about in such habits, that a moderate
spam	statement of the quantity of wine and punch which one man would swallow
ham	in the course of a night, without any detriment to his reputation as a
ham	perfect gentleman, would seem, in these days, a ridiculous exaggeration.
spam	The learned profession of the law was certainly not behind any other
spam	learned profession in its Bacchanalian propensities; neither was Mr.
ham	Stryver, already fast shouldering his way to a large and lucrative
ham	practice, behind his compeers in this particular, any more than in the
ham	drier parts of the legal race.
ham	A favourite at the Old Bailey, and eke at the Sessions, Mr. Stryver had
spam	begun cautiously to hew away the lower staves of the ladder on which
ham	he mounted. Sessions and Old Bailey had now to summon their favourite,
ham	specially, to their longing arms; and shouldering itself towards the
ham	visage of the Lord Chief Justice in the Court of King's Bench, the
spam	florid countenance of Mr. Stryver might be daily seen, bursting out of
ham	the bed of wigs, like a great sunflower pushing its way at the sun from
ham	among a rank garden-full of flaring companions.
spam	It had once been noted at the Bar, that while Mr. Stryver was a glib
spam	man, and an unscrupulous, and a ready, and a bold, he had not that
spam	faculty of extracting the essence from a heap of statements, which is
ham	among the most striking and necessary of the advocate's accomplishments.
ham	But, a remarkable improvement came upon him as to this. The more
ham	business he got, the greater his power seemed to grow of getting at its
spam	pith and marrow; and however late at night he sat carousing with Sydney
ham	Carton, he always had his points at his fingers' ends in the morning.
ham	Sydney Carton, idlest and most unpromising of men, was Stryver's great
ham	ally. What the two drank together, between Hilary Term and Michaelmas,
ham	might have floated a king's ship. Stryver never had a case in hand,
spam	anywhere, but Carton was there, with his hands in his pockets, staring
ham	at the ceiling of the court; they went the same Circuit, and even there
spam	they prolonged their usual orgies late into the night, and Carton was
spam	rumoured to be seen at broad day, going home stealthily and unsteadily
spam	to his lodgings, like a dissipated cat. At last, it began to get about,
spam	among such as were interested in the matter, that although Sydney Carton
spam	would never be a lion, he was an amazingly good jackal, and that he
ham	rendered suit and service to Stryver in that humble capacity.
spam	"Ten o'clock, sir," said the man at the tavern, whom he had charged to
spam	wake him--"ten o'clock, sir."
spam	"_What's_ the matter?"
ham	"Ten o'clock, sir."
spam	"What do you mean? Ten o'clock at night?"
ham	"Yes, sir. Your honour told me to call you."
ham	"Oh! I remember. Very well, very well."
spam	After a few dull efforts to get to sleep again, which the man
spam	dexterously combated by stirring the fire continuously for five minutes,
ham	he got up, tossed his hat on, and walked out. He turned into the Temple,
spam	and, having revived himself by twice pacing the pavements of King's
ham	Bench-walk and Paper-buildings, turned into the Stryver chambers.
ham	The Stryver clerk, who never assisted at these conferences, had gone
ham	home, and the Stryver principal opened the door. He had his slippers on,
ham	and a loose bed-gown, and his throat was bare for his greater ease. He
spam	had that rather wild, strained, seared marking about the eyes, which
spam	may be observed in all free livers of his class, from the portrait of
spam	Jeffries downward, and which can be traced, under various disguises of
spam	Art, through the portraits of every Drinking Age.
spam	"You are a little late, Memory," said Stryver.
ham	"About the usual time; it may be a quarter of an hour later."
ham	They went into a dingy room lined with books and littered with papers,
ham	where there was a blazing fire. A kettle steamed upon the hob, and in
ham	the midst of the wreck of papers a table shone, with plenty of wine upon
ham	it, and brandy, and rum, and sugar, and lemons.
spam	"You have had your bottle, I perceive, Sydney."
ham	"Two to-night, I think. I have been dining with the day's client; or
spam	seeing him dine--it's all one!"
ham	"That was a rare point, Sydney, that you brought to bear upon the
spam	identification. How did you come by it? When did it strike you?"
ham	"I thought he was rather a handsome fellow, and I thought I should have
spam	been much the same sort of fellow, if I had had any luck."
spam	Mr. Stryver laughed till he shook his precocious paunch.
spam	"You and your luck, Sydney! Get to work, get to work."
ham	Sullenly enough, the jackal loosened his dress, went into an adjoining
ham	room, and came back with a large jug of cold water, a basin, and a towel
ham	or two. Steeping the towels in the water, and partially wringing them
spam	out, he folded them on his head in a manner hideous to behold, sat down
ham	at the table, and said, "Now I am ready!"
spam	"Not much boiling down to be done to-night, Memory," said Mr. Stryver,
spam	gaily, as he looked among his papers.
spam	"How much?"
spam	"Only two sets of them."
ham	"Give me the worst first."
spam	"There they are, Sydney. Fire away!"
ham	"He has paid all, Monseigneur. He is dead."
ham	"Well! He is quiet. Can I restore him to you?"
spam	"Alas, no, Monseigneur! But he lies yonder, under a little heap of poor
spam	grass."
spam	"Well?"
spam	"Monseigneur, there are so many little heaps of poor grass?"
ham	"Again, well?"
ham	She looked an old woman, but was young. Her manner was one of passionate
spam	grief; by turns she clasped her veinous and knotted hands together
spam	with wild energy, and laid one of them on the carriage-door--tenderly,
ham	caressingly, as if it had been a human breast, and could be expected to
ham	feel the appealing touch.
spam	"Monseigneur, hear me! Monseigneur, hear my petition! My husband died of
spam	want; so many die of want; so many more will die of want."
ham	"Again, well? Can I feed them?"
ham	"Monseigneur, the good God knows; but I don't ask it. My petition is,
spam	that a morsel of stone or wood, with my husband's name, may be placed
spam	over him to show where he lies. Otherwise, the place will be quickly
ham	forgotten, it will never be found when I am dead of the same malady, I
ham	shall be laid under some other heap of poor grass. Monseigneur, they
ham	are so many, they increase so fast, there is so much want. Monseigneur!
spam	Monseigneur!"
ham	The valet had put her away from the door, the carriage had broken into
spam	a brisk trot, the postilions had quickened the pace, she was left far
spam	behind, and Monseigneur, again escorted by the Furies, was rapidly
spam	diminishing the league or two of distance that remained between him and
spam	his chateau.
ham	The sweet scents of the summer night rose all around him, and rose, as
spam	the rain falls, impartially, on the dusty, ragged, and toil-worn group
spam	at the fountain not far away; to whom the mender of roads, with the aid
ham	of the blue cap without which he was nothing, still enlarged upon his
ham	man like a spectre, as long as they could bear it. By degrees, as they
spam	could bear no more, they dropped off one by one, and lights twinkled
spam	in little casements; which lights, as the casements darkened, and more
spam	stars came out, seemed to have shot up into the sky instead of having
ham	been extinguished.
spam	The shadow of a large high-roofed house, and of many over-hanging trees,
ham	was upon Monsieur the Marquis by that time; and the shadow was exchanged
spam	for the light of a flambeau, as his carriage stopped, and the great door
ham	of his chateau was opened to him.
spam	"Monsieur Charles, whom I expect; is he arrived from England?"
ham	"Monseigneur, not yet."
spam	IX. The Gorgon's Head
spam	It was a heavy mass of building, that chateau of Monsieur the Marquis,
ham	with a large stone courtyard before it, and two stone sweeps of
spam	staircase meeting in a stone terrace before the principal door. A stony
spam	business altogether, with heavy stone balustrades, and stone urns, and
spam	stone flowers, and stone faces of men, and stone heads of lions, in
ham	all directions. As if the Gorgon's head had surveyed it, when it was
spam	finished, two centuries ago.
spam	Up the broad flight of shallow steps, Monsieur the Marquis, flambeau
ham	preceded, went from his carriage, sufficiently disturbing the darkness
spam	to elicit loud remonstrance from an owl in the roof of the great pile
spam	of stable building away among the trees. All else was so quiet, that the
spam	flambeau carried up the steps, and the other flambeau held at the great
spam	door, burnt as if they were in a close room of state, instead of being
spam	in the open night-air. Other sound than the owl's voice there was none,
ham	save the falling of a fountain into its stone basin; for, it was one of
spam	those dark nights that hold their breath by the hour together, and then
ham	heave a long low sigh, and hold their breath again.
spam	The great door clanged behind him, and Monsieur the Marquis crossed a
ham	hall grim with certain old boar-spears, swords, and knives of the chase;
ham	grimmer with certain heavy riding-rods and riding-whips, of which many a
ham	peasant, gone to his benefactor Death, had felt the weight when his lord
spam	was angry.
spam	Avoiding the larger rooms, which were dark and made fast for the night,
spam	Monsieur the Marquis, with his flambeau-bearer going on before, went up
ham	the staircase to a door in a corridor. This thrown open, admitted him
spam	to his own private apartment of three rooms: his bed-chamber and two
spam	others. High vaulted rooms with cool uncarpeted floors, great dogs upon
ham	the hearths for the burning of wood in winter time, and all luxuries
ham	befitting the state of a marquis in a luxurious age and country.
spam	The fashion of the last Louis but one, of the line that was never to
spam	break--the fourteenth Louis--was conspicuous in their rich furniture;
spam	but, it was diversified by many objects that were illustrations of old
spam	pages in the history of France.
spam	A supper-table was laid for two, in the third of the rooms; a round
ham	room, in one of the chateau's four extinguisher-topped towers. A small
spam	lofty room, with its window wide open, and the wooden jalousie-blinds
ham	closed, so that the dark night only showed in slight horizontal lines of
ham	black, alternating with their broad lines of stone colour.
ham	"My nephew," said the Marquis, glancing at the supper preparation; "they
spam	said he was not arrived."
spam	Nor was he; but, he had been expected with Monseigneur.
ham	"Ah! It is not probable he will arrive to-night; nevertheless, leave the
spam	table as it is. I shall be ready in a quarter of an hour."
spam	In a quarter of an hour Monseigneur was ready, and sat down alone to his
spam	sumptuous and choice supper. His chair was opposite to the window, and
spam	he had taken his soup, and was raising his glass of Bordeaux to his
ham	lips, when he put it down.
spam	"What is that?" he calmly asked, looking with attention at the
ham	horizontal lines of black and stone colour.
ham	"Monseigneur? That?"
ham	"Outside the blinds. Open the blinds."
spam	It was done.
spam	"Well?"
ham	"Monseigneur, it is nothing. The trees and the night are all that are
ham	here."
spam	The servant who spoke, had thrown the blinds wide, had looked out into
ham	the vacant darkness, and stood with that blank behind him, looking round
spam	for instructions.
spam	"Good," said the imperturbable master. "Close them again."
spam	That was done too, and the Marquis went on with his supper. He was
spam	half way through it, when he again stopped with his glass in his hand,
ham	hearing the sound of wheels. It came on briskly, and came up to the
spam	front of the chateau.
ham	"Ask who is arrived."
spam	It was the nephew of Monseigneur. He had been some few leagues behind
ham	Monseigneur, early in the afternoon. He had diminished the distance
spam	rapidly, but not so rapidly as to come up with Monseigneur on the road.
spam	He had heard of Monseigneur, at the posting-houses, as being before him.
ham	He was to be told (said Monseigneur) that supper awaited him then and
ham	there, and that he was prayed to come to it. In a little while he came.
ham	He had been known in England as Charles Darnay.
ham	Monseigneur received him in a courtly manner, but they did not shake
ham	hands.
ham	"You left Paris yesterday, sir?" he said to Monseigneur, as he took his
spam	seat at table.
ham	"Yesterday. And you?"
ham	"I come direct."
spam	"From London?"
ham	"Yes."
ham	"You have been a long time coming," said the Marquis, with a smile.
spam	"On the contrary; I come direct."
ham	"Pardon me! I mean, not a long time on the journey; a long time
ham	intending the journey."
ham	"I have been detained by"--the nephew stopped a moment in his
spam	answer--"various business."
ham	"Without doubt," said the polished uncle.
ham	So long as a servant was present, no other words passed between them.
ham	When coffee had been served and they were alone together, the nephew,
spam	looking at the uncle and meeting the eyes of the face that was like a
spam	fine mask, opened a conversation.
spam	"I have come back, sir, as you anticipate, pursuing the object that
spam	took me away. It carried me into great and unexpected peril; but it is
ham	a sacred object, and if it had carried me to death I hope it would have
spam	sustained me."
ham	"Not to death," said the uncle; "it is not necessary to say, to death."
ham	"I doubt, sir," returned the nephew, "whether, if it had carried me to
ham	the utmost brink of death, you would have cared to stop me there."
spam	The deepened marks in the nose, and the lengthening of the fine straight
spam	lines in the cruel face, looked ominous as to that; the uncle made a
ham	graceful gesture of protest, which was so clearly a slight form of good
ham	breeding that it was not reassuring.
ham	"Indeed, sir," pursued the nephew, "for anything I know, you may have
spam	expressly worked to give a more suspicious appearance to the suspicious
ham	circumstances that surrounded me."
ham	"No, no, no," said the uncle, pleasantly.
ham	"But, however that may be," resumed the nephew, glancing at him with
spam	deep distrust, "I know that your diplomacy would stop me by any means,
ham	and would know no scruple as to means."
spam	"My friend, I told you so," said the uncle, with a fine pulsation in the
spam	two marks. "Do me the favour to recall that I told you so, long ago."
spam	"I recall it."
spam	"Thank you," said the Marquis--very sweetly indeed.
spam	His tone lingered in the air, almost like the tone of a musical
ham	instrument.
spam	"In effect, sir," pursued the nephew, "I believe it to be at once your
ham	bad fortune, and my good fortune, that has kept me out of a prison in
ham	France here."
ham	"I do not quite understand," returned the uncle, sipping his coffee.
spam	"Dare I ask you to explain?"
ham	"I believe that if you were not in disgrace with the Court, and had not
ham	been overshadowed by that cloud for years past, a letter de cachet would
spam	have sent me to some fortress indefinitely."
ham	"It is possible," said the uncle, with great calmness. "For the honour
ham	of the family, I could even resolve to incommode you to that extent.
spam	Pray excuse me!"
ham	"I perceive that, happily for me, the Reception of the day before
spam	yesterday was, as usual, a cold one," observed the nephew.
ham	"I would not say happily, my friend," returned the uncle, with refined
ham	politeness; "I would not be sure of that. A good opportunity for
spam	consideration, surrounded by the advantages of solitude, might influence
spam	your destiny to far greater advantage than you influence it for
spam	yourself. But it is useless to discuss the question. I am, as you say,
spam	at a disadvantage. These little instruments of correction, these gentle
spam	aids to the power and honour of families, these slight favours that
spam	might so incommode you, are only to be obtained now by interest
ham	and importunity. They are sought by so many, and they are granted
spam	(comparatively) to so few! It used not to be so, but France in all such
spam	things is changed for the worse. Our not remote ancestors held the right
ham	of life and death over the surrounding vulgar. From this room, many such
spam	dogs have been taken out to be hanged; in the next room (my bedroom),
spam	one fellow, to our knowledge, was poniarded on the spot for professing
ham	some insolent delicacy respecting his daughter--_his_ daughter? We have
ham	lost many privileges; a new philosophy has become the mode; and the
ham	assertion of our station, in these days, might (I do not go so far as
ham	to say would, but might) cause us real inconvenience. All very bad, very
ham	bad!"
spam	The Marquis took a gentle little pinch of snuff, and shook his head;
spam	as elegantly despondent as he could becomingly be of a country still
ham	containing himself, that great means of regeneration.
ham	"We have so asserted our station, both in the old time and in the modern
ham	time also," said the nephew, gloomily, "that I believe our name to be
spam	more detested than any name in France."
spam	"Let us hope so," said the uncle. "Detestation of the high is the
ham	involuntary homage of the low."
spam	"There is not," pursued the nephew, in his former tone, "a face I can
ham	look at, in all this country round about us, which looks at me with any
spam	deference on it but the dark deference of fear and slavery."
ham	"A compliment," said the Marquis, "to the grandeur of the family,
spam	merited by the manner in which the family has sustained its grandeur.
spam	Hah!" And he took another gentle little pinch of snuff, and lightly
spam	crossed his legs.
ham	But, when his nephew, leaning an elbow on the table, covered his eyes
ham	thoughtfully and dejectedly with his hand, the fine mask looked at
ham	him sideways with a stronger concentration of keenness, closeness,
spam	and dislike, than was comportable with its wearer's assumption of
spam	indifference.
spam	"Repression is the only lasting philosophy. The dark deference of fear
spam	and slavery, my friend," observed the Marquis, "will keep the dogs
ham	obedient to the whip, as long as this roof," looking up to it, "shuts
ham	out the sky."
spam	That might not be so long as the Marquis supposed. If a picture of the
spam	chateau as it was to be a very few years hence, and of fifty like it as
spam	they too were to be a very few years hence, could have been shown to
spam	him that night, he might have been at a loss to claim his own from
spam	the ghastly, fire-charred, plunder-wrecked rains. As for the roof
ham	he vaunted, he might have found _that_ shutting out the sky in a new
spam	way--to wit, for ever, from the eyes of the bodies into which its lead
ham	was fired, out of the barrels of a hundred thousand muskets.
spam	"Meanwhile," said the Marquis, "I will preserve the honour and repose
spam	of the family, if you will not. But you must be fatigued. Shall we
ham	terminate our conference for the night?"
ham	"A moment more."
ham	"An hour, if you please."
spam	"Sir," said the nephew, "we have done wrong, and are reaping the fruits
ham	of wrong."
spam	"_We_ have done wrong?" repeated the Marquis, with an inquiring smile,
ham	and delicately pointing, first to his nephew, then to himself.
spam	"Our family; our honourable family, whose honour is of so much account
spam	to both of us, in such different ways. Even in my father's time, we did
spam	a world of wrong, injuring every human creature who came between us and
spam	our pleasure, whatever it was. Why need I speak of my father's time,
spam	when it is equally yours? Can I separate my father's twin-brother, joint
ham	inheritor, and next successor, from himself?"
spam	"Death has done that!" said the Marquis.
ham	"And has left me," answered the nephew, "bound to a system that is
spam	frightful to me, responsible for it, but powerless in it; seeking to
ham	execute the last request of my dear mother's lips, and obey the last
spam	look of my dear mother's eyes, which implored me to have mercy and to
ham	redress; and tortured by seeking assistance and power in vain."
ham	"Seeking them from me, my nephew," said the Marquis, touching him on the
spam	breast with his forefinger--they were now standing by the hearth--"you
ham	will for ever seek them in vain, be assured."
spam	Every fine straight line in the clear whiteness of his face, was
spam	cruelly, craftily, and closely compressed, while he stood looking
ham	quietly at his nephew, with his snuff-box in his hand. Once again he
spam	touched him on the breast, as though his finger were the fine point of
ham	a small sword, with which, in delicate finesse, he ran him through the
ham	body, and said,
ham	"My friend, I will die, perpetuating the system under which I have
ham	lived."
ham	When he had said it, he took a culminating pinch of snuff, and put his
ham	box in his pocket.
ham	"Better to be a rational creature," he added then, after ringing a small
ham	bell on the table, "and accept your natural destiny. But you are lost,
ham	Monsieur Charles, I see."
spam	"This property and France are lost to me," said the nephew, sadly; "I
ham	renounce them."
spam	"Are they both yours to renounce? France may be, but is the property? It
spam	is scarcely worth mentioning; but, is it yet?"
ham	"I had no intention, in the words I used, to claim it yet. If it passed
ham	to me from you, to-morrow--"
spam	"Which I have the vanity to hope is not probable."
spam	"--or twenty years hence--"
spam	"You do me too much honour," said the Marquis; "still, I prefer that
ham	supposition."
spam	"--I would abandon it, and live otherwise and elsewhere. It is little to
spam	relinquish. What is it but a wilderness of misery and ruin!"
spam	"Hah!" said the Marquis, glancing round the luxurious room.
ham	"To the eye it is fair enough, here; but seen in its integrity,
ham	under the sky, and by the daylight, it is a crumbling tower of waste,
spam	mismanagement, extortion, debt, mortgage, oppression, hunger, nakedness,
spam	and suffering."
spam	"Hah!" said the Marquis again, in a well-satisfied manner.
ham	"If it ever becomes mine, it shall be put into some hands better
spam	qualified to free it slowly (if such a thing is possible) from the
ham	weight that drags it down, so that the miserable people who cannot leave
spam	it and who have been long wrung to the last point of endurance, may, in
ham	another generation, suffer less; but it is not for me. There is a curse
ham	on it, and on all this land."
spam	"And you?" said the uncle. "Forgive my curiosity; do you, under your new
spam	philosophy, graciously intend to live?"
ham	"I must do, to live, what others of my countrymen, even with nobility at
ham	their backs, may have to do some day--work."
ham	"In England, for example?"
ham	"Yes. The family honour, sir, is safe from me in this country. The
ham	family name can suffer from me in no other, for I bear it in no other."
ham	The ringing of the bell had caused the adjoining bed-chamber to be
ham	lighted. It now shone brightly, through the door of communication. The
ham	Marquis looked that way, and listened for the retreating step of his
ham	valet.
ham	"England is very attractive to you, seeing how indifferently you have
spam	prospered there," he observed then, turning his calm face to his nephew
spam	with a smile.
ham	"I have already said, that for my prospering there, I am sensible I may
ham	be indebted to you, sir. For the rest, it is my Refuge."
spam	"They say, those boastful English, that it is the Refuge of many. You
spam	know a compatriot who has found a Refuge there? A Doctor?"
spam	"Yes."
spam	"With a daughter?"
spam	"Yes."
ham	"Yes," said the Marquis. "You are fatigued. Good night!"
ham	As he bent his head in his most courtly manner, there was a secrecy
ham	in his smiling face, and he conveyed an air of mystery to those words,
ham	which struck the eyes and ears of his nephew forcibly. At the same
spam	time, the thin straight lines of the setting of the eyes, and the thin
spam	straight lips, and the markings in the nose, curved with a sarcasm that
spam	looked handsomely diabolic.
ham	"Yes," repeated the Marquis. "A Doctor with a daughter. Yes. So
spam	commences the new philosophy! You are fatigued. Good night!"
spam	It would have been of as much avail to interrogate any stone face
spam	outside the chateau as to interrogate that face of his. The nephew
spam	looked at him, in vain, in passing on to the door.
ham	"Good night!" said the uncle. "I look to the pleasure of seeing you
spam	again in the morning. Good repose! Light Monsieur my nephew to his
spam	chamber there!--And burn Monsieur my nephew in his bed, if you will," he
ham	added to himself, before he rang his little bell again, and summoned his
ham	valet to his own bedroom.
spam	The valet come and gone, Monsieur the Marquis walked to and fro in his
spam	loose chamber-robe, to prepare himself gently for sleep, that hot still
ham	night. Rustling about the room, his softly-slippered feet making no
ham	noise on the floor, he moved like a refined tiger:--looked like some
ham	enchanted marquis of the impenitently wicked sort, in story, whose
spam	periodical change into tiger form was either just going off, or just
ham	coming on.
spam	He moved from end to end of his voluptuous bedroom, looking again at the
spam	scraps of the day's journey that came unbidden into his mind; the slow
spam	toil up the hill at sunset, the setting sun, the descent, the mill, the
spam	prison on the crag, the little village in the hollow, the peasants at
ham	the fountain, and the mender of roads with his blue cap pointing out the
spam	chain under the carriage. That fountain suggested the Paris fountain,
ham	the little bundle lying on the step, the women bending over it, and the
ham	tall man with his arms up, crying, "Dead!"
spam	"I am cool now," said Monsieur the Marquis, "and may go to bed."
ham	So, leaving only one light burning on the large hearth, he let his thin
spam	gauze curtains fall around him, and heard the night break its silence
ham	with a long sigh as he composed himself to sleep.
spam	The stone faces on the outer walls stared blindly at the black night
spam	for three heavy hours; for three heavy hours, the horses in the stables
ham	rattled at their racks, the dogs barked, and the owl made a noise with
spam	very little resemblance in it to the noise conventionally assigned to
spam	the owl by men-poets. But it is the obstinate custom of such creatures
spam	hardly ever to say what is set down for them.
spam	For three heavy hours, the stone faces of the chateau, lion and human,
spam	stared blindly at the night. Dead darkness lay on all the landscape,
spam	dead darkness added its own hush to the hushing dust on all the roads.
spam	The burial-place had got to the pass that its little heaps of poor grass
ham	were undistinguishable from one another; the figure on the Cross might
spam	have come down, for anything that could be seen of it. In the village,
spam	taxers and taxed were fast asleep. Dreaming, perhaps, of banquets, as
ham	the starved usually do, and of ease and rest, as the driven slave and
ham	the yoked ox may, its lean inhabitants slept soundly, and were fed and
spam	freed.
spam	The fountain in the village flowed unseen and unheard, and the fountain
spam	at the chateau dropped unseen and unheard--both melting away, like the
ham	minutes that were falling from the spring of Time--through three dark
spam	hours. Then, the grey water of both began to be ghostly in the light,
spam	and the eyes of the stone faces of the chateau were opened.
spam	Lighter and lighter, until at last the sun touched the tops of the still
spam	trees, and poured its radiance over the hill. In the glow, the water
ham	of the chateau fountain seemed to turn to blood, and the stone faces
ham	crimsoned. The carol of the birds was loud and high, and, on the
ham	weather-beaten sill of the great window of the bed-chamber of Monsieur
spam	the Marquis, one little bird sang its sweetest song with all its might.
spam	At this, the nearest stone face seemed to stare amazed, and, with open
ham	mouth and dropped under-jaw, looked awe-stricken.
ham	Now, the sun was full up, and movement began in the village. Casement
ham	windows opened, crazy doors were unbarred, and people came forth
ham	shivering--chilled, as yet, by the new sweet air. Then began the rarely
ham	lightened toil of the day among the village population. Some, to the
ham	fountain; some, to the fields; men and women here, to dig and delve; men
spam	and women there, to see to the poor live stock, and lead the bony cows
spam	out, to such pasture as could be found by the roadside. In the church
ham	and at the Cross, a kneeling figure or two; attendant on the latter
spam	prayers, the led cow, trying for a breakfast among the weeds at its
spam	foot.
spam	The chateau awoke later, as became its quality, but awoke gradually and
ham	surely. First, the lonely boar-spears and knives of the chase had been
ham	reddened as of old; then, had gleamed trenchant in the morning sunshine;
spam	now, doors and windows were thrown open, horses in their stables looked
ham	round over their shoulders at the light and freshness pouring in at
spam	doorways, leaves sparkled and rustled at iron-grated windows, dogs
ham	pulled hard at their chains, and reared impatient to be loosed.
spam	All these trivial incidents belonged to the routine of life, and the
spam	return of morning. Surely, not so the ringing of the great bell of the
ham	chateau, nor the running up and down the stairs; nor the hurried
ham	figures on the terrace; nor the booting and tramping here and there and
ham	everywhere, nor the quick saddling of horses and riding away?
spam	What winds conveyed this hurry to the grizzled mender of roads, already
spam	at work on the hill-top beyond the village, with his day's dinner (not
spam	much to carry) lying in a bundle that it was worth no crow's while to
ham	peck at, on a heap of stones? Had the birds, carrying some grains of it
spam	to a distance, dropped one over him as they sow chance seeds? Whether or
spam	no, the mender of roads ran, on the sultry morning, as if for his life,
spam	down the hill, knee-high in dust, and never stopped till he got to the
spam	fountain.
ham	All the people of the village were at the fountain, standing about
ham	in their depressed manner, and whispering low, but showing no other
spam	emotions than grim curiosity and surprise. The led cows, hastily brought
spam	in and tethered to anything that would hold them, were looking stupidly
spam	on, or lying down chewing the cud of nothing particularly repaying their
ham	trouble, which they had picked up in their interrupted saunter. Some of
spam	the people of the chateau, and some of those of the posting-house, and
ham	all the taxing authorities, were armed more or less, and were crowded
ham	on the other side of the little street in a purposeless way, that was
spam	highly fraught with nothing. Already, the mender of roads had penetrated
spam	into the midst of a group of fifty particular friends, and was smiting
spam	himself in the breast with his blue cap. What did all this portend,
spam	and what portended the swift hoisting-up of Monsieur Gabelle behind
spam	a servant on horseback, and the conveying away of the said Gabelle
ham	(double-laden though the horse was), at a gallop, like a new version of
ham	the German ballad of Leonora?
spam	It portended that there was one stone face too many, up at the chateau.
spam	The Gorgon had surveyed the building again in the night, and had added
spam	the one stone face wanting; the stone face for which it had waited
spam	through about two hundred years.
spam	It lay back on the pillow of Monsieur the Marquis. It was like a fine
spam	mask, suddenly startled, made angry, and petrified. Driven home into the
ham	heart of the stone figure attached to it, was a knife. Round its hilt
ham	was a frill of paper, on which was scrawled:
ham	"Drive him fast to his tomb. This, from Jacques."
spam	X. Two Promises
ham	More months, to the number of twelve, had come and gone, and Mr. Charles
ham	Darnay was established in England as a higher teacher of the French
spam	language who was conversant with French literature. In this age, he
ham	would have been a Professor; in that age, he was a Tutor. He read with
ham	young men who could find any leisure and interest for the study of a
ham	living tongue spoken all over the world, and he cultivated a taste for
ham	its stores of knowledge and fancy. He could write of them, besides, in
ham	sound English, and render them into sound English. Such masters were not
ham	at that time easily found; Princes that had been, and Kings that were
ham	to be, were not yet of the Teacher class, and no ruined nobility had
spam	dropped out of Tellson's ledgers, to turn cooks and carpenters. As a
ham	tutor, whose attainments made the student's way unusually pleasant and
ham	profitable, and as an elegant translator who brought something to his
spam	work besides mere dictionary knowledge, young Mr. Darnay soon became
spam	known and encouraged. He was well acquainted, more-over, with the
ham	circumstances of his country, and those were of ever-growing interest.
ham	So, with great perseverance and untiring industry, he prospered.
ham	In London, he had expected neither to walk on pavements of gold, nor
ham	to lie on beds of roses; if he had had any such exalted expectation, he
ham	would not have prospered. He had expected labour, and he found it, and
ham	did it and made the best of it. In this, his prosperity consisted.
ham	A certain portion of his time was passed at Cambridge, where he
ham	read with undergraduates as a sort of tolerated smuggler who drove a
ham	contraband trade in European languages, instead of conveying Greek
spam	and Latin through the Custom-house. The rest of his time he passed in
spam	London.
spam	Now, from the days when it was always summer in Eden, to these days
spam	when it is mostly winter in fallen latitudes, the world of a man has
spam	invariably gone one way--Charles Darnay's way--the way of the love of a
ham	woman.
spam	He had loved Lucie Manette from the hour of his danger. He had never
spam	heard a sound so sweet and dear as the sound of her compassionate voice;
spam	he had never seen a face so tenderly beautiful, as hers when it was
ham	confronted with his own on the edge of the grave that had been dug for
ham	him. But, he had not yet spoken to her on the subject; the assassination
spam	at the deserted chateau far away beyond the heaving water and the long,
ham	long, dusty roads--the solid stone chateau which had itself become the
spam	mere mist of a dream--had been done a year, and he had never yet, by so
spam	much as a single spoken word, disclosed to her the state of his heart.
ham	That he had his reasons for this, he knew full well. It was again a
ham	summer day when, lately arrived in London from his college occupation,
ham	he turned into the quiet corner in Soho, bent on seeking an opportunity
ham	of opening his mind to Doctor Manette. It was the close of the summer
spam	day, and he knew Lucie to be out with Miss Pross.
ham	He found the Doctor reading in his arm-chair at a window. The energy
ham	which had at once supported him under his old sufferings and aggravated
ham	their sharpness, had been gradually restored to him. He was now a
spam	very energetic man indeed, with great firmness of purpose, strength
ham	of resolution, and vigour of action. In his recovered energy he was
ham	sometimes a little fitful and sudden, as he had at first been in the
spam	exercise of his other recovered faculties; but, this had never been
ham	frequently observable, and had grown more and more rare.
ham	He studied much, slept little, sustained a great deal of fatigue with
ham	ease, and was equably cheerful. To him, now entered Charles Darnay, at
spam	sight of whom he laid aside his book and held out his hand.
ham	"Charles Darnay! I rejoice to see you. We have been counting on your
ham	return these three or four days past. Mr. Stryver and Sydney Carton were
spam	both here yesterday, and both made you out to be more than due."
ham	"I am obliged to them for their interest in the matter," he answered,
spam	a little coldly as to them, though very warmly as to the Doctor. "Miss
ham	Manette--"
spam	"Is well," said the Doctor, as he stopped short, "and your return will
spam	delight us all. She has gone out on some household matters, but will
ham	soon be home."
spam	"Doctor Manette, I knew she was from home. I took the opportunity of her
spam	being from home, to beg to speak to you."
ham	There was a blank silence.
spam	"Yes?" said the Doctor, with evident constraint. "Bring your chair here,
spam	and speak on."
spam	He complied as to the chair, but appeared to find the speaking on less
spam	easy.
ham	"I have had the happiness, Doctor Manette, of being so intimate here,"
spam	so he at length began, "for some year and a half, that I hope the topic
ham	on which I am about to touch may not--"
spam	He was stayed by the Doctor's putting out his hand to stop him. When he
ham	had kept it so a little while, he said, drawing it back:
spam	"Is Lucie the topic?"
spam	"She is."
spam	"It is hard for me to speak of her at any time. It is very hard for me
spam	to hear her spoken of in that tone of yours, Charles Darnay."
ham	"It is a tone of fervent admiration, true homage, and deep love, Doctor
spam	Manette!" he said deferentially.
ham	There was another blank silence before her father rejoined:
spam	"I believe it. I do you justice; I believe it."
ham	His constraint was so manifest, and it was so manifest, too, that it
ham	originated in an unwillingness to approach the subject, that Charles
spam	Darnay hesitated.
spam	"Shall I go on, sir?"
ham	Another blank.
ham	"Yes, go on."
ham	"You anticipate what I would say, though you cannot know how earnestly
ham	I say it, how earnestly I feel it, without knowing my secret heart, and
spam	the hopes and fears and anxieties with which it has long been
ham	laden. Dear Doctor Manette, I love your daughter fondly, dearly,
spam	disinterestedly, devotedly. If ever there were love in the world, I love
ham	her. You have loved yourself; let your old love speak for me!"
spam	The Doctor sat with his face turned away, and his eyes bent on the
ham	ground. At the last words, he stretched out his hand again, hurriedly,
ham	and cried:
ham	"Not that, sir! Let that be! I adjure you, do not recall that!"
spam	His cry was so like a cry of actual pain, that it rang in Charles
ham	Darnay's ears long after he had ceased. He motioned with the hand he had
spam	extended, and it seemed to be an appeal to Darnay to pause. The latter
ham	so received it, and remained silent.
spam	"I ask your pardon," said the Doctor, in a subdued tone, after some
spam	moments. "I do not doubt your loving Lucie; you may be satisfied of it."
spam	He turned towards him in his chair, but did not look at him, or
ham	raise his eyes. His chin dropped upon his hand, and his white hair
ham	overshadowed his face:
ham	"Have you spoken to Lucie?"
ham	"No."
spam	"Nor written?"
ham	"Never."
spam	"It would be ungenerous to affect not to know that your self-denial is
ham	to be referred to your consideration for her father. Her father thanks
spam	you."
ham	He offered his hand; but his eyes did not go with it.
ham	"I know," said Darnay, respectfully, "how can I fail to know, Doctor
ham	Manette, I who have seen you together from day to day, that between
ham	you and Miss Manette there is an affection so unusual, so touching, so
spam	belonging to the circumstances in which it has been nurtured, that it
spam	can have few parallels, even in the tenderness between a father and
ham	child. I know, Doctor Manette--how can I fail to know--that, mingled
spam	with the affection and duty of a daughter who has become a woman, there
ham	is, in her heart, towards you, all the love and reliance of infancy
ham	itself. I know that, as in her childhood she had no parent, so she is
spam	now devoted to you with all the constancy and fervour of her present
ham	years and character, united to the trustfulness and attachment of the
spam	early days in which you were lost to her. I know perfectly well that if
spam	you had been restored to her from the world beyond this life, you could
spam	hardly be invested, in her sight, with a more sacred character than that
ham	in which you are always with her. I know that when she is clinging to
ham	you, the hands of baby, girl, and woman, all in one, are round your
spam	neck. I know that in loving you she sees and loves her mother at her
ham	own age, sees and loves you at my age, loves her mother broken-hearted,
ham	loves you through your dreadful trial and in your blessed restoration. I
spam	have known this, night and day, since I have known you in your home."
spam	Her father sat silent, with his face bent down. His breathing was a
ham	little quickened; but he repressed all other signs of agitation.
ham	"Dear Doctor Manette, always knowing this, always seeing her and you
ham	with this hallowed light about you, I have forborne, and forborne, as
ham	long as it was in the nature of man to do it. I have felt, and do even
ham	now feel, that to bring my love--even mine--between you, is to touch
spam	your history with something not quite so good as itself. But I love her.
ham	Heaven is my witness that I love her!"
ham	"I believe it," answered her father, mournfully. "I have thought so
ham	before now. I believe it."
ham	"But, do not believe," said Darnay, upon whose ear the mournful voice
spam	struck with a reproachful sound, "that if my fortune were so cast as
ham	that, being one day so happy as to make her my wife, I must at any time
spam	put any separation between her and you, I could or would breathe a
ham	word of what I now say. Besides that I should know it to be hopeless, I
ham	should know it to be a baseness. If I had any such possibility, even at
spam	a remote distance of years, harboured in my thoughts, and hidden in my
spam	heart--if it ever had been there--if it ever could be there--I could not
ham	now touch this honoured hand."
spam	He laid his own upon it as he spoke.
ham	"No, dear Doctor Manette. Like you, a voluntary exile from France; like
ham	you, driven from it by its distractions, oppressions, and miseries; like
ham	you, striving to live away from it by my own exertions, and trusting
spam	in a happier future; I look only to sharing your fortunes, sharing your
spam	life and home, and being faithful to you to the death. Not to divide
ham	with Lucie her privilege as your child, companion, and friend; but to
ham	come in aid of it, and bind her closer to you, if such a thing can be."
spam	His touch still lingered on her father's hand. Answering the touch for a
spam	moment, but not coldly, her father rested his hands upon the arms of
spam	his chair, and looked up for the first time since the beginning of the
spam	conference. A struggle was evidently in his face; a struggle with that
spam	occasional look which had a tendency in it to dark doubt and dread.
spam	"You speak so feelingly and so manfully, Charles Darnay, that I thank
spam	you with all my heart, and will open all my heart--or nearly so. Have
ham	you any reason to believe that Lucie loves you?"
ham	"None. As yet, none."
ham	"Is it the immediate object of this confidence, that you may at once
ham	ascertain that, with my knowledge?"
spam	"Not even so. I might not have the hopefulness to do it for weeks; I
ham	might (mistaken or not mistaken) have that hopefulness to-morrow."
ham	"Do you seek any guidance from me?"
spam	"I ask none, sir. But I have thought it possible that you might have it
spam	in your power, if you should deem it right, to give me some."
spam	"Do you seek any promise from me?"
ham	"I do seek that."
ham	"What is it?"
ham	"I well understand that, without you, I could have no hope. I well
ham	understand that, even if Miss Manette held me at this moment in her
spam	innocent heart--do not think I have the presumption to assume so much--I
spam	could retain no place in it against her love for her father."
ham	"If that be so, do you see what, on the other hand, is involved in it?"
ham	"I understand equally well, that a word from her father in any suitor's
spam	favour, would outweigh herself and all the world. For which reason,
ham	Doctor Manette," said Darnay, modestly but firmly, "I would not ask that
ham	word, to save my life."
spam	"I am sure of it. Charles Darnay, mysteries arise out of close love, as
spam	well as out of wide division; in the former case, they are subtle and
ham	delicate, and difficult to penetrate. My daughter Lucie is, in this one
ham	respect, such a mystery to me; I can make no guess at the state of her
spam	heart."
spam	"May I ask, sir, if you think she is--" As he hesitated, her father
ham	supplied the rest.
spam	"Is sought by any other suitor?"
ham	"It is what I meant to say."
spam	Her father considered a little before he answered:
spam	"You have seen Mr. Carton here, yourself. Mr. Stryver is here too,
spam	occasionally. If it be at all, it can only be by one of these."
ham	"Or both," said Darnay.
ham	"I had not thought of both; I should not think either, likely. You want
spam	a promise from me. Tell me what it is."
ham	"It is, that if Miss Manette should bring to you at any time, on her own
spam	part, such a confidence as I have ventured to lay before you, you will
ham	bear testimony to what I have said, and to your belief in it. I hope you
spam	may be able to think so well of me, as to urge no influence against
ham	me. I say nothing more of my stake in this; this is what I ask. The
spam	condition on which I ask it, and which you have an undoubted right to
spam	require, I will observe immediately."
spam	"I give the promise," said the Doctor, "without any condition. I believe
spam	your object to be, purely and truthfully, as you have stated it. I
ham	believe your intention is to perpetuate, and not to weaken, the ties
ham	between me and my other and far dearer self. If she should ever tell me
spam	that you are essential to her perfect happiness, I will give her to you.
ham	If there were--Charles Darnay, if there were--"
ham	The young man had taken his hand gratefully; their hands were joined as
ham	the Doctor spoke:
ham	"--any fancies, any reasons, any apprehensions, anything whatsoever,
ham	new or old, against the man she really loved--the direct responsibility
ham	thereof not lying on his head--they should all be obliterated for her
spam	sake. She is everything to me; more to me than suffering, more to me
spam	than wrong, more to me--Well! This is idle talk."
ham	So strange was the way in which he faded into silence, and so strange
spam	his fixed look when he had ceased to speak, that Darnay felt his own
ham	hand turn cold in the hand that slowly released and dropped it.
spam	"You said something to me," said Doctor Manette, breaking into a smile.
spam	"What was it you said to me?"
ham	He was at a loss how to answer, until he remembered having spoken of a
spam	condition. Relieved as his mind reverted to that, he answered:
ham	"Your confidence in me ought to be returned with full confidence on my
spam	part. My present name, though but slightly changed from my mother's, is
spam	not, as you will remember, my own. I wish to tell you what that is, and
ham	why I am in England."
ham	"Stop!" said the Doctor of Beauvais.
spam	"I wish it, that I may the better deserve your confidence, and have no
ham	secret from you."
spam	"Stop!"
spam	For an instant, the Doctor even had his two hands at his ears; for
spam	another instant, even had his two hands laid on Darnay's lips.
ham	"Tell me when I ask you, not now. If your suit should prosper, if Lucie
spam	should love you, you shall tell me on your marriage morning. Do you
ham	promise?"
ham	"Willingly.
ham	"Give me your hand. She will be home directly, and it is better she
ham	should not see us together to-night. Go! God bless you!"
spam	It was dark when Charles Darnay left him, and it was an hour later and
spam	darker when Lucie came home; she hurried into the room alone--for
ham	Miss Pross had gone straight up-stairs--and was surprised to find his
ham	reading-chair empty.
ham	"My father!" she called to him. "Father dear!"
spam	Nothing was said in answer, but she heard a low hammering sound in his
spam	bedroom. Passing lightly across the intermediate room, she looked in at
ham	his door and came running back frightened, crying to herself, with her
spam	blood all chilled, "What shall I do! What shall I do!"
ham	Her uncertainty lasted but a moment; she hurried back, and tapped at
spam	his door, and softly called to him. The noise ceased at the sound of
spam	her voice, and he presently came out to her, and they walked up and down
ham	together for a long time.
ham	She came down from her bed, to look at him in his sleep that night. He
ham	slept heavily, and his tray of shoemaking tools, and his old unfinished
ham	work, were all as usual.
ham	XI. A Companion Picture
spam	"Sydney," said Mr. Stryver, on that self-same night, or morning, to his
ham	jackal; "mix another bowl of punch; I have something to say to you."
spam	Sydney had been working double tides that night, and the night before,
spam	and the night before that, and a good many nights in succession, making
ham	a grand clearance among Mr. Stryver's papers before the setting in
ham	of the long vacation. The clearance was effected at last; the Stryver
ham	arrears were handsomely fetched up; everything was got rid of until
spam	November should come with its fogs atmospheric, and fogs legal, and
ham	bring grist to the mill again.
spam	Sydney was none the livelier and none the soberer for so much
spam	application. It had taken a deal of extra wet-towelling to pull him
ham	through the night; a correspondingly extra quantity of wine had preceded
ham	the towelling; and he was in a very damaged condition, as he now pulled
spam	his turban off and threw it into the basin in which he had steeped it at
ham	intervals for the last six hours.
ham	"Are you mixing that other bowl of punch?" said Stryver the portly, with
spam	his hands in his waistband, glancing round from the sofa where he lay on
spam	his back.
ham	"I am."
ham	"Now, look here! I am going to tell you something that will rather
ham	surprise you, and that perhaps will make you think me not quite as
ham	shrewd as you usually do think me. I intend to marry."
ham	"_Do_ you?"
ham	"Yes. And not for money. What do you say now?"
spam	"I don't feel disposed to say much. Who is she?"
spam	"Guess."
ham	"Do I know her?"
spam	"Guess."
spam	"I am not going to guess, at five o'clock in the morning, with my brains
spam	frying and sputtering in my head. If you want me to guess, you must ask
spam	me to dinner."
spam	"Well then, I'll tell you," said Stryver, coming slowly into a sitting
spam	posture. "Sydney, I rather despair of making myself intelligible to you,
spam	because you are such an insensible dog."
ham	"And you," returned Sydney, busy concocting the punch, "are such a
spam	sensitive and poetical spirit--"
ham	"Come!" rejoined Stryver, laughing boastfully, "though I don't prefer
spam	any claim to being the soul of Romance (for I hope I know better), still
spam	I am a tenderer sort of fellow than _you_."
spam	"You are a luckier, if you mean that."
ham	"I don't mean that. I mean I am a man of more--more--"
spam	"Say gallantry, while you are about it," suggested Carton.
ham	"Well! I'll say gallantry. My meaning is that I am a man," said Stryver,
spam	inflating himself at his friend as he made the punch, "who cares more to
spam	be agreeable, who takes more pains to be agreeable, who knows better how
ham	to be agreeable, in a woman's society, than you do."
spam	"Go on," said Sydney Carton.
spam	"No; but before I go on," said Stryver, shaking his head in his bullying
spam	way, "I'll have this out with you. You've been at Doctor Manette's house
spam	as much as I have, or more than I have. Why, I have been ashamed of your
ham	moroseness there! Your manners have been of that silent and sullen and
ham	hangdog kind, that, upon my life and soul, I have been ashamed of you,
ham	Sydney!"
ham	"It should be very beneficial to a man in your practice at the bar, to
spam	be ashamed of anything," returned Sydney; "you ought to be much obliged
ham	to me."
ham	"You shall not get off in that way," rejoined Stryver, shouldering the
spam	rejoinder at him; "no, Sydney, it's my duty to tell you--and I tell you
spam	to your face to do you good--that you are a devilish ill-conditioned
ham	fellow in that sort of society. You are a disagreeable fellow."
spam	Sydney drank a bumper of the punch he had made, and laughed.
spam	"Look at me!" said Stryver, squaring himself; "I have less need to make
ham	myself agreeable than you have, being more independent in circumstances.
ham	Why do I do it?"
spam	"I never saw you do it yet," muttered Carton.
ham	"I do it because it's politic; I do it on principle. And look at me! I
ham	get on."
ham	"You don't get on with your account of your matrimonial intentions,"
ham	answered Carton, with a careless air; "I wish you would keep to that. As
spam	to me--will you never understand that I am incorrigible?"
ham	He asked the question with some appearance of scorn.
ham	"You have no business to be incorrigible," was his friend's answer,
ham	delivered in no very soothing tone.
spam	"I have no business to be, at all, that I know of," said Sydney Carton.
spam	"Who is the lady?"
ham	"Now, don't let my announcement of the name make you uncomfortable,
ham	Sydney," said Mr. Stryver, preparing him with ostentatious friendliness
spam	for the disclosure he was about to make, "because I know you don't mean
spam	half you say; and if you meant it all, it would be of no importance. I
ham	make this little preface, because you once mentioned the young lady to
spam	me in slighting terms."
ham	"I did?"
spam	"Certainly; and in these chambers."
spam	Sydney Carton looked at his punch and looked at his complacent friend;
spam	drank his punch and looked at his complacent friend.
ham	"You made mention of the young lady as a golden-haired doll. The young
ham	lady is Miss Manette. If you had been a fellow of any sensitiveness or
ham	delicacy of feeling in that kind of way, Sydney, I might have been a
spam	little resentful of your employing such a designation; but you are not.
ham	You want that sense altogether; therefore I am no more annoyed when I
ham	think of the expression, than I should be annoyed by a man's opinion of
ham	a picture of mine, who had no eye for pictures: or of a piece of music
spam	of mine, who had no ear for music."
spam	Sydney Carton drank the punch at a great rate; drank it by bumpers,
ham	looking at his friend.
spam	"Now you know all about it, Syd," said Mr. Stryver. "I don't care about
spam	fortune: she is a charming creature, and I have made up my mind to
ham	please myself: on the whole, I think I can afford to please myself. She
ham	will have in me a man already pretty well off, and a rapidly rising man,
ham	and a man of some distinction: it is a piece of good fortune for her,
ham	but she is worthy of good fortune. Are you astonished?"
spam	Carton, still drinking the punch, rejoined, "Why should I be
ham	astonished?"
ham	"You approve?"
ham	Carton, still drinking the punch, rejoined, "Why should I not approve?"
spam	"Well!" said his friend Stryver, "you take it more easily than I fancied
ham	you would, and are less mercenary on my behalf than I thought you would
spam	be; though, to be sure, you know well enough by this time that your
ham	ancient chum is a man of a pretty strong will. Yes, Sydney, I have had
ham	enough of this style of life, with no other as a change from it; I
spam	feel that it is a pleasant thing for a man to have a home when he feels
spam	inclined to go to it (when he doesn't, he can stay away), and I feel
ham	that Miss Manette will tell well in any station, and will always do me
spam	credit. So I have made up my mind. And now, Sydney, old boy, I want to
spam	say a word to _you_ about _your_ prospects. You are in a bad way, you
spam	know; you really are in a bad way. You don't know the value of money,
spam	you live hard, you'll knock up one of these days, and be ill and poor;
spam	you really ought to think about a nurse."
ham	The prosperous patronage with which he said it, made him look twice as
spam	big as he was, and four times as offensive.
spam	"Now, let me recommend you," pursued Stryver, "to look it in the face.
ham	I have looked it in the face, in my different way; look it in the face,
ham	you, in your different way. Marry. Provide somebody to take care of
ham	you. Never mind your having no enjoyment of women's society, nor
spam	understanding of it, nor tact for it. Find out somebody. Find out some
spam	respectable woman with a little property--somebody in the landlady way,
spam	or lodging-letting way--and marry her, against a rainy day. That's the
spam	kind of thing for _you_. Now think of it, Sydney."
ham	"I'll think of it," said Sydney.
spam	XII. The Fellow of Delicacy
spam	Mr. Stryver having made up his mind to that magnanimous bestowal of good
ham	fortune on the Doctor's daughter, resolved to make her happiness known
ham	to her before he left town for the Long Vacation. After some mental
spam	debating of the point, he came to the conclusion that it would be as
spam	well to get all the preliminaries done with, and they could then arrange
ham	at their leisure whether he should give her his hand a week or two
spam	before Michaelmas Term, or in the little Christmas vacation between it
spam	and Hilary.
ham	As to the strength of his case, he had not a doubt about it, but clearly
ham	saw his way to the verdict. Argued with the jury on substantial worldly
ham	grounds--the only grounds ever worth taking into account--it was a
spam	plain case, and had not a weak spot in it. He called himself for the
spam	plaintiff, there was no getting over his evidence, the counsel for
ham	the defendant threw up his brief, and the jury did not even turn to
ham	consider. After trying it, Stryver, C. J., was satisfied that no plainer
ham	case could be.
spam	Accordingly, Mr. Stryver inaugurated the Long Vacation with a formal
spam	proposal to take Miss Manette to Vauxhall Gardens; that failing, to
spam	Ranelagh; that unaccountably failing too, it behoved him to present
ham	himself in Soho, and there declare his noble mind.
spam	Towards Soho, therefore, Mr. Stryver shouldered his way from the Temple,
ham	while the bloom of the Long Vacation's infancy was still upon it.
spam	Anybody who had seen him projecting himself into Soho while he was yet
ham	on Saint Dunstan's side of Temple Bar, bursting in his full-blown way
spam	along the pavement, to the jostlement of all weaker people, might have
spam	seen how safe and strong he was.
ham	His way taking him past Tellson's, and he both banking at Tellson's and
spam	knowing Mr. Lorry as the intimate friend of the Manettes, it entered Mr.
ham	Stryver's mind to enter the bank, and reveal to Mr. Lorry the brightness
ham	of the Soho horizon. So, he pushed open the door with the weak rattle
spam	in its throat, stumbled down the two steps, got past the two ancient
ham	cashiers, and shouldered himself into the musty back closet where Mr.
ham	Lorry sat at great books ruled for figures, with perpendicular iron
ham	bars to his window as if that were ruled for figures too, and everything
spam	under the clouds were a sum.
ham	"Halloa!" said Mr. Stryver. "How do you do? I hope you are well!"
ham	It was Stryver's grand peculiarity that he always seemed too big for any
ham	place, or space. He was so much too big for Tellson's, that old clerks
spam	in distant corners looked up with looks of remonstrance, as though he
ham	squeezed them against the wall. The House itself, magnificently reading
ham	the paper quite in the far-off perspective, lowered displeased, as if
spam	the Stryver head had been butted into its responsible waistcoat.
spam	The discreet Mr. Lorry said, in a sample tone of the voice he would
spam	recommend under the circumstances, "How do you do, Mr. Stryver? How do
ham	you do, sir?" and shook hands. There was a peculiarity in his manner
spam	of shaking hands, always to be seen in any clerk at Tellson's who shook
ham	hands with a customer when the House pervaded the air. He shook in a
ham	self-abnegating way, as one who shook for Tellson and Co.
ham	"Can I do anything for you, Mr. Stryver?" asked Mr. Lorry, in his
ham	business character.
spam	"Why, no, thank you; this is a private visit to yourself, Mr. Lorry; I
spam	have come for a private word."
ham	"Oh indeed!" said Mr. Lorry, bending down his ear, while his eye strayed
spam	to the House afar off.
spam	"I am going," said Mr. Stryver, leaning his arms confidentially on the
spam	desk: whereupon, although it was a large double one, there appeared to
spam	be not half desk enough for him: "I am going to make an offer of myself
spam	in marriage to your agreeable little friend, Miss Manette, Mr. Lorry."
ham	"Oh dear me!" cried Mr. Lorry, rubbing his chin, and looking at his
spam	visitor dubiously.
spam	"Oh dear me, sir?" repeated Stryver, drawing back. "Oh dear you, sir?
spam	What may your meaning be, Mr. Lorry?"
spam	"My meaning," answered the man of business, "is, of course, friendly and
spam	appreciative, and that it does you the greatest credit, and--in short,
spam	my meaning is everything you could desire. But--really, you know, Mr.
ham	Stryver--" Mr. Lorry paused, and shook his head at him in the oddest
ham	manner, as if he were compelled against his will to add, internally,
ham	"you know there really is so much too much of you!"
ham	"Well!" said Stryver, slapping the desk with his contentious hand,
spam	opening his eyes wider, and taking a long breath, "if I understand you,
ham	Mr. Lorry, I'll be hanged!"
ham	Mr. Lorry adjusted his little wig at both ears as a means towards that
ham	end, and bit the feather of a pen.
spam	"D--n it all, sir!" said Stryver, staring at him, "am I not eligible?"
spam	"Oh dear yes! Yes. Oh yes, you're eligible!" said Mr. Lorry. "If you say
ham	eligible, you are eligible."
ham	"Am I not prosperous?" asked Stryver.
ham	"Oh! if you come to prosperous, you are prosperous," said Mr. Lorry.
spam	"And advancing?"
ham	"If you come to advancing you know," said Mr. Lorry, delighted to be
spam	able to make another admission, "nobody can doubt that."
ham	"Then what on earth is your meaning, Mr. Lorry?" demanded Stryver,
ham	perceptibly crestfallen.
ham	"Well! I--Were you going there now?" asked Mr. Lorry.
spam	"Straight!" said Stryver, with a plump of his fist on the desk.
spam	"Then I think I wouldn't, if I was you."
spam	"Why?" said Stryver. "Now, I'll put you in a corner," forensically
ham	shaking a forefinger at him. "You are a man of business and bound to
ham	have a reason. State your reason. Why wouldn't you go?"
spam	"Because," said Mr. Lorry, "I wouldn't go on such an object without
ham	having some cause to believe that I should succeed."
ham	"D--n _me_!" cried Stryver, "but this beats everything."
ham	Mr. Lorry glanced at the distant House, and glanced at the angry
ham	Stryver.
spam	"Here's a man of business--a man of years--a man of experience--_in_
ham	a Bank," said Stryver; "and having summed up three leading reasons for
ham	complete success, he says there's no reason at all! Says it with his
ham	head on!" Mr. Stryver remarked upon the peculiarity as if it would have
ham	been infinitely less remarkable if he had said it with his head off.
ham	"When I speak of success, I speak of success with the young lady; and
spam	when I speak of causes and reasons to make success probable, I speak of
ham	causes and reasons that will tell as such with the young lady. The young
ham	lady, my good sir," said Mr. Lorry, mildly tapping the Stryver arm, "the
ham	young lady. The young lady goes before all."
spam	"Then you mean to tell me, Mr. Lorry," said Stryver, squaring his
spam	elbows, "that it is your deliberate opinion that the young lady at
spam	present in question is a mincing Fool?"
spam	"Not exactly so. I mean to tell you, Mr. Stryver," said Mr. Lorry,
spam	reddening, "that I will hear no disrespectful word of that young lady
ham	from any lips; and that if I knew any man--which I hope I do not--whose
spam	taste was so coarse, and whose temper was so overbearing, that he could
ham	not restrain himself from speaking disrespectfully of that young lady at
spam	this desk, not even Tellson's should prevent my giving him a piece of my
ham	mind."
spam	The necessity of being angry in a suppressed tone had put Mr. Stryver's
ham	blood-vessels into a dangerous state when it was his turn to be angry;
ham	Mr. Lorry's veins, methodical as their courses could usually be, were in
spam	no better state now it was his turn.
ham	"That is what I mean to tell you, sir," said Mr. Lorry. "Pray let there
spam	be no mistake about it."
spam	Mr. Stryver sucked the end of a ruler for a little while, and then stood
spam	hitting a tune out of his teeth with it, which probably gave him the
spam	toothache. He broke the awkward silence by saying:
spam	"This is something new to me, Mr. Lorry. You deliberately advise me not
spam	to go up to Soho and offer myself--_my_self, Stryver of the King's Bench
spam	bar?"
ham	"Do you ask me for my advice, Mr. Stryver?"
ham	"Yes, I do."
