ham	"Very good. Then I give it, and you have repeated it correctly."
ham	"And all I can say of it is," laughed Stryver with a vexed laugh, "that
spam	this--ha, ha!--beats everything past, present, and to come."
spam	"Now understand me," pursued Mr. Lorry. "As a man of business, I am
ham	not justified in saying anything about this matter, for, as a man of
spam	business, I know nothing of it. But, as an old fellow, who has carried
ham	Miss Manette in his arms, who is the trusted friend of Miss Manette and
spam	of her father too, and who has a great affection for them both, I have
spam	spoken. The confidence is not of my seeking, recollect. Now, you think I
spam	may not be right?"
spam	"Not I!" said Stryver, whistling. "I can't undertake to find third
ham	parties in common sense; I can only find it for myself. I suppose sense
spam	in certain quarters; you suppose mincing bread-and-butter nonsense. It's
ham	new to me, but you are right, I dare say."
spam	"What I suppose, Mr. Stryver, I claim to characterise for myself--And
ham	understand me, sir," said Mr. Lorry, quickly flushing again, "I
spam	will not--not even at Tellson's--have it characterised for me by any
ham	gentleman breathing."
ham	"There! I beg your pardon!" said Stryver.
ham	"Granted. Thank you. Well, Mr. Stryver, I was about to say:--it might be
ham	painful to you to find yourself mistaken, it might be painful to Doctor
spam	Manette to have the task of being explicit with you, it might be very
ham	painful to Miss Manette to have the task of being explicit with you. You
ham	know the terms upon which I have the honour and happiness to stand with
ham	the family. If you please, committing you in no way, representing you
spam	in no way, I will undertake to correct my advice by the exercise of a
ham	little new observation and judgment expressly brought to bear upon
spam	it. If you should then be dissatisfied with it, you can but test its
ham	soundness for yourself; if, on the other hand, you should be satisfied
spam	with it, and it should be what it now is, it may spare all sides what is
spam	best spared. What do you say?"
ham	"How long would you keep me in town?"
spam	"Oh! It is only a question of a few hours. I could go to Soho in the
ham	evening, and come to your chambers afterwards."
spam	"Then I say yes," said Stryver: "I won't go up there now, I am not so
spam	hot upon it as that comes to; I say yes, and I shall expect you to look
ham	in to-night. Good morning."
ham	Then Mr. Stryver turned and burst out of the Bank, causing such a
spam	concussion of air on his passage through, that to stand up against it
spam	bowing behind the two counters, required the utmost remaining strength
ham	of the two ancient clerks. Those venerable and feeble persons were
spam	always seen by the public in the act of bowing, and were popularly
spam	believed, when they had bowed a customer out, still to keep on bowing in
ham	the empty office until they bowed another customer in.
ham	The barrister was keen enough to divine that the banker would not have
ham	gone so far in his expression of opinion on any less solid ground than
spam	moral certainty. Unprepared as he was for the large pill he had to
ham	swallow, he got it down. "And now," said Mr. Stryver, shaking his
spam	forensic forefinger at the Temple in general, when it was down, "my way
spam	out of this, is, to put you all in the wrong."
ham	It was a bit of the art of an Old Bailey tactician, in which he found
spam	great relief. "You shall not put me in the wrong, young lady," said Mr.
spam	Stryver; "I'll do that for you."
ham	Accordingly, when Mr. Lorry called that night as late as ten o'clock,
ham	Mr. Stryver, among a quantity of books and papers littered out for the
spam	purpose, seemed to have nothing less on his mind than the subject of
ham	the morning. He even showed surprise when he saw Mr. Lorry, and was
ham	altogether in an absent and preoccupied state.
ham	"Well!" said that good-natured emissary, after a full half-hour of
ham	bootless attempts to bring him round to the question. "I have been to
spam	Soho."
ham	"To Soho?" repeated Mr. Stryver, coldly. "Oh, to be sure! What am I
spam	thinking of!"
spam	"And I have no doubt," said Mr. Lorry, "that I was right in the
ham	conversation we had. My opinion is confirmed, and I reiterate my
ham	advice."
ham	"I assure you," returned Mr. Stryver, in the friendliest way, "that I
spam	am sorry for it on your account, and sorry for it on the poor father's
spam	account. I know this must always be a sore subject with the family; let
spam	us say no more about it."
spam	"I don't understand you," said Mr. Lorry.
spam	"I dare say not," rejoined Stryver, nodding his head in a smoothing and
ham	final way; "no matter, no matter."
ham	"But it does matter," Mr. Lorry urged.
ham	"No it doesn't; I assure you it doesn't. Having supposed that there was
spam	sense where there is no sense, and a laudable ambition where there is
ham	not a laudable ambition, I am well out of my mistake, and no harm is
ham	done. Young women have committed similar follies often before, and have
ham	repented them in poverty and obscurity often before. In an unselfish
ham	aspect, I am sorry that the thing is dropped, because it would have been
ham	a bad thing for me in a worldly point of view; in a selfish aspect, I am
ham	glad that the thing has dropped, because it would have been a bad thing
spam	for me in a worldly point of view--it is hardly necessary to say I could
spam	have gained nothing by it. There is no harm at all done. I have not
spam	proposed to the young lady, and, between ourselves, I am by no means
ham	certain, on reflection, that I ever should have committed myself to
ham	that extent. Mr. Lorry, you cannot control the mincing vanities and
spam	giddinesses of empty-headed girls; you must not expect to do it, or you
ham	will always be disappointed. Now, pray say no more about it. I tell you,
spam	I regret it on account of others, but I am satisfied on my own account.
ham	And I am really very much obliged to you for allowing me to sound you,
spam	and for giving me your advice; you know the young lady better than I do;
ham	you were right, it never would have done."
ham	Mr. Lorry was so taken aback, that he looked quite stupidly at Mr.
ham	Stryver shouldering him towards the door, with an appearance of
spam	showering generosity, forbearance, and goodwill, on his erring head.
ham	"Make the best of it, my dear sir," said Stryver; "say no more about it;
ham	thank you again for allowing me to sound you; good night!"
spam	Mr. Lorry was out in the night, before he knew where he was. Mr. Stryver
spam	was lying back on his sofa, winking at his ceiling.
spam	XIII. The Fellow of No Delicacy
ham	If Sydney Carton ever shone anywhere, he certainly never shone in the
spam	house of Doctor Manette. He had been there often, during a whole year,
ham	and had always been the same moody and morose lounger there. When he
spam	cared to talk, he talked well; but, the cloud of caring for nothing,
spam	which overshadowed him with such a fatal darkness, was very rarely
ham	pierced by the light within him.
ham	And yet he did care something for the streets that environed that house,
spam	and for the senseless stones that made their pavements. Many a night
ham	he vaguely and unhappily wandered there, when wine had brought no
ham	transitory gladness to him; many a dreary daybreak revealed his solitary
spam	figure lingering there, and still lingering there when the first beams
ham	of the sun brought into strong relief, removed beauties of architecture
ham	in spires of churches and lofty buildings, as perhaps the quiet time
spam	brought some sense of better things, else forgotten and unattainable,
ham	into his mind. Of late, the neglected bed in the Temple Court had known
ham	him more scantily than ever; and often when he had thrown himself upon
spam	it no longer than a few minutes, he had got up again, and haunted that
ham	neighbourhood.
spam	On a day in August, when Mr. Stryver (after notifying to his jackal
ham	that "he had thought better of that marrying matter") had carried his
spam	delicacy into Devonshire, and when the sight and scent of flowers in the
ham	City streets had some waifs of goodness in them for the worst, of health
ham	for the sickliest, and of youth for the oldest, Sydney's feet still trod
spam	those stones. From being irresolute and purposeless, his feet became
spam	animated by an intention, and, in the working out of that intention,
spam	they took him to the Doctor's door.
spam	He was shown up-stairs, and found Lucie at her work, alone. She had
ham	never been quite at her ease with him, and received him with some little
spam	embarrassment as he seated himself near her table. But, looking up at
spam	his face in the interchange of the first few common-places, she observed
spam	a change in it.
spam	"I fear you are not well, Mr. Carton!"
spam	"No. But the life I lead, Miss Manette, is not conducive to health. What
spam	is to be expected of, or by, such profligates?"
spam	"Is it not--forgive me; I have begun the question on my lips--a pity to
ham	live no better life?"
ham	"God knows it is a shame!"
spam	"Then why not change it?"
ham	Looking gently at him again, she was surprised and saddened to see that
spam	there were tears in his eyes. There were tears in his voice too, as he
spam	answered:
ham	"It is too late for that. I shall never be better than I am. I shall
spam	sink lower, and be worse."
spam	He leaned an elbow on her table, and covered his eyes with his hand. The
ham	table trembled in the silence that followed.
ham	She had never seen him softened, and was much distressed. He knew her to
spam	be so, without looking at her, and said:
spam	"Pray forgive me, Miss Manette. I break down before the knowledge of
spam	what I want to say to you. Will you hear me?"
spam	"If it will do you any good, Mr. Carton, if it would make you happier,
ham	it would make me very glad!"
ham	"God bless you for your sweet compassion!"
spam	He unshaded his face after a little while, and spoke steadily.
spam	"Don't be afraid to hear me. Don't shrink from anything I say. I am like
ham	one who died young. All my life might have been."
spam	"No, Mr. Carton. I am sure that the best part of it might still be; I am
ham	sure that you might be much, much worthier of yourself."
ham	"Say of you, Miss Manette, and although I know better--although in the
ham	mystery of my own wretched heart I know better--I shall never forget
ham	it!"
spam	She was pale and trembling. He came to her relief with a fixed despair
spam	of himself which made the interview unlike any other that could have
spam	been holden.
ham	"If it had been possible, Miss Manette, that you could have returned the
ham	love of the man you see before yourself--flung away, wasted, drunken,
ham	poor creature of misuse as you know him to be--he would have been
ham	conscious this day and hour, in spite of his happiness, that he would
spam	bring you to misery, bring you to sorrow and repentance, blight you,
ham	disgrace you, pull you down with him. I know very well that you can have
ham	no tenderness for me; I ask for none; I am even thankful that it cannot
spam	be."
spam	"Without it, can I not save you, Mr. Carton? Can I not recall
ham	you--forgive me again!--to a better course? Can I in no way repay your
ham	confidence? I know this is a confidence," she modestly said, after a
ham	little hesitation, and in earnest tears, "I know you would say this to
ham	no one else. Can I turn it to no good account for yourself, Mr. Carton?"
spam	He shook his head.
ham	"To none. No, Miss Manette, to none. If you will hear me through a very
spam	little more, all you can ever do for me is done. I wish you to know that
spam	you have been the last dream of my soul. In my degradation I have not
spam	been so degraded but that the sight of you with your father, and of this
ham	home made such a home by you, has stirred old shadows that I thought had
spam	died out of me. Since I knew you, I have been troubled by a remorse that
ham	I thought would never reproach me again, and have heard whispers from
ham	old voices impelling me upward, that I thought were silent for ever. I
spam	have had unformed ideas of striving afresh, beginning anew, shaking off
spam	sloth and sensuality, and fighting out the abandoned fight. A dream, all
ham	a dream, that ends in nothing, and leaves the sleeper where he lay down,
ham	but I wish you to know that you inspired it."
ham	"Will nothing of it remain? O Mr. Carton, think again! Try again!"
spam	"No, Miss Manette; all through it, I have known myself to be quite
spam	undeserving. And yet I have had the weakness, and have still the
ham	weakness, to wish you to know with what a sudden mastery you kindled me,
spam	heap of ashes that I am, into fire--a fire, however, inseparable in
spam	its nature from myself, quickening nothing, lighting nothing, doing no
spam	service, idly burning away."
ham	"Since it is my misfortune, Mr. Carton, to have made you more unhappy
ham	than you were before you knew me--"
ham	"Don't say that, Miss Manette, for you would have reclaimed me, if
spam	anything could. You will not be the cause of my becoming worse."
spam	"Since the state of your mind that you describe, is, at all events,
spam	attributable to some influence of mine--this is what I mean, if I can
ham	make it plain--can I use no influence to serve you? Have I no power for
ham	good, with you, at all?"
spam	"The utmost good that I am capable of now, Miss Manette, I have come
spam	here to realise. Let me carry through the rest of my misdirected life,
ham	the remembrance that I opened my heart to you, last of all the world;
spam	and that there was something left in me at this time which you could
ham	deplore and pity."
ham	"Which I entreated you to believe, again and again, most fervently, with
spam	all my heart, was capable of better things, Mr. Carton!"
spam	"Entreat me to believe it no more, Miss Manette. I have proved myself,
ham	and I know better. I distress you; I draw fast to an end. Will you let
spam	me believe, when I recall this day, that the last confidence of my life
spam	was reposed in your pure and innocent breast, and that it lies there
spam	alone, and will be shared by no one?"
spam	"If that will be a consolation to you, yes."
spam	"Not even by the dearest one ever to be known to you?"
ham	"Mr. Carton," she answered, after an agitated pause, "the secret is
ham	yours, not mine; and I promise to respect it."
spam	"Thank you. And again, God bless you."
ham	He put her hand to his lips, and moved towards the door.
spam	"Be under no apprehension, Miss Manette, of my ever resuming this
spam	conversation by so much as a passing word. I will never refer to it
ham	again. If I were dead, that could not be surer than it is henceforth. In
spam	the hour of my death, I shall hold sacred the one good remembrance--and
ham	shall thank and bless you for it--that my last avowal of myself was made
ham	to you, and that my name, and faults, and miseries were gently carried
spam	in your heart. May it otherwise be light and happy!"
ham	He was so unlike what he had ever shown himself to be, and it was so
spam	sad to think how much he had thrown away, and how much he every day kept
ham	down and perverted, that Lucie Manette wept mournfully for him as he
ham	stood looking back at her.
ham	"Be comforted!" he said, "I am not worth such feeling, Miss Manette. An
ham	hour or two hence, and the low companions and low habits that I scorn
ham	but yield to, will render me less worth such tears as those, than any
ham	wretch who creeps along the streets. Be comforted! But, within myself, I
spam	shall always be, towards you, what I am now, though outwardly I shall be
spam	what you have heretofore seen me. The last supplication but one I make
ham	to you, is, that you will believe this of me."
ham	"I will, Mr. Carton."
ham	"My last supplication of all, is this; and with it, I will relieve
ham	you of a visitor with whom I well know you have nothing in unison, and
ham	between whom and you there is an impassable space. It is useless to say
ham	it, I know, but it rises out of my soul. For you, and for any dear to
spam	you, I would do anything. If my career were of that better kind that
spam	there was any opportunity or capacity of sacrifice in it, I would
spam	embrace any sacrifice for you and for those dear to you. Try to hold
spam	me in your mind, at some quiet times, as ardent and sincere in this one
ham	thing. The time will come, the time will not be long in coming, when new
ham	ties will be formed about you--ties that will bind you yet more tenderly
spam	and strongly to the home you so adorn--the dearest ties that will ever
spam	grace and gladden you. O Miss Manette, when the little picture of a
ham	happy father's face looks up in yours, when you see your own bright
spam	beauty springing up anew at your feet, think now and then that there is
spam	a man who would give his life, to keep a life you love beside you!"
ham	He said, "Farewell!" said a last "God bless you!" and left her.
ham	XIV. The Honest Tradesman
ham	To the eyes of Mr. Jeremiah Cruncher, sitting on his stool in
ham	Fleet-street with his grisly urchin beside him, a vast number and
ham	variety of objects in movement were every day presented. Who could sit
spam	upon anything in Fleet-street during the busy hours of the day, and
spam	not be dazed and deafened by two immense processions, one ever tending
spam	westward with the sun, the other ever tending eastward from the sun,
spam	both ever tending to the plains beyond the range of red and purple where
spam	the sun goes down!
spam	With his straw in his mouth, Mr. Cruncher sat watching the two streams,
spam	like the heathen rustic who has for several centuries been on duty
ham	watching one stream--saving that Jerry had no expectation of their ever
ham	running dry. Nor would it have been an expectation of a hopeful kind,
spam	since a small part of his income was derived from the pilotage of timid
spam	women (mostly of a full habit and past the middle term of life) from
ham	Tellson's side of the tides to the opposite shore. Brief as such
ham	companionship was in every separate instance, Mr. Cruncher never failed
ham	to become so interested in the lady as to express a strong desire to
spam	have the honour of drinking her very good health. And it was from
ham	the gifts bestowed upon him towards the execution of this benevolent
ham	purpose, that he recruited his finances, as just now observed.
spam	Time was, when a poet sat upon a stool in a public place, and mused in
spam	the sight of men. Mr. Cruncher, sitting on a stool in a public place,
spam	but not being a poet, mused as little as possible, and looked about him.
ham	It fell out that he was thus engaged in a season when crowds were
spam	few, and belated women few, and when his affairs in general were so
spam	unprosperous as to awaken a strong suspicion in his breast that Mrs.
ham	Cruncher must have been "flopping" in some pointed manner, when an
ham	unusual concourse pouring down Fleet-street westward, attracted his
spam	attention. Looking that way, Mr. Cruncher made out that some kind of
ham	funeral was coming along, and that there was popular objection to this
spam	funeral, which engendered uproar.
ham	"Young Jerry," said Mr. Cruncher, turning to his offspring, "it's a
ham	buryin'."
ham	"Hooroar, father!" cried Young Jerry.
ham	The young gentleman uttered this exultant sound with mysterious
ham	significance. The elder gentleman took the cry so ill, that he watched
ham	his opportunity, and smote the young gentleman on the ear.
ham	"What d'ye mean? What are you hooroaring at? What do you want to conwey
ham	to your own father, you young Rip? This boy is a getting too many for
ham	_me_!" said Mr. Cruncher, surveying him. "Him and his hooroars! Don't
ham	let me hear no more of you, or you shall feel some more of me. D'ye
spam	hear?"
ham	"I warn't doing no harm," Young Jerry protested, rubbing his cheek.
spam	"Drop it then," said Mr. Cruncher; "I won't have none of _your_ no
spam	harms. Get a top of that there seat, and look at the crowd."
ham	His son obeyed, and the crowd approached; they were bawling and hissing
ham	round a dingy hearse and dingy mourning coach, in which mourning coach
spam	there was only one mourner, dressed in the dingy trappings that were
ham	considered essential to the dignity of the position. The position
ham	appeared by no means to please him, however, with an increasing rabble
spam	surrounding the coach, deriding him, making grimaces at him, and
spam	incessantly groaning and calling out: "Yah! Spies! Tst! Yaha! Spies!"
spam	with many compliments too numerous and forcible to repeat.
ham	Funerals had at all times a remarkable attraction for Mr. Cruncher; he
ham	always pricked up his senses, and became excited, when a funeral passed
spam	Tellson's. Naturally, therefore, a funeral with this uncommon attendance
spam	excited him greatly, and he asked of the first man who ran against him:
ham	"What is it, brother? What's it about?"
spam	"_I_ don't know," said the man. "Spies! Yaha! Tst! Spies!"
spam	He asked another man. "Who is it?"
ham	"_I_ don't know," returned the man, clapping his hands to his mouth
ham	nevertheless, and vociferating in a surprising heat and with the
ham	greatest ardour, "Spies! Yaha! Tst, tst! Spi--ies!"
ham	At length, a person better informed on the merits of the case, tumbled
spam	against him, and from this person he learned that the funeral was the
spam	funeral of one Roger Cly.
ham	"Was He a spy?" asked Mr. Cruncher.
spam	"Old Bailey spy," returned his informant. "Yaha! Tst! Yah! Old Bailey
ham	Spi--i--ies!"
spam	"Why, to be sure!" exclaimed Jerry, recalling the Trial at which he had
spam	assisted. "I've seen him. Dead, is he?"
spam	"Dead as mutton," returned the other, "and can't be too dead. Have 'em
ham	out, there! Spies! Pull 'em out, there! Spies!"
ham	The idea was so acceptable in the prevalent absence of any idea,
ham	that the crowd caught it up with eagerness, and loudly repeating the
spam	suggestion to have 'em out, and to pull 'em out, mobbed the two vehicles
ham	so closely that they came to a stop. On the crowd's opening the coach
ham	doors, the one mourner scuffled out of himself and was in their hands
spam	for a moment; but he was so alert, and made such good use of his time,
ham	that in another moment he was scouring away up a bye-street, after
ham	shedding his cloak, hat, long hatband, white pocket-handkerchief, and
ham	other symbolical tears.
ham	These, the people tore to pieces and scattered far and wide with great
ham	enjoyment, while the tradesmen hurriedly shut up their shops; for a
ham	crowd in those times stopped at nothing, and was a monster much dreaded.
spam	They had already got the length of opening the hearse to take the coffin
spam	out, when some brighter genius proposed instead, its being escorted to
ham	its destination amidst general rejoicing. Practical suggestions being
spam	much needed, this suggestion, too, was received with acclamation, and
ham	the coach was immediately filled with eight inside and a dozen out,
spam	while as many people got on the roof of the hearse as could by any
spam	exercise of ingenuity stick upon it. Among the first of these volunteers
spam	was Jerry Cruncher himself, who modestly concealed his spiky head from
spam	the observation of Tellson's, in the further corner of the mourning
spam	coach.
spam	The officiating undertakers made some protest against these changes in
ham	the ceremonies; but, the river being alarmingly near, and several voices
spam	remarking on the efficacy of cold immersion in bringing refractory
spam	members of the profession to reason, the protest was faint and brief.
ham	The remodelled procession started, with a chimney-sweep driving the
ham	hearse--advised by the regular driver, who was perched beside him, under
ham	close inspection, for the purpose--and with a pieman, also attended
ham	by his cabinet minister, driving the mourning coach. A bear-leader, a
ham	popular street character of the time, was impressed as an additional
spam	ornament, before the cavalcade had gone far down the Strand; and his
spam	bear, who was black and very mangy, gave quite an Undertaking air to
spam	that part of the procession in which he walked.
spam	Thus, with beer-drinking, pipe-smoking, song-roaring, and infinite
ham	caricaturing of woe, the disorderly procession went its way, recruiting
spam	at every step, and all the shops shutting up before it. Its destination
spam	was the old church of Saint Pancras, far off in the fields. It got there
ham	in course of time; insisted on pouring into the burial-ground; finally,
ham	accomplished the interment of the deceased Roger Cly in its own way, and
spam	highly to its own satisfaction.
spam	The dead man disposed of, and the crowd being under the necessity of
spam	providing some other entertainment for itself, another brighter
spam	genius (or perhaps the same) conceived the humour of impeaching casual
ham	passers-by, as Old Bailey spies, and wreaking vengeance on them. Chase
spam	was given to some scores of inoffensive persons who had never been near
spam	the Old Bailey in their lives, in the realisation of this fancy, and
spam	they were roughly hustled and maltreated. The transition to the sport of
ham	window-breaking, and thence to the plundering of public-houses, was easy
ham	and natural. At last, after several hours, when sundry summer-houses had
spam	been pulled down, and some area-railings had been torn up, to arm
spam	the more belligerent spirits, a rumour got about that the Guards were
ham	coming. Before this rumour, the crowd gradually melted away, and perhaps
spam	the Guards came, and perhaps they never came, and this was the usual
ham	progress of a mob.
spam	Mr. Cruncher did not assist at the closing sports, but had remained
spam	behind in the churchyard, to confer and condole with the undertakers.
ham	The place had a soothing influence on him. He procured a pipe from a
spam	neighbouring public-house, and smoked it, looking in at the railings and
spam	maturely considering the spot.
spam	"Jerry," said Mr. Cruncher, apostrophising himself in his usual way,
spam	"you see that there Cly that day, and you see with your own eyes that he
ham	was a young 'un and a straight made 'un."
spam	Having smoked his pipe out, and ruminated a little longer, he turned
ham	himself about, that he might appear, before the hour of closing, on his
ham	station at Tellson's. Whether his meditations on mortality had touched
ham	his liver, or whether his general health had been previously at all
ham	amiss, or whether he desired to show a little attention to an eminent
ham	man, is not so much to the purpose, as that he made a short call upon
ham	his medical adviser--a distinguished surgeon--on his way back.
ham	Young Jerry relieved his father with dutiful interest, and reported No
spam	job in his absence. The bank closed, the ancient clerks came out, the
spam	usual watch was set, and Mr. Cruncher and his son went home to tea.
spam	"Now, I tell you where it is!" said Mr. Cruncher to his wife, on
ham	entering. "If, as a honest tradesman, my wenturs goes wrong to-night, I
spam	shall make sure that you've been praying again me, and I shall work you
spam	for it just the same as if I seen you do it."
spam	The dejected Mrs. Cruncher shook her head.
spam	"Why, you're at it afore my face!" said Mr. Cruncher, with signs of
spam	angry apprehension.
spam	"I am saying nothing."
ham	"Well, then; don't meditate nothing. You might as well flop as meditate.
spam	You may as well go again me one way as another. Drop it altogether."
ham	"Yes, Jerry."
spam	"Yes, Jerry," repeated Mr. Cruncher sitting down to tea. "Ah! It _is_
spam	yes, Jerry. That's about it. You may say yes, Jerry."
spam	Mr. Cruncher had no particular meaning in these sulky corroborations,
ham	but made use of them, as people not unfrequently do, to express general
spam	ironical dissatisfaction.
ham	"You and your yes, Jerry," said Mr. Cruncher, taking a bite out of his
spam	bread-and-butter, and seeming to help it down with a large invisible
spam	oyster out of his saucer. "Ah! I think so. I believe you."
spam	"You are going out to-night?" asked his decent wife, when he took
spam	another bite.
ham	"Yes, I am."
spam	"May I go with you, father?" asked his son, briskly.
ham	"No, you mayn't. I'm a going--as your mother knows--a fishing. That's
spam	where I'm going to. Going a fishing."
spam	"Your fishing-rod gets rayther rusty; don't it, father?"
ham	"Never you mind."
ham	"Shall you bring any fish home, father?"
ham	"If I don't, you'll have short commons, to-morrow," returned that
spam	gentleman, shaking his head; "that's questions enough for you; I ain't a
spam	going out, till you've been long abed."
ham	He devoted himself during the remainder of the evening to keeping a
spam	most vigilant watch on Mrs. Cruncher, and sullenly holding her in
ham	conversation that she might be prevented from meditating any petitions
ham	to his disadvantage. With this view, he urged his son to hold her in
ham	conversation also, and led the unfortunate woman a hard life by dwelling
ham	on any causes of complaint he could bring against her, rather than
ham	he would leave her for a moment to her own reflections. The devoutest
ham	person could have rendered no greater homage to the efficacy of an
spam	honest prayer than he did in this distrust of his wife. It was as if a
ham	professed unbeliever in ghosts should be frightened by a ghost story.
ham	"And mind you!" said Mr. Cruncher. "No games to-morrow! If I, as a
spam	honest tradesman, succeed in providing a jinte of meat or two, none
ham	of your not touching of it, and sticking to bread. If I, as a honest
spam	tradesman, am able to provide a little beer, none of your declaring
spam	on water. When you go to Rome, do as Rome does. Rome will be a ugly
ham	customer to you, if you don't. _I_'m your Rome, you know."
spam	Then he began grumbling again:
spam	"With your flying into the face of your own wittles and drink! I don't
spam	know how scarce you mayn't make the wittles and drink here, by your
ham	flopping tricks and your unfeeling conduct. Look at your boy: he _is_
ham	your'n, ain't he? He's as thin as a lath. Do you call yourself a mother,
ham	and not know that a mother's first duty is to blow her boy out?"
ham	This touched Young Jerry on a tender place; who adjured his mother to
spam	perform her first duty, and, whatever else she did or neglected, above
spam	all things to lay especial stress on the discharge of that maternal
ham	function so affectingly and delicately indicated by his other parent.
spam	Thus the evening wore away with the Cruncher family, until Young Jerry
ham	was ordered to bed, and his mother, laid under similar injunctions,
ham	obeyed them. Mr. Cruncher beguiled the earlier watches of the night with
spam	solitary pipes, and did not start upon his excursion until nearly one
ham	o'clock. Towards that small and ghostly hour, he rose up from his chair,
ham	took a key out of his pocket, opened a locked cupboard, and brought
spam	forth a sack, a crowbar of convenient size, a rope and chain, and other
spam	fishing tackle of that nature. Disposing these articles about him
ham	in skilful manner, he bestowed a parting defiance on Mrs. Cruncher,
ham	extinguished the light, and went out.
spam	Young Jerry, who had only made a feint of undressing when he went to
ham	bed, was not long after his father. Under cover of the darkness he
ham	followed out of the room, followed down the stairs, followed down the
spam	court, followed out into the streets. He was in no uneasiness concerning
spam	his getting into the house again, for it was full of lodgers, and the
ham	door stood ajar all night.
spam	Impelled by a laudable ambition to study the art and mystery of his
spam	father's honest calling, Young Jerry, keeping as close to house fronts,
spam	walls, and doorways, as his eyes were close to one another, held his
spam	honoured parent in view. The honoured parent steering Northward, had not
spam	gone far, when he was joined by another disciple of Izaak Walton, and
ham	the two trudged on together.
spam	Within half an hour from the first starting, they were beyond the
spam	winking lamps, and the more than winking watchmen, and were out upon a
spam	lonely road. Another fisherman was picked up here--and that so silently,
ham	that if Young Jerry had been superstitious, he might have supposed the
spam	second follower of the gentle craft to have, all of a sudden, split
spam	himself into two.
ham	The three went on, and Young Jerry went on, until the three stopped
spam	under a bank overhanging the road. Upon the top of the bank was a low
spam	brick wall, surmounted by an iron railing. In the shadow of bank and
ham	wall the three turned out of the road, and up a blind lane, of which
ham	the wall--there, risen to some eight or ten feet high--formed one side.
ham	Crouching down in a corner, peeping up the lane, the next object that
spam	Young Jerry saw, was the form of his honoured parent, pretty well
ham	defined against a watery and clouded moon, nimbly scaling an iron gate.
spam	He was soon over, and then the second fisherman got over, and then the
spam	third. They all dropped softly on the ground within the gate, and lay
spam	there a little--listening perhaps. Then, they moved away on their hands
ham	and knees.
spam	It was now Young Jerry's turn to approach the gate: which he did,
ham	holding his breath. Crouching down again in a corner there, and looking
ham	in, he made out the three fishermen creeping through some rank grass!
spam	and all the gravestones in the churchyard--it was a large churchyard
ham	that they were in--looking on like ghosts in white, while the church
spam	tower itself looked on like the ghost of a monstrous giant. They did not
ham	creep far, before they stopped and stood upright. And then they began to
spam	fish.
spam	They fished with a spade, at first. Presently the honoured parent
ham	appeared to be adjusting some instrument like a great corkscrew.
ham	Whatever tools they worked with, they worked hard, until the awful
spam	striking of the church clock so terrified Young Jerry, that he made off,
spam	with his hair as stiff as his father's.
ham	But, his long-cherished desire to know more about these matters, not
ham	only stopped him in his running away, but lured him back again. They
ham	were still fishing perseveringly, when he peeped in at the gate for
ham	the second time; but, now they seemed to have got a bite. There was a
spam	screwing and complaining sound down below, and their bent figures were
ham	strained, as if by a weight. By slow degrees the weight broke away the
spam	earth upon it, and came to the surface. Young Jerry very well knew what
spam	it would be; but, when he saw it, and saw his honoured parent about to
spam	wrench it open, he was so frightened, being new to the sight, that he
ham	made off again, and never stopped until he had run a mile or more.
ham	He would not have stopped then, for anything less necessary than breath,
ham	it being a spectral sort of race that he ran, and one highly desirable
ham	to get to the end of. He had a strong idea that the coffin he had seen
ham	was running after him; and, pictured as hopping on behind him, bolt
ham	upright, upon its narrow end, always on the point of overtaking him
spam	and hopping on at his side--perhaps taking his arm--it was a pursuer to
ham	shun. It was an inconsistent and ubiquitous fiend too, for, while it
spam	was making the whole night behind him dreadful, he darted out into the
ham	roadway to avoid dark alleys, fearful of its coming hopping out of them
ham	like a dropsical boy's Kite without tail and wings. It hid in doorways
spam	too, rubbing its horrible shoulders against doors, and drawing them up
spam	to its ears, as if it were laughing. It got into shadows on the road,
ham	and lay cunningly on its back to trip him up. All this time it was
ham	incessantly hopping on behind and gaining on him, so that when the boy
ham	got to his own door he had reason for being half dead. And even then
ham	it would not leave him, but followed him upstairs with a bump on every
ham	stair, scrambled into bed with him, and bumped down, dead and heavy, on
ham	his breast when he fell asleep.
ham	From his oppressed slumber, Young Jerry in his closet was awakened after
spam	daybreak and before sunrise, by the presence of his father in the
spam	family room. Something had gone wrong with him; at least, so Young Jerry
ham	inferred, from the circumstance of his holding Mrs. Cruncher by the
spam	ears, and knocking the back of her head against the head-board of the
spam	bed.
spam	"I told you I would," said Mr. Cruncher, "and I did."
ham	"Jerry, Jerry, Jerry!" his wife implored.
ham	"You oppose yourself to the profit of the business," said Jerry, "and me
ham	and my partners suffer. You was to honour and obey; why the devil don't
spam	you?"
spam	"I try to be a good wife, Jerry," the poor woman protested, with tears.
spam	"Is it being a good wife to oppose your husband's business? Is it
spam	honouring your husband to dishonour his business? Is it obeying your
spam	husband to disobey him on the wital subject of his business?"
ham	"You hadn't taken to the dreadful business then, Jerry."
spam	"It's enough for you," retorted Mr. Cruncher, "to be the wife of a
ham	honest tradesman, and not to occupy your female mind with calculations
ham	when he took to his trade or when he didn't. A honouring and obeying
spam	wife would let his trade alone altogether. Call yourself a religious
ham	woman? If you're a religious woman, give me a irreligious one! You have
spam	no more nat'ral sense of duty than the bed of this here Thames river has
ham	of a pile, and similarly it must be knocked into you."
spam	The altercation was conducted in a low tone of voice, and terminated in
ham	the honest tradesman's kicking off his clay-soiled boots, and lying down
spam	at his length on the floor. After taking a timid peep at him lying on
spam	his back, with his rusty hands under his head for a pillow, his son lay
spam	down too, and fell asleep again.
ham	There was no fish for breakfast, and not much of anything else. Mr.
spam	Cruncher was out of spirits, and out of temper, and kept an iron pot-lid
ham	by him as a projectile for the correction of Mrs. Cruncher, in case
ham	he should observe any symptoms of her saying Grace. He was brushed
spam	and washed at the usual hour, and set off with his son to pursue his
ham	ostensible calling.
ham	Young Jerry, walking with the stool under his arm at his father's side
spam	along sunny and crowded Fleet-street, was a very different Young Jerry
ham	from him of the previous night, running home through darkness and
ham	solitude from his grim pursuer. His cunning was fresh with the day,
spam	and his qualms were gone with the night--in which particulars it is not
spam	improbable that he had compeers in Fleet-street and the City of London,
spam	that fine morning.
spam	"Father," said Young Jerry, as they walked along: taking care to keep
spam	at arm's length and to have the stool well between them: "what's a
ham	Resurrection-Man?"
spam	Mr. Cruncher came to a stop on the pavement before he answered, "How
ham	should I know?"
spam	"I thought you knowed everything, father," said the artless boy.
ham	"Hem! Well," returned Mr. Cruncher, going on again, and lifting off his
spam	hat to give his spikes free play, "he's a tradesman."
spam	"What's his goods, father?" asked the brisk Young Jerry.
spam	"His goods," said Mr. Cruncher, after turning it over in his mind, "is a
spam	branch of Scientific goods."
ham	"Persons' bodies, ain't it, father?" asked the lively boy.
spam	"I believe it is something of that sort," said Mr. Cruncher.
spam	"Oh, father, I should so like to be a Resurrection-Man when I'm quite
spam	growed up!"
ham	Mr. Cruncher was soothed, but shook his head in a dubious and moral way.
ham	"It depends upon how you dewelop your talents. Be careful to dewelop
ham	your talents, and never to say no more than you can help to nobody, and
spam	there's no telling at the present time what you may not come to be fit
spam	for." As Young Jerry, thus encouraged, went on a few yards in advance,
spam	to plant the stool in the shadow of the Bar, Mr. Cruncher added to
spam	himself: "Jerry, you honest tradesman, there's hopes wot that boy will
ham	yet be a blessing to you, and a recompense to you for his mother!"
ham	XV. Knitting
ham	There had been earlier drinking than usual in the wine-shop of Monsieur
ham	Defarge. As early as six o'clock in the morning, sallow faces peeping
spam	through its barred windows had descried other faces within, bending over
spam	measures of wine. Monsieur Defarge sold a very thin wine at the best
spam	of times, but it would seem to have been an unusually thin wine that
ham	he sold at this time. A sour wine, moreover, or a souring, for its
ham	influence on the mood of those who drank it was to make them gloomy. No
ham	vivacious Bacchanalian flame leaped out of the pressed grape of Monsieur
ham	Defarge: but, a smouldering fire that burnt in the dark, lay hidden in
ham	the dregs of it.
ham	This had been the third morning in succession, on which there had been
ham	early drinking at the wine-shop of Monsieur Defarge. It had begun
ham	on Monday, and here was Wednesday come. There had been more of early
ham	brooding than drinking; for, many men had listened and whispered and
ham	slunk about there from the time of the opening of the door, who could
spam	not have laid a piece of money on the counter to save their souls. These
ham	were to the full as interested in the place, however, as if they could
ham	have commanded whole barrels of wine; and they glided from seat to seat,
spam	and from corner to corner, swallowing talk in lieu of drink, with greedy
ham	looks.
spam	Notwithstanding an unusual flow of company, the master of the wine-shop
ham	was not visible. He was not missed; for, nobody who crossed the
spam	threshold looked for him, nobody asked for him, nobody wondered to see
ham	only Madame Defarge in her seat, presiding over the distribution of
spam	wine, with a bowl of battered small coins before her, as much defaced
ham	and beaten out of their original impress as the small coinage of
spam	humanity from whose ragged pockets they had come.
ham	A suspended interest and a prevalent absence of mind, were perhaps
spam	observed by the spies who looked in at the wine-shop, as they looked in
ham	at every place, high and low, from the king's palace to the criminal's
ham	gaol. Games at cards languished, players at dominoes musingly built
spam	towers with them, drinkers drew figures on the tables with spilt drops
ham	of wine, Madame Defarge herself picked out the pattern on her sleeve
spam	with her toothpick, and saw and heard something inaudible and invisible
spam	a long way off.
spam	Thus, Saint Antoine in this vinous feature of his, until midday. It was
ham	high noontide, when two dusty men passed through his streets and under
spam	his swinging lamps: of whom, one was Monsieur Defarge: the other a
spam	mender of roads in a blue cap. All adust and athirst, the two entered
spam	the wine-shop. Their arrival had lighted a kind of fire in the breast
spam	of Saint Antoine, fast spreading as they came along, which stirred and
spam	flickered in flames of faces at most doors and windows. Yet, no one had
spam	followed them, and no man spoke when they entered the wine-shop, though
ham	the eyes of every man there were turned upon them.
ham	"Good day, gentlemen!" said Monsieur Defarge.
spam	It may have been a signal for loosening the general tongue. It elicited
spam	an answering chorus of "Good day!"
ham	"It is bad weather, gentlemen," said Defarge, shaking his head.
ham	Upon which, every man looked at his neighbour, and then all cast down
ham	their eyes and sat silent. Except one man, who got up and went out.
ham	"My wife," said Defarge aloud, addressing Madame Defarge: "I have
ham	travelled certain leagues with this good mender of roads, called
spam	Jacques. I met him--by accident--a day and half's journey out of Paris.
ham	He is a good child, this mender of roads, called Jacques. Give him to
ham	drink, my wife!"
spam	A second man got up and went out. Madame Defarge set wine before the
ham	mender of roads called Jacques, who doffed his blue cap to the company,
spam	and drank. In the breast of his blouse he carried some coarse dark
spam	bread; he ate of this between whiles, and sat munching and drinking near
ham	Madame Defarge's counter. A third man got up and went out.
ham	Defarge refreshed himself with a draught of wine--but, he took less
spam	than was given to the stranger, as being himself a man to whom it was no
ham	rarity--and stood waiting until the countryman had made his breakfast.
ham	He looked at no one present, and no one now looked at him; not even
ham	Madame Defarge, who had taken up her knitting, and was at work.
ham	"Have you finished your repast, friend?" he asked, in due season.
ham	"Yes, thank you."
spam	"Come, then! You shall see the apartment that I told you you could
ham	occupy. It will suit you to a marvel."
ham	Out of the wine-shop into the street, out of the street into a
ham	courtyard, out of the courtyard up a steep staircase, out of the
spam	staircase into a garret--formerly the garret where a white-haired man
ham	sat on a low bench, stooping forward and very busy, making shoes.
spam	No white-haired man was there now; but, the three men were there who had
spam	gone out of the wine-shop singly. And between them and the white-haired
spam	man afar off, was the one small link, that they had once looked in at
spam	him through the chinks in the wall.
spam	Defarge closed the door carefully, and spoke in a subdued voice:
ham	"Jacques One, Jacques Two, Jacques Three! This is the witness
spam	encountered by appointment, by me, Jacques Four. He will tell you all.
spam	Speak, Jacques Five!"
spam	The mender of roads, blue cap in hand, wiped his swarthy forehead with
spam	it, and said, "Where shall I commence, monsieur?"
ham	"Commence," was Monsieur Defarge's not unreasonable reply, "at the
spam	commencement."
ham	"I saw him then, messieurs," began the mender of roads, "a year ago this
ham	running summer, underneath the carriage of the Marquis, hanging by the
spam	chain. Behold the manner of it. I leaving my work on the road, the sun
spam	going to bed, the carriage of the Marquis slowly ascending the hill, he
spam	hanging by the chain--like this."
ham	Again the mender of roads went through the whole performance; in which
spam	he ought to have been perfect by that time, seeing that it had been
ham	the infallible resource and indispensable entertainment of his village
ham	during a whole year.
spam	Jacques One struck in, and asked if he had ever seen the man before?
ham	"Never," answered the mender of roads, recovering his perpendicular.
ham	Jacques Three demanded how he afterwards recognised him then?
spam	"By his tall figure," said the mender of roads, softly, and with his
ham	finger at his nose. "When Monsieur the Marquis demands that evening,
ham	'Say, what is he like?' I make response, 'Tall as a spectre.'"
ham	"You should have said, short as a dwarf," returned Jacques Two.
spam	"But what did I know? The deed was not then accomplished, neither did he
spam	confide in me. Observe! Under those circumstances even, I do not
spam	offer my testimony. Monsieur the Marquis indicates me with his finger,
ham	standing near our little fountain, and says, 'To me! Bring that rascal!'
ham	My faith, messieurs, I offer nothing."
ham	"He is right there, Jacques," murmured Defarge, to him who had
ham	interrupted. "Go on!"
ham	"Good!" said the mender of roads, with an air of mystery. "The tall man
spam	is lost, and he is sought--how many months? Nine, ten, eleven?"
spam	"No matter, the number," said Defarge. "He is well hidden, but at last
spam	he is unluckily found. Go on!"
spam	"I am again at work upon the hill-side, and the sun is again about to
ham	go to bed. I am collecting my tools to descend to my cottage down in the
spam	village below, where it is already dark, when I raise my eyes, and see
spam	coming over the hill six soldiers. In the midst of them is a tall man
spam	with his arms bound--tied to his sides--like this!"
spam	With the aid of his indispensable cap, he represented a man with his
ham	elbows bound fast at his hips, with cords that were knotted behind him.
ham	"I stand aside, messieurs, by my heap of stones, to see the soldiers
ham	and their prisoner pass (for it is a solitary road, that, where any
ham	spectacle is well worth looking at), and at first, as they approach, I
ham	see no more than that they are six soldiers with a tall man bound, and
ham	that they are almost black to my sight--except on the side of the sun
spam	going to bed, where they have a red edge, messieurs. Also, I see that
spam	their long shadows are on the hollow ridge on the opposite side of the
spam	road, and are on the hill above it, and are like the shadows of giants.
spam	Also, I see that they are covered with dust, and that the dust moves
ham	with them as they come, tramp, tramp! But when they advance quite near
ham	to me, I recognise the tall man, and he recognises me. Ah, but he would
spam	be well content to precipitate himself over the hill-side once again, as
ham	on the evening when he and I first encountered, close to the same spot!"
spam	He described it as if he were there, and it was evident that he saw it
ham	vividly; perhaps he had not seen much in his life.
spam	"I do not show the soldiers that I recognise the tall man; he does not
spam	show the soldiers that he recognises me; we do it, and we know it, with
spam	our eyes. 'Come on!' says the chief of that company, pointing to the
spam	village, 'bring him fast to his tomb!' and they bring him faster. I
spam	follow. His arms are swelled because of being bound so tight, his wooden
spam	shoes are large and clumsy, and he is lame. Because he is lame, and
ham	consequently slow, they drive him with their guns--like this!"
ham	He imitated the action of a man's being impelled forward by the
spam	butt-ends of muskets.
ham	"As they descend the hill like madmen running a race, he falls. They
spam	laugh and pick him up again. His face is bleeding and covered with dust,
ham	but he cannot touch it; thereupon they laugh again. They bring him into
ham	the village; all the village runs to look; they take him past the mill,
spam	and up to the prison; all the village sees the prison gate open in the
ham	darkness of the night, and swallow him--like this!"
spam	He opened his mouth as wide as he could, and shut it with a sounding
spam	snap of his teeth. Observant of his unwillingness to mar the effect by
spam	opening it again, Defarge said, "Go on, Jacques."
ham	"All the village," pursued the mender of roads, on tiptoe and in a low
spam	voice, "withdraws; all the village whispers by the fountain; all the
spam	village sleeps; all the village dreams of that unhappy one, within the
ham	locks and bars of the prison on the crag, and never to come out of it,
spam	except to perish. In the morning, with my tools upon my shoulder, eating
spam	my morsel of black bread as I go, I make a circuit by the prison, on
ham	my way to my work. There I see him, high up, behind the bars of a lofty
ham	iron cage, bloody and dusty as last night, looking through. He has no
spam	hand free, to wave to me; I dare not call to him; he regards me like a
spam	dead man."
ham	Defarge and the three glanced darkly at one another. The looks of all
spam	of them were dark, repressed, and revengeful, as they listened to the
spam	countryman's story; the manner of all of them, while it was secret, was
ham	authoritative too. They had the air of a rough tribunal; Jacques One
ham	and Two sitting on the old pallet-bed, each with his chin resting on
ham	his hand, and his eyes intent on the road-mender; Jacques Three, equally
spam	intent, on one knee behind them, with his agitated hand always gliding
spam	over the network of fine nerves about his mouth and nose; Defarge
ham	standing between them and the narrator, whom he had stationed in the
spam	light of the window, by turns looking from him to them, and from them to
spam	him.
spam	"Go on, Jacques," said Defarge.
ham	"He remains up there in his iron cage some days. The village looks
spam	at him by stealth, for it is afraid. But it always looks up, from a
spam	distance, at the prison on the crag; and in the evening, when the work
ham	of the day is achieved and it assembles to gossip at the fountain, all
spam	faces are turned towards the prison. Formerly, they were turned towards
ham	the posting-house; now, they are turned towards the prison. They
spam	whisper at the fountain, that although condemned to death he will not be
ham	executed; they say that petitions have been presented in Paris, showing
ham	that he was enraged and made mad by the death of his child; they say
ham	that a petition has been presented to the King himself. What do I know?
spam	It is possible. Perhaps yes, perhaps no."
spam	"Listen then, Jacques," Number One of that name sternly interposed.
spam	"Know that a petition was presented to the King and Queen. All here,
spam	yourself excepted, saw the King take it, in his carriage in the street,
spam	sitting beside the Queen. It is Defarge whom you see here, who, at the
spam	hazard of his life, darted out before the horses, with the petition in
spam	his hand."
spam	"And once again listen, Jacques!" said the kneeling Number Three:
spam	his fingers ever wandering over and over those fine nerves, with a
spam	strikingly greedy air, as if he hungered for something--that was neither
spam	food nor drink; "the guard, horse and foot, surrounded the petitioner,
spam	and struck him blows. You hear?"
spam	"I hear, messieurs."
spam	"Go on then," said Defarge.
ham	"Again; on the other hand, they whisper at the fountain," resumed the
spam	countryman, "that he is brought down into our country to be executed on
spam	the spot, and that he will very certainly be executed. They even whisper
ham	that because he has slain Monseigneur, and because Monseigneur was the
ham	father of his tenants--serfs--what you will--he will be executed as a
spam	parricide. One old man says at the fountain, that his right hand, armed
ham	with the knife, will be burnt off before his face; that, into wounds
ham	which will be made in his arms, his breast, and his legs, there will be
ham	poured boiling oil, melted lead, hot resin, wax, and sulphur; finally,
ham	that he will be torn limb from limb by four strong horses. That old man
ham	says, all this was actually done to a prisoner who made an attempt on
ham	the life of the late King, Louis Fifteen. But how do I know if he lies?
spam	I am not a scholar."
ham	"Listen once again then, Jacques!" said the man with the restless hand
ham	and the craving air. "The name of that prisoner was Damiens, and it was
spam	all done in open day, in the open streets of this city of Paris; and
spam	nothing was more noticed in the vast concourse that saw it done, than
ham	the crowd of ladies of quality and fashion, who were full of eager
spam	attention to the last--to the last, Jacques, prolonged until nightfall,
spam	when he had lost two legs and an arm, and still breathed! And it was
spam	done--why, how old are you?"
spam	"Thirty-five," said the mender of roads, who looked sixty.
spam	"It was done when you were more than ten years old; you might have seen
ham	it."
spam	"Enough!" said Defarge, with grim impatience. "Long live the Devil! Go
ham	on."
ham	"Well! Some whisper this, some whisper that; they speak of nothing else;
spam	even the fountain appears to fall to that tune. At length, on Sunday
ham	night when all the village is asleep, come soldiers, winding down from
spam	the prison, and their guns ring on the stones of the little street.
spam	Workmen dig, workmen hammer, soldiers laugh and sing; in the morning, by
ham	the fountain, there is raised a gallows forty feet high, poisoning the
spam	water."
spam	The mender of roads looked _through_ rather than _at_ the low ceiling,
spam	and pointed as if he saw the gallows somewhere in the sky.
spam	"All work is stopped, all assemble there, nobody leads the cows out,
spam	the cows are there with the rest. At midday, the roll of drums. Soldiers
spam	have marched into the prison in the night, and he is in the midst
ham	of many soldiers. He is bound as before, and in his mouth there is
ham	a gag--tied so, with a tight string, making him look almost as if he
ham	laughed." He suggested it, by creasing his face with his two thumbs,
ham	from the corners of his mouth to his ears. "On the top of the gallows is
spam	fixed the knife, blade upwards, with its point in the air. He is hanged
ham	there forty feet high--and is left hanging, poisoning the water."
spam	They looked at one another, as he used his blue cap to wipe his face,
ham	on which the perspiration had started afresh while he recalled the
spam	spectacle.
ham	"It is frightful, messieurs. How can the women and the children draw
spam	water! Who can gossip of an evening, under that shadow! Under it, have
ham	I said? When I left the village, Monday evening as the sun was going to
ham	bed, and looked back from the hill, the shadow struck across the church,
ham	across the mill, across the prison--seemed to strike across the earth,
ham	messieurs, to where the sky rests upon it!"
ham	The hungry man gnawed one of his fingers as he looked at the other
spam	three, and his finger quivered with the craving that was on him.
spam	"That's all, messieurs. I left at sunset (as I had been warned to do),
ham	and I walked on, that night and half next day, until I met (as I was
ham	warned I should) this comrade. With him, I came on, now riding and now
spam	walking, through the rest of yesterday and through last night. And here
spam	you see me!"
spam	After a gloomy silence, the first Jacques said, "Good! You have acted
ham	and recounted faithfully. Will you wait for us a little, outside the
ham	door?"
spam	"Very willingly," said the mender of roads. Whom Defarge escorted to the
ham	top of the stairs, and, leaving seated there, returned.
ham	The three had risen, and their heads were together when he came back to
ham	the garret.
spam	"How say you, Jacques?" demanded Number One. "To be registered?"
ham	"To be registered, as doomed to destruction," returned Defarge.
spam	"Magnificent!" croaked the man with the craving.
ham	"The chateau, and all the race?" inquired the first.
ham	"The chateau and all the race," returned Defarge. "Extermination."
ham	The hungry man repeated, in a rapturous croak, "Magnificent!" and began
ham	gnawing another finger.
ham	"Are you sure," asked Jacques Two, of Defarge, "that no embarrassment
spam	can arise from our manner of keeping the register? Without doubt it is
ham	safe, for no one beyond ourselves can decipher it; but shall we always
spam	be able to decipher it--or, I ought to say, will she?"
ham	"Jacques," returned Defarge, drawing himself up, "if madame my wife
ham	undertook to keep the register in her memory alone, she would not lose
ham	a word of it--not a syllable of it. Knitted, in her own stitches and her
ham	own symbols, it will always be as plain to her as the sun. Confide in
ham	Madame Defarge. It would be easier for the weakest poltroon that lives,
ham	to erase himself from existence, than to erase one letter of his name or
spam	crimes from the knitted register of Madame Defarge."
ham	There was a murmur of confidence and approval, and then the man who
ham	hungered, asked: "Is this rustic to be sent back soon? I hope so. He is
spam	very simple; is he not a little dangerous?"
ham	"He knows nothing," said Defarge; "at least nothing more than would
spam	easily elevate himself to a gallows of the same height. I charge myself
ham	with him; let him remain with me; I will take care of him, and set him
spam	on his road. He wishes to see the fine world--the King, the Queen, and
ham	Court; let him see them on Sunday."
spam	"What?" exclaimed the hungry man, staring. "Is it a good sign, that he
spam	wishes to see Royalty and Nobility?"
spam	"Jacques," said Defarge; "judiciously show a cat milk, if you wish her
spam	to thirst for it. Judiciously show a dog his natural prey, if you wish
spam	him to bring it down one day."
ham	Nothing more was said, and the mender of roads, being found already
spam	dozing on the topmost stair, was advised to lay himself down on the
ham	pallet-bed and take some rest. He needed no persuasion, and was soon
ham	asleep.
ham	Worse quarters than Defarge's wine-shop, could easily have been found
ham	in Paris for a provincial slave of that degree. Saving for a mysterious
spam	dread of madame by which he was constantly haunted, his life was very
spam	new and agreeable. But, madame sat all day at her counter, so expressly
spam	unconscious of him, and so particularly determined not to perceive that
spam	his being there had any connection with anything below the surface, that
spam	he shook in his wooden shoes whenever his eye lighted on her. For, he
ham	contended with himself that it was impossible to foresee what that lady
spam	might pretend next; and he felt assured that if she should take it
spam	into her brightly ornamented head to pretend that she had seen him do a
ham	murder and afterwards flay the victim, she would infallibly go through
ham	with it until the play was played out.
spam	Therefore, when Sunday came, the mender of roads was not enchanted
ham	(though he said he was) to find that madame was to accompany monsieur
spam	and himself to Versailles. It was additionally disconcerting to have
spam	madame knitting all the way there, in a public conveyance; it was
spam	additionally disconcerting yet, to have madame in the crowd in the
spam	afternoon, still with her knitting in her hands as the crowd waited to
spam	see the carriage of the King and Queen.
ham	"You work hard, madame," said a man near her.
spam	"Yes," answered Madame Defarge; "I have a good deal to do."
spam	"What do you make, madame?"
spam	"Many things."
ham	"For instance--"
spam	"For instance," returned Madame Defarge, composedly, "shrouds."
ham	The man moved a little further away, as soon as he could, and the mender
spam	of roads fanned himself with his blue cap: feeling it mightily close
spam	and oppressive. If he needed a King and Queen to restore him, he was
ham	fortunate in having his remedy at hand; for, soon the large-faced King
spam	and the fair-faced Queen came in their golden coach, attended by the
spam	shining Bull's Eye of their Court, a glittering multitude of laughing
spam	ladies and fine lords; and in jewels and silks and powder and splendour
spam	and elegantly spurning figures and handsomely disdainful faces of both
spam	sexes, the mender of roads bathed himself, so much to his temporary
ham	intoxication, that he cried Long live the King, Long live the Queen,
spam	Long live everybody and everything! as if he had never heard of
ham	ubiquitous Jacques in his time. Then, there were gardens, courtyards,
spam	terraces, fountains, green banks, more King and Queen, more Bull's Eye,
ham	more lords and ladies, more Long live they all! until he absolutely wept
spam	with sentiment. During the whole of this scene, which lasted some three
spam	hours, he had plenty of shouting and weeping and sentimental company,
spam	and throughout Defarge held him by the collar, as if to restrain him
spam	from flying at the objects of his brief devotion and tearing them to
spam	pieces.
spam	"Bravo!" said Defarge, clapping him on the back when it was over, like a
ham	patron; "you are a good boy!"
ham	The mender of roads was now coming to himself, and was mistrustful of
ham	having made a mistake in his late demonstrations; but no.
spam	"You are the fellow we want," said Defarge, in his ear; "you make
spam	these fools believe that it will last for ever. Then, they are the more
spam	insolent, and it is the nearer ended."
spam	"Hey!" cried the mender of roads, reflectively; "that's true."
spam	"These fools know nothing. While they despise your breath, and would
spam	stop it for ever and ever, in you or in a hundred like you rather than
spam	in one of their own horses or dogs, they only know what your breath
ham	tells them. Let it deceive them, then, a little longer; it cannot
spam	deceive them too much."
spam	Madame Defarge looked superciliously at the client, and nodded in
spam	confirmation.
spam	"As to you," said she, "you would shout and shed tears for anything, if
ham	it made a show and a noise. Say! Would you not?"
ham	"Truly, madame, I think so. For the moment."
spam	"If you were shown a great heap of dolls, and were set upon them to
ham	pluck them to pieces and despoil them for your own advantage, you would
spam	pick out the richest and gayest. Say! Would you not?"
ham	"Truly yes, madame."
ham	"Yes. And if you were shown a flock of birds, unable to fly, and were
spam	set upon them to strip them of their feathers for your own advantage,
spam	you would set upon the birds of the finest feathers; would you not?"
ham	"It is true, madame."
ham	"You have seen both dolls and birds to-day," said Madame Defarge, with
spam	a wave of her hand towards the place where they had last been apparent;
spam	"now, go home!"
ham	XVI. Still Knitting
spam	Madame Defarge and monsieur her husband returned amicably to the
ham	bosom of Saint Antoine, while a speck in a blue cap toiled through the
spam	darkness, and through the dust, and down the weary miles of avenue by
ham	the wayside, slowly tending towards that point of the compass where
spam	the chateau of Monsieur the Marquis, now in his grave, listened to
ham	the whispering trees. Such ample leisure had the stone faces, now,
spam	for listening to the trees and to the fountain, that the few village
spam	scarecrows who, in their quest for herbs to eat and fragments of dead
spam	stick to burn, strayed within sight of the great stone courtyard and
ham	terrace staircase, had it borne in upon their starved fancy that
spam	the expression of the faces was altered. A rumour just lived in the
ham	village--had a faint and bare existence there, as its people had--that
ham	when the knife struck home, the faces changed, from faces of pride to
ham	faces of anger and pain; also, that when that dangling figure was hauled
spam	up forty feet above the fountain, they changed again, and bore a cruel
spam	look of being avenged, which they would henceforth bear for ever. In the
ham	stone face over the great window of the bed-chamber where the murder
spam	was done, two fine dints were pointed out in the sculptured nose, which
ham	everybody recognised, and which nobody had seen of old; and on the
spam	scarce occasions when two or three ragged peasants emerged from the
ham	crowd to take a hurried peep at Monsieur the Marquis petrified, a
ham	skinny finger would not have pointed to it for a minute, before they all
spam	started away among the moss and leaves, like the more fortunate hares
spam	who could find a living there.
ham	Chateau and hut, stone face and dangling figure, the red stain on the
ham	stone floor, and the pure water in the village well--thousands of acres
ham	of land--a whole province of France--all France itself--lay under the
ham	night sky, concentrated into a faint hair-breadth line. So does a whole
ham	world, with all its greatnesses and littlenesses, lie in a twinkling
spam	star. And as mere human knowledge can split a ray of light and analyse
ham	the manner of its composition, so, sublimer intelligences may read in
ham	the feeble shining of this earth of ours, every thought and act, every
ham	vice and virtue, of every responsible creature on it.
ham	The Defarges, husband and wife, came lumbering under the starlight,
spam	in their public vehicle, to that gate of Paris whereunto their
spam	journey naturally tended. There was the usual stoppage at the barrier
ham	guardhouse, and the usual lanterns came glancing forth for the usual
spam	examination and inquiry. Monsieur Defarge alighted; knowing one or two
ham	of the soldiery there, and one of the police. The latter he was intimate
ham	with, and affectionately embraced.
ham	When Saint Antoine had again enfolded the Defarges in his dusky wings,
ham	and they, having finally alighted near the Saint's boundaries, were
spam	picking their way on foot through the black mud and offal of his
spam	streets, Madame Defarge spoke to her husband:
ham	"Say then, my friend; what did Jacques of the police tell thee?"
ham	"Very little to-night, but all he knows. There is another spy
spam	commissioned for our quarter. There may be many more, for all that he
spam	can say, but he knows of one."
spam	"Eh well!" said Madame Defarge, raising her eyebrows with a cool
ham	business air. "It is necessary to register him. How do they call that
ham	man?"
spam	"He is English."
ham	"So much the better. His name?"
spam	"Barsad," said Defarge, making it French by pronunciation. But, he had
ham	been so careful to get it accurately, that he then spelt it with perfect
ham	correctness.
spam	"Barsad," repeated madame. "Good. Christian name?"
spam	"John."
spam	"John Barsad," repeated madame, after murmuring it once to herself.
spam	"Good. His appearance; is it known?"
spam	"Age, about forty years; height, about five feet nine; black hair;
spam	complexion dark; generally, rather handsome visage; eyes dark, face
spam	thin, long, and sallow; nose aquiline, but not straight, having a
ham	peculiar inclination towards the left cheek; expression, therefore,
ham	sinister."
ham	"Eh my faith. It is a portrait!" said madame, laughing. "He shall be
ham	registered to-morrow."
spam	They turned into the wine-shop, which was closed (for it was midnight),
spam	and where Madame Defarge immediately took her post at her desk, counted
spam	the small moneys that had been taken during her absence, examined the
ham	stock, went through the entries in the book, made other entries of
ham	her own, checked the serving man in every possible way, and finally
ham	dismissed him to bed. Then she turned out the contents of the bowl
ham	of money for the second time, and began knotting them up in her
ham	handkerchief, in a chain of separate knots, for safe keeping through the
spam	night. All this while, Defarge, with his pipe in his mouth, walked
ham	up and down, complacently admiring, but never interfering; in which
spam	condition, indeed, as to the business and his domestic affairs, he
spam	walked up and down through life.
ham	The night was hot, and the shop, close shut and surrounded by so foul a
spam	neighbourhood, was ill-smelling. Monsieur Defarge's olfactory sense was
spam	by no means delicate, but the stock of wine smelt much stronger than
spam	it ever tasted, and so did the stock of rum and brandy and aniseed. He
spam	whiffed the compound of scents away, as he put down his smoked-out pipe.
spam	"You are fatigued," said madame, raising her glance as she knotted the
ham	money. "There are only the usual odours."
ham	"I am a little tired," her husband acknowledged.
ham	"You are a little depressed, too," said madame, whose quick eyes had
ham	never been so intent on the accounts, but they had had a ray or two for
spam	him. "Oh, the men, the men!"
ham	"But my dear!" began Defarge.
ham	"But my dear!" repeated madame, nodding firmly; "but my dear! You are
spam	faint of heart to-night, my dear!"
ham	"Well, then," said Defarge, as if a thought were wrung out of his
spam	breast, "it _is_ a long time."
spam	"It is a long time," repeated his wife; "and when is it not a long time?
ham	Vengeance and retribution require a long time; it is the rule."
spam	"It does not take a long time to strike a man with Lightning," said
spam	Defarge.
spam	"How long," demanded madame, composedly, "does it take to make and store
spam	the lightning? Tell me."
ham	Defarge raised his head thoughtfully, as if there were something in that
ham	too.
ham	"It does not take a long time," said madame, "for an earthquake to
spam	swallow a town. Eh well! Tell me how long it takes to prepare the
ham	earthquake?"
ham	"A long time, I suppose," said Defarge.
ham	"But when it is ready, it takes place, and grinds to pieces everything
spam	before it. In the meantime, it is always preparing, though it is not
spam	seen or heard. That is your consolation. Keep it."
ham	She tied a knot with flashing eyes, as if it throttled a foe.
ham	"I tell thee," said madame, extending her right hand, for emphasis,
spam	"that although it is a long time on the road, it is on the road and
spam	coming. I tell thee it never retreats, and never stops. I tell thee it
ham	is always advancing. Look around and consider the lives of all the world
ham	that we know, consider the faces of all the world that we know, consider
spam	the rage and discontent to which the Jacquerie addresses itself with
ham	more and more of certainty every hour. Can such things last? Bah! I mock
spam	you."
spam	"My brave wife," returned Defarge, standing before her with his head
ham	a little bent, and his hands clasped at his back, like a docile and
spam	attentive pupil before his catechist, "I do not question all this. But
spam	it has lasted a long time, and it is possible--you know well, my wife,
ham	it is possible--that it may not come, during our lives."
ham	"Eh well! How then?" demanded madame, tying another knot, as if there
spam	were another enemy strangled.
ham	"Well!" said Defarge, with a half complaining and half apologetic shrug.
ham	"We shall not see the triumph."
spam	"We shall have helped it," returned madame, with her extended hand in
spam	strong action. "Nothing that we do, is done in vain. I believe, with all
spam	my soul, that we shall see the triumph. But even if not, even if I knew
ham	certainly not, show me the neck of an aristocrat and tyrant, and still I
spam	would--"
ham	Then madame, with her teeth set, tied a very terrible knot indeed.
spam	"Hold!" cried Defarge, reddening a little as if he felt charged with
ham	cowardice; "I too, my dear, will stop at nothing."
spam	"Yes! But it is your weakness that you sometimes need to see your victim
spam	and your opportunity, to sustain you. Sustain yourself without that.
ham	When the time comes, let loose a tiger and a devil; but wait for the
ham	time with the tiger and the devil chained--not shown--yet always ready."
spam	Madame enforced the conclusion of this piece of advice by striking her
spam	little counter with her chain of money as if she knocked its brains
ham	out, and then gathering the heavy handkerchief under her arm in a serene
ham	manner, and observing that it was time to go to bed.
ham	Next noontide saw the admirable woman in her usual place in the
ham	wine-shop, knitting away assiduously. A rose lay beside her, and if she
spam	now and then glanced at the flower, it was with no infraction of her
spam	usual preoccupied air. There were a few customers, drinking or not
spam	drinking, standing or seated, sprinkled about. The day was very hot,
ham	and heaps of flies, who were extending their inquisitive and adventurous
spam	perquisitions into all the glutinous little glasses near madame, fell
ham	dead at the bottom. Their decease made no impression on the other flies
ham	out promenading, who looked at them in the coolest manner (as if they
ham	themselves were elephants, or something as far removed), until they met
spam	the same fate. Curious to consider how heedless flies are!--perhaps they
spam	thought as much at Court that sunny summer day.
ham	A figure entering at the door threw a shadow on Madame Defarge which she
ham	felt to be a new one. She laid down her knitting, and began to pin her
spam	rose in her head-dress, before she looked at the figure.
spam	It was curious. The moment Madame Defarge took up the rose, the
ham	customers ceased talking, and began gradually to drop out of the
ham	wine-shop.
ham	"Good day, madame," said the new-comer.
ham	"Good day, monsieur."
ham	She said it aloud, but added to herself, as she resumed her knitting:
ham	"Hah! Good day, age about forty, height about five feet nine, black
spam	hair, generally rather handsome visage, complexion dark, eyes dark,
ham	thin, long and sallow face, aquiline nose but not straight, having a
ham	peculiar inclination towards the left cheek which imparts a sinister
spam	expression! Good day, one and all!"
spam	"Have the goodness to give me a little glass of old cognac, and a
spam	mouthful of cool fresh water, madame."
ham	Madame complied with a polite air.
spam	"Marvellous cognac this, madame!"
spam	It was the first time it had ever been so complimented, and Madame
ham	Defarge knew enough of its antecedents to know better. She said,
ham	however, that the cognac was flattered, and took up her knitting. The
spam	visitor watched her fingers for a few moments, and took the opportunity
ham	of observing the place in general.
ham	"You knit with great skill, madame."
spam	"I am accustomed to it."
spam	"A pretty pattern too!"
ham	"_You_ think so?" said madame, looking at him with a smile.
spam	"Decidedly. May one ask what it is for?"
spam	"Pastime," said madame, still looking at him with a smile while her
ham	fingers moved nimbly.
ham	"Not for use?"
spam	"That depends. I may find a use for it one day. If I do--Well," said
ham	madame, drawing a breath and nodding her head with a stern kind of
ham	coquetry, "I'll use it!"
spam	It was remarkable; but, the taste of Saint Antoine seemed to be
spam	decidedly opposed to a rose on the head-dress of Madame Defarge. Two
spam	men had entered separately, and had been about to order drink, when,
spam	catching sight of that novelty, they faltered, made a pretence of
ham	looking about as if for some friend who was not there, and went away.
spam	Nor, of those who had been there when this visitor entered, was there
spam	one left. They had all dropped off. The spy had kept his eyes open,
ham	but had been able to detect no sign. They had lounged away in a
ham	poverty-stricken, purposeless, accidental manner, quite natural and
spam	unimpeachable.
spam	"_John_," thought madame, checking off her work as her fingers knitted,
ham	and her eyes looked at the stranger. "Stay long enough, and I shall knit
spam	'BARSAD' before you go."
ham	"You have a husband, madame?"
ham	"I have."
spam	"Children?"
ham	"No children."
ham	"Business seems bad?"
spam	"Business is very bad; the people are so poor."
spam	"Ah, the unfortunate, miserable people! So oppressed, too--as you say."
ham	"As _you_ say," madame retorted, correcting him, and deftly knitting an
ham	extra something into his name that boded him no good.
spam	"Pardon me; certainly it was I who said so, but you naturally think so.
ham	Of course."
spam	"_I_ think?" returned madame, in a high voice. "I and my husband have
ham	enough to do to keep this wine-shop open, without thinking. All we
ham	think, here, is how to live. That is the subject _we_ think of, and
ham	it gives us, from morning to night, enough to think about, without
spam	embarrassing our heads concerning others. _I_ think for others? No, no."
spam	The spy, who was there to pick up any crumbs he could find or make, did
ham	not allow his baffled state to express itself in his sinister face; but,
ham	stood with an air of gossiping gallantry, leaning his elbow on Madame
ham	Defarge's little counter, and occasionally sipping his cognac.
spam	"A bad business this, madame, of Gaspard's execution. Ah! the poor
ham	Gaspard!" With a sigh of great compassion.
ham	"My faith!" returned madame, coolly and lightly, "if people use knives
ham	for such purposes, they have to pay for it. He knew beforehand what the
spam	price of his luxury was; he has paid the price."
spam	"I believe," said the spy, dropping his soft voice to a tone
ham	that invited confidence, and expressing an injured revolutionary
