spam	susceptibility in every muscle of his wicked face: "I believe there
ham	is much compassion and anger in this neighbourhood, touching the poor
spam	fellow? Between ourselves."
ham	"Is there?" asked madame, vacantly.
ham	"Is there not?"
spam	"--Here is my husband!" said Madame Defarge.
spam	As the keeper of the wine-shop entered at the door, the spy saluted
ham	him by touching his hat, and saying, with an engaging smile, "Good day,
spam	Jacques!" Defarge stopped short, and stared at him.
ham	"Good day, Jacques!" the spy repeated; with not quite so much
spam	confidence, or quite so easy a smile under the stare.
spam	"You deceive yourself, monsieur," returned the keeper of the wine-shop.
spam	"You mistake me for another. That is not my name. I am Ernest Defarge."
ham	"It is all the same," said the spy, airily, but discomfited too: "good
ham	day!"
ham	"Good day!" answered Defarge, drily.
spam	"I was saying to madame, with whom I had the pleasure of chatting when
spam	you entered, that they tell me there is--and no wonder!--much sympathy
ham	and anger in Saint Antoine, touching the unhappy fate of poor Gaspard."
ham	"No one has told me so," said Defarge, shaking his head. "I know nothing
ham	of it."
ham	Having said it, he passed behind the little counter, and stood with his
ham	hand on the back of his wife's chair, looking over that barrier at the
spam	person to whom they were both opposed, and whom either of them would
spam	have shot with the greatest satisfaction.
ham	The spy, well used to his business, did not change his unconscious
ham	attitude, but drained his little glass of cognac, took a sip of fresh
spam	water, and asked for another glass of cognac. Madame Defarge poured it
spam	out for him, took to her knitting again, and hummed a little song over
ham	it.
spam	"You seem to know this quarter well; that is to say, better than I do?"
ham	observed Defarge.
spam	"Not at all, but I hope to know it better. I am so profoundly interested
spam	in its miserable inhabitants."
ham	"Hah!" muttered Defarge.
spam	"The pleasure of conversing with you, Monsieur Defarge, recalls to me,"
spam	pursued the spy, "that I have the honour of cherishing some interesting
spam	associations with your name."
spam	"Indeed!" said Defarge, with much indifference.
ham	"Yes, indeed. When Doctor Manette was released, you, his old domestic,
ham	had the charge of him, I know. He was delivered to you. You see I am
spam	informed of the circumstances?"
spam	"Such is the fact, certainly," said Defarge. He had had it conveyed
spam	to him, in an accidental touch of his wife's elbow as she knitted and
ham	warbled, that he would do best to answer, but always with brevity.
spam	"It was to you," said the spy, "that his daughter came; and it was
spam	from your care that his daughter took him, accompanied by a neat brown
ham	monsieur; how is he called?--in a little wig--Lorry--of the bank of
spam	Tellson and Company--over to England."
ham	"Such is the fact," repeated Defarge.
ham	"Very interesting remembrances!" said the spy. "I have known Doctor
spam	Manette and his daughter, in England."
spam	"Yes?" said Defarge.
ham	"You don't hear much about them now?" said the spy.
spam	"No," said Defarge.
ham	"In effect," madame struck in, looking up from her work and her little
ham	song, "we never hear about them. We received the news of their safe
ham	arrival, and perhaps another letter, or perhaps two; but, since then,
spam	they have gradually taken their road in life--we, ours--and we have held
ham	no correspondence."
ham	"Perfectly so, madame," replied the spy. "She is going to be married."
ham	"Going?" echoed madame. "She was pretty enough to have been married long
ham	ago. You English are cold, it seems to me."
ham	"Oh! You know I am English."
spam	"I perceive your tongue is," returned madame; "and what the tongue is, I
spam	suppose the man is."
ham	He did not take the identification as a compliment; but he made the best
ham	of it, and turned it off with a laugh. After sipping his cognac to the
ham	end, he added:
spam	"Yes, Miss Manette is going to be married. But not to an Englishman; to
spam	one who, like herself, is French by birth. And speaking of Gaspard (ah,
ham	poor Gaspard! It was cruel, cruel!), it is a curious thing that she is
ham	going to marry the nephew of Monsieur the Marquis, for whom Gaspard
spam	was exalted to that height of so many feet; in other words, the present
spam	Marquis. But he lives unknown in England, he is no Marquis there; he is
spam	Mr. Charles Darnay. D'Aulnais is the name of his mother's family."
spam	Madame Defarge knitted steadily, but the intelligence had a palpable
ham	effect upon her husband. Do what he would, behind the little counter,
spam	as to the striking of a light and the lighting of his pipe, he was
spam	troubled, and his hand was not trustworthy. The spy would have been no
ham	spy if he had failed to see it, or to record it in his mind.
ham	Having made, at least, this one hit, whatever it might prove to be
spam	worth, and no customers coming in to help him to any other, Mr. Barsad
spam	paid for what he had drunk, and took his leave: taking occasion to say,
spam	in a genteel manner, before he departed, that he looked forward to the
spam	pleasure of seeing Monsieur and Madame Defarge again. For some minutes
ham	after he had emerged into the outer presence of Saint Antoine, the
ham	husband and wife remained exactly as he had left them, lest he should
ham	come back.
ham	"Can it be true," said Defarge, in a low voice, looking down at his wife
ham	as he stood smoking with his hand on the back of her chair: "what he has
ham	said of Ma'amselle Manette?"
ham	"As he has said it," returned madame, lifting her eyebrows a little, "it
spam	is probably false. But it may be true."
ham	"If it is--" Defarge began, and stopped.
spam	"If it is?" repeated his wife.
spam	"--And if it does come, while we live to see it triumph--I hope, for her
ham	sake, Destiny will keep her husband out of France."
ham	"Her husband's destiny," said Madame Defarge, with her usual composure,
spam	"will take him where he is to go, and will lead him to the end that is
spam	to end him. That is all I know."
ham	"But it is very strange--now, at least, is it not very strange"--said
ham	Defarge, rather pleading with his wife to induce her to admit it,
spam	"that, after all our sympathy for Monsieur her father, and herself, her
ham	husband's name should be proscribed under your hand at this moment, by
spam	the side of that infernal dog's who has just left us?"
ham	"Stranger things than that will happen when it does come," answered
spam	madame. "I have them both here, of a certainty; and they are both here
ham	for their merits; that is enough."
spam	She rolled up her knitting when she had said those words, and presently
ham	took the rose out of the handkerchief that was wound about her head.
spam	Either Saint Antoine had an instinctive sense that the objectionable
spam	decoration was gone, or Saint Antoine was on the watch for its
ham	disappearance; howbeit, the Saint took courage to lounge in, very
spam	shortly afterwards, and the wine-shop recovered its habitual aspect.
spam	In the evening, at which season of all others Saint Antoine turned
ham	himself inside out, and sat on door-steps and window-ledges, and came
spam	to the corners of vile streets and courts, for a breath of air, Madame
ham	Defarge with her work in her hand was accustomed to pass from place
ham	to place and from group to group: a Missionary--there were many like
ham	her--such as the world will do well never to breed again. All the women
ham	knitted. They knitted worthless things; but, the mechanical work was a
spam	mechanical substitute for eating and drinking; the hands moved for the
ham	jaws and the digestive apparatus: if the bony fingers had been still,
spam	the stomachs would have been more famine-pinched.
spam	But, as the fingers went, the eyes went, and the thoughts. And as Madame
ham	Defarge moved on from group to group, all three went quicker and fiercer
spam	among every little knot of women that she had spoken with, and left
ham	behind.
ham	Her husband smoked at his door, looking after her with admiration. "A
ham	great woman," said he, "a strong woman, a grand woman, a frightfully
ham	grand woman!"
ham	Darkness closed around, and then came the ringing of church bells and
ham	the distant beating of the military drums in the Palace Courtyard, as
ham	the women sat knitting, knitting. Darkness encompassed them. Another
spam	darkness was closing in as surely, when the church bells, then ringing
spam	pleasantly in many an airy steeple over France, should be melted into
ham	thundering cannon; when the military drums should be beating to drown a
ham	wretched voice, that night all potent as the voice of Power and Plenty,
spam	Freedom and Life. So much was closing in about the women who sat
spam	knitting, knitting, that they their very selves were closing in around
ham	a structure yet unbuilt, where they were to sit knitting, knitting,
ham	counting dropping heads.
ham	XVII. One Night
ham	Never did the sun go down with a brighter glory on the quiet corner in
spam	Soho, than one memorable evening when the Doctor and his daughter sat
spam	under the plane-tree together. Never did the moon rise with a milder
ham	radiance over great London, than on that night when it found them still
spam	seated under the tree, and shone upon their faces through its leaves.
ham	Lucie was to be married to-morrow. She had reserved this last evening
spam	for her father, and they sat alone under the plane-tree.
ham	"You are happy, my dear father?"
ham	"Quite, my child."
ham	They had said little, though they had been there a long time. When it
spam	was yet light enough to work and read, she had neither engaged herself
spam	in her usual work, nor had she read to him. She had employed herself in
ham	both ways, at his side under the tree, many and many a time; but, this
ham	time was not quite like any other, and nothing could make it so.
spam	"And I am very happy to-night, dear father. I am deeply happy in the
ham	love that Heaven has so blessed--my love for Charles, and Charles's love
spam	for me. But, if my life were not to be still consecrated to you, or
ham	if my marriage were so arranged as that it would part us, even by
spam	the length of a few of these streets, I should be more unhappy and
spam	self-reproachful now than I can tell you. Even as it is--"
spam	Even as it was, she could not command her voice.
ham	In the sad moonlight, she clasped him by the neck, and laid her face
ham	upon his breast. In the moonlight which is always sad, as the light of
spam	the sun itself is--as the light called human life is--at its coming and
ham	its going.
ham	"Dearest dear! Can you tell me, this last time, that you feel quite,
ham	quite sure, no new affections of mine, and no new duties of mine, will
ham	ever interpose between us? _I_ know it well, but do you know it? In your
ham	own heart, do you feel quite certain?"
ham	Her father answered, with a cheerful firmness of conviction he could
spam	scarcely have assumed, "Quite sure, my darling! More than that," he
spam	added, as he tenderly kissed her: "my future is far brighter, Lucie,
spam	seen through your marriage, than it could have been--nay, than it ever
spam	was--without it."
spam	"If I could hope _that_, my father!--"
ham	"Believe it, love! Indeed it is so. Consider how natural and how plain
spam	it is, my dear, that it should be so. You, devoted and young, cannot
ham	fully appreciate the anxiety I have felt that your life should not be
ham	wasted--"
ham	She moved her hand towards his lips, but he took it in his, and repeated
spam	the word.
spam	"--wasted, my child--should not be wasted, struck aside from the
spam	natural order of things--for my sake. Your unselfishness cannot entirely
spam	comprehend how much my mind has gone on this; but, only ask yourself,
ham	how could my happiness be perfect, while yours was incomplete?"
spam	"If I had never seen Charles, my father, I should have been quite happy
spam	with you."
ham	He smiled at her unconscious admission that she would have been unhappy
ham	without Charles, having seen him; and replied:
spam	"My child, you did see him, and it is Charles. If it had not been
ham	Charles, it would have been another. Or, if it had been no other, I
ham	should have been the cause, and then the dark part of my life would have
spam	cast its shadow beyond myself, and would have fallen on you."
spam	It was the first time, except at the trial, of her ever hearing him
spam	refer to the period of his suffering. It gave her a strange and new
ham	sensation while his words were in her ears; and she remembered it long
ham	afterwards.
spam	"See!" said the Doctor of Beauvais, raising his hand towards the moon.
ham	"I have looked at her from my prison-window, when I could not bear her
spam	light. I have looked at her when it has been such torture to me to think
spam	of her shining upon what I had lost, that I have beaten my head against
ham	my prison-walls. I have looked at her, in a state so dull and lethargic,
ham	that I have thought of nothing but the number of horizontal lines I
ham	could draw across her at the full, and the number of perpendicular lines
ham	with which I could intersect them." He added in his inward and pondering
spam	manner, as he looked at the moon, "It was twenty either way, I remember,
ham	and the twentieth was difficult to squeeze in."
ham	The strange thrill with which she heard him go back to that time,
spam	deepened as he dwelt upon it; but, there was nothing to shock her in
ham	the manner of his reference. He only seemed to contrast his present
spam	cheerfulness and felicity with the dire endurance that was over.
spam	"I have looked at her, speculating thousands of times upon the unborn
spam	child from whom I had been rent. Whether it was alive. Whether it had
ham	been born alive, or the poor mother's shock had killed it. Whether it
ham	was a son who would some day avenge his father. (There was a time in my
ham	imprisonment, when my desire for vengeance was unbearable.) Whether it
spam	was a son who would never know his father's story; who might even live
ham	to weigh the possibility of his father's having disappeared of his own
spam	will and act. Whether it was a daughter who would grow to be a woman."
spam	She drew closer to him, and kissed his cheek and his hand.
spam	"I have pictured my daughter, to myself, as perfectly forgetful of
spam	me--rather, altogether ignorant of me, and unconscious of me. I have
ham	cast up the years of her age, year after year. I have seen her married
spam	to a man who knew nothing of my fate. I have altogether perished from
ham	the remembrance of the living, and in the next generation my place was a
spam	blank."
ham	"My father! Even to hear that you had such thoughts of a daughter who
ham	never existed, strikes to my heart as if I had been that child."
spam	"You, Lucie? It is out of the Consolation and restoration you have
spam	brought to me, that these remembrances arise, and pass between us and
ham	the moon on this last night.--What did I say just now?"
spam	"She knew nothing of you. She cared nothing for you."
spam	"So! But on other moonlight nights, when the sadness and the silence
spam	have touched me in a different way--have affected me with something as
ham	like a sorrowful sense of peace, as any emotion that had pain for its
ham	foundations could--I have imagined her as coming to me in my cell, and
ham	leading me out into the freedom beyond the fortress. I have seen her
spam	image in the moonlight often, as I now see you; except that I never held
spam	her in my arms; it stood between the little grated window and the door.
spam	But, you understand that that was not the child I am speaking of?"
spam	"The figure was not; the--the--image; the fancy?"
ham	"No. That was another thing. It stood before my disturbed sense of
spam	sight, but it never moved. The phantom that my mind pursued, was another
spam	and more real child. Of her outward appearance I know no more than
spam	that she was like her mother. The other had that likeness too--as you
spam	have--but was not the same. Can you follow me, Lucie? Hardly, I think?
spam	I doubt you must have been a solitary prisoner to understand these
spam	perplexed distinctions."
spam	His collected and calm manner could not prevent her blood from running
ham	cold, as he thus tried to anatomise his old condition.
ham	"In that more peaceful state, I have imagined her, in the moonlight,
spam	coming to me and taking me out to show me that the home of her married
ham	life was full of her loving remembrance of her lost father. My picture
spam	was in her room, and I was in her prayers. Her life was active,
spam	cheerful, useful; but my poor history pervaded it all."
ham	"I was that child, my father, I was not half so good, but in my love
spam	that was I."
ham	"And she showed me her children," said the Doctor of Beauvais, "and
spam	they had heard of me, and had been taught to pity me. When they passed
spam	a prison of the State, they kept far from its frowning walls, and looked
ham	up at its bars, and spoke in whispers. She could never deliver me; I
spam	imagined that she always brought me back after showing me such things.
ham	But then, blessed with the relief of tears, I fell upon my knees, and
spam	blessed her."
ham	"I am that child, I hope, my father. O my dear, my dear, will you bless
spam	me as fervently to-morrow?"
ham	"Lucie, I recall these old troubles in the reason that I have to-night
ham	for loving you better than words can tell, and thanking God for my great
spam	happiness. My thoughts, when they were wildest, never rose near the
ham	happiness that I have known with you, and that we have before us."
spam	He embraced her, solemnly commended her to Heaven, and humbly thanked
ham	Heaven for having bestowed her on him. By-and-bye, they went into the
spam	house.
ham	There was no one bidden to the marriage but Mr. Lorry; there was even to
spam	be no bridesmaid but the gaunt Miss Pross. The marriage was to make no
ham	change in their place of residence; they had been able to extend it,
spam	by taking to themselves the upper rooms formerly belonging to the
spam	apocryphal invisible lodger, and they desired nothing more.
spam	Doctor Manette was very cheerful at the little supper. They were only
ham	three at table, and Miss Pross made the third. He regretted that Charles
spam	was not there; was more than half disposed to object to the loving
spam	little plot that kept him away; and drank to him affectionately.
ham	So, the time came for him to bid Lucie good night, and they separated.
spam	But, in the stillness of the third hour of the morning, Lucie came
ham	downstairs again, and stole into his room; not free from unshaped fears,
spam	beforehand.
spam	All things, however, were in their places; all was quiet; and he lay
ham	asleep, his white hair picturesque on the untroubled pillow, and his
spam	hands lying quiet on the coverlet. She put her needless candle in the
ham	shadow at a distance, crept up to his bed, and put her lips to his;
ham	then, leaned over him, and looked at him.
ham	Into his handsome face, the bitter waters of captivity had worn; but, he
ham	covered up their tracks with a determination so strong, that he held the
spam	mastery of them even in his sleep. A more remarkable face in its quiet,
ham	resolute, and guarded struggle with an unseen assailant, was not to be
ham	beheld in all the wide dominions of sleep, that night.
ham	She timidly laid her hand on his dear breast, and put up a prayer that
spam	she might ever be as true to him as her love aspired to be, and as his
spam	sorrows deserved. Then, she withdrew her hand, and kissed his lips once
ham	more, and went away. So, the sunrise came, and the shadows of the leaves
spam	of the plane-tree moved upon his face, as softly as her lips had moved
ham	in praying for him.
ham	XVIII. Nine Days
spam	The marriage-day was shining brightly, and they were ready outside the
spam	closed door of the Doctor's room, where he was speaking with Charles
spam	Darnay. They were ready to go to church; the beautiful bride, Mr.
ham	Lorry, and Miss Pross--to whom the event, through a gradual process of
ham	reconcilement to the inevitable, would have been one of absolute bliss,
spam	but for the yet lingering consideration that her brother Solomon should
spam	have been the bridegroom.
ham	"And so," said Mr. Lorry, who could not sufficiently admire the bride,
spam	and who had been moving round her to take in every point of her quiet,
spam	pretty dress; "and so it was for this, my sweet Lucie, that I brought
ham	you across the Channel, such a baby! Lord bless me! How little I thought
spam	what I was doing! How lightly I valued the obligation I was conferring
spam	on my friend Mr. Charles!"
ham	"You didn't mean it," remarked the matter-of-fact Miss Pross, "and
spam	therefore how could you know it? Nonsense!"
spam	"Really? Well; but don't cry," said the gentle Mr. Lorry.
ham	"I am not crying," said Miss Pross; "_you_ are."
ham	"I, my Pross?" (By this time, Mr. Lorry dared to be pleasant with her,
ham	on occasion.)
spam	"You were, just now; I saw you do it, and I don't wonder at it. Such
ham	a present of plate as you have made 'em, is enough to bring tears into
ham	anybody's eyes. There's not a fork or a spoon in the collection," said
spam	Miss Pross, "that I didn't cry over, last night after the box came, till
ham	I couldn't see it."
ham	"I am highly gratified," said Mr. Lorry, "though, upon my honour, I
ham	had no intention of rendering those trifling articles of remembrance
ham	invisible to any one. Dear me! This is an occasion that makes a man
ham	speculate on all he has lost. Dear, dear, dear! To think that there
ham	might have been a Mrs. Lorry, any time these fifty years almost!"
spam	"Not at all!" From Miss Pross.
spam	"You think there never might have been a Mrs. Lorry?" asked the
spam	gentleman of that name.
spam	"Pooh!" rejoined Miss Pross; "you were a bachelor in your cradle."
spam	"Well!" observed Mr. Lorry, beamingly adjusting his little wig, "that
ham	seems probable, too."
ham	"And you were cut out for a bachelor," pursued Miss Pross, "before you
spam	were put in your cradle."
ham	"Then, I think," said Mr. Lorry, "that I was very unhandsomely dealt
ham	with, and that I ought to have had a voice in the selection of my
ham	pattern. Enough! Now, my dear Lucie," drawing his arm soothingly round
ham	her waist, "I hear them moving in the next room, and Miss Pross and
spam	I, as two formal folks of business, are anxious not to lose the final
ham	opportunity of saying something to you that you wish to hear. You leave
ham	your good father, my dear, in hands as earnest and as loving as your
ham	own; he shall be taken every conceivable care of; during the next
spam	fortnight, while you are in Warwickshire and thereabouts, even Tellson's
spam	shall go to the wall (comparatively speaking) before him. And when, at
ham	the fortnight's end, he comes to join you and your beloved husband, on
ham	your other fortnight's trip in Wales, you shall say that we have sent
spam	him to you in the best health and in the happiest frame. Now, I hear
ham	Somebody's step coming to the door. Let me kiss my dear girl with an
ham	old-fashioned bachelor blessing, before Somebody comes to claim his
spam	own."
ham	For a moment, he held the fair face from him to look at the
spam	well-remembered expression on the forehead, and then laid the bright
spam	golden hair against his little brown wig, with a genuine tenderness and
spam	delicacy which, if such things be old-fashioned, were as old as Adam.
spam	The door of the Doctor's room opened, and he came out with Charles
spam	Darnay. He was so deadly pale--which had not been the case when they
spam	went in together--that no vestige of colour was to be seen in his face.
ham	But, in the composure of his manner he was unaltered, except that to the
spam	shrewd glance of Mr. Lorry it disclosed some shadowy indication that the
spam	old air of avoidance and dread had lately passed over him, like a cold
ham	wind.
ham	He gave his arm to his daughter, and took her down-stairs to the chariot
ham	which Mr. Lorry had hired in honour of the day. The rest followed in
spam	another carriage, and soon, in a neighbouring church, where no strange
spam	eyes looked on, Charles Darnay and Lucie Manette were happily married.
ham	Besides the glancing tears that shone among the smiles of the little
ham	group when it was done, some diamonds, very bright and sparkling,
spam	glanced on the bride's hand, which were newly released from the
ham	dark obscurity of one of Mr. Lorry's pockets. They returned home to
ham	breakfast, and all went well, and in due course the golden hair that had
ham	mingled with the poor shoemaker's white locks in the Paris garret, were
ham	mingled with them again in the morning sunlight, on the threshold of the
spam	door at parting.
spam	It was a hard parting, though it was not for long. But her father
ham	cheered her, and said at last, gently disengaging himself from her
spam	enfolding arms, "Take her, Charles! She is yours!"
ham	And her agitated hand waved to them from a chaise window, and she was
ham	gone.
ham	The corner being out of the way of the idle and curious, and the
ham	preparations having been very simple and few, the Doctor, Mr. Lorry,
spam	and Miss Pross, were left quite alone. It was when they turned into
spam	the welcome shade of the cool old hall, that Mr. Lorry observed a great
spam	change to have come over the Doctor; as if the golden arm uplifted
spam	there, had struck him a poisoned blow.
spam	He had naturally repressed much, and some revulsion might have been
ham	expected in him when the occasion for repression was gone. But, it was
ham	the old scared lost look that troubled Mr. Lorry; and through his absent
ham	manner of clasping his head and drearily wandering away into his own
ham	room when they got up-stairs, Mr. Lorry was reminded of Defarge the
ham	wine-shop keeper, and the starlight ride.
ham	"I think," he whispered to Miss Pross, after anxious consideration, "I
spam	think we had best not speak to him just now, or at all disturb him.
ham	I must look in at Tellson's; so I will go there at once and come back
spam	presently. Then, we will take him a ride into the country, and dine
ham	there, and all will be well."
spam	It was easier for Mr. Lorry to look in at Tellson's, than to look out of
spam	Tellson's. He was detained two hours. When he came back, he ascended the
ham	old staircase alone, having asked no question of the servant; going thus
spam	into the Doctor's rooms, he was stopped by a low sound of knocking.
spam	"Good God!" he said, with a start. "What's that?"
spam	Miss Pross, with a terrified face, was at his ear. "O me, O me! All is
spam	lost!" cried she, wringing her hands. "What is to be told to Ladybird?
spam	He doesn't know me, and is making shoes!"
ham	Mr. Lorry said what he could to calm her, and went himself into the
ham	Doctor's room. The bench was turned towards the light, as it had been
ham	when he had seen the shoemaker at his work before, and his head was bent
spam	down, and he was very busy.
ham	"Doctor Manette. My dear friend, Doctor Manette!"
ham	The Doctor looked at him for a moment--half inquiringly, half as if he
ham	were angry at being spoken to--and bent over his work again.
spam	He had laid aside his coat and waistcoat; his shirt was open at the
ham	throat, as it used to be when he did that work; and even the old
spam	haggard, faded surface of face had come back to him. He worked
spam	hard--impatiently--as if in some sense of having been interrupted.
spam	Mr. Lorry glanced at the work in his hand, and observed that it was a
ham	shoe of the old size and shape. He took up another that was lying by
spam	him, and asked what it was.
spam	"A young lady's walking shoe," he muttered, without looking up. "It
spam	ought to have been finished long ago. Let it be."
ham	"But, Doctor Manette. Look at me!"
spam	He obeyed, in the old mechanically submissive manner, without pausing in
ham	his work.
ham	"You know me, my dear friend? Think again. This is not your proper
spam	occupation. Think, dear friend!"
ham	Nothing would induce him to speak more. He looked up, for an instant at
ham	a time, when he was requested to do so; but, no persuasion would extract
spam	a word from him. He worked, and worked, and worked, in silence, and
ham	words fell on him as they would have fallen on an echoless wall, or on
ham	the air. The only ray of hope that Mr. Lorry could discover, was, that
ham	he sometimes furtively looked up without being asked. In that, there
spam	seemed a faint expression of curiosity or perplexity--as though he were
ham	trying to reconcile some doubts in his mind.
ham	Two things at once impressed themselves on Mr. Lorry, as important above
spam	all others; the first, that this must be kept secret from Lucie;
ham	the second, that it must be kept secret from all who knew him. In
ham	conjunction with Miss Pross, he took immediate steps towards the latter
ham	precaution, by giving out that the Doctor was not well, and required a
spam	few days of complete rest. In aid of the kind deception to be practised
ham	on his daughter, Miss Pross was to write, describing his having been
spam	called away professionally, and referring to an imaginary letter of
ham	two or three hurried lines in his own hand, represented to have been
ham	addressed to her by the same post.
spam	These measures, advisable to be taken in any case, Mr. Lorry took in
ham	the hope of his coming to himself. If that should happen soon, he kept
ham	another course in reserve; which was, to have a certain opinion that he
spam	thought the best, on the Doctor's case.
ham	In the hope of his recovery, and of resort to this third course
ham	being thereby rendered practicable, Mr. Lorry resolved to watch him
spam	attentively, with as little appearance as possible of doing so. He
spam	therefore made arrangements to absent himself from Tellson's for the
spam	first time in his life, and took his post by the window in the same
spam	room.
ham	He was not long in discovering that it was worse than useless to speak
ham	to him, since, on being pressed, he became worried. He abandoned that
ham	attempt on the first day, and resolved merely to keep himself always
ham	before him, as a silent protest against the delusion into which he had
ham	fallen, or was falling. He remained, therefore, in his seat near the
spam	window, reading and writing, and expressing in as many pleasant and
spam	natural ways as he could think of, that it was a free place.
spam	Doctor Manette took what was given him to eat and drink, and worked on,
spam	that first day, until it was too dark to see--worked on, half an hour
ham	after Mr. Lorry could not have seen, for his life, to read or write.
spam	When he put his tools aside as useless, until morning, Mr. Lorry rose
spam	and said to him:
spam	"Will you go out?"
ham	He looked down at the floor on either side of him in the old manner,
ham	looked up in the old manner, and repeated in the old low voice:
spam	"Out?"
spam	"Yes; for a walk with me. Why not?"
spam	He made no effort to say why not, and said not a word more. But, Mr.
spam	Lorry thought he saw, as he leaned forward on his bench in the dusk,
spam	with his elbows on his knees and his head in his hands, that he was in
ham	some misty way asking himself, "Why not?" The sagacity of the man of
spam	business perceived an advantage here, and determined to hold it.
spam	Miss Pross and he divided the night into two watches, and observed him
spam	at intervals from the adjoining room. He paced up and down for a long
ham	time before he lay down; but, when he did finally lay himself down, he
ham	fell asleep. In the morning, he was up betimes, and went straight to his
spam	bench and to work.
spam	On this second day, Mr. Lorry saluted him cheerfully by his name,
ham	and spoke to him on topics that had been of late familiar to them. He
ham	returned no reply, but it was evident that he heard what was said, and
spam	that he thought about it, however confusedly. This encouraged Mr. Lorry
spam	to have Miss Pross in with her work, several times during the day;
spam	at those times, they quietly spoke of Lucie, and of her father then
spam	present, precisely in the usual manner, and as if there were nothing
ham	amiss. This was done without any demonstrative accompaniment, not long
ham	enough, or often enough to harass him; and it lightened Mr. Lorry's
spam	friendly heart to believe that he looked up oftener, and that he
ham	appeared to be stirred by some perception of inconsistencies surrounding
ham	him.
ham	When it fell dark again, Mr. Lorry asked him as before:
ham	"Dear Doctor, will you go out?"
spam	As before, he repeated, "Out?"
ham	"Yes; for a walk with me. Why not?"
spam	This time, Mr. Lorry feigned to go out when he could extract no answer
ham	from him, and, after remaining absent for an hour, returned. In the
spam	meanwhile, the Doctor had removed to the seat in the window, and had
ham	sat there looking down at the plane-tree; but, on Mr. Lorry's return, he
ham	slipped away to his bench.
spam	The time went very slowly on, and Mr. Lorry's hope darkened, and his
spam	heart grew heavier again, and grew yet heavier and heavier every day.
ham	The third day came and went, the fourth, the fifth. Five days, six days,
spam	seven days, eight days, nine days.
ham	With a hope ever darkening, and with a heart always growing heavier and
ham	heavier, Mr. Lorry passed through this anxious time. The secret was
spam	well kept, and Lucie was unconscious and happy; but he could not fail to
spam	observe that the shoemaker, whose hand had been a little out at first,
ham	was growing dreadfully skilful, and that he had never been so intent on
spam	his work, and that his hands had never been so nimble and expert, as in
spam	the dusk of the ninth evening.
spam	XIX. An Opinion
ham	Worn out by anxious watching, Mr. Lorry fell asleep at his post. On the
ham	tenth morning of his suspense, he was startled by the shining of the sun
spam	into the room where a heavy slumber had overtaken him when it was dark
spam	night.
ham	He rubbed his eyes and roused himself; but he doubted, when he had
spam	done so, whether he was not still asleep. For, going to the door of the
spam	Doctor's room and looking in, he perceived that the shoemaker's bench
spam	and tools were put aside again, and that the Doctor himself sat reading
spam	at the window. He was in his usual morning dress, and his face (which
ham	Mr. Lorry could distinctly see), though still very pale, was calmly
spam	studious and attentive.
spam	Even when he had satisfied himself that he was awake, Mr. Lorry felt
spam	giddily uncertain for some few moments whether the late shoemaking might
ham	not be a disturbed dream of his own; for, did not his eyes show him his
spam	friend before him in his accustomed clothing and aspect, and employed
ham	as usual; and was there any sign within their range, that the change of
ham	which he had so strong an impression had actually happened?
spam	It was but the inquiry of his first confusion and astonishment, the
spam	answer being obvious. If the impression were not produced by a real
spam	corresponding and sufficient cause, how came he, Jarvis Lorry, there?
ham	How came he to have fallen asleep, in his clothes, on the sofa in Doctor
spam	Manette's consulting-room, and to be debating these points outside the
ham	Doctor's bedroom door in the early morning?
spam	Within a few minutes, Miss Pross stood whispering at his side. If he
ham	had had any particle of doubt left, her talk would of necessity have
spam	resolved it; but he was by that time clear-headed, and had none.
spam	He advised that they should let the time go by until the regular
spam	breakfast-hour, and should then meet the Doctor as if nothing unusual
spam	had occurred. If he appeared to be in his customary state of mind, Mr.
spam	Lorry would then cautiously proceed to seek direction and guidance from
spam	the opinion he had been, in his anxiety, so anxious to obtain.
spam	Miss Pross, submitting herself to his judgment, the scheme was worked
spam	out with care. Having abundance of time for his usual methodical
spam	toilette, Mr. Lorry presented himself at the breakfast-hour in his usual
spam	white linen, and with his usual neat leg. The Doctor was summoned in the
ham	usual way, and came to breakfast.
ham	So far as it was possible to comprehend him without overstepping those
ham	delicate and gradual approaches which Mr. Lorry felt to be the only safe
spam	advance, he at first supposed that his daughter's marriage had taken
spam	place yesterday. An incidental allusion, purposely thrown out, to
spam	the day of the week, and the day of the month, set him thinking and
spam	counting, and evidently made him uneasy. In all other respects, however,
spam	he was so composedly himself, that Mr. Lorry determined to have the aid
spam	he sought. And that aid was his own.
spam	Therefore, when the breakfast was done and cleared away, and he and the
ham	Doctor were left together, Mr. Lorry said, feelingly:
spam	"My dear Manette, I am anxious to have your opinion, in confidence, on a
spam	very curious case in which I am deeply interested; that is to say, it is
ham	very curious to me; perhaps, to your better information it may be less
ham	so."
spam	Glancing at his hands, which were discoloured by his late work, the
spam	Doctor looked troubled, and listened attentively. He had already glanced
spam	at his hands more than once.
ham	"Doctor Manette," said Mr. Lorry, touching him affectionately on the
spam	arm, "the case is the case of a particularly dear friend of mine. Pray
ham	give your mind to it, and advise me well for his sake--and above all,
spam	for his daughter's--his daughter's, my dear Manette."
ham	"If I understand," said the Doctor, in a subdued tone, "some mental
spam	shock--?"
ham	"Yes!"
spam	"Be explicit," said the Doctor. "Spare no detail."
ham	Mr. Lorry saw that they understood one another, and proceeded.
ham	"My dear Manette, it is the case of an old and a prolonged shock,
spam	of great acuteness and severity to the affections, the feelings,
spam	the--the--as you express it--the mind. The mind. It is the case of a
ham	shock under which the sufferer was borne down, one cannot say for how
ham	long, because I believe he cannot calculate the time himself, and there
ham	are no other means of getting at it. It is the case of a shock from
spam	which the sufferer recovered, by a process that he cannot trace
ham	himself--as I once heard him publicly relate in a striking manner. It is
ham	the case of a shock from which he has recovered, so completely, as to
spam	be a highly intelligent man, capable of close application of mind, and
ham	great exertion of body, and of constantly making fresh additions to his
ham	stock of knowledge, which was already very large. But, unfortunately,
spam	there has been," he paused and took a deep breath--"a slight relapse."
ham	The Doctor, in a low voice, asked, "Of how long duration?"
ham	"Nine days and nights."
ham	"How did it show itself? I infer," glancing at his hands again, "in the
ham	resumption of some old pursuit connected with the shock?"
spam	"That is the fact."
spam	"Now, did you ever see him," asked the Doctor, distinctly and
spam	collectedly, though in the same low voice, "engaged in that pursuit
spam	originally?"
ham	"Once."
spam	"And when the relapse fell on him, was he in most respects--or in all
ham	respects--as he was then?"
ham	"I think in all respects."
spam	"You spoke of his daughter. Does his daughter know of the relapse?"
ham	"No. It has been kept from her, and I hope will always be kept from her.
spam	It is known only to myself, and to one other who may be trusted."
spam	The Doctor grasped his hand, and murmured, "That was very kind. That was
ham	very thoughtful!" Mr. Lorry grasped his hand in return, and neither of
spam	the two spoke for a little while.
spam	"Now, my dear Manette," said Mr. Lorry, at length, in his most
spam	considerate and most affectionate way, "I am a mere man of business,
ham	and unfit to cope with such intricate and difficult matters. I do not
ham	possess the kind of information necessary; I do not possess the kind of
ham	intelligence; I want guiding. There is no man in this world on whom
spam	I could so rely for right guidance, as on you. Tell me, how does this
spam	relapse come about? Is there danger of another? Could a repetition of it
ham	be prevented? How should a repetition of it be treated? How does it come
ham	about at all? What can I do for my friend? No man ever can have been
ham	more desirous in his heart to serve a friend, than I am to serve mine,
ham	if I knew how.
spam	"But I don't know how to originate, in such a case. If your sagacity,
spam	knowledge, and experience, could put me on the right track, I might be
ham	able to do so much; unenlightened and undirected, I can do so little.
ham	Pray discuss it with me; pray enable me to see it a little more clearly,
ham	and teach me how to be a little more useful."
ham	Doctor Manette sat meditating after these earnest words were spoken, and
spam	Mr. Lorry did not press him.
ham	"I think it probable," said the Doctor, breaking silence with an effort,
ham	"that the relapse you have described, my dear friend, was not quite
spam	unforeseen by its subject."
ham	"Was it dreaded by him?" Mr. Lorry ventured to ask.
spam	"Very much." He said it with an involuntary shudder.
spam	"You have no idea how such an apprehension weighs on the sufferer's
ham	mind, and how difficult--how almost impossible--it is, for him to force
ham	himself to utter a word upon the topic that oppresses him."
spam	"Would he," asked Mr. Lorry, "be sensibly relieved if he could prevail
spam	upon himself to impart that secret brooding to any one, when it is on
spam	him?"
ham	"I think so. But it is, as I have told you, next to impossible. I even
spam	believe it--in some cases--to be quite impossible."
spam	"Now," said Mr. Lorry, gently laying his hand on the Doctor's arm again,
spam	after a short silence on both sides, "to what would you refer this
ham	attack?"
ham	"I believe," returned Doctor Manette, "that there had been a strong and
ham	extraordinary revival of the train of thought and remembrance that
spam	was the first cause of the malady. Some intense associations of a most
spam	distressing nature were vividly recalled, I think. It is probable that
spam	there had long been a dread lurking in his mind, that those associations
ham	would be recalled--say, under certain circumstances--say, on a
spam	particular occasion. He tried to prepare himself in vain; perhaps the
spam	effort to prepare himself made him less able to bear it."
spam	"Would he remember what took place in the relapse?" asked Mr. Lorry,
spam	with natural hesitation.
spam	The Doctor looked desolately round the room, shook his head, and
spam	answered, in a low voice, "Not at all."
ham	"Now, as to the future," hinted Mr. Lorry.
spam	"As to the future," said the Doctor, recovering firmness, "I should have
spam	great hope. As it pleased Heaven in its mercy to restore him so soon, I
ham	should have great hope. He, yielding under the pressure of a complicated
spam	something, long dreaded and long vaguely foreseen and contended against,
ham	and recovering after the cloud had burst and passed, I should hope that
ham	the worst was over."
spam	"Well, well! That's good comfort. I am thankful!" said Mr. Lorry.
ham	"I am thankful!" repeated the Doctor, bending his head with reverence.
ham	"There are two other points," said Mr. Lorry, "on which I am anxious to
ham	be instructed. I may go on?"
spam	"You cannot do your friend a better service." The Doctor gave him his
ham	hand.
spam	"To the first, then. He is of a studious habit, and unusually energetic;
ham	he applies himself with great ardour to the acquisition of professional
ham	knowledge, to the conducting of experiments, to many things. Now, does
spam	he do too much?"
ham	"I think not. It may be the character of his mind, to be always in
ham	singular need of occupation. That may be, in part, natural to it; in
ham	part, the result of affliction. The less it was occupied with healthy
spam	things, the more it would be in danger of turning in the unhealthy
ham	direction. He may have observed himself, and made the discovery."
spam	"You are sure that he is not under too great a strain?"
spam	"I think I am quite sure of it."
spam	"My dear Manette, if he were overworked now--"
spam	"My dear Lorry, I doubt if that could easily be. There has been a
spam	violent stress in one direction, and it needs a counterweight."
spam	"Excuse me, as a persistent man of business. Assuming for a moment,
ham	that he _was_ overworked; it would show itself in some renewal of this
ham	disorder?"
ham	"I do not think so. I do not think," said Doctor Manette with the
spam	firmness of self-conviction, "that anything but the one train of
ham	association would renew it. I think that, henceforth, nothing but some
ham	extraordinary jarring of that chord could renew it. After what has
spam	happened, and after his recovery, I find it difficult to imagine any
ham	such violent sounding of that string again. I trust, and I almost
ham	believe, that the circumstances likely to renew it are exhausted."
ham	He spoke with the diffidence of a man who knew how slight a thing
spam	would overset the delicate organisation of the mind, and yet with the
spam	confidence of a man who had slowly won his assurance out of personal
ham	endurance and distress. It was not for his friend to abate that
ham	confidence. He professed himself more relieved and encouraged than he
ham	really was, and approached his second and last point. He felt it to
spam	be the most difficult of all; but, remembering his old Sunday morning
ham	conversation with Miss Pross, and remembering what he had seen in the
spam	last nine days, he knew that he must face it.
ham	"The occupation resumed under the influence of this passing affliction
spam	so happily recovered from," said Mr. Lorry, clearing his throat, "we
ham	will call--Blacksmith's work, Blacksmith's work. We will say, to put a
spam	case and for the sake of illustration, that he had been used, in his bad
ham	time, to work at a little forge. We will say that he was unexpectedly
spam	found at his forge again. Is it not a pity that he should keep it by
ham	him?"
ham	The Doctor shaded his forehead with his hand, and beat his foot
spam	nervously on the ground.
ham	"He has always kept it by him," said Mr. Lorry, with an anxious look at
ham	his friend. "Now, would it not be better that he should let it go?"
spam	Still, the Doctor, with shaded forehead, beat his foot nervously on the
ham	ground.
spam	"You do not find it easy to advise me?" said Mr. Lorry. "I quite
ham	understand it to be a nice question. And yet I think--" And there he
spam	shook his head, and stopped.
spam	"You see," said Doctor Manette, turning to him after an uneasy pause,
ham	"it is very hard to explain, consistently, the innermost workings
ham	of this poor man's mind. He once yearned so frightfully for that
spam	occupation, and it was so welcome when it came; no doubt it relieved
spam	his pain so much, by substituting the perplexity of the fingers for
ham	the perplexity of the brain, and by substituting, as he became more
spam	practised, the ingenuity of the hands, for the ingenuity of the mental
spam	torture; that he has never been able to bear the thought of putting it
ham	quite out of his reach. Even now, when I believe he is more hopeful of
spam	himself than he has ever been, and even speaks of himself with a kind
spam	of confidence, the idea that he might need that old employment, and not
ham	find it, gives him a sudden sense of terror, like that which one may
spam	fancy strikes to the heart of a lost child."
ham	He looked like his illustration, as he raised his eyes to Mr. Lorry's
spam	face.
spam	"But may not--mind! I ask for information, as a plodding man of business
spam	who only deals with such material objects as guineas, shillings, and
spam	bank-notes--may not the retention of the thing involve the retention of
ham	the idea? If the thing were gone, my dear Manette, might not the fear go
spam	with it? In short, is it not a concession to the misgiving, to keep the
ham	forge?"
ham	There was another silence.
ham	"You see, too," said the Doctor, tremulously, "it is such an old
ham	companion."
spam	"I would not keep it," said Mr. Lorry, shaking his head; for he gained
spam	in firmness as he saw the Doctor disquieted. "I would recommend him to
spam	sacrifice it. I only want your authority. I am sure it does no good.
spam	Come! Give me your authority, like a dear good man. For his daughter's
ham	sake, my dear Manette!"
ham	Very strange to see what a struggle there was within him!
ham	"In her name, then, let it be done; I sanction it. But, I would not take
ham	it away while he was present. Let it be removed when he is not there;
ham	let him miss his old companion after an absence."
spam	Mr. Lorry readily engaged for that, and the conference was ended. They
ham	passed the day in the country, and the Doctor was quite restored. On the
ham	three following days he remained perfectly well, and on the fourteenth
ham	day he went away to join Lucie and her husband. The precaution that
ham	had been taken to account for his silence, Mr. Lorry had previously
ham	explained to him, and he had written to Lucie in accordance with it, and
spam	she had no suspicions.
spam	On the night of the day on which he left the house, Mr. Lorry went into
spam	his room with a chopper, saw, chisel, and hammer, attended by Miss Pross
ham	carrying a light. There, with closed doors, and in a mysterious and
spam	guilty manner, Mr. Lorry hacked the shoemaker's bench to pieces, while
ham	Miss Pross held the candle as if she were assisting at a murder--for
spam	which, indeed, in her grimness, she was no unsuitable figure. The
spam	burning of the body (previously reduced to pieces convenient for the
ham	purpose) was commenced without delay in the kitchen fire; and the tools,
ham	shoes, and leather, were buried in the garden. So wicked do destruction
spam	and secrecy appear to honest minds, that Mr. Lorry and Miss Pross,
ham	while engaged in the commission of their deed and in the removal of its
spam	traces, almost felt, and almost looked, like accomplices in a horrible
spam	crime.
ham	XX. A Plea
spam	When the newly-married pair came home, the first person who appeared, to
spam	offer his congratulations, was Sydney Carton. They had not been at home
spam	many hours, when he presented himself. He was not improved in habits, or
spam	in looks, or in manner; but there was a certain rugged air of fidelity
ham	about him, which was new to the observation of Charles Darnay.
spam	He watched his opportunity of taking Darnay aside into a window, and of
ham	speaking to him when no one overheard.
ham	"Mr. Darnay," said Carton, "I wish we might be friends."
ham	"We are already friends, I hope."
ham	"You are good enough to say so, as a fashion of speech; but, I don't
ham	mean any fashion of speech. Indeed, when I say I wish we might be
ham	friends, I scarcely mean quite that, either."
ham	Charles Darnay--as was natural--asked him, in all good-humour and
spam	good-fellowship, what he did mean?
spam	"Upon my life," said Carton, smiling, "I find that easier to comprehend
ham	in my own mind, than to convey to yours. However, let me try. You
spam	remember a certain famous occasion when I was more drunk than--than
ham	usual?"
ham	"I remember a certain famous occasion when you forced me to confess that
ham	you had been drinking."
ham	"I remember it too. The curse of those occasions is heavy upon me, for I
spam	always remember them. I hope it may be taken into account one day,
ham	when all days are at an end for me! Don't be alarmed; I am not going to
ham	preach."
ham	"I am not at all alarmed. Earnestness in you, is anything but alarming
ham	to me."
ham	"Ah!" said Carton, with a careless wave of his hand, as if he waved that
spam	away. "On the drunken occasion in question (one of a large number, as
ham	you know), I was insufferable about liking you, and not liking you. I
spam	wish you would forget it."
spam	"I forgot it long ago."
ham	"Fashion of speech again! But, Mr. Darnay, oblivion is not so easy to
spam	me, as you represent it to be to you. I have by no means forgotten it,
spam	and a light answer does not help me to forget it."
spam	"If it was a light answer," returned Darnay, "I beg your forgiveness
ham	for it. I had no other object than to turn a slight thing, which, to my
ham	surprise, seems to trouble you too much, aside. I declare to you, on the
ham	faith of a gentleman, that I have long dismissed it from my mind. Good
spam	Heaven, what was there to dismiss! Have I had nothing more important to
ham	remember, in the great service you rendered me that day?"
spam	"As to the great service," said Carton, "I am bound to avow to you, when
spam	you speak of it in that way, that it was mere professional claptrap, I
spam	don't know that I cared what became of you, when I rendered it.--Mind! I
spam	say when I rendered it; I am speaking of the past."
spam	"You make light of the obligation," returned Darnay, "but I will not
ham	quarrel with _your_ light answer."
spam	"Genuine truth, Mr. Darnay, trust me! I have gone aside from my purpose;
spam	I was speaking about our being friends. Now, you know me; you know I am
spam	incapable of all the higher and better flights of men. If you doubt it,
spam	ask Stryver, and he'll tell you so."
ham	"I prefer to form my own opinion, without the aid of his."
spam	"Well! At any rate you know me as a dissolute dog, who has never done
ham	any good, and never will."
ham	"I don't know that you 'never will.'"
spam	"But I do, and you must take my word for it. Well! If you could endure
spam	to have such a worthless fellow, and a fellow of such indifferent
ham	reputation, coming and going at odd times, I should ask that I might be
ham	permitted to come and go as a privileged person here; that I might
ham	be regarded as an useless (and I would add, if it were not for the
ham	resemblance I detected between you and me, an unornamental) piece of
ham	furniture, tolerated for its old service, and taken no notice of. I
spam	doubt if I should abuse the permission. It is a hundred to one if I
ham	should avail myself of it four times in a year. It would satisfy me, I
spam	dare say, to know that I had it."
ham	"Will you try?"
ham	"That is another way of saying that I am placed on the footing I have
spam	indicated. I thank you, Darnay. I may use that freedom with your name?"
ham	"I think so, Carton, by this time."
spam	They shook hands upon it, and Sydney turned away. Within a minute
ham	afterwards, he was, to all outward appearance, as unsubstantial as ever.
ham	When he was gone, and in the course of an evening passed with Miss
ham	Pross, the Doctor, and Mr. Lorry, Charles Darnay made some mention of
spam	this conversation in general terms, and spoke of Sydney Carton as a
spam	problem of carelessness and recklessness. He spoke of him, in short, not
ham	bitterly or meaning to bear hard upon him, but as anybody might who saw
spam	him as he showed himself.
ham	He had no idea that this could dwell in the thoughts of his fair young
ham	wife; but, when he afterwards joined her in their own rooms, he found
ham	her waiting for him with the old pretty lifting of the forehead strongly
spam	marked.
ham	"We are thoughtful to-night!" said Darnay, drawing his arm about her.
ham	"Yes, dearest Charles," with her hands on his breast, and the inquiring
spam	and attentive expression fixed upon him; "we are rather thoughtful
spam	to-night, for we have something on our mind to-night."
spam	"What is it, my Lucie?"
ham	"Will you promise not to press one question on me, if I beg you not to
spam	ask it?"
spam	"Will I promise? What will I not promise to my Love?"
ham	What, indeed, with his hand putting aside the golden hair from the
ham	cheek, and his other hand against the heart that beat for him!
spam	"I think, Charles, poor Mr. Carton deserves more consideration and
ham	respect than you expressed for him to-night."
ham	"Indeed, my own? Why so?"
spam	"That is what you are not to ask me. But I think--I know--he does."
spam	"If you know it, it is enough. What would you have me do, my Life?"
ham	"I would ask you, dearest, to be very generous with him always, and very
spam	lenient on his faults when he is not by. I would ask you to believe that
ham	he has a heart he very, very seldom reveals, and that there are deep
spam	wounds in it. My dear, I have seen it bleeding."
ham	"It is a painful reflection to me," said Charles Darnay, quite
ham	astounded, "that I should have done him any wrong. I never thought this
spam	of him."
ham	"My husband, it is so. I fear he is not to be reclaimed; there is
ham	scarcely a hope that anything in his character or fortunes is reparable
spam	now. But, I am sure that he is capable of good things, gentle things,
spam	even magnanimous things."
ham	She looked so beautiful in the purity of her faith in this lost man,
ham	that her husband could have looked at her as she was for hours.
spam	"And, O my dearest Love!" she urged, clinging nearer to him, laying her
ham	head upon his breast, and raising her eyes to his, "remember how strong
ham	we are in our happiness, and how weak he is in his misery!"
ham	The supplication touched him home. "I will always remember it, dear
ham	Heart! I will remember it as long as I live."
spam	He bent over the golden head, and put the rosy lips to his, and folded
ham	her in his arms. If one forlorn wanderer then pacing the dark streets,
ham	could have heard her innocent disclosure, and could have seen the drops
ham	of pity kissed away by her husband from the soft blue eyes so loving of
ham	that husband, he might have cried to the night--and the words would not
spam	have parted from his lips for the first time--
spam	"God bless her for her sweet compassion!"
spam	XXI. Echoing Footsteps
ham	A wonderful corner for echoes, it has been remarked, that corner where
spam	the Doctor lived. Ever busily winding the golden thread which bound
ham	her husband, and her father, and herself, and her old directress and
ham	companion, in a life of quiet bliss, Lucie sat in the still house in
spam	the tranquilly resounding corner, listening to the echoing footsteps of
spam	years.
ham	At first, there were times, though she was a perfectly happy young wife,
spam	when her work would slowly fall from her hands, and her eyes would be
ham	dimmed. For, there was something coming in the echoes, something light,
ham	afar off, and scarcely audible yet, that stirred her heart too much.
ham	Fluttering hopes and doubts--hopes, of a love as yet unknown to her:
spam	doubts, of her remaining upon earth, to enjoy that new delight--divided
ham	her breast. Among the echoes then, there would arise the sound of
ham	footsteps at her own early grave; and thoughts of the husband who would
spam	be left so desolate, and who would mourn for her so much, swelled to her
spam	eyes, and broke like waves.
ham	That time passed, and her little Lucie lay on her bosom. Then, among the
ham	advancing echoes, there was the tread of her tiny feet and the sound of
ham	her prattling words. Let greater echoes resound as they would, the young
ham	mother at the cradle side could always hear those coming. They came, and
spam	the shady house was sunny with a child's laugh, and the Divine friend of
ham	children, to whom in her trouble she had confided hers, seemed to take
ham	her child in his arms, as He took the child of old, and made it a sacred
spam	joy to her.
spam	Ever busily winding the golden thread that bound them all together,
ham	weaving the service of her happy influence through the tissue of all
ham	their lives, and making it predominate nowhere, Lucie heard in the
spam	echoes of years none but friendly and soothing sounds. Her husband's
ham	step was strong and prosperous among them; her father's firm and equal.
spam	Lo, Miss Pross, in harness of string, awakening the echoes, as an
spam	unruly charger, whip-corrected, snorting and pawing the earth under the
ham	plane-tree in the garden!
ham	Even when there were sounds of sorrow among the rest, they were not
ham	harsh nor cruel. Even when golden hair, like her own, lay in a halo on a
ham	pillow round the worn face of a little boy, and he said, with a radiant
spam	smile, "Dear papa and mamma, I am very sorry to leave you both, and to
spam	leave my pretty sister; but I am called, and I must go!" those were not
spam	tears all of agony that wetted his young mother's cheek, as the spirit
ham	departed from her embrace that had been entrusted to it. Suffer them and
ham	forbid them not. They see my Father's face. O Father, blessed words!
spam	Thus, the rustling of an Angel's wings got blended with the other
spam	echoes, and they were not wholly of earth, but had in them that breath
ham	of Heaven. Sighs of the winds that blew over a little garden-tomb were
spam	mingled with them also, and both were audible to Lucie, in a hushed
spam	murmur--like the breathing of a summer sea asleep upon a sandy shore--as
ham	the little Lucie, comically studious at the task of the morning, or
ham	dressing a doll at her mother's footstool, chattered in the tongues of
spam	the Two Cities that were blended in her life.
spam	The Echoes rarely answered to the actual tread of Sydney Carton. Some
ham	half-dozen times a year, at most, he claimed his privilege of coming in
ham	uninvited, and would sit among them through the evening, as he had once
spam	done often. He never came there heated with wine. And one other thing
spam	regarding him was whispered in the echoes, which has been whispered by
spam	all true echoes for ages and ages.
spam	No man ever really loved a woman, lost her, and knew her with a
spam	blameless though an unchanged mind, when she was a wife and a mother,
ham	but her children had a strange sympathy with him--an instinctive
ham	delicacy of pity for him. What fine hidden sensibilities are touched in
ham	such a case, no echoes tell; but it is so, and it was so here. Carton
spam	was the first stranger to whom little Lucie held out her chubby arms,
ham	and he kept his place with her as she grew. The little boy had spoken of
spam	him, almost at the last. "Poor Carton! Kiss him for me!"
spam	Mr. Stryver shouldered his way through the law, like some great engine
ham	forcing itself through turbid water, and dragged his useful friend in
spam	his wake, like a boat towed astern. As the boat so favoured is usually
spam	in a rough plight, and mostly under water, so, Sydney had a swamped
spam	life of it. But, easy and strong custom, unhappily so much easier and
spam	stronger in him than any stimulating sense of desert or disgrace, made
spam	it the life he was to lead; and he no more thought of emerging from his
ham	state of lion's jackal, than any real jackal may be supposed to think of
ham	rising to be a lion. Stryver was rich; had married a florid widow with
ham	property and three boys, who had nothing particularly shining about them
ham	but the straight hair of their dumpling heads.
ham	These three young gentlemen, Mr. Stryver, exuding patronage of the most
spam	offensive quality from every pore, had walked before him like three
spam	sheep to the quiet corner in Soho, and had offered as pupils to
spam	Lucie's husband: delicately saying "Halloa! here are three lumps of
ham	bread-and-cheese towards your matrimonial picnic, Darnay!" The polite
spam	rejection of the three lumps of bread-and-cheese had quite bloated Mr.
ham	Stryver with indignation, which he afterwards turned to account in the
ham	training of the young gentlemen, by directing them to beware of the
spam	pride of Beggars, like that tutor-fellow. He was also in the habit of
spam	declaiming to Mrs. Stryver, over his full-bodied wine, on the arts
spam	Mrs. Darnay had once put in practice to "catch" him, and on the
ham	diamond-cut-diamond arts in himself, madam, which had rendered him "not
spam	to be caught." Some of his King's Bench familiars, who were occasionally
ham	parties to the full-bodied wine and the lie, excused him for the
spam	latter by saying that he had told it so often, that he believed
ham	it himself--which is surely such an incorrigible aggravation of an
spam	originally bad offence, as to justify any such offender's being carried
spam	off to some suitably retired spot, and there hanged out of the way.
spam	These were among the echoes to which Lucie, sometimes pensive, sometimes
spam	amused and laughing, listened in the echoing corner, until her little
spam	daughter was six years old. How near to her heart the echoes of her
ham	child's tread came, and those of her own dear father's, always active
spam	and self-possessed, and those of her dear husband's, need not be told.
ham	Nor, how the lightest echo of their united home, directed by herself
ham	with such a wise and elegant thrift that it was more abundant than any
spam	waste, was music to her. Nor, how there were echoes all about her, sweet
ham	in her ears, of the many times her father had told her that he found her
ham	more devoted to him married (if that could be) than single, and of the
ham	many times her husband had said to her that no cares and duties seemed
ham	to divide her love for him or her help to him, and asked her "What is
ham	the magic secret, my darling, of your being everything to all of us,
spam	as if there were only one of us, yet never seeming to be hurried, or to
ham	have too much to do?"
ham	But, there were other echoes, from a distance, that rumbled menacingly
ham	in the corner all through this space of time. And it was now, about
ham	little Lucie's sixth birthday, that they began to have an awful sound,
spam	as of a great storm in France with a dreadful sea rising.
spam	On a night in mid-July, one thousand seven hundred and eighty-nine, Mr.
ham	Lorry came in late, from Tellson's, and sat himself down by Lucie and
ham	her husband in the dark window. It was a hot, wild night, and they were
spam	all three reminded of the old Sunday night when they had looked at the
spam	lightning from the same place.
spam	"I began to think," said Mr. Lorry, pushing his brown wig back, "that
spam	I should have to pass the night at Tellson's. We have been so full of
spam	business all day, that we have not known what to do first, or which way
ham	to turn. There is such an uneasiness in Paris, that we have actually a
spam	run of confidence upon us! Our customers over there, seem not to be able
ham	to confide their property to us fast enough. There is positively a mania
ham	among some of them for sending it to England."
ham	"That has a bad look," said Darnay--
spam	"A bad look, you say, my dear Darnay? Yes, but we don't know what reason
ham	there is in it. People are so unreasonable! Some of us at Tellson's are
ham	getting old, and we really can't be troubled out of the ordinary course
spam	without due occasion."
spam	"Still," said Darnay, "you know how gloomy and threatening the sky is."
ham	"I know that, to be sure," assented Mr. Lorry, trying to persuade
ham	himself that his sweet temper was soured, and that he grumbled, "but I
ham	am determined to be peevish after my long day's botheration. Where is
spam	Manette?"
spam	"Here he is," said the Doctor, entering the dark room at the moment.
ham	"I am quite glad you are at home; for these hurries and forebodings by
ham	which I have been surrounded all day long, have made me nervous without
ham	reason. You are not going out, I hope?"
ham	"No; I am going to play backgammon with you, if you like," said the
ham	Doctor.
spam	"I don't think I do like, if I may speak my mind. I am not fit to be
ham	pitted against you to-night. Is the teaboard still there, Lucie? I can't
ham	see."
ham	"Of course, it has been kept for you."
ham	"Thank ye, my dear. The precious child is safe in bed?"
ham	"And sleeping soundly."
spam	"That's right; all safe and well! I don't know why anything should be
spam	otherwise than safe and well here, thank God; but I have been so put out
ham	all day, and I am not as young as I was! My tea, my dear! Thank ye. Now,
spam	come and take your place in the circle, and let us sit quiet, and hear
ham	the echoes about which you have your theory."
ham	"Not a theory; it was a fancy."
spam	"A fancy, then, my wise pet," said Mr. Lorry, patting her hand. "They
spam	are very numerous and very loud, though, are they not? Only hear them!"
spam	Headlong, mad, and dangerous footsteps to force their way into anybody's
ham	life, footsteps not easily made clean again if once stained red, the
ham	footsteps raging in Saint Antoine afar off, as the little circle sat in
spam	the dark London window.
ham	Saint Antoine had been, that morning, a vast dusky mass of scarecrows
spam	heaving to and fro, with frequent gleams of light above the billowy
spam	heads, where steel blades and bayonets shone in the sun. A tremendous
spam	roar arose from the throat of Saint Antoine, and a forest of naked arms
spam	struggled in the air like shrivelled branches of trees in a winter wind:
ham	all the fingers convulsively clutching at every weapon or semblance of a
ham	weapon that was thrown up from the depths below, no matter how far off.
ham	Who gave them out, whence they last came, where they began, through what
spam	agency they crookedly quivered and jerked, scores at a time, over the
spam	heads of the crowd, like a kind of lightning, no eye in the throng could
spam	have told; but, muskets were being distributed--so were cartridges,
ham	powder, and ball, bars of iron and wood, knives, axes, pikes, every
ham	weapon that distracted ingenuity could discover or devise. People who
ham	could lay hold of nothing else, set themselves with bleeding hands to
ham	force stones and bricks out of their places in walls. Every pulse and
ham	heart in Saint Antoine was on high-fever strain and at high-fever heat.
ham	Every living creature there held life as of no account, and was demented
ham	with a passionate readiness to sacrifice it.
spam	As a whirlpool of boiling waters has a centre point, so, all this raging
ham	circled round Defarge's wine-shop, and every human drop in the caldron
ham	had a tendency to be sucked towards the vortex where Defarge himself,
spam	already begrimed with gunpowder and sweat, issued orders, issued arms,
ham	thrust this man back, dragged this man forward, disarmed one to arm
spam	another, laboured and strove in the thickest of the uproar.
ham	"Keep near to me, Jacques Three," cried Defarge; "and do you, Jacques
ham	One and Two, separate and put yourselves at the head of as many of these
ham	patriots as you can. Where is my wife?"
ham	"Eh, well! Here you see me!" said madame, composed as ever, but not
spam	knitting to-day. Madame's resolute right hand was occupied with an axe,
ham	in place of the usual softer implements, and in her girdle were a pistol
ham	and a cruel knife.
ham	"Where do you go, my wife?"
ham	"I go," said madame, "with you at present. You shall see me at the head
ham	of women, by-and-bye."
ham	"Come, then!" cried Defarge, in a resounding voice. "Patriots and
ham	friends, we are ready! The Bastille!"
ham	With a roar that sounded as if all the breath in France had been shaped
spam	into the detested word, the living sea rose, wave on wave, depth on
spam	depth, and overflowed the city to that point. Alarm-bells ringing, drums
spam	beating, the sea raging and thundering on its new beach, the attack
spam	began.
spam	Deep ditches, double drawbridge, massive stone walls, eight great
spam	towers, cannon, muskets, fire and smoke. Through the fire and through
ham	the smoke--in the fire and in the smoke, for the sea cast him up against
spam	a cannon, and on the instant he became a cannonier--Defarge of the
ham	wine-shop worked like a manful soldier, Two fierce hours.
spam	Deep ditch, single drawbridge, massive stone walls, eight great towers,
spam	cannon, muskets, fire and smoke. One drawbridge down! "Work, comrades
ham	all, work! Work, Jacques One, Jacques Two, Jacques One Thousand, Jacques
spam	Two Thousand, Jacques Five-and-Twenty Thousand; in the name of all
spam	the Angels or the Devils--which you prefer--work!" Thus Defarge of the
spam	wine-shop, still at his gun, which had long grown hot.
spam	"To me, women!" cried madame his wife. "What! We can kill as well as
spam	the men when the place is taken!" And to her, with a shrill thirsty
ham	cry, trooping women variously armed, but all armed alike in hunger and
ham	revenge.
ham	Cannon, muskets, fire and smoke; but, still the deep ditch, the single
ham	drawbridge, the massive stone walls, and the eight great towers. Slight
spam	displacements of the raging sea, made by the falling wounded. Flashing
ham	weapons, blazing torches, smoking waggonloads of wet straw, hard work
ham	at neighbouring barricades in all directions, shrieks, volleys,
spam	execrations, bravery without stint, boom smash and rattle, and the
ham	furious sounding of the living sea; but, still the deep ditch, and the
spam	single drawbridge, and the massive stone walls, and the eight great
ham	towers, and still Defarge of the wine-shop at his gun, grown doubly hot
ham	by the service of Four fierce hours.
spam	A white flag from within the fortress, and a parley--this dimly
spam	perceptible through the raging storm, nothing audible in it--suddenly
ham	the sea rose immeasurably wider and higher, and swept Defarge of the
spam	wine-shop over the lowered drawbridge, past the massive stone outer
ham	walls, in among the eight great towers surrendered!
spam	So resistless was the force of the ocean bearing him on, that even to
spam	draw his breath or turn his head was as impracticable as if he had been
ham	struggling in the surf at the South Sea, until he was landed in the
ham	outer courtyard of the Bastille. There, against an angle of a wall, he
ham	made a struggle to look about him. Jacques Three was nearly at his side;
spam	Madame Defarge, still heading some of her women, was visible in the
ham	inner distance, and her knife was in her hand. Everywhere was tumult,
spam	exultation, deafening and maniacal bewilderment, astounding noise, yet
spam	furious dumb-show.
ham	"The Prisoners!"
ham	"The Records!"
spam	"The secret cells!"
ham	"The instruments of torture!"
ham	"The Prisoners!"
ham	Of all these cries, and ten thousand incoherences, "The Prisoners!" was
ham	the cry most taken up by the sea that rushed in, as if there were an
ham	eternity of people, as well as of time and space. When the foremost
spam	billows rolled past, bearing the prison officers with them, and
spam	threatening them all with instant death if any secret nook remained
spam	undisclosed, Defarge laid his strong hand on the breast of one of
ham	these men--a man with a grey head, who had a lighted torch in his
ham	hand--separated him from the rest, and got him between himself and the
spam	wall.
ham	"Show me the North Tower!" said Defarge. "Quick!"
ham	"I will faithfully," replied the man, "if you will come with me. But
spam	there is no one there."
spam	"What is the meaning of One Hundred and Five, North Tower?" asked
ham	Defarge. "Quick!"
spam	"The meaning, monsieur?"
ham	"Does it mean a captive, or a place of captivity? Or do you mean that I
spam	shall strike you dead?"
ham	"Kill him!" croaked Jacques Three, who had come close up.
ham	"Monsieur, it is a cell."
ham	"Show it me!"
ham	"Pass this way, then."
spam	Jacques Three, with his usual craving on him, and evidently disappointed
spam	by the dialogue taking a turn that did not seem to promise bloodshed,
ham	held by Defarge's arm as he held by the turnkey's. Their three heads had
ham	been close together during this brief discourse, and it had been as much
spam	as they could do to hear one another, even then: so tremendous was the
spam	noise of the living ocean, in its irruption into the Fortress, and
spam	its inundation of the courts and passages and staircases. All around
ham	outside, too, it beat the walls with a deep, hoarse roar, from which,
ham	occasionally, some partial shouts of tumult broke and leaped into the
ham	air like spray.
ham	Through gloomy vaults where the light of day had never shone, past
ham	hideous doors of dark dens and cages, down cavernous flights of steps,
spam	and again up steep rugged ascents of stone and brick, more like dry
ham	waterfalls than staircases, Defarge, the turnkey, and Jacques Three,
ham	linked hand and arm, went with all the speed they could make. Here and
ham	there, especially at first, the inundation started on them and swept by;
ham	but when they had done descending, and were winding and climbing up a
spam	tower, they were alone. Hemmed in here by the massive thickness of walls
ham	and arches, the storm within the fortress and without was only audible
ham	to them in a dull, subdued way, as if the noise out of which they had
spam	come had almost destroyed their sense of hearing.
spam	The turnkey stopped at a low door, put a key in a clashing lock, swung
ham	the door slowly open, and said, as they all bent their heads and passed
ham	in:
ham	"One hundred and five, North Tower!"
spam	There was a small, heavily-grated, unglazed window high in the wall,
ham	with a stone screen before it, so that the sky could be only seen by
ham	stooping low and looking up. There was a small chimney, heavily barred
ham	across, a few feet within. There was a heap of old feathery wood-ashes
ham	on the hearth. There was a stool, and table, and a straw bed. There were
ham	the four blackened walls, and a rusted iron ring in one of them.
spam	"Pass that torch slowly along these walls, that I may see them," said
ham	Defarge to the turnkey.
ham	The man obeyed, and Defarge followed the light closely with his eyes.
spam	"Stop!--Look here, Jacques!"
ham	"A. M.!" croaked Jacques Three, as he read greedily.
spam	"Alexandre Manette," said Defarge in his ear, following the letters
ham	with his swart forefinger, deeply engrained with gunpowder. "And here he
spam	wrote 'a poor physician.' And it was he, without doubt, who scratched
spam	a calendar on this stone. What is that in your hand? A crowbar? Give it
ham	me!"
ham	He had still the linstock of his gun in his own hand. He made a sudden
spam	exchange of the two instruments, and turning on the worm-eaten stool and
ham	table, beat them to pieces in a few blows.
spam	"Hold the light higher!" he said, wrathfully, to the turnkey. "Look
spam	among those fragments with care, Jacques. And see! Here is my knife,"
spam	throwing it to him; "rip open that bed, and search the straw. Hold the
spam	light higher, you!"
ham	With a menacing look at the turnkey he crawled upon the hearth, and,
ham	peering up the chimney, struck and prised at its sides with the crowbar,
ham	and worked at the iron grating across it. In a few minutes, some mortar
spam	and dust came dropping down, which he averted his face to avoid; and
ham	in it, and in the old wood-ashes, and in a crevice in the chimney
spam	into which his weapon had slipped or wrought itself, he groped with a
spam	cautious touch.
ham	"Nothing in the wood, and nothing in the straw, Jacques?"
ham	"Nothing."
ham	"Let us collect them together, in the middle of the cell. So! Light
spam	them, you!"
ham	The turnkey fired the little pile, which blazed high and hot. Stooping
ham	again to come out at the low-arched door, they left it burning, and
spam	retraced their way to the courtyard; seeming to recover their sense
ham	of hearing as they came down, until they were in the raging flood once
spam	more.
spam	They found it surging and tossing, in quest of Defarge himself. Saint
spam	Antoine was clamorous to have its wine-shop keeper foremost in the guard
