spam	upon the governor who had defended the Bastille and shot the people.
ham	Otherwise, the governor would not be marched to the Hotel de Ville for
spam	judgment. Otherwise, the governor would escape, and the people's
spam	blood (suddenly of some value, after many years of worthlessness) be
ham	unavenged.
spam	In the howling universe of passion and contention that seemed to
ham	encompass this grim old officer conspicuous in his grey coat and red
spam	decoration, there was but one quite steady figure, and that was a
ham	woman's. "See, there is my husband!" she cried, pointing him out.
ham	"See Defarge!" She stood immovable close to the grim old officer, and
spam	remained immovable close to him; remained immovable close to him through
ham	the streets, as Defarge and the rest bore him along; remained immovable
spam	close to him when he was got near his destination, and began to
ham	be struck at from behind; remained immovable close to him when the
ham	long-gathering rain of stabs and blows fell heavy; was so close to him
ham	when he dropped dead under it, that, suddenly animated, she put her foot
spam	upon his neck, and with her cruel knife--long ready--hewed off his head.
ham	The hour was come, when Saint Antoine was to execute his horrible idea
ham	of hoisting up men for lamps to show what he could be and do. Saint
ham	Antoine's blood was up, and the blood of tyranny and domination by the
spam	iron hand was down--down on the steps of the Hotel de Ville where the
ham	governor's body lay--down on the sole of the shoe of Madame Defarge
ham	where she had trodden on the body to steady it for mutilation. "Lower
spam	the lamp yonder!" cried Saint Antoine, after glaring round for a new
spam	means of death; "here is one of his soldiers to be left on guard!" The
spam	swinging sentinel was posted, and the sea rushed on.
ham	The sea of black and threatening waters, and of destructive upheaving
ham	of wave against wave, whose depths were yet unfathomed and whose forces
ham	were yet unknown. The remorseless sea of turbulently swaying shapes,
ham	voices of vengeance, and faces hardened in the furnaces of suffering
ham	until the touch of pity could make no mark on them.
ham	But, in the ocean of faces where every fierce and furious expression was
spam	in vivid life, there were two groups of faces--each seven in number--so
ham	fixedly contrasting with the rest, that never did sea roll which bore
spam	more memorable wrecks with it. Seven faces of prisoners, suddenly
ham	released by the storm that had burst their tomb, were carried high
spam	overhead: all scared, all lost, all wondering and amazed, as if the Last
ham	Day were come, and those who rejoiced around them were lost spirits.
spam	Other seven faces there were, carried higher, seven dead faces, whose
spam	drooping eyelids and half-seen eyes awaited the Last Day. Impassive
spam	faces, yet with a suspended--not an abolished--expression on them;
ham	faces, rather, in a fearful pause, as having yet to raise the dropped
spam	lids of the eyes, and bear witness with the bloodless lips, "THOU DIDST
spam	IT!"
ham	Seven prisoners released, seven gory heads on pikes, the keys of the
ham	accursed fortress of the eight strong towers, some discovered letters
ham	and other memorials of prisoners of old time, long dead of broken
ham	hearts,--such, and such--like, the loudly echoing footsteps of Saint
ham	Antoine escort through the Paris streets in mid-July, one thousand seven
ham	hundred and eighty-nine. Now, Heaven defeat the fancy of Lucie Darnay,
spam	and keep these feet far out of her life! For, they are headlong, mad,
ham	and dangerous; and in the years so long after the breaking of the cask
ham	at Defarge's wine-shop door, they are not easily purified when once
ham	stained red.
ham	XXII. The Sea Still Rises
ham	Haggard Saint Antoine had had only one exultant week, in which to soften
ham	his modicum of hard and bitter bread to such extent as he could, with
ham	the relish of fraternal embraces and congratulations, when Madame
ham	Defarge sat at her counter, as usual, presiding over the customers.
ham	Madame Defarge wore no rose in her head, for the great brotherhood of
ham	Spies had become, even in one short week, extremely chary of trusting
spam	themselves to the saint's mercies. The lamps across his streets had a
spam	portentously elastic swing with them.
ham	Madame Defarge, with her arms folded, sat in the morning light and heat,
spam	contemplating the wine-shop and the street. In both, there were several
spam	knots of loungers, squalid and miserable, but now with a manifest sense
spam	of power enthroned on their distress. The raggedest nightcap, awry on
spam	the wretchedest head, had this crooked significance in it: "I know how
ham	hard it has grown for me, the wearer of this, to support life in myself;
ham	but do you know how easy it has grown for me, the wearer of this, to
spam	destroy life in you?" Every lean bare arm, that had been without work
spam	before, had this work always ready for it now, that it could strike.
ham	The fingers of the knitting women were vicious, with the experience that
ham	they could tear. There was a change in the appearance of Saint Antoine;
spam	the image had been hammering into this for hundreds of years, and the
spam	last finishing blows had told mightily on the expression.
ham	Madame Defarge sat observing it, with such suppressed approval as was
spam	to be desired in the leader of the Saint Antoine women. One of her
spam	sisterhood knitted beside her. The short, rather plump wife of a starved
spam	grocer, and the mother of two children withal, this lieutenant had
spam	already earned the complimentary name of The Vengeance.
ham	"Hark!" said The Vengeance. "Listen, then! Who comes?"
ham	As if a train of powder laid from the outermost bound of Saint Antoine
spam	Quarter to the wine-shop door, had been suddenly fired, a fast-spreading
spam	murmur came rushing along.
ham	"It is Defarge," said madame. "Silence, patriots!"
spam	Defarge came in breathless, pulled off a red cap he wore, and looked
ham	around him! "Listen, everywhere!" said madame again. "Listen to him!"
spam	Defarge stood, panting, against a background of eager eyes and open
spam	mouths, formed outside the door; all those within the wine-shop had
ham	sprung to their feet.
ham	"Say then, my husband. What is it?"
ham	"News from the other world!"
spam	"How, then?" cried madame, contemptuously. "The other world?"
ham	"Does everybody here recall old Foulon, who told the famished people
spam	that they might eat grass, and who died, and went to Hell?"
spam	"Everybody!" from all throats.
spam	"The news is of him. He is among us!"
ham	"Among us!" from the universal throat again. "And dead?"
ham	"Not dead! He feared us so much--and with reason--that he caused himself
ham	to be represented as dead, and had a grand mock-funeral. But they have
ham	found him alive, hiding in the country, and have brought him in. I have
ham	seen him but now, on his way to the Hotel de Ville, a prisoner. I have
spam	said that he had reason to fear us. Say all! _Had_ he reason?"
ham	Wretched old sinner of more than threescore years and ten, if he had
ham	never known it yet, he would have known it in his heart of hearts if he
ham	could have heard the answering cry.
spam	A moment of profound silence followed. Defarge and his wife looked
spam	steadfastly at one another. The Vengeance stooped, and the jar of a drum
ham	was heard as she moved it at her feet behind the counter.
spam	"Patriots!" said Defarge, in a determined voice, "are we ready?"
ham	Instantly Madame Defarge's knife was in her girdle; the drum was beating
spam	in the streets, as if it and a drummer had flown together by magic; and
ham	The Vengeance, uttering terrific shrieks, and flinging her arms about
spam	her head like all the forty Furies at once, was tearing from house to
ham	house, rousing the women.
ham	The men were terrible, in the bloody-minded anger with which they looked
spam	from windows, caught up what arms they had, and came pouring down into
ham	the streets; but, the women were a sight to chill the boldest. From
ham	such household occupations as their bare poverty yielded, from their
ham	children, from their aged and their sick crouching on the bare ground
ham	famished and naked, they ran out with streaming hair, urging one
spam	another, and themselves, to madness with the wildest cries and actions.
ham	Villain Foulon taken, my sister! Old Foulon taken, my mother! Miscreant
ham	Foulon taken, my daughter! Then, a score of others ran into the midst of
spam	these, beating their breasts, tearing their hair, and screaming, Foulon
ham	alive! Foulon who told the starving people they might eat grass! Foulon
spam	who told my old father that he might eat grass, when I had no bread
ham	to give him! Foulon who told my baby it might suck grass, when these
ham	breasts were dry with want! O mother of God, this Foulon! O Heaven our
ham	suffering! Hear me, my dead baby and my withered father: I swear on my
ham	knees, on these stones, to avenge you on Foulon! Husbands, and brothers,
spam	and young men, Give us the blood of Foulon, Give us the head of Foulon,
spam	Give us the heart of Foulon, Give us the body and soul of Foulon, Rend
spam	Foulon to pieces, and dig him into the ground, that grass may grow from
ham	him! With these cries, numbers of the women, lashed into blind frenzy,
spam	whirled about, striking and tearing at their own friends until they
spam	dropped into a passionate swoon, and were only saved by the men
ham	belonging to them from being trampled under foot.
spam	Nevertheless, not a moment was lost; not a moment! This Foulon was at
spam	the Hotel de Ville, and might be loosed. Never, if Saint Antoine knew
spam	his own sufferings, insults, and wrongs! Armed men and women flocked out
spam	of the Quarter so fast, and drew even these last dregs after them with
spam	such a force of suction, that within a quarter of an hour there was not
spam	a human creature in Saint Antoine's bosom but a few old crones and the
ham	wailing children.
spam	No. They were all by that time choking the Hall of Examination where
spam	this old man, ugly and wicked, was, and overflowing into the adjacent
ham	open space and streets. The Defarges, husband and wife, The Vengeance,
ham	and Jacques Three, were in the first press, and at no great distance
ham	from him in the Hall.
ham	"See!" cried madame, pointing with her knife. "See the old villain bound
ham	with ropes. That was well done to tie a bunch of grass upon his back.
ham	Ha, ha! That was well done. Let him eat it now!" Madame put her knife
ham	under her arm, and clapped her hands as at a play.
spam	The people immediately behind Madame Defarge, explaining the cause of
ham	her satisfaction to those behind them, and those again explaining to
ham	others, and those to others, the neighbouring streets resounded with the
spam	clapping of hands. Similarly, during two or three hours of drawl,
spam	and the winnowing of many bushels of words, Madame Defarge's frequent
ham	expressions of impatience were taken up, with marvellous quickness, at
ham	a distance: the more readily, because certain men who had by some
ham	wonderful exercise of agility climbed up the external architecture
spam	to look in from the windows, knew Madame Defarge well, and acted as a
ham	telegraph between her and the crowd outside the building.
ham	At length the sun rose so high that it struck a kindly ray as of hope or
ham	protection, directly down upon the old prisoner's head. The favour was
spam	too much to bear; in an instant the barrier of dust and chaff that had
ham	stood surprisingly long, went to the winds, and Saint Antoine had got
spam	him!
ham	It was known directly, to the furthest confines of the crowd. Defarge
ham	had but sprung over a railing and a table, and folded the miserable
spam	wretch in a deadly embrace--Madame Defarge had but followed and turned
ham	her hand in one of the ropes with which he was tied--The Vengeance and
spam	Jacques Three were not yet up with them, and the men at the windows
ham	had not yet swooped into the Hall, like birds of prey from their high
spam	perches--when the cry seemed to go up, all over the city, "Bring him
spam	out! Bring him to the lamp!"
ham	Down, and up, and head foremost on the steps of the building; now, on
ham	his knees; now, on his feet; now, on his back; dragged, and struck at,
ham	and stifled by the bunches of grass and straw that were thrust into his
ham	face by hundreds of hands; torn, bruised, panting, bleeding, yet always
ham	entreating and beseeching for mercy; now full of vehement agony of
spam	action, with a small clear space about him as the people drew one
ham	another back that they might see; now, a log of dead wood drawn through
spam	a forest of legs; he was hauled to the nearest street corner where one
ham	of the fatal lamps swung, and there Madame Defarge let him go--as a cat
ham	might have done to a mouse--and silently and composedly looked at him
spam	while they made ready, and while he besought her: the women passionately
spam	screeching at him all the time, and the men sternly calling out to have
spam	him killed with grass in his mouth. Once, he went aloft, and the rope
ham	broke, and they caught him shrieking; twice, he went aloft, and the rope
spam	broke, and they caught him shrieking; then, the rope was merciful, and
spam	held him, and his head was soon upon a pike, with grass enough in the
spam	mouth for all Saint Antoine to dance at the sight of.
ham	Nor was this the end of the day's bad work, for Saint Antoine so shouted
spam	and danced his angry blood up, that it boiled again, on hearing when
spam	the day closed in that the son-in-law of the despatched, another of the
spam	people's enemies and insulters, was coming into Paris under a guard
ham	five hundred strong, in cavalry alone. Saint Antoine wrote his crimes
spam	on flaring sheets of paper, seized him--would have torn him out of the
spam	breast of an army to bear Foulon company--set his head and heart on
spam	pikes, and carried the three spoils of the day, in Wolf-procession
spam	through the streets.
ham	Not before dark night did the men and women come back to the children,
ham	wailing and breadless. Then, the miserable bakers' shops were beset by
ham	long files of them, patiently waiting to buy bad bread; and while
spam	they waited with stomachs faint and empty, they beguiled the time by
spam	embracing one another on the triumphs of the day, and achieving them
ham	again in gossip. Gradually, these strings of ragged people shortened and
ham	frayed away; and then poor lights began to shine in high windows, and
spam	slender fires were made in the streets, at which neighbours cooked in
ham	common, afterwards supping at their doors.
ham	Scanty and insufficient suppers those, and innocent of meat, as of
spam	most other sauce to wretched bread. Yet, human fellowship infused
ham	some nourishment into the flinty viands, and struck some sparks of
ham	cheerfulness out of them. Fathers and mothers who had had their full
ham	share in the worst of the day, played gently with their meagre children;
ham	and lovers, with such a world around them and before them, loved and
ham	hoped.
spam	It was almost morning, when Defarge's wine-shop parted with its last
spam	knot of customers, and Monsieur Defarge said to madame his wife, in
ham	husky tones, while fastening the door:
spam	"At last it is come, my dear!"
spam	"Eh well!" returned madame. "Almost."
ham	Saint Antoine slept, the Defarges slept: even The Vengeance slept with
ham	her starved grocer, and the drum was at rest. The drum's was the
spam	only voice in Saint Antoine that blood and hurry had not changed. The
ham	Vengeance, as custodian of the drum, could have wakened him up and had
ham	the same speech out of him as before the Bastille fell, or old Foulon
ham	was seized; not so with the hoarse tones of the men and women in Saint
spam	Antoine's bosom.
ham	XXIII. Fire Rises
ham	There was a change on the village where the fountain fell, and where
ham	the mender of roads went forth daily to hammer out of the stones on the
ham	highway such morsels of bread as might serve for patches to hold his
ham	poor ignorant soul and his poor reduced body together. The prison on the
spam	crag was not so dominant as of yore; there were soldiers to guard it,
spam	but not many; there were officers to guard the soldiers, but not one of
spam	them knew what his men would do--beyond this: that it would probably not
spam	be what he was ordered.
ham	Far and wide lay a ruined country, yielding nothing but desolation.
ham	Every green leaf, every blade of grass and blade of grain, was as
ham	shrivelled and poor as the miserable people. Everything was bowed down,
spam	dejected, oppressed, and broken. Habitations, fences, domesticated
ham	animals, men, women, children, and the soil that bore them--all worn
spam	out.
spam	Monseigneur (often a most worthy individual gentleman) was a national
ham	blessing, gave a chivalrous tone to things, was a polite example of
spam	luxurious and shining life, and a great deal more to equal purpose;
ham	nevertheless, Monseigneur as a class had, somehow or other, brought
spam	things to this. Strange that Creation, designed expressly for
spam	Monseigneur, should be so soon wrung dry and squeezed out! There must
ham	be something short-sighted in the eternal arrangements, surely! Thus it
spam	was, however; and the last drop of blood having been extracted from the
ham	flints, and the last screw of the rack having been turned so often that
ham	its purchase crumbled, and it now turned and turned with nothing
spam	to bite, Monseigneur began to run away from a phenomenon so low and
spam	unaccountable.
spam	But, this was not the change on the village, and on many a village like
spam	it. For scores of years gone by, Monseigneur had squeezed it and wrung
ham	it, and had seldom graced it with his presence except for the pleasures
ham	of the chase--now, found in hunting the people; now, found in hunting
ham	the beasts, for whose preservation Monseigneur made edifying spaces
ham	of barbarous and barren wilderness. No. The change consisted in
ham	the appearance of strange faces of low caste, rather than in the
spam	disappearance of the high caste, chiselled, and otherwise beautified and
spam	beautifying features of Monseigneur.
spam	For, in these times, as the mender of roads worked, solitary, in the
spam	dust, not often troubling himself to reflect that dust he was and
spam	to dust he must return, being for the most part too much occupied in
ham	thinking how little he had for supper and how much more he would eat if
ham	he had it--in these times, as he raised his eyes from his lonely labour,
spam	and viewed the prospect, he would see some rough figure approaching on
spam	foot, the like of which was once a rarity in those parts, but was now
spam	a frequent presence. As it advanced, the mender of roads would discern
ham	without surprise, that it was a shaggy-haired man, of almost barbarian
spam	aspect, tall, in wooden shoes that were clumsy even to the eyes of a
ham	mender of roads, grim, rough, swart, steeped in the mud and dust of many
ham	highways, dank with the marshy moisture of many low grounds, sprinkled
ham	with the thorns and leaves and moss of many byways through woods.
ham	Such a man came upon him, like a ghost, at noon in the July weather,
spam	as he sat on his heap of stones under a bank, taking such shelter as he
ham	could get from a shower of hail.
spam	The man looked at him, looked at the village in the hollow, at the mill,
spam	and at the prison on the crag. When he had identified these objects
ham	in what benighted mind he had, he said, in a dialect that was just
ham	intelligible:
spam	"How goes it, Jacques?"
ham	"All well, Jacques."
spam	"Touch then!"
ham	They joined hands, and the man sat down on the heap of stones.
spam	"No dinner?"
spam	"Nothing but supper now," said the mender of roads, with a hungry face.
ham	"It is the fashion," growled the man. "I meet no dinner anywhere."
spam	He took out a blackened pipe, filled it, lighted it with flint and
spam	steel, pulled at it until it was in a bright glow: then, suddenly held
spam	it from him and dropped something into it from between his finger and
ham	thumb, that blazed and went out in a puff of smoke.
ham	"Touch then." It was the turn of the mender of roads to say it this
ham	time, after observing these operations. They again joined hands.
spam	"To-night?" said the mender of roads.
spam	"To-night," said the man, putting the pipe in his mouth.
ham	"Where?"
ham	"Here."
spam	He and the mender of roads sat on the heap of stones looking silently at
ham	one another, with the hail driving in between them like a pigmy charge
ham	of bayonets, until the sky began to clear over the village.
spam	"Show me!" said the traveller then, moving to the brow of the hill.
ham	"See!" returned the mender of roads, with extended finger. "You go down
ham	here, and straight through the street, and past the fountain--"
spam	"To the Devil with all that!" interrupted the other, rolling his eye
ham	over the landscape. "_I_ go through no streets and past no fountains.
ham	Well?"
spam	"Well! About two leagues beyond the summit of that hill above the
ham	village."
ham	"Good. When do you cease to work?"
ham	"At sunset."
spam	"Will you wake me, before departing? I have walked two nights without
spam	resting. Let me finish my pipe, and I shall sleep like a child. Will you
ham	wake me?"
spam	"Surely."
spam	The wayfarer smoked his pipe out, put it in his breast, slipped off his
spam	great wooden shoes, and lay down on his back on the heap of stones. He
spam	was fast asleep directly.
ham	As the road-mender plied his dusty labour, and the hail-clouds, rolling
ham	away, revealed bright bars and streaks of sky which were responded to
spam	by silver gleams upon the landscape, the little man (who wore a red cap
ham	now, in place of his blue one) seemed fascinated by the figure on the
spam	heap of stones. His eyes were so often turned towards it, that he used
ham	his tools mechanically, and, one would have said, to very poor account.
ham	The bronze face, the shaggy black hair and beard, the coarse woollen
ham	red cap, the rough medley dress of home-spun stuff and hairy skins of
spam	beasts, the powerful frame attenuated by spare living, and the sullen
spam	and desperate compression of the lips in sleep, inspired the mender
spam	of roads with awe. The traveller had travelled far, and his feet were
ham	footsore, and his ankles chafed and bleeding; his great shoes, stuffed
ham	with leaves and grass, had been heavy to drag over the many long
ham	leagues, and his clothes were chafed into holes, as he himself was into
spam	sores. Stooping down beside him, the road-mender tried to get a peep at
ham	secret weapons in his breast or where not; but, in vain, for he slept
ham	with his arms crossed upon him, and set as resolutely as his lips.
spam	Fortified towns with their stockades, guard-houses, gates, trenches, and
ham	drawbridges, seemed to the mender of roads, to be so much air as against
spam	this figure. And when he lifted his eyes from it to the horizon and
ham	looked around, he saw in his small fancy similar figures, stopped by no
spam	obstacle, tending to centres all over France.
spam	The man slept on, indifferent to showers of hail and intervals of
ham	brightness, to sunshine on his face and shadow, to the paltering lumps
ham	of dull ice on his body and the diamonds into which the sun changed
ham	them, until the sun was low in the west, and the sky was glowing. Then,
ham	the mender of roads having got his tools together and all things ready
spam	to go down into the village, roused him.
ham	"Good!" said the sleeper, rising on his elbow. "Two leagues beyond the
spam	summit of the hill?"
ham	"About."
ham	"About. Good!"
spam	The mender of roads went home, with the dust going on before him
ham	according to the set of the wind, and was soon at the fountain,
ham	squeezing himself in among the lean kine brought there to drink, and
ham	appearing even to whisper to them in his whispering to all the village.
spam	When the village had taken its poor supper, it did not creep to bed,
spam	as it usually did, but came out of doors again, and remained there. A
ham	curious contagion of whispering was upon it, and also, when it gathered
ham	together at the fountain in the dark, another curious contagion of
ham	looking expectantly at the sky in one direction only. Monsieur Gabelle,
spam	chief functionary of the place, became uneasy; went out on his house-top
ham	alone, and looked in that direction too; glanced down from behind his
spam	chimneys at the darkening faces by the fountain below, and sent word to
ham	the sacristan who kept the keys of the church, that there might be need
ham	to ring the tocsin by-and-bye.
ham	The night deepened. The trees environing the old chateau, keeping its
spam	solitary state apart, moved in a rising wind, as though they threatened
spam	the pile of building massive and dark in the gloom. Up the two terrace
spam	flights of steps the rain ran wildly, and beat at the great door, like a
spam	swift messenger rousing those within; uneasy rushes of wind went through
ham	the hall, among the old spears and knives, and passed lamenting up the
spam	stairs, and shook the curtains of the bed where the last Marquis
spam	had slept. East, West, North, and South, through the woods, four
ham	heavy-treading, unkempt figures crushed the high grass and cracked the
ham	branches, striding on cautiously to come together in the courtyard. Four
spam	lights broke out there, and moved away in different directions, and all
ham	was black again.
spam	But, not for long. Presently, the chateau began to make itself strangely
spam	visible by some light of its own, as though it were growing luminous.
ham	Then, a flickering streak played behind the architecture of the front,
spam	picking out transparent places, and showing where balustrades, arches,
ham	and windows were. Then it soared higher, and grew broader and brighter.
ham	Soon, from a score of the great windows, flames burst forth, and the
spam	stone faces awakened, stared out of fire.
spam	A faint murmur arose about the house from the few people who were left
ham	there, and there was a saddling of a horse and riding away. There was
spam	spurring and splashing through the darkness, and bridle was drawn in the
ham	space by the village fountain, and the horse in a foam stood at Monsieur
spam	Gabelle's door. "Help, Gabelle! Help, every one!" The tocsin rang
ham	impatiently, but other help (if that were any) there was none. The
spam	mender of roads, and two hundred and fifty particular friends, stood
ham	with folded arms at the fountain, looking at the pillar of fire in the
spam	sky. "It must be forty feet high," said they, grimly; and never moved.
spam	The rider from the chateau, and the horse in a foam, clattered away
spam	through the village, and galloped up the stony steep, to the prison on
spam	the crag. At the gate, a group of officers were looking at the fire;
spam	removed from them, a group of soldiers. "Help, gentlemen--officers! The
spam	chateau is on fire; valuable objects may be saved from the flames by
spam	timely aid! Help, help!" The officers looked towards the soldiers who
spam	looked at the fire; gave no orders; and answered, with shrugs and biting
ham	of lips, "It must burn."
ham	As the rider rattled down the hill again and through the street, the
spam	village was illuminating. The mender of roads, and the two hundred and
ham	fifty particular friends, inspired as one man and woman by the idea of
ham	lighting up, had darted into their houses, and were putting candles in
spam	every dull little pane of glass. The general scarcity of everything,
spam	occasioned candles to be borrowed in a rather peremptory manner of
spam	Monsieur Gabelle; and in a moment of reluctance and hesitation on
ham	that functionary's part, the mender of roads, once so submissive to
spam	authority, had remarked that carriages were good to make bonfires with,
ham	and that post-horses would roast.
spam	The chateau was left to itself to flame and burn. In the roaring and
spam	raging of the conflagration, a red-hot wind, driving straight from the
ham	infernal regions, seemed to be blowing the edifice away. With the rising
spam	and falling of the blaze, the stone faces showed as if they were in
spam	torment. When great masses of stone and timber fell, the face with the
spam	two dints in the nose became obscured: anon struggled out of the smoke
ham	again, as if it were the face of the cruel Marquis, burning at the stake
spam	and contending with the fire.
spam	The chateau burned; the nearest trees, laid hold of by the fire,
spam	scorched and shrivelled; trees at a distance, fired by the four fierce
spam	figures, begirt the blazing edifice with a new forest of smoke. Molten
ham	lead and iron boiled in the marble basin of the fountain; the water ran
spam	dry; the extinguisher tops of the towers vanished like ice before the
spam	heat, and trickled down into four rugged wells of flame. Great rents and
spam	splits branched out in the solid walls, like crystallisation; stupefied
spam	birds wheeled about and dropped into the furnace; four fierce figures
spam	trudged away, East, West, North, and South, along the night-enshrouded
spam	roads, guided by the beacon they had lighted, towards their next
ham	destination. The illuminated village had seized hold of the tocsin, and,
ham	abolishing the lawful ringer, rang for joy.
ham	Not only that; but the village, light-headed with famine, fire, and
ham	bell-ringing, and bethinking itself that Monsieur Gabelle had to do with
spam	the collection of rent and taxes--though it was but a small instalment
spam	of taxes, and no rent at all, that Gabelle had got in those latter
spam	days--became impatient for an interview with him, and, surrounding his
ham	house, summoned him to come forth for personal conference. Whereupon,
spam	Monsieur Gabelle did heavily bar his door, and retire to hold counsel
ham	with himself. The result of that conference was, that Gabelle again
ham	withdrew himself to his housetop behind his stack of chimneys; this time
spam	resolved, if his door were broken in (he was a small Southern man
spam	of retaliative temperament), to pitch himself head foremost over the
spam	parapet, and crush a man or two below.
spam	Probably, Monsieur Gabelle passed a long night up there, with the
ham	distant chateau for fire and candle, and the beating at his door,
ham	combined with the joy-ringing, for music; not to mention his having an
spam	ill-omened lamp slung across the road before his posting-house gate,
ham	which the village showed a lively inclination to displace in his favour.
ham	A trying suspense, to be passing a whole summer night on the brink of
ham	the black ocean, ready to take that plunge into it upon which Monsieur
ham	Gabelle had resolved! But, the friendly dawn appearing at last, and the
spam	rush-candles of the village guttering out, the people happily dispersed,
ham	and Monsieur Gabelle came down bringing his life with him for that
spam	while.
spam	Within a hundred miles, and in the light of other fires, there were
ham	other functionaries less fortunate, that night and other nights, whom
ham	the rising sun found hanging across once-peaceful streets, where they
ham	had been born and bred; also, there were other villagers and townspeople
spam	less fortunate than the mender of roads and his fellows, upon whom the
spam	functionaries and soldiery turned with success, and whom they strung up
ham	in their turn. But, the fierce figures were steadily wending East, West,
spam	North, and South, be that as it would; and whosoever hung, fire burned.
spam	The altitude of the gallows that would turn to water and quench it,
spam	no functionary, by any stretch of mathematics, was able to calculate
spam	successfully.
spam	XXIV. Drawn to the Loadstone Rock
ham	In such risings of fire and risings of sea--the firm earth shaken by
spam	the rushes of an angry ocean which had now no ebb, but was always on the
ham	flow, higher and higher, to the terror and wonder of the beholders on
spam	the shore--three years of tempest were consumed. Three more birthdays
spam	of little Lucie had been woven by the golden thread into the peaceful
ham	tissue of the life of her home.
ham	Many a night and many a day had its inmates listened to the echoes in
spam	the corner, with hearts that failed them when they heard the thronging
spam	feet. For, the footsteps had become to their minds as the footsteps of
ham	a people, tumultuous under a red flag and with their country declared in
ham	danger, changed into wild beasts, by terrible enchantment long persisted
spam	in.
ham	Monseigneur, as a class, had dissociated himself from the phenomenon of
spam	his not being appreciated: of his being so little wanted in France, as
spam	to incur considerable danger of receiving his dismissal from it, and
spam	this life together. Like the fabled rustic who raised the Devil with
spam	infinite pains, and was so terrified at the sight of him that he could
spam	ask the Enemy no question, but immediately fled; so, Monseigneur, after
ham	boldly reading the Lord's Prayer backwards for a great number of years,
spam	and performing many other potent spells for compelling the Evil One, no
ham	sooner beheld him in his terrors than he took to his noble heels.
ham	The shining Bull's Eye of the Court was gone, or it would have been the
ham	mark for a hurricane of national bullets. It had never been a good
spam	eye to see with--had long had the mote in it of Lucifer's pride,
spam	Sardanapalus's luxury, and a mole's blindness--but it had dropped
ham	out and was gone. The Court, from that exclusive inner circle to its
ham	outermost rotten ring of intrigue, corruption, and dissimulation, was
ham	all gone together. Royalty was gone; had been besieged in its Palace and
ham	"suspended," when the last tidings came over.
ham	The August of the year one thousand seven hundred and ninety-two was
ham	come, and Monseigneur was by this time scattered far and wide.
ham	As was natural, the head-quarters and great gathering-place of
ham	Monseigneur, in London, was Tellson's Bank. Spirits are supposed to
ham	haunt the places where their bodies most resorted, and Monseigneur
spam	without a guinea haunted the spot where his guineas used to be.
ham	Moreover, it was the spot to which such French intelligence as was most
spam	to be relied upon, came quickest. Again: Tellson's was a munificent
spam	house, and extended great liberality to old customers who had fallen
ham	from their high estate. Again: those nobles who had seen the coming
ham	storm in time, and anticipating plunder or confiscation, had made
spam	provident remittances to Tellson's, were always to be heard of there
spam	by their needy brethren. To which it must be added that every new-comer
ham	from France reported himself and his tidings at Tellson's, almost as
ham	a matter of course. For such variety of reasons, Tellson's was at that
ham	time, as to French intelligence, a kind of High Exchange; and this
ham	was so well known to the public, and the inquiries made there were in
ham	consequence so numerous, that Tellson's sometimes wrote the latest news
spam	out in a line or so and posted it in the Bank windows, for all who ran
spam	through Temple Bar to read.
spam	On a steaming, misty afternoon, Mr. Lorry sat at his desk, and Charles
spam	Darnay stood leaning on it, talking with him in a low voice. The
ham	penitential den once set apart for interviews with the House, was now
ham	the news-Exchange, and was filled to overflowing. It was within half an
spam	hour or so of the time of closing.
ham	"But, although you are the youngest man that ever lived," said Charles
spam	Darnay, rather hesitating, "I must still suggest to you--"
spam	"I understand. That I am too old?" said Mr. Lorry.
spam	"Unsettled weather, a long journey, uncertain means of travelling, a
spam	disorganised country, a city that may not be even safe for you."
spam	"My dear Charles," said Mr. Lorry, with cheerful confidence, "you touch
spam	some of the reasons for my going: not for my staying away. It is safe
spam	enough for me; nobody will care to interfere with an old fellow of hard
ham	upon fourscore when there are so many people there much better worth
ham	interfering with. As to its being a disorganised city, if it were not a
ham	disorganised city there would be no occasion to send somebody from our
ham	House here to our House there, who knows the city and the business, of
spam	old, and is in Tellson's confidence. As to the uncertain travelling, the
ham	long journey, and the winter weather, if I were not prepared to submit
spam	myself to a few inconveniences for the sake of Tellson's, after all
ham	these years, who ought to be?"
ham	"I wish I were going myself," said Charles Darnay, somewhat restlessly,
spam	and like one thinking aloud.
spam	"Indeed! You are a pretty fellow to object and advise!" exclaimed Mr.
spam	Lorry. "You wish you were going yourself? And you a Frenchman born? You
ham	are a wise counsellor."
spam	"My dear Mr. Lorry, it is because I am a Frenchman born, that the
spam	thought (which I did not mean to utter here, however) has passed through
ham	my mind often. One cannot help thinking, having had some sympathy for
spam	the miserable people, and having abandoned something to them," he spoke
ham	here in his former thoughtful manner, "that one might be listened to,
spam	and might have the power to persuade to some restraint. Only last night,
ham	after you had left us, when I was talking to Lucie--"
ham	"When you were talking to Lucie," Mr. Lorry repeated. "Yes. I wonder you
ham	are not ashamed to mention the name of Lucie! Wishing you were going to
spam	France at this time of day!"
ham	"However, I am not going," said Charles Darnay, with a smile. "It is
spam	more to the purpose that you say you are."
spam	"And I am, in plain reality. The truth is, my dear Charles," Mr. Lorry
ham	glanced at the distant House, and lowered his voice, "you can have no
ham	conception of the difficulty with which our business is transacted, and
spam	of the peril in which our books and papers over yonder are involved. The
ham	Lord above knows what the compromising consequences would be to numbers
ham	of people, if some of our documents were seized or destroyed; and they
spam	might be, at any time, you know, for who can say that Paris is not set
spam	afire to-day, or sacked to-morrow! Now, a judicious selection from these
spam	with the least possible delay, and the burying of them, or otherwise
ham	getting of them out of harm's way, is within the power (without loss of
spam	precious time) of scarcely any one but myself, if any one. And shall
ham	I hang back, when Tellson's knows this and says this--Tellson's, whose
ham	bread I have eaten these sixty years--because I am a little stiff about
ham	the joints? Why, I am a boy, sir, to half a dozen old codgers here!"
spam	"How I admire the gallantry of your youthful spirit, Mr. Lorry."
ham	"Tut! Nonsense, sir!--And, my dear Charles," said Mr. Lorry, glancing at
spam	the House again, "you are to remember, that getting things out of
spam	Paris at this present time, no matter what things, is next to an
ham	impossibility. Papers and precious matters were this very day brought
spam	to us here (I speak in strict confidence; it is not business-like to
ham	whisper it, even to you), by the strangest bearers you can imagine,
spam	every one of whom had his head hanging on by a single hair as he passed
spam	the Barriers. At another time, our parcels would come and go, as easily
ham	as in business-like Old England; but now, everything is stopped."
ham	"And do you really go to-night?"
spam	"I really go to-night, for the case has become too pressing to admit of
spam	delay."
spam	"And do you take no one with you?"
ham	"All sorts of people have been proposed to me, but I will have nothing
ham	to say to any of them. I intend to take Jerry. Jerry has been my
ham	bodyguard on Sunday nights for a long time past and I am used to him.
spam	Nobody will suspect Jerry of being anything but an English bull-dog, or
spam	of having any design in his head but to fly at anybody who touches his
ham	master."
spam	"I must say again that I heartily admire your gallantry and
ham	youthfulness."
ham	"I must say again, nonsense, nonsense! When I have executed this little
ham	commission, I shall, perhaps, accept Tellson's proposal to retire and
ham	live at my ease. Time enough, then, to think about growing old."
spam	This dialogue had taken place at Mr. Lorry's usual desk, with
ham	Monseigneur swarming within a yard or two of it, boastful of what he
ham	would do to avenge himself on the rascal-people before long. It was too
ham	much the way of Monseigneur under his reverses as a refugee, and it
spam	was much too much the way of native British orthodoxy, to talk of this
ham	terrible Revolution as if it were the only harvest ever known under
spam	the skies that had not been sown--as if nothing had ever been done, or
ham	omitted to be done, that had led to it--as if observers of the wretched
ham	millions in France, and of the misused and perverted resources that
ham	should have made them prosperous, had not seen it inevitably coming,
ham	years before, and had not in plain words recorded what they saw. Such
spam	vapouring, combined with the extravagant plots of Monseigneur for the
ham	restoration of a state of things that had utterly exhausted itself,
spam	and worn out Heaven and earth as well as itself, was hard to be endured
spam	without some remonstrance by any sane man who knew the truth. And it was
ham	such vapouring all about his ears, like a troublesome confusion of blood
ham	in his own head, added to a latent uneasiness in his mind, which had
ham	already made Charles Darnay restless, and which still kept him so.
spam	Among the talkers, was Stryver, of the King's Bench Bar, far on his
ham	way to state promotion, and, therefore, loud on the theme: broaching
spam	to Monseigneur, his devices for blowing the people up and exterminating
ham	them from the face of the earth, and doing without them: and for
spam	accomplishing many similar objects akin in their nature to the abolition
spam	of eagles by sprinkling salt on the tails of the race. Him, Darnay heard
ham	with a particular feeling of objection; and Darnay stood divided between
ham	going away that he might hear no more, and remaining to interpose his
spam	word, when the thing that was to be, went on to shape itself out.
spam	The House approached Mr. Lorry, and laying a soiled and unopened letter
spam	before him, asked if he had yet discovered any traces of the person to
spam	whom it was addressed? The House laid the letter down so close to Darnay
ham	that he saw the direction--the more quickly because it was his own right
spam	name. The address, turned into English, ran:
spam	"Very pressing. To Monsieur heretofore the Marquis St. Evremonde, of
spam	France. Confided to the cares of Messrs. Tellson and Co., Bankers,
spam	London, England."
spam	On the marriage morning, Doctor Manette had made it his one urgent and
spam	express request to Charles Darnay, that the secret of this name should
spam	be--unless he, the Doctor, dissolved the obligation--kept inviolate
spam	between them. Nobody else knew it to be his name; his own wife had no
spam	suspicion of the fact; Mr. Lorry could have none.
ham	"No," said Mr. Lorry, in reply to the House; "I have referred it,
ham	I think, to everybody now here, and no one can tell me where this
ham	gentleman is to be found."
spam	The hands of the clock verging upon the hour of closing the Bank, there
ham	was a general set of the current of talkers past Mr. Lorry's desk. He
ham	held the letter out inquiringly; and Monseigneur looked at it, in the
ham	person of this plotting and indignant refugee; and Monseigneur looked at
ham	it in the person of that plotting and indignant refugee; and This, That,
spam	and The Other, all had something disparaging to say, in French or in
spam	English, concerning the Marquis who was not to be found.
ham	"Nephew, I believe--but in any case degenerate successor--of the
spam	polished Marquis who was murdered," said one. "Happy to say, I never
ham	knew him."
spam	"A craven who abandoned his post," said another--this Monseigneur had
ham	been got out of Paris, legs uppermost and half suffocated, in a load of
spam	hay--"some years ago."
spam	"Infected with the new doctrines," said a third, eyeing the direction
spam	through his glass in passing; "set himself in opposition to the last
ham	Marquis, abandoned the estates when he inherited them, and left them to
ham	the ruffian herd. They will recompense him now, I hope, as he deserves."
spam	"Hey?" cried the blatant Stryver. "Did he though? Is that the sort of
ham	fellow? Let us look at his infamous name. D--n the fellow!"
ham	Darnay, unable to restrain himself any longer, touched Mr. Stryver on
ham	the shoulder, and said:
spam	"I know the fellow."
ham	"Do you, by Jupiter?" said Stryver. "I am sorry for it."
spam	"Why?"
ham	"Why, Mr. Darnay? D'ye hear what he did? Don't ask, why, in these
ham	times."
ham	"But I do ask why?"
spam	"Then I tell you again, Mr. Darnay, I am sorry for it. I am sorry to
ham	hear you putting any such extraordinary questions. Here is a fellow,
ham	who, infected by the most pestilent and blasphemous code of devilry that
spam	ever was known, abandoned his property to the vilest scum of the earth
ham	that ever did murder by wholesale, and you ask me why I am sorry that a
spam	man who instructs youth knows him? Well, but I'll answer you. I am sorry
spam	because I believe there is contamination in such a scoundrel. That's
spam	why."
ham	Mindful of the secret, Darnay with great difficulty checked himself, and
ham	said: "You may not understand the gentleman."
spam	"I understand how to put _you_ in a corner, Mr. Darnay," said Bully
ham	Stryver, "and I'll do it. If this fellow is a gentleman, I _don't_
spam	understand him. You may tell him so, with my compliments. You may also
spam	tell him, from me, that after abandoning his worldly goods and position
spam	to this butcherly mob, I wonder he is not at the head of them. But, no,
spam	gentlemen," said Stryver, looking all round, and snapping his fingers,
ham	"I know something of human nature, and I tell you that you'll never
spam	find a fellow like this fellow, trusting himself to the mercies of such
ham	precious _protégés_. No, gentlemen; he'll always show 'em a clean pair
ham	of heels very early in the scuffle, and sneak away."
spam	With those words, and a final snap of his fingers, Mr. Stryver
ham	shouldered himself into Fleet-street, amidst the general approbation of
ham	his hearers. Mr. Lorry and Charles Darnay were left alone at the desk,
ham	in the general departure from the Bank.
ham	"Will you take charge of the letter?" said Mr. Lorry. "You know where to
spam	deliver it?"
ham	"I do."
spam	"Will you undertake to explain, that we suppose it to have been
ham	addressed here, on the chance of our knowing where to forward it, and
ham	that it has been here some time?"
spam	"I will do so. Do you start for Paris from here?"
spam	"From here, at eight."
ham	"I will come back, to see you off."
ham	Very ill at ease with himself, and with Stryver and most other men,
spam	Darnay made the best of his way into the quiet of the Temple, opened the
ham	letter, and read it. These were its contents:
spam	"Prison of the Abbaye, Paris.
ham	"June 21, 1792. "MONSIEUR HERETOFORE THE MARQUIS.
ham	"After having long been in danger of my life at the hands of the
spam	village, I have been seized, with great violence and indignity, and
spam	brought a long journey on foot to Paris. On the road I have suffered a
ham	great deal. Nor is that all; my house has been destroyed--razed to the
ham	ground.
spam	"The crime for which I am imprisoned, Monsieur heretofore the Marquis,
ham	and for which I shall be summoned before the tribunal, and shall lose my
ham	life (without your so generous help), is, they tell me, treason against
ham	the majesty of the people, in that I have acted against them for an
ham	emigrant. It is in vain I represent that I have acted for them, and not
spam	against, according to your commands. It is in vain I represent that,
spam	before the sequestration of emigrant property, I had remitted the
spam	imposts they had ceased to pay; that I had collected no rent; that I had
ham	had recourse to no process. The only response is, that I have acted for
ham	an emigrant, and where is that emigrant?
ham	"Ah! most gracious Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, where is that
spam	emigrant? I cry in my sleep where is he? I demand of Heaven, will he
spam	not come to deliver me? No answer. Ah Monsieur heretofore the Marquis,
ham	I send my desolate cry across the sea, hoping it may perhaps reach your
ham	ears through the great bank of Tilson known at Paris!
spam	"For the love of Heaven, of justice, of generosity, of the honour of
ham	your noble name, I supplicate you, Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, to
spam	succour and release me. My fault is, that I have been true to you. Oh
spam	Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, I pray you be you true to me!
ham	"From this prison here of horror, whence I every hour tend nearer and
ham	nearer to destruction, I send you, Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, the
ham	assurance of my dolorous and unhappy service.
spam	"Your afflicted,
ham	"Gabelle."
spam	The latent uneasiness in Darnay's mind was roused to vigourous life
spam	by this letter. The peril of an old servant and a good one, whose
spam	only crime was fidelity to himself and his family, stared him so
ham	reproachfully in the face, that, as he walked to and fro in the Temple
spam	considering what to do, he almost hid his face from the passersby.
ham	He knew very well, that in his horror of the deed which had culminated
ham	the bad deeds and bad reputation of the old family house, in his
spam	resentful suspicions of his uncle, and in the aversion with which his
ham	conscience regarded the crumbling fabric that he was supposed to uphold,
ham	he had acted imperfectly. He knew very well, that in his love for Lucie,
spam	his renunciation of his social place, though by no means new to his own
spam	mind, had been hurried and incomplete. He knew that he ought to have
ham	systematically worked it out and supervised it, and that he had meant to
spam	do it, and that it had never been done.
ham	The happiness of his own chosen English home, the necessity of being
ham	always actively employed, the swift changes and troubles of the time
spam	which had followed on one another so fast, that the events of this week
ham	annihilated the immature plans of last week, and the events of the week
ham	following made all new again; he knew very well, that to the force of
spam	these circumstances he had yielded:--not without disquiet, but still
spam	without continuous and accumulating resistance. That he had watched
ham	the times for a time of action, and that they had shifted and struggled
ham	until the time had gone by, and the nobility were trooping from
spam	France by every highway and byway, and their property was in course of
spam	confiscation and destruction, and their very names were blotting out,
spam	was as well known to himself as it could be to any new authority in
spam	France that might impeach him for it.
ham	But, he had oppressed no man, he had imprisoned no man; he was so
ham	far from having harshly exacted payment of his dues, that he had
spam	relinquished them of his own will, thrown himself on a world with no
ham	favour in it, won his own private place there, and earned his own
ham	bread. Monsieur Gabelle had held the impoverished and involved estate
spam	on written instructions, to spare the people, to give them what little
ham	there was to give--such fuel as the heavy creditors would let them have
spam	in the winter, and such produce as could be saved from the same grip in
ham	the summer--and no doubt he had put the fact in plea and proof, for his
ham	own safety, so that it could not but appear now.
ham	This favoured the desperate resolution Charles Darnay had begun to make,
ham	that he would go to Paris.
ham	Yes. Like the mariner in the old story, the winds and streams had driven
spam	him within the influence of the Loadstone Rock, and it was drawing him
spam	to itself, and he must go. Everything that arose before his mind drifted
ham	him on, faster and faster, more and more steadily, to the terrible
ham	attraction. His latent uneasiness had been, that bad aims were being
ham	worked out in his own unhappy land by bad instruments, and that he who
ham	could not fail to know that he was better than they, was not there,
ham	trying to do something to stay bloodshed, and assert the claims of mercy
spam	and humanity. With this uneasiness half stifled, and half reproaching
ham	him, he had been brought to the pointed comparison of himself with the
ham	brave old gentleman in whom duty was so strong; upon that comparison
ham	(injurious to himself) had instantly followed the sneers of Monseigneur,
ham	which had stung him bitterly, and those of Stryver, which above all were
spam	coarse and galling, for old reasons. Upon those, had followed Gabelle's
spam	letter: the appeal of an innocent prisoner, in danger of death, to his
ham	justice, honour, and good name.
ham	His resolution was made. He must go to Paris.
ham	Yes. The Loadstone Rock was drawing him, and he must sail on, until he
spam	struck. He knew of no rock; he saw hardly any danger. The intention
spam	with which he had done what he had done, even although he had left
spam	it incomplete, presented it before him in an aspect that would be
spam	gratefully acknowledged in France on his presenting himself to assert
ham	it. Then, that glorious vision of doing good, which is so often the
ham	sanguine mirage of so many good minds, arose before him, and he even
ham	saw himself in the illusion with some influence to guide this raging
spam	Revolution that was running so fearfully wild.
spam	As he walked to and fro with his resolution made, he considered that
ham	neither Lucie nor her father must know of it until he was gone.
ham	Lucie should be spared the pain of separation; and her father, always
spam	reluctant to turn his thoughts towards the dangerous ground of old,
ham	should come to the knowledge of the step, as a step taken, and not in
ham	the balance of suspense and doubt. How much of the incompleteness of his
ham	situation was referable to her father, through the painful anxiety
spam	to avoid reviving old associations of France in his mind, he did not
spam	discuss with himself. But, that circumstance too, had had its influence
ham	in his course.
ham	He walked to and fro, with thoughts very busy, until it was time to
spam	return to Tellson's and take leave of Mr. Lorry. As soon as he arrived
spam	in Paris he would present himself to this old friend, but he must say
ham	nothing of his intention now.
spam	A carriage with post-horses was ready at the Bank door, and Jerry was
spam	booted and equipped.
spam	"I have delivered that letter," said Charles Darnay to Mr. Lorry. "I
ham	would not consent to your being charged with any written answer, but
spam	perhaps you will take a verbal one?"
ham	"That I will, and readily," said Mr. Lorry, "if it is not dangerous."
ham	"Not at all. Though it is to a prisoner in the Abbaye."
spam	"What is his name?" said Mr. Lorry, with his open pocket-book in his
ham	hand.
spam	"Gabelle."
ham	"Gabelle. And what is the message to the unfortunate Gabelle in prison?"
ham	"Simply, 'that he has received the letter, and will come.'"
ham	"Any time mentioned?"
ham	"He will start upon his journey to-morrow night."
ham	"Any person mentioned?"
ham	"No."
spam	He helped Mr. Lorry to wrap himself in a number of coats and cloaks,
ham	and went out with him from the warm atmosphere of the old Bank, into the
ham	misty air of Fleet-street. "My love to Lucie, and to little Lucie," said
ham	Mr. Lorry at parting, "and take precious care of them till I come back."
spam	Charles Darnay shook his head and doubtfully smiled, as the carriage
ham	rolled away.
spam	That night--it was the fourteenth of August--he sat up late, and wrote
spam	two fervent letters; one was to Lucie, explaining the strong obligation
ham	he was under to go to Paris, and showing her, at length, the reasons
ham	that he had, for feeling confident that he could become involved in no
ham	personal danger there; the other was to the Doctor, confiding Lucie and
spam	their dear child to his care, and dwelling on the same topics with the
ham	strongest assurances. To both, he wrote that he would despatch letters
ham	in proof of his safety, immediately after his arrival.
spam	It was a hard day, that day of being among them, with the first
spam	reservation of their joint lives on his mind. It was a hard matter to
spam	preserve the innocent deceit of which they were profoundly unsuspicious.
spam	But, an affectionate glance at his wife, so happy and busy, made him
ham	resolute not to tell her what impended (he had been half moved to do it,
spam	so strange it was to him to act in anything without her quiet aid), and
spam	the day passed quickly. Early in the evening he embraced her, and her
spam	scarcely less dear namesake, pretending that he would return by-and-bye
spam	(an imaginary engagement took him out, and he had secreted a valise
ham	of clothes ready), and so he emerged into the heavy mist of the heavy
spam	streets, with a heavier heart.
ham	The unseen force was drawing him fast to itself, now, and all the tides
ham	and winds were setting straight and strong towards it. He left his
spam	two letters with a trusty porter, to be delivered half an hour before
spam	midnight, and no sooner; took horse for Dover; and began his journey.
ham	"For the love of Heaven, of justice, of generosity, of the honour of
ham	your noble name!" was the poor prisoner's cry with which he strengthened
ham	his sinking heart, as he left all that was dear on earth behind him, and
ham	floated away for the Loadstone Rock.
ham	The end of the second book.
ham	Book the Third--the Track of a Storm
ham	I. In Secret
ham	The traveller fared slowly on his way, who fared towards Paris from
ham	England in the autumn of the year one thousand seven hundred and
spam	ninety-two. More than enough of bad roads, bad equipages, and bad
spam	horses, he would have encountered to delay him, though the fallen and
spam	unfortunate King of France had been upon his throne in all his glory;
spam	but, the changed times were fraught with other obstacles than
spam	these. Every town-gate and village taxing-house had its band of
spam	citizen-patriots, with their national muskets in a most explosive state
ham	of readiness, who stopped all comers and goers, cross-questioned them,
ham	inspected their papers, looked for their names in lists of their own,
spam	turned them back, or sent them on, or stopped them and laid them in
spam	hold, as their capricious judgment or fancy deemed best for the dawning
ham	Republic One and Indivisible, of Liberty, Equality, Fraternity, or
spam	Death.
ham	A very few French leagues of his journey were accomplished, when Charles
ham	Darnay began to perceive that for him along these country roads there
ham	was no hope of return until he should have been declared a good citizen
spam	at Paris. Whatever might befall now, he must on to his journey's end.
ham	Not a mean village closed upon him, not a common barrier dropped across
spam	the road behind him, but he knew it to be another iron door in
ham	the series that was barred between him and England. The universal
ham	watchfulness so encompassed him, that if he had been taken in a net,
spam	or were being forwarded to his destination in a cage, he could not have
spam	felt his freedom more completely gone.
spam	This universal watchfulness not only stopped him on the highway twenty
spam	times in a stage, but retarded his progress twenty times in a day, by
spam	riding after him and taking him back, riding before him and stopping him
ham	by anticipation, riding with him and keeping him in charge. He had been
spam	days upon his journey in France alone, when he went to bed tired out, in
spam	a little town on the high road, still a long way from Paris.
spam	Nothing but the production of the afflicted Gabelle's letter from his
ham	prison of the Abbaye would have got him on so far. His difficulty at the
spam	guard-house in this small place had been such, that he felt his journey
ham	to have come to a crisis. And he was, therefore, as little surprised as
spam	a man could be, to find himself awakened at the small inn to which he
spam	had been remitted until morning, in the middle of the night.
spam	Awakened by a timid local functionary and three armed patriots in rough
spam	red caps and with pipes in their mouths, who sat down on the bed.
ham	"Emigrant," said the functionary, "I am going to send you on to Paris,
spam	under an escort."
ham	"Citizen, I desire nothing more than to get to Paris, though I could
ham	dispense with the escort."
spam	"Silence!" growled a red-cap, striking at the coverlet with the butt-end
ham	of his musket. "Peace, aristocrat!"
ham	"It is as the good patriot says," observed the timid functionary. "You
spam	are an aristocrat, and must have an escort--and must pay for it."
ham	"I have no choice," said Charles Darnay.
ham	"Choice! Listen to him!" cried the same scowling red-cap. "As if it was
ham	not a favour to be protected from the lamp-iron!"
ham	"It is always as the good patriot says," observed the functionary. "Rise
ham	and dress yourself, emigrant."
ham	Darnay complied, and was taken back to the guard-house, where other
spam	patriots in rough red caps were smoking, drinking, and sleeping, by
spam	a watch-fire. Here he paid a heavy price for his escort, and hence he
spam	started with it on the wet, wet roads at three o'clock in the morning.
ham	The escort were two mounted patriots in red caps and tri-coloured
spam	cockades, armed with national muskets and sabres, who rode one on either
spam	side of him.
spam	The escorted governed his own horse, but a loose line was attached to
spam	his bridle, the end of which one of the patriots kept girded round his
spam	wrist. In this state they set forth with the sharp rain driving in their
spam	faces: clattering at a heavy dragoon trot over the uneven town pavement,
ham	and out upon the mire-deep roads. In this state they traversed without
spam	change, except of horses and pace, all the mire-deep leagues that lay
ham	between them and the capital.
ham	They travelled in the night, halting an hour or two after daybreak, and
spam	lying by until the twilight fell. The escort were so wretchedly clothed,
spam	that they twisted straw round their bare legs, and thatched their ragged
ham	shoulders to keep the wet off. Apart from the personal discomfort of
spam	being so attended, and apart from such considerations of present danger
spam	as arose from one of the patriots being chronically drunk, and carrying
ham	his musket very recklessly, Charles Darnay did not allow the restraint
spam	that was laid upon him to awaken any serious fears in his breast; for,
spam	he reasoned with himself that it could have no reference to the merits
spam	of an individual case that was not yet stated, and of representations,
spam	confirmable by the prisoner in the Abbaye, that were not yet made.
spam	But when they came to the town of Beauvais--which they did at eventide,
ham	when the streets were filled with people--he could not conceal from
ham	himself that the aspect of affairs was very alarming. An ominous crowd
ham	gathered to see him dismount of the posting-yard, and many voices called
spam	out loudly, "Down with the emigrant!"
spam	He stopped in the act of swinging himself out of his saddle, and,
spam	resuming it as his safest place, said:
ham	"Emigrant, my friends! Do you not see me here, in France, of my own
spam	will?"
spam	"You are a cursed emigrant," cried a farrier, making at him in a
spam	furious manner through the press, hammer in hand; "and you are a cursed
spam	aristocrat!"
ham	The postmaster interposed himself between this man and the rider's
ham	bridle (at which he was evidently making), and soothingly said, "Let him
ham	be; let him be! He will be judged at Paris."
spam	"Judged!" repeated the farrier, swinging his hammer. "Ay! and condemned
ham	as a traitor." At this the crowd roared approval.
spam	Checking the postmaster, who was for turning his horse's head to the
ham	yard (the drunken patriot sat composedly in his saddle looking on, with
ham	the line round his wrist), Darnay said, as soon as he could make his
ham	voice heard:
ham	"Friends, you deceive yourselves, or you are deceived. I am not a
spam	traitor."
ham	"He lies!" cried the smith. "He is a traitor since the decree. His life
spam	is forfeit to the people. His cursed life is not his own!"
spam	At the instant when Darnay saw a rush in the eyes of the crowd, which
spam	another instant would have brought upon him, the postmaster turned his
spam	horse into the yard, the escort rode in close upon his horse's flanks,
ham	and the postmaster shut and barred the crazy double gates. The farrier
spam	struck a blow upon them with his hammer, and the crowd groaned; but, no
ham	more was done.
ham	"What is this decree that the smith spoke of?" Darnay asked the
spam	postmaster, when he had thanked him, and stood beside him in the yard.
spam	"Truly, a decree for selling the property of emigrants."
ham	"When passed?"
spam	"On the fourteenth."
spam	"The day I left England!"
spam	"Everybody says it is but one of several, and that there will be
ham	others--if there are not already--banishing all emigrants, and
spam	condemning all to death who return. That is what he meant when he said
ham	your life was not your own."
spam	"But there are no such decrees yet?"
ham	"What do I know!" said the postmaster, shrugging his shoulders; "there
spam	may be, or there will be. It is all the same. What would you have?"
spam	They rested on some straw in a loft until the middle of the night, and
ham	then rode forward again when all the town was asleep. Among the many
ham	wild changes observable on familiar things which made this wild ride
ham	unreal, not the least was the seeming rarity of sleep. After long and
ham	lonely spurring over dreary roads, they would come to a cluster of poor
ham	cottages, not steeped in darkness, but all glittering with lights, and
spam	would find the people, in a ghostly manner in the dead of the night,
spam	circling hand in hand round a shrivelled tree of Liberty, or all drawn
spam	up together singing a Liberty song. Happily, however, there was sleep in
spam	Beauvais that night to help them out of it and they passed on once more
spam	into solitude and loneliness: jingling through the untimely cold and
spam	wet, among impoverished fields that had yielded no fruits of the earth
ham	that year, diversified by the blackened remains of burnt houses, and by
spam	the sudden emergence from ambuscade, and sharp reining up across their
spam	way, of patriot patrols on the watch on all the roads.
ham	Daylight at last found them before the wall of Paris. The barrier was
ham	closed and strongly guarded when they rode up to it.
ham	"Where are the papers of this prisoner?" demanded a resolute-looking man
spam	in authority, who was summoned out by the guard.
ham	Naturally struck by the disagreeable word, Charles Darnay requested the
ham	speaker to take notice that he was a free traveller and French citizen,
spam	in charge of an escort which the disturbed state of the country had
spam	imposed upon him, and which he had paid for.
ham	"Where," repeated the same personage, without taking any heed of him
ham	whatever, "are the papers of this prisoner?"
ham	The drunken patriot had them in his cap, and produced them. Casting his
ham	eyes over Gabelle's letter, the same personage in authority showed some
ham	disorder and surprise, and looked at Darnay with a close attention.
spam	He left escort and escorted without saying a word, however, and went
spam	into the guard-room; meanwhile, they sat upon their horses outside the
spam	gate. Looking about him while in this state of suspense, Charles
ham	Darnay observed that the gate was held by a mixed guard of soldiers and
spam	patriots, the latter far outnumbering the former; and that while ingress
ham	into the city for peasants' carts bringing in supplies, and for similar
ham	traffic and traffickers, was easy enough, egress, even for the homeliest
ham	people, was very difficult. A numerous medley of men and women, not
ham	to mention beasts and vehicles of various sorts, was waiting to issue
ham	forth; but, the previous identification was so strict, that they
ham	filtered through the barrier very slowly. Some of these people knew
spam	their turn for examination to be so far off, that they lay down on the
ham	ground to sleep or smoke, while others talked together, or loitered
spam	about. The red cap and tri-colour cockade were universal, both among men
ham	and women.
ham	When he had sat in his saddle some half-hour, taking note of these
spam	things, Darnay found himself confronted by the same man in authority,
spam	who directed the guard to open the barrier. Then he delivered to the
spam	escort, drunk and sober, a receipt for the escorted, and requested him
spam	to dismount. He did so, and the two patriots, leading his tired horse,
ham	turned and rode away without entering the city.
ham	He accompanied his conductor into a guard-room, smelling of common wine
ham	and tobacco, where certain soldiers and patriots, asleep and awake,
spam	drunk and sober, and in various neutral states between sleeping and
spam	waking, drunkenness and sobriety, were standing and lying about. The
spam	light in the guard-house, half derived from the waning oil-lamps of
ham	the night, and half from the overcast day, was in a correspondingly
spam	uncertain condition. Some registers were lying open on a desk, and an
spam	officer of a coarse, dark aspect, presided over these.
ham	"Citizen Defarge," said he to Darnay's conductor, as he took a slip of
ham	paper to write on. "Is this the emigrant Evremonde?"
spam	"This is the man."
spam	"Your age, Evremonde?"
ham	"Thirty-seven."
ham	"Married, Evremonde?"
ham	"Yes."
spam	"Where married?"
ham	"In England."
spam	"Without doubt. Where is your wife, Evremonde?"
spam	"In England."
ham	"Without doubt. You are consigned, Evremonde, to the prison of La
ham	Force."
ham	"Just Heaven!" exclaimed Darnay. "Under what law, and for what offence?"
spam	The officer looked up from his slip of paper for a moment.
spam	"We have new laws, Evremonde, and new offences, since you were here." He
spam	said it with a hard smile, and went on writing.
ham	"I entreat you to observe that I have come here voluntarily, in response
ham	to that written appeal of a fellow-countryman which lies before you. I
ham	demand no more than the opportunity to do so without delay. Is not that
spam	my right?"
spam	"Emigrants have no rights, Evremonde," was the stolid reply. The officer
ham	wrote until he had finished, read over to himself what he had written,
spam	sanded it, and handed it to Defarge, with the words "In secret."
spam	Defarge motioned with the paper to the prisoner that he must accompany
ham	him. The prisoner obeyed, and a guard of two armed patriots attended
spam	them.
spam	"Is it you," said Defarge, in a low voice, as they went down the
ham	guardhouse steps and turned into Paris, "who married the daughter of
ham	Doctor Manette, once a prisoner in the Bastille that is no more?"
ham	"Yes," replied Darnay, looking at him with surprise.
ham	"My name is Defarge, and I keep a wine-shop in the Quarter Saint
ham	Antoine. Possibly you have heard of me."
ham	"My wife came to your house to reclaim her father? Yes!"
spam	The word "wife" seemed to serve as a gloomy reminder to Defarge, to say
spam	with sudden impatience, "In the name of that sharp female newly-born,
ham	and called La Guillotine, why did you come to France?"
ham	"You heard me say why, a minute ago. Do you not believe it is the
ham	truth?"
ham	"A bad truth for you," said Defarge, speaking with knitted brows, and
spam	looking straight before him.
ham	"Indeed I am lost here. All here is so unprecedented, so changed, so
ham	sudden and unfair, that I am absolutely lost. Will you render me a
ham	little help?"
spam	"None." Defarge spoke, always looking straight before him.
spam	"Will you answer me a single question?"
ham	"Perhaps. According to its nature. You can say what it is."
ham	"In this prison that I am going to so unjustly, shall I have some free
spam	communication with the world outside?"
spam	"You will see."
spam	"I am not to be buried there, prejudged, and without any means of
ham	presenting my case?"
ham	"You will see. But, what then? Other people have been similarly buried
ham	in worse prisons, before now."
spam	"But never by me, Citizen Defarge."
spam	Defarge glanced darkly at him for answer, and walked on in a steady
spam	and set silence. The deeper he sank into this silence, the fainter hope
ham	there was--or so Darnay thought--of his softening in any slight degree.
spam	He, therefore, made haste to say:
spam	"It is of the utmost importance to me (you know, Citizen, even better
ham	than I, of how much importance), that I should be able to communicate to
ham	Mr. Lorry of Tellson's Bank, an English gentleman who is now in Paris,
spam	the simple fact, without comment, that I have been thrown into the
ham	prison of La Force. Will you cause that to be done for me?"
ham	"I will do," Defarge doggedly rejoined, "nothing for you. My duty is to
spam	my country and the People. I am the sworn servant of both, against you.
spam	I will do nothing for you."
ham	Charles Darnay felt it hopeless to entreat him further, and his pride
ham	was touched besides. As they walked on in silence, he could not but see
spam	how used the people were to the spectacle of prisoners passing along the
ham	streets. The very children scarcely noticed him. A few passers turned
ham	their heads, and a few shook their fingers at him as an aristocrat;
spam	otherwise, that a man in good clothes should be going to prison, was no
spam	more remarkable than that a labourer in working clothes should be
ham	going to work. In one narrow, dark, and dirty street through which they
spam	passed, an excited orator, mounted on a stool, was addressing an excited
spam	audience on the crimes against the people, of the king and the royal
spam	family. The few words that he caught from this man's lips, first made
ham	it known to Charles Darnay that the king was in prison, and that the
spam	foreign ambassadors had one and all left Paris. On the road (except at
ham	Beauvais) he had heard absolutely nothing. The escort and the universal
spam	watchfulness had completely isolated him.
ham	That he had fallen among far greater dangers than those which had
spam	developed themselves when he left England, he of course knew now. That
spam	perils had thickened about him fast, and might thicken faster and faster
ham	yet, he of course knew now. He could not but admit to himself that he
ham	might not have made this journey, if he could have foreseen the events
ham	of a few days. And yet his misgivings were not so dark as, imagined by
spam	the light of this later time, they would appear. Troubled as the future
spam	was, it was the unknown future, and in its obscurity there was ignorant
spam	hope. The horrible massacre, days and nights long, which, within a few
spam	rounds of the clock, was to set a great mark of blood upon the blessed
ham	garnering time of harvest, was as far out of his knowledge as if it had
spam	been a hundred thousand years away. The "sharp female newly-born, and
ham	called La Guillotine," was hardly known to him, or to the generality
spam	of people, by name. The frightful deeds that were to be soon done, were
spam	probably unimagined at that time in the brains of the doers. How could
ham	they have a place in the shadowy conceptions of a gentle mind?
ham	Of unjust treatment in detention and hardship, and in cruel separation
spam	from his wife and child, he foreshadowed the likelihood, or the
ham	certainty; but, beyond this, he dreaded nothing distinctly. With this on
ham	his mind, which was enough to carry into a dreary prison courtyard, he
spam	arrived at the prison of La Force.
ham	A man with a bloated face opened the strong wicket, to whom Defarge
spam	presented "The Emigrant Evremonde."
spam	"What the Devil! How many more of them!" exclaimed the man with the
spam	bloated face.
ham	Defarge took his receipt without noticing the exclamation, and withdrew,
ham	with his two fellow-patriots.
ham	"What the Devil, I say again!" exclaimed the gaoler, left with his wife.
ham	"How many more!"
ham	The gaoler's wife, being provided with no answer to the question, merely
ham	replied, "One must have patience, my dear!" Three turnkeys who entered
spam	responsive to a bell she rang, echoed the sentiment, and one added, "For
ham	the love of Liberty;" which sounded in that place like an inappropriate
spam	conclusion.
spam	The prison of La Force was a gloomy prison, dark and filthy, and with a
spam	horrible smell of foul sleep in it. Extraordinary how soon the noisome
spam	flavour of imprisoned sleep, becomes manifest in all such places that
ham	are ill cared for!
spam	"In secret, too," grumbled the gaoler, looking at the written paper. "As
ham	if I was not already full to bursting!"
spam	He stuck the paper on a file, in an ill-humour, and Charles Darnay
spam	awaited his further pleasure for half an hour: sometimes, pacing to and
spam	fro in the strong arched room: sometimes, resting on a stone seat: in
ham	either case detained to be imprinted on the memory of the chief and his
ham	subordinates.
spam	"Come!" said the chief, at length taking up his keys, "come with me,
ham	emigrant."
ham	Through the dismal prison twilight, his new charge accompanied him by
spam	corridor and staircase, many doors clanging and locking behind them,
spam	until they came into a large, low, vaulted chamber, crowded with
ham	prisoners of both sexes. The women were seated at a long table, reading
ham	and writing, knitting, sewing, and embroidering; the men were for the
ham	most part standing behind their chairs, or lingering up and down the
ham	room.
ham	In the instinctive association of prisoners with shameful crime and
spam	disgrace, the new-comer recoiled from this company. But the crowning
spam	unreality of his long unreal ride, was, their all at once rising to
spam	receive him, with every refinement of manner known to the time, and with
ham	all the engaging graces and courtesies of life.
spam	So strangely clouded were these refinements by the prison manners and
spam	gloom, so spectral did they become in the inappropriate squalor and
ham	misery through which they were seen, that Charles Darnay seemed to stand
ham	in a company of the dead. Ghosts all! The ghost of beauty, the ghost
ham	of stateliness, the ghost of elegance, the ghost of pride, the ghost of
ham	frivolity, the ghost of wit, the ghost of youth, the ghost of age, all
ham	waiting their dismissal from the desolate shore, all turning on him eyes
spam	that were changed by the death they had died in coming there.
spam	It struck him motionless. The gaoler standing at his side, and the other
ham	gaolers moving about, who would have been well enough as to appearance
spam	in the ordinary exercise of their functions, looked so extravagantly
ham	coarse contrasted with sorrowing mothers and blooming daughters who were
ham	there--with the apparitions of the coquette, the young beauty, and the
