spam	mature woman delicately bred--that the inversion of all experience and
spam	likelihood which the scene of shadows presented, was heightened to its
ham	utmost. Surely, ghosts all. Surely, the long unreal ride some progress
spam	of disease that had brought him to these gloomy shades!
ham	"In the name of the assembled companions in misfortune," said a
ham	gentleman of courtly appearance and address, coming forward, "I have the
ham	honour of giving you welcome to La Force, and of condoling with you
ham	on the calamity that has brought you among us. May it soon terminate
spam	happily! It would be an impertinence elsewhere, but it is not so here,
ham	to ask your name and condition?"
ham	Charles Darnay roused himself, and gave the required information, in
spam	words as suitable as he could find.
spam	"But I hope," said the gentleman, following the chief gaoler with his
spam	eyes, who moved across the room, "that you are not in secret?"
ham	"I do not understand the meaning of the term, but I have heard them say
spam	so."
spam	"Ah, what a pity! We so much regret it! But take courage; several
ham	members of our society have been in secret, at first, and it has lasted
ham	but a short time." Then he added, raising his voice, "I grieve to inform
spam	the society--in secret."
spam	There was a murmur of commiseration as Charles Darnay crossed the room
ham	to a grated door where the gaoler awaited him, and many voices--among
spam	which, the soft and compassionate voices of women were conspicuous--gave
ham	him good wishes and encouragement. He turned at the grated door, to
spam	render the thanks of his heart; it closed under the gaoler's hand; and
spam	the apparitions vanished from his sight forever.
spam	The wicket opened on a stone staircase, leading upward. When they had
ham	ascended forty steps (the prisoner of half an hour already counted
ham	them), the gaoler opened a low black door, and they passed into a
ham	solitary cell. It struck cold and damp, but was not dark.
ham	"Yours," said the gaoler.
ham	"Why am I confined alone?"
ham	"How do I know!"
ham	"I can buy pen, ink, and paper?"
ham	"Such are not my orders. You will be visited, and can ask then. At
ham	present, you may buy your food, and nothing more."
spam	There were in the cell, a chair, a table, and a straw mattress. As
spam	the gaoler made a general inspection of these objects, and of the four
spam	walls, before going out, a wandering fancy wandered through the mind of
ham	the prisoner leaning against the wall opposite to him, that this gaoler
ham	was so unwholesomely bloated, both in face and person, as to look like
spam	a man who had been drowned and filled with water. When the gaoler was
spam	gone, he thought in the same wandering way, "Now am I left, as if I were
ham	dead." Stopping then, to look down at the mattress, he turned from it
ham	with a sick feeling, and thought, "And here in these crawling creatures
ham	is the first condition of the body after death."
spam	"Five paces by four and a half, five paces by four and a half, five
ham	paces by four and a half." The prisoner walked to and fro in his cell,
spam	counting its measurement, and the roar of the city arose like muffled
spam	drums with a wild swell of voices added to them. "He made shoes, he made
spam	shoes, he made shoes." The prisoner counted the measurement again, and
spam	paced faster, to draw his mind with him from that latter repetition.
ham	"The ghosts that vanished when the wicket closed. There was one among
spam	them, the appearance of a lady dressed in black, who was leaning in the
spam	embrasure of a window, and she had a light shining upon her golden
ham	hair, and she looked like * * * * Let us ride on again, for God's sake,
ham	through the illuminated villages with the people all awake! * * * * He
ham	made shoes, he made shoes, he made shoes. * * * * Five paces by four and
spam	a half." With such scraps tossing and rolling upward from the depths of
ham	his mind, the prisoner walked faster and faster, obstinately counting
spam	and counting; and the roar of the city changed to this extent--that it
ham	still rolled in like muffled drums, but with the wail of voices that he
ham	knew, in the swell that rose above them.
spam	II. The Grindstone
ham	Tellson's Bank, established in the Saint Germain Quarter of Paris, was
ham	in a wing of a large house, approached by a courtyard and shut off from
spam	the street by a high wall and a strong gate. The house belonged to
ham	a great nobleman who had lived in it until he made a flight from the
spam	troubles, in his own cook's dress, and got across the borders. A
spam	mere beast of the chase flying from hunters, he was still in his
ham	metempsychosis no other than the same Monseigneur, the preparation
ham	of whose chocolate for whose lips had once occupied three strong men
spam	besides the cook in question.
spam	Monseigneur gone, and the three strong men absolving themselves from the
ham	sin of having drawn his high wages, by being more than ready and
ham	willing to cut his throat on the altar of the dawning Republic one and
spam	indivisible of Liberty, Equality, Fraternity, or Death, Monseigneur's
spam	house had been first sequestrated, and then confiscated. For, all
ham	things moved so fast, and decree followed decree with that fierce
ham	precipitation, that now upon the third night of the autumn month
ham	of September, patriot emissaries of the law were in possession of
ham	Monseigneur's house, and had marked it with the tri-colour, and were
ham	drinking brandy in its state apartments.
ham	A place of business in London like Tellson's place of business in Paris,
spam	would soon have driven the House out of its mind and into the Gazette.
spam	For, what would staid British responsibility and respectability have
ham	said to orange-trees in boxes in a Bank courtyard, and even to a Cupid
ham	over the counter? Yet such things were. Tellson's had whitewashed the
spam	Cupid, but he was still to be seen on the ceiling, in the coolest
ham	linen, aiming (as he very often does) at money from morning to
ham	night. Bankruptcy must inevitably have come of this young Pagan, in
spam	Lombard-street, London, and also of a curtained alcove in the rear of
ham	the immortal boy, and also of a looking-glass let into the wall, and
ham	also of clerks not at all old, who danced in public on the slightest
ham	provocation. Yet, a French Tellson's could get on with these things
spam	exceedingly well, and, as long as the times held together, no man had
ham	taken fright at them, and drawn out his money.
ham	What money would be drawn out of Tellson's henceforth, and what would
spam	lie there, lost and forgotten; what plate and jewels would tarnish in
ham	Tellson's hiding-places, while the depositors rusted in prisons,
ham	and when they should have violently perished; how many accounts with
ham	Tellson's never to be balanced in this world, must be carried over into
spam	the next; no man could have said, that night, any more than Mr. Jarvis
ham	Lorry could, though he thought heavily of these questions. He sat by
ham	a newly-lighted wood fire (the blighted and unfruitful year was
ham	prematurely cold), and on his honest and courageous face there was a
ham	deeper shade than the pendent lamp could throw, or any object in the
spam	room distortedly reflect--a shade of horror.
ham	He occupied rooms in the Bank, in his fidelity to the House of which
ham	he had grown to be a part, like strong root-ivy. It chanced that they
spam	derived a kind of security from the patriotic occupation of the main
ham	building, but the true-hearted old gentleman never calculated about
ham	that. All such circumstances were indifferent to him, so that he did
ham	his duty. On the opposite side of the courtyard, under a colonnade,
ham	was extensive standing--for carriages--where, indeed, some carriages
spam	of Monseigneur yet stood. Against two of the pillars were fastened two
spam	great flaring flambeaux, and in the light of these, standing out in the
spam	open air, was a large grindstone: a roughly mounted thing which appeared
ham	to have hurriedly been brought there from some neighbouring smithy,
ham	or other workshop. Rising and looking out of window at these harmless
ham	objects, Mr. Lorry shivered, and retired to his seat by the fire. He had
ham	opened, not only the glass window, but the lattice blind outside it, and
spam	he had closed both again, and he shivered through his frame.
ham	From the streets beyond the high wall and the strong gate, there came
spam	the usual night hum of the city, with now and then an indescribable ring
ham	in it, weird and unearthly, as if some unwonted sounds of a terrible
spam	nature were going up to Heaven.
spam	"Thank God," said Mr. Lorry, clasping his hands, "that no one near and
spam	dear to me is in this dreadful town to-night. May He have mercy on all
spam	who are in danger!"
spam	Soon afterwards, the bell at the great gate sounded, and he thought,
ham	"They have come back!" and sat listening. But, there was no loud
ham	irruption into the courtyard, as he had expected, and he heard the gate
spam	clash again, and all was quiet.
ham	The nervousness and dread that were upon him inspired that vague
spam	uneasiness respecting the Bank, which a great change would naturally
ham	awaken, with such feelings roused. It was well guarded, and he got up to
spam	go among the trusty people who were watching it, when his door suddenly
ham	opened, and two figures rushed in, at sight of which he fell back in
ham	amazement.
spam	Lucie and her father! Lucie with her arms stretched out to him, and with
spam	that old look of earnestness so concentrated and intensified, that it
ham	seemed as though it had been stamped upon her face expressly to give
spam	force and power to it in this one passage of her life.
ham	"What is this?" cried Mr. Lorry, breathless and confused. "What is the
spam	matter? Lucie! Manette! What has happened? What has brought you here?
ham	What is it?"
spam	With the look fixed upon him, in her paleness and wildness, she panted
spam	out in his arms, imploringly, "O my dear friend! My husband!"
ham	"Your husband, Lucie?"
spam	"Charles."
ham	"What of Charles?"
ham	"Here.
spam	"Here, in Paris?"
ham	"Has been here some days--three or four--I don't know how many--I can't
spam	collect my thoughts. An errand of generosity brought him here unknown to
spam	us; he was stopped at the barrier, and sent to prison."
spam	The old man uttered an irrepressible cry. Almost at the same moment, the
spam	bell of the great gate rang again, and a loud noise of feet and voices
ham	came pouring into the courtyard.
ham	"What is that noise?" said the Doctor, turning towards the window.
ham	"Don't look!" cried Mr. Lorry. "Don't look out! Manette, for your life,
spam	don't touch the blind!"
spam	The Doctor turned, with his hand upon the fastening of the window, and
spam	said, with a cool, bold smile:
ham	"My dear friend, I have a charmed life in this city. I have been
ham	a Bastille prisoner. There is no patriot in Paris--in Paris? In
spam	France--who, knowing me to have been a prisoner in the Bastille, would
spam	touch me, except to overwhelm me with embraces, or carry me in triumph.
ham	My old pain has given me a power that has brought us through the
spam	barrier, and gained us news of Charles there, and brought us here. I
spam	knew it would be so; I knew I could help Charles out of all danger; I
ham	told Lucie so.--What is that noise?" His hand was again upon the window.
spam	"Don't look!" cried Mr. Lorry, absolutely desperate. "No, Lucie, my
spam	dear, nor you!" He got his arm round her, and held her. "Don't be so
ham	terrified, my love. I solemnly swear to you that I know of no harm
ham	having happened to Charles; that I had no suspicion even of his being in
ham	this fatal place. What prison is he in?"
spam	"La Force!"
spam	"La Force! Lucie, my child, if ever you were brave and serviceable in
ham	your life--and you were always both--you will compose yourself now, to
ham	do exactly as I bid you; for more depends upon it than you can think, or
spam	I can say. There is no help for you in any action on your part to-night;
spam	you cannot possibly stir out. I say this, because what I must bid you
ham	to do for Charles's sake, is the hardest thing to do of all. You must
ham	instantly be obedient, still, and quiet. You must let me put you in a
ham	room at the back here. You must leave your father and me alone for
spam	two minutes, and as there are Life and Death in the world you must not
spam	delay."
ham	"I will be submissive to you. I see in your face that you know I can do
ham	nothing else than this. I know you are true."
spam	The old man kissed her, and hurried her into his room, and turned the
spam	key; then, came hurrying back to the Doctor, and opened the window and
spam	partly opened the blind, and put his hand upon the Doctor's arm, and
spam	looked out with him into the courtyard.
ham	Looked out upon a throng of men and women: not enough in number, or near
ham	enough, to fill the courtyard: not more than forty or fifty in all. The
spam	people in possession of the house had let them in at the gate, and they
spam	had rushed in to work at the grindstone; it had evidently been set up
spam	there for their purpose, as in a convenient and retired spot.
ham	But, such awful workers, and such awful work!
spam	The grindstone had a double handle, and, turning at it madly were two
spam	men, whose faces, as their long hair flapped back when the whirlings of
spam	the grindstone brought their faces up, were more horrible and cruel than
spam	the visages of the wildest savages in their most barbarous disguise.
spam	False eyebrows and false moustaches were stuck upon them, and their
spam	hideous countenances were all bloody and sweaty, and all awry with
ham	howling, and all staring and glaring with beastly excitement and want of
spam	sleep. As these ruffians turned and turned, their matted locks now flung
spam	forward over their eyes, now flung backward over their necks, some women
spam	held wine to their mouths that they might drink; and what with dropping
spam	blood, and what with dropping wine, and what with the stream of sparks
ham	struck out of the stone, all their wicked atmosphere seemed gore and
ham	fire. The eye could not detect one creature in the group free from
ham	the smear of blood. Shouldering one another to get next at the
spam	sharpening-stone, were men stripped to the waist, with the stain all
ham	over their limbs and bodies; men in all sorts of rags, with the stain
spam	upon those rags; men devilishly set off with spoils of women's lace
ham	and silk and ribbon, with the stain dyeing those trifles through
spam	and through. Hatchets, knives, bayonets, swords, all brought to be
spam	sharpened, were all red with it. Some of the hacked swords were tied to
spam	the wrists of those who carried them, with strips of linen and fragments
spam	of dress: ligatures various in kind, but all deep of the one colour. And
spam	as the frantic wielders of these weapons snatched them from the stream
spam	of sparks and tore away into the streets, the same red hue was red in
spam	their frenzied eyes;--eyes which any unbrutalised beholder would have
spam	given twenty years of life, to petrify with a well-directed gun.
ham	All this was seen in a moment, as the vision of a drowning man, or of
ham	any human creature at any very great pass, could see a world if it
ham	were there. They drew back from the window, and the Doctor looked for
ham	explanation in his friend's ashy face.
ham	"They are," Mr. Lorry whispered the words, glancing fearfully round at
ham	the locked room, "murdering the prisoners. If you are sure of what you
ham	say; if you really have the power you think you have--as I believe you
spam	have--make yourself known to these devils, and get taken to La Force. It
ham	may be too late, I don't know, but let it not be a minute later!"
ham	Doctor Manette pressed his hand, hastened bareheaded out of the room,
spam	and was in the courtyard when Mr. Lorry regained the blind.
spam	His streaming white hair, his remarkable face, and the impetuous
spam	confidence of his manner, as he put the weapons aside like water,
ham	carried him in an instant to the heart of the concourse at the stone.
ham	For a few moments there was a pause, and a hurry, and a murmur, and
spam	the unintelligible sound of his voice; and then Mr. Lorry saw him,
ham	surrounded by all, and in the midst of a line of twenty men long, all
spam	linked shoulder to shoulder, and hand to shoulder, hurried out with
spam	cries of--"Live the Bastille prisoner! Help for the Bastille prisoner's
spam	kindred in La Force! Room for the Bastille prisoner in front there! Save
spam	the prisoner Evremonde at La Force!" and a thousand answering shouts.
ham	He closed the lattice again with a fluttering heart, closed the window
spam	and the curtain, hastened to Lucie, and told her that her father was
ham	assisted by the people, and gone in search of her husband. He found
spam	her child and Miss Pross with her; but, it never occurred to him to be
ham	surprised by their appearance until a long time afterwards, when he sat
ham	watching them in such quiet as the night knew.
ham	Lucie had, by that time, fallen into a stupor on the floor at his feet,
spam	clinging to his hand. Miss Pross had laid the child down on his own
ham	bed, and her head had gradually fallen on the pillow beside her pretty
spam	charge. O the long, long night, with the moans of the poor wife! And O
ham	the long, long night, with no return of her father and no tidings!
spam	Twice more in the darkness the bell at the great gate sounded, and the
spam	irruption was repeated, and the grindstone whirled and spluttered.
spam	"What is it?" cried Lucie, affrighted. "Hush! The soldiers' swords are
spam	sharpened there," said Mr. Lorry. "The place is national property now,
spam	and used as a kind of armoury, my love."
ham	Twice more in all; but, the last spell of work was feeble and fitful.
spam	Soon afterwards the day began to dawn, and he softly detached himself
ham	from the clasping hand, and cautiously looked out again. A man, so
spam	besmeared that he might have been a sorely wounded soldier creeping back
ham	to consciousness on a field of slain, was rising from the pavement by
ham	the side of the grindstone, and looking about him with a vacant air.
ham	Shortly, this worn-out murderer descried in the imperfect light one of
spam	the carriages of Monseigneur, and, staggering to that gorgeous vehicle,
spam	climbed in at the door, and shut himself up to take his rest on its
ham	dainty cushions.
spam	The great grindstone, Earth, had turned when Mr. Lorry looked out again,
spam	and the sun was red on the courtyard. But, the lesser grindstone stood
spam	alone there in the calm morning air, with a red upon it that the sun had
spam	never given, and would never take away.
spam	III. The Shadow
spam	One of the first considerations which arose in the business mind of Mr.
ham	Lorry when business hours came round, was this:--that he had no right to
ham	imperil Tellson's by sheltering the wife of an emigrant prisoner under
ham	the Bank roof. His own possessions, safety, life, he would have hazarded
spam	for Lucie and her child, without a moment's demur; but the great trust
ham	he held was not his own, and as to that business charge he was a strict
ham	man of business.
spam	At first, his mind reverted to Defarge, and he thought of finding out
spam	the wine-shop again and taking counsel with its master in reference to
ham	the safest dwelling-place in the distracted state of the city. But, the
ham	same consideration that suggested him, repudiated him; he lived in the
ham	most violent Quarter, and doubtless was influential there, and deep in
spam	its dangerous workings.
ham	Noon coming, and the Doctor not returning, and every minute's delay
spam	tending to compromise Tellson's, Mr. Lorry advised with Lucie. She said
spam	that her father had spoken of hiring a lodging for a short term, in that
ham	Quarter, near the Banking-house. As there was no business objection to
ham	this, and as he foresaw that even if it were all well with Charles, and
ham	he were to be released, he could not hope to leave the city, Mr. Lorry
spam	went out in quest of such a lodging, and found a suitable one, high up
spam	in a removed by-street where the closed blinds in all the other windows
spam	of a high melancholy square of buildings marked deserted homes.
spam	To this lodging he at once removed Lucie and her child, and Miss Pross:
spam	giving them what comfort he could, and much more than he had himself.
ham	He left Jerry with them, as a figure to fill a doorway that would bear
spam	considerable knocking on the head, and retained to his own occupations.
ham	A disturbed and doleful mind he brought to bear upon them, and slowly
spam	and heavily the day lagged on with him.
spam	It wore itself out, and wore him out with it, until the Bank closed. He
ham	was again alone in his room of the previous night, considering what to
spam	do next, when he heard a foot upon the stair. In a few moments, a
spam	man stood in his presence, who, with a keenly observant look at him,
spam	addressed him by his name.
ham	"Your servant," said Mr. Lorry. "Do you know me?"
spam	He was a strongly made man with dark curling hair, from forty-five
ham	to fifty years of age. For answer he repeated, without any change of
spam	emphasis, the words:
spam	"Do you know me?"
spam	"I have seen you somewhere."
ham	"Perhaps at my wine-shop?"
ham	Much interested and agitated, Mr. Lorry said: "You come from Doctor
spam	Manette?"
spam	"Yes. I come from Doctor Manette."
ham	"And what says he? What does he send me?"
spam	Defarge gave into his anxious hand, an open scrap of paper. It bore the
ham	words in the Doctor's writing:
ham	    "Charles is safe, but I cannot safely leave this place yet.
spam	     I have obtained the favour that the bearer has a short note
spam	     from Charles to his wife.  Let the bearer see his wife."
ham	It was dated from La Force, within an hour.
ham	"Will you accompany me," said Mr. Lorry, joyfully relieved after reading
ham	this note aloud, "to where his wife resides?"
ham	"Yes," returned Defarge.
spam	Scarcely noticing as yet, in what a curiously reserved and mechanical
spam	way Defarge spoke, Mr. Lorry put on his hat and they went down into the
spam	courtyard. There, they found two women; one, knitting.
spam	"Madame Defarge, surely!" said Mr. Lorry, who had left her in exactly
ham	the same attitude some seventeen years ago.
spam	"It is she," observed her husband.
ham	"Does Madame go with us?" inquired Mr. Lorry, seeing that she moved as
spam	they moved.
spam	"Yes. That she may be able to recognise the faces and know the persons.
spam	It is for their safety."
spam	Beginning to be struck by Defarge's manner, Mr. Lorry looked dubiously
spam	at him, and led the way. Both the women followed; the second woman being
ham	The Vengeance.
ham	They passed through the intervening streets as quickly as they might,
spam	ascended the staircase of the new domicile, were admitted by Jerry,
ham	and found Lucie weeping, alone. She was thrown into a transport by the
spam	tidings Mr. Lorry gave her of her husband, and clasped the hand that
spam	delivered his note--little thinking what it had been doing near him in
spam	the night, and might, but for a chance, have done to him.
ham	     "DEAREST,--Take courage.  I am well, and your father has
ham	      influence around me.  You cannot answer this.
ham	      Kiss our child for me."
ham	That was all the writing. It was so much, however, to her who received
ham	it, that she turned from Defarge to his wife, and kissed one of the
ham	hands that knitted. It was a passionate, loving, thankful, womanly
spam	action, but the hand made no response--dropped cold and heavy, and took
spam	to its knitting again.
ham	There was something in its touch that gave Lucie a check. She stopped in
ham	the act of putting the note in her bosom, and, with her hands yet at her
spam	neck, looked terrified at Madame Defarge. Madame Defarge met the lifted
spam	eyebrows and forehead with a cold, impassive stare.
ham	"My dear," said Mr. Lorry, striking in to explain; "there are frequent
ham	risings in the streets; and, although it is not likely they will ever
ham	trouble you, Madame Defarge wishes to see those whom she has the power
spam	to protect at such times, to the end that she may know them--that she
spam	may identify them. I believe," said Mr. Lorry, rather halting in his
spam	reassuring words, as the stony manner of all the three impressed itself
spam	upon him more and more, "I state the case, Citizen Defarge?"
spam	Defarge looked gloomily at his wife, and gave no other answer than a
ham	gruff sound of acquiescence.
spam	"You had better, Lucie," said Mr. Lorry, doing all he could to
ham	propitiate, by tone and manner, "have the dear child here, and our
ham	good Pross. Our good Pross, Defarge, is an English lady, and knows no
spam	French."
spam	The lady in question, whose rooted conviction that she was more than a
ham	match for any foreigner, was not to be shaken by distress and, danger,
spam	appeared with folded arms, and observed in English to The Vengeance,
ham	whom her eyes first encountered, "Well, I am sure, Boldface! I hope
spam	_you_ are pretty well!" She also bestowed a British cough on Madame
spam	Defarge; but, neither of the two took much heed of her.
spam	"Is that his child?" said Madame Defarge, stopping in her work for the
ham	first time, and pointing her knitting-needle at little Lucie as if it
ham	were the finger of Fate.
ham	"Yes, madame," answered Mr. Lorry; "this is our poor prisoner's darling
spam	daughter, and only child."
ham	The shadow attendant on Madame Defarge and her party seemed to fall so
ham	threatening and dark on the child, that her mother instinctively
ham	kneeled on the ground beside her, and held her to her breast. The
ham	shadow attendant on Madame Defarge and her party seemed then to fall,
spam	threatening and dark, on both the mother and the child.
ham	"It is enough, my husband," said Madame Defarge. "I have seen them. We
spam	may go."
spam	But, the suppressed manner had enough of menace in it--not visible and
ham	presented, but indistinct and withheld--to alarm Lucie into saying, as
ham	she laid her appealing hand on Madame Defarge's dress:
ham	"You will be good to my poor husband. You will do him no harm. You will
spam	help me to see him if you can?"
spam	"Your husband is not my business here," returned Madame Defarge, looking
ham	down at her with perfect composure. "It is the daughter of your father
spam	who is my business here."
ham	"For my sake, then, be merciful to my husband. For my child's sake! She
spam	will put her hands together and pray you to be merciful. We are more
ham	afraid of you than of these others."
ham	Madame Defarge received it as a compliment, and looked at her husband.
ham	Defarge, who had been uneasily biting his thumb-nail and looking at her,
spam	collected his face into a sterner expression.
ham	"What is it that your husband says in that little letter?" asked Madame
spam	Defarge, with a lowering smile. "Influence; he says something touching
ham	influence?"
spam	"That my father," said Lucie, hurriedly taking the paper from her
spam	breast, but with her alarmed eyes on her questioner and not on it, "has
ham	much influence around him."
spam	"Surely it will release him!" said Madame Defarge. "Let it do so."
spam	"As a wife and mother," cried Lucie, most earnestly, "I implore you to
ham	have pity on me and not to exercise any power that you possess, against
spam	my innocent husband, but to use it in his behalf. O sister-woman, think
spam	of me. As a wife and mother!"
ham	Madame Defarge looked, coldly as ever, at the suppliant, and said,
ham	turning to her friend The Vengeance:
ham	"The wives and mothers we have been used to see, since we were as little
spam	as this child, and much less, have not been greatly considered? We have
ham	known _their_ husbands and fathers laid in prison and kept from them,
spam	often enough? All our lives, we have seen our sister-women suffer, in
ham	themselves and in their children, poverty, nakedness, hunger, thirst,
spam	sickness, misery, oppression and neglect of all kinds?"
ham	"We have seen nothing else," returned The Vengeance.
spam	"We have borne this a long time," said Madame Defarge, turning her eyes
ham	again upon Lucie. "Judge you! Is it likely that the trouble of one wife
spam	and mother would be much to us now?"
spam	She resumed her knitting and went out. The Vengeance followed. Defarge
spam	went last, and closed the door.
spam	"Courage, my dear Lucie," said Mr. Lorry, as he raised her. "Courage,
spam	courage! So far all goes well with us--much, much better than it has of
ham	late gone with many poor souls. Cheer up, and have a thankful heart."
ham	"I am not thankless, I hope, but that dreadful woman seems to throw a
ham	shadow on me and on all my hopes."
ham	"Tut, tut!" said Mr. Lorry; "what is this despondency in the brave
spam	little breast? A shadow indeed! No substance in it, Lucie."
spam	But the shadow of the manner of these Defarges was dark upon himself,
ham	for all that, and in his secret mind it troubled him greatly.
ham	IV. Calm in Storm
ham	Doctor Manette did not return until the morning of the fourth day of his
spam	absence. So much of what had happened in that dreadful time as could be
spam	kept from the knowledge of Lucie was so well concealed from her, that
spam	not until long afterwards, when France and she were far apart, did she
ham	know that eleven hundred defenceless prisoners of both sexes and all
ham	ages had been killed by the populace; that four days and nights had been
spam	darkened by this deed of horror; and that the air around her had been
spam	tainted by the slain. She only knew that there had been an attack upon
ham	the prisons, that all political prisoners had been in danger, and that
ham	some had been dragged out by the crowd and murdered.
spam	To Mr. Lorry, the Doctor communicated under an injunction of secrecy on
spam	which he had no need to dwell, that the crowd had taken him through a
spam	scene of carnage to the prison of La Force. That, in the prison he had
ham	found a self-appointed Tribunal sitting, before which the prisoners were
spam	brought singly, and by which they were rapidly ordered to be put forth
ham	to be massacred, or to be released, or (in a few cases) to be sent back
ham	to their cells. That, presented by his conductors to this Tribunal, he
spam	had announced himself by name and profession as having been for eighteen
ham	years a secret and unaccused prisoner in the Bastille; that, one of the
ham	body so sitting in judgment had risen and identified him, and that this
spam	man was Defarge.
spam	That, hereupon he had ascertained, through the registers on the table,
spam	that his son-in-law was among the living prisoners, and had pleaded hard
spam	to the Tribunal--of whom some members were asleep and some awake, some
ham	dirty with murder and some clean, some sober and some not--for his life
ham	and liberty. That, in the first frantic greetings lavished on himself as
spam	a notable sufferer under the overthrown system, it had been accorded
ham	to him to have Charles Darnay brought before the lawless Court, and
spam	examined. That, he seemed on the point of being at once released, when
ham	the tide in his favour met with some unexplained check (not intelligible
ham	to the Doctor), which led to a few words of secret conference. That,
ham	the man sitting as President had then informed Doctor Manette that
ham	the prisoner must remain in custody, but should, for his sake, be held
ham	inviolate in safe custody. That, immediately, on a signal, the prisoner
ham	was removed to the interior of the prison again; but, that he, the
spam	Doctor, had then so strongly pleaded for permission to remain and
spam	assure himself that his son-in-law was, through no malice or mischance,
ham	delivered to the concourse whose murderous yells outside the gate had
ham	often drowned the proceedings, that he had obtained the permission, and
ham	had remained in that Hall of Blood until the danger was over.
spam	The sights he had seen there, with brief snatches of food and sleep by
spam	intervals, shall remain untold. The mad joy over the prisoners who were
ham	saved, had astounded him scarcely less than the mad ferocity against
spam	those who were cut to pieces. One prisoner there was, he said, who had
ham	been discharged into the street free, but at whom a mistaken savage had
ham	thrust a pike as he passed out. Being besought to go to him and dress
spam	the wound, the Doctor had passed out at the same gate, and had found him
ham	in the arms of a company of Samaritans, who were seated on the bodies
spam	of their victims. With an inconsistency as monstrous as anything in this
spam	awful nightmare, they had helped the healer, and tended the wounded man
spam	with the gentlest solicitude--had made a litter for him and escorted him
ham	carefully from the spot--had then caught up their weapons and plunged
ham	anew into a butchery so dreadful, that the Doctor had covered his eyes
ham	with his hands, and swooned away in the midst of it.
ham	As Mr. Lorry received these confidences, and as he watched the face of
spam	his friend now sixty-two years of age, a misgiving arose within him that
ham	such dread experiences would revive the old danger.
ham	But, he had never seen his friend in his present aspect: he had never
spam	at all known him in his present character. For the first time the Doctor
spam	felt, now, that his suffering was strength and power. For the first time
ham	he felt that in that sharp fire, he had slowly forged the iron which
spam	could break the prison door of his daughter's husband, and deliver him.
spam	"It all tended to a good end, my friend; it was not mere waste and ruin.
ham	As my beloved child was helpful in restoring me to myself, I will be
ham	helpful now in restoring the dearest part of herself to her; by the aid
spam	of Heaven I will do it!" Thus, Doctor Manette. And when Jarvis Lorry saw
ham	the kindled eyes, the resolute face, the calm strong look and bearing
spam	of the man whose life always seemed to him to have been stopped, like a
ham	clock, for so many years, and then set going again with an energy which
spam	had lain dormant during the cessation of its usefulness, he believed.
spam	Greater things than the Doctor had at that time to contend with, would
spam	have yielded before his persevering purpose. While he kept himself
spam	in his place, as a physician, whose business was with all degrees
ham	of mankind, bond and free, rich and poor, bad and good, he used his
ham	personal influence so wisely, that he was soon the inspecting physician
spam	of three prisons, and among them of La Force. He could now assure Lucie
spam	that her husband was no longer confined alone, but was mixed with the
spam	general body of prisoners; he saw her husband weekly, and brought sweet
spam	messages to her, straight from his lips; sometimes her husband himself
spam	sent a letter to her (though never by the Doctor's hand), but she was
spam	not permitted to write to him: for, among the many wild suspicions of
ham	plots in the prisons, the wildest of all pointed at emigrants who were
spam	known to have made friends or permanent connections abroad.
ham	This new life of the Doctor's was an anxious life, no doubt; still, the
ham	sagacious Mr. Lorry saw that there was a new sustaining pride in it.
spam	Nothing unbecoming tinged the pride; it was a natural and worthy one;
ham	but he observed it as a curiosity. The Doctor knew, that up to that
ham	time, his imprisonment had been associated in the minds of his daughter
ham	and his friend, with his personal affliction, deprivation, and weakness.
spam	Now that this was changed, and he knew himself to be invested through
spam	that old trial with forces to which they both looked for Charles's
spam	ultimate safety and deliverance, he became so far exalted by the change,
spam	that he took the lead and direction, and required them as the weak, to
spam	trust to him as the strong. The preceding relative positions of himself
spam	and Lucie were reversed, yet only as the liveliest gratitude and
spam	affection could reverse them, for he could have had no pride but in
ham	rendering some service to her who had rendered so much to him. "All
ham	curious to see," thought Mr. Lorry, in his amiably shrewd way, "but all
spam	natural and right; so, take the lead, my dear friend, and keep it; it
spam	couldn't be in better hands."
spam	But, though the Doctor tried hard, and never ceased trying, to get
ham	Charles Darnay set at liberty, or at least to get him brought to trial,
spam	the public current of the time set too strong and fast for him. The new
ham	era began; the king was tried, doomed, and beheaded; the Republic of
spam	Liberty, Equality, Fraternity, or Death, declared for victory or death
ham	against the world in arms; the black flag waved night and day from the
ham	great towers of Notre Dame; three hundred thousand men, summoned to rise
ham	against the tyrants of the earth, rose from all the varying soils
spam	of France, as if the dragon's teeth had been sown broadcast, and
spam	had yielded fruit equally on hill and plain, on rock, in gravel, and
spam	alluvial mud, under the bright sky of the South and under the clouds of
spam	the North, in fell and forest, in the vineyards and the olive-grounds
ham	and among the cropped grass and the stubble of the corn, along the
spam	fruitful banks of the broad rivers, and in the sand of the sea-shore.
spam	What private solicitude could rear itself against the deluge of the Year
ham	One of Liberty--the deluge rising from below, not falling from above,
ham	and with the windows of Heaven shut, not opened!
spam	There was no pause, no pity, no peace, no interval of relenting rest, no
ham	measurement of time. Though days and nights circled as regularly as when
ham	time was young, and the evening and morning were the first day, other
ham	count of time there was none. Hold of it was lost in the raging fever
spam	of a nation, as it is in the fever of one patient. Now, breaking the
ham	unnatural silence of a whole city, the executioner showed the people the
spam	head of the king--and now, it seemed almost in the same breath, the
spam	head of his fair wife which had had eight weary months of imprisoned
spam	widowhood and misery, to turn it grey.
spam	And yet, observing the strange law of contradiction which obtains in
ham	all such cases, the time was long, while it flamed by so fast. A
ham	revolutionary tribunal in the capital, and forty or fifty thousand
ham	revolutionary committees all over the land; a law of the Suspected,
ham	which struck away all security for liberty or life, and delivered over
spam	any good and innocent person to any bad and guilty one; prisons gorged
ham	with people who had committed no offence, and could obtain no hearing;
ham	these things became the established order and nature of appointed
ham	things, and seemed to be ancient usage before they were many weeks old.
spam	Above all, one hideous figure grew as familiar as if it had been before
spam	the general gaze from the foundations of the world--the figure of the
ham	sharp female called La Guillotine.
ham	It was the popular theme for jests; it was the best cure for headache,
ham	it infallibly prevented the hair from turning grey, it imparted a
ham	peculiar delicacy to the complexion, it was the National Razor which
spam	shaved close: who kissed La Guillotine, looked through the little window
ham	and sneezed into the sack. It was the sign of the regeneration of the
spam	human race. It superseded the Cross. Models of it were worn on breasts
spam	from which the Cross was discarded, and it was bowed down to and
ham	believed in where the Cross was denied.
ham	It sheared off heads so many, that it, and the ground it most polluted,
ham	were a rotten red. It was taken to pieces, like a toy-puzzle for a young
ham	Devil, and was put together again when the occasion wanted it. It hushed
spam	the eloquent, struck down the powerful, abolished the beautiful and
spam	good. Twenty-two friends of high public mark, twenty-one living and one
spam	dead, it had lopped the heads off, in one morning, in as many minutes.
spam	The name of the strong man of Old Scripture had descended to the chief
spam	functionary who worked it; but, so armed, he was stronger than his
spam	namesake, and blinder, and tore away the gates of God's own Temple every
ham	day.
ham	Among these terrors, and the brood belonging to them, the Doctor walked
ham	with a steady head: confident in his power, cautiously persistent in his
spam	end, never doubting that he would save Lucie's husband at last. Yet the
spam	current of the time swept by, so strong and deep, and carried the time
ham	away so fiercely, that Charles had lain in prison one year and three
ham	months when the Doctor was thus steady and confident. So much more
ham	wicked and distracted had the Revolution grown in that December month,
ham	that the rivers of the South were encumbered with the bodies of the
spam	violently drowned by night, and prisoners were shot in lines and squares
spam	under the southern wintry sun. Still, the Doctor walked among the
spam	terrors with a steady head. No man better known than he, in Paris at
spam	that day; no man in a stranger situation. Silent, humane, indispensable
ham	in hospital and prison, using his art equally among assassins and
ham	victims, he was a man apart. In the exercise of his skill, the
ham	appearance and the story of the Bastille Captive removed him from all
spam	other men. He was not suspected or brought in question, any more than if
ham	he had indeed been recalled to life some eighteen years before, or were
spam	a Spirit moving among mortals.
spam	V. The Wood-Sawyer
spam	One year and three months. During all that time Lucie was never
spam	sure, from hour to hour, but that the Guillotine would strike off her
spam	husband's head next day. Every day, through the stony streets, the
spam	tumbrils now jolted heavily, filled with Condemned. Lovely girls; bright
spam	women, brown-haired, black-haired, and grey; youths; stalwart men and
spam	old; gentle born and peasant born; all red wine for La Guillotine, all
ham	daily brought into light from the dark cellars of the loathsome prisons,
ham	and carried to her through the streets to slake her devouring thirst.
ham	Liberty, equality, fraternity, or death;--the last, much the easiest to
ham	bestow, O Guillotine!
spam	If the suddenness of her calamity, and the whirling wheels of the time,
spam	had stunned the Doctor's daughter into awaiting the result in idle
spam	despair, it would but have been with her as it was with many. But, from
spam	the hour when she had taken the white head to her fresh young bosom in
spam	the garret of Saint Antoine, she had been true to her duties. She was
ham	truest to them in the season of trial, as all the quietly loyal and good
ham	will always be.
ham	As soon as they were established in their new residence, and her father
ham	had entered on the routine of his avocations, she arranged the little
ham	household as exactly as if her husband had been there. Everything had
spam	its appointed place and its appointed time. Little Lucie she taught,
spam	as regularly, as if they had all been united in their English home. The
spam	slight devices with which she cheated herself into the show of a belief
spam	that they would soon be reunited--the little preparations for his speedy
spam	return, the setting aside of his chair and his books--these, and the
ham	solemn prayer at night for one dear prisoner especially, among the many
spam	unhappy souls in prison and the shadow of death--were almost the only
spam	outspoken reliefs of her heavy mind.
ham	She did not greatly alter in appearance. The plain dark dresses, akin to
ham	mourning dresses, which she and her child wore, were as neat and as well
ham	attended to as the brighter clothes of happy days. She lost her colour,
ham	and the old and intent expression was a constant, not an occasional,
spam	thing; otherwise, she remained very pretty and comely. Sometimes, at
spam	night on kissing her father, she would burst into the grief she had
spam	repressed all day, and would say that her sole reliance, under Heaven,
spam	was on him. He always resolutely answered: "Nothing can happen to him
spam	without my knowledge, and I know that I can save him, Lucie."
ham	They had not made the round of their changed life many weeks, when her
spam	father said to her, on coming home one evening:
spam	"My dear, there is an upper window in the prison, to which Charles can
ham	sometimes gain access at three in the afternoon. When he can get to
ham	it--which depends on many uncertainties and incidents--he might see you
ham	in the street, he thinks, if you stood in a certain place that I can
spam	show you. But you will not be able to see him, my poor child, and even
ham	if you could, it would be unsafe for you to make a sign of recognition."
ham	"O show me the place, my father, and I will go there every day."
spam	From that time, in all weathers, she waited there two hours. As the
ham	clock struck two, she was there, and at four she turned resignedly away.
spam	When it was not too wet or inclement for her child to be with her, they
ham	went together; at other times she was alone; but, she never missed a
spam	single day.
ham	It was the dark and dirty corner of a small winding street. The hovel
spam	of a cutter of wood into lengths for burning, was the only house at that
ham	end; all else was wall. On the third day of her being there, he noticed
ham	her.
ham	"Good day, citizeness."
ham	"Good day, citizen."
spam	This mode of address was now prescribed by decree. It had been
ham	established voluntarily some time ago, among the more thorough patriots;
ham	but, was now law for everybody.
spam	"Walking here again, citizeness?"
ham	"You see me, citizen!"
spam	The wood-sawyer, who was a little man with a redundancy of gesture (he
spam	had once been a mender of roads), cast a glance at the prison, pointed
spam	at the prison, and putting his ten fingers before his face to represent
ham	bars, peeped through them jocosely.
ham	"But it's not my business," said he. And went on sawing his wood.
spam	Next day he was looking out for her, and accosted her the moment she
ham	appeared.
ham	"What? Walking here again, citizeness?"
ham	"Yes, citizen."
ham	"Ah! A child too! Your mother, is it not, my little citizeness?"
ham	"Do I say yes, mamma?" whispered little Lucie, drawing close to her.
ham	"Yes, dearest."
ham	"Yes, citizen."
spam	"Ah! But it's not my business. My work is my business. See my saw! I
ham	call it my Little Guillotine. La, la, la; La, la, la! And off his head
spam	comes!"
spam	The billet fell as he spoke, and he threw it into a basket.
ham	"I call myself the Samson of the firewood guillotine. See here again!
ham	Loo, loo, loo; Loo, loo, loo! And off _her_ head comes! Now, a child.
ham	Tickle, tickle; Pickle, pickle! And off _its_ head comes. All the
spam	family!"
spam	Lucie shuddered as he threw two more billets into his basket, but it was
spam	impossible to be there while the wood-sawyer was at work, and not be in
ham	his sight. Thenceforth, to secure his good will, she always spoke to him
ham	first, and often gave him drink-money, which he readily received.
ham	He was an inquisitive fellow, and sometimes when she had quite forgotten
ham	him in gazing at the prison roof and grates, and in lifting her heart
ham	up to her husband, she would come to herself to find him looking at her,
spam	with his knee on his bench and his saw stopped in its work. "But it's
spam	not my business!" he would generally say at those times, and would
ham	briskly fall to his sawing again.
spam	In all weathers, in the snow and frost of winter, in the bitter winds of
spam	spring, in the hot sunshine of summer, in the rains of autumn, and again
spam	in the snow and frost of winter, Lucie passed two hours of every day at
ham	this place; and every day on leaving it, she kissed the prison wall.
spam	Her husband saw her (so she learned from her father) it might be once in
ham	five or six times: it might be twice or thrice running: it might be, not
spam	for a week or a fortnight together. It was enough that he could and did
spam	see her when the chances served, and on that possibility she would have
ham	waited out the day, seven days a week.
ham	These occupations brought her round to the December month, wherein her
spam	father walked among the terrors with a steady head. On a lightly-snowing
ham	afternoon she arrived at the usual corner. It was a day of some wild
spam	rejoicing, and a festival. She had seen the houses, as she came along,
spam	decorated with little pikes, and with little red caps stuck upon them;
spam	also, with tricoloured ribbons; also, with the standard inscription
spam	(tricoloured letters were the favourite), Republic One and Indivisible.
ham	Liberty, Equality, Fraternity, or Death!
ham	The miserable shop of the wood-sawyer was so small, that its whole
spam	surface furnished very indifferent space for this legend. He had got
spam	somebody to scrawl it up for him, however, who had squeezed Death in
ham	with most inappropriate difficulty. On his house-top, he displayed pike
ham	and cap, as a good citizen must, and in a window he had stationed his
spam	saw inscribed as his "Little Sainte Guillotine"--for the great sharp
spam	female was by that time popularly canonised. His shop was shut and he
spam	was not there, which was a relief to Lucie, and left her quite alone.
ham	But, he was not far off, for presently she heard a troubled movement
spam	and a shouting coming along, which filled her with fear. A moment
spam	afterwards, and a throng of people came pouring round the corner by the
ham	prison wall, in the midst of whom was the wood-sawyer hand in hand with
spam	The Vengeance. There could not be fewer than five hundred people, and
ham	they were dancing like five thousand demons. There was no other music
spam	than their own singing. They danced to the popular Revolution song,
ham	keeping a ferocious time that was like a gnashing of teeth in unison.
spam	Men and women danced together, women danced together, men danced
spam	together, as hazard had brought them together. At first, they were a
spam	mere storm of coarse red caps and coarse woollen rags; but, as they
ham	filled the place, and stopped to dance about Lucie, some ghastly
ham	apparition of a dance-figure gone raving mad arose among them. They
ham	advanced, retreated, struck at one another's hands, clutched at one
spam	another's heads, spun round alone, caught one another and spun round
ham	in pairs, until many of them dropped. While those were down, the rest
ham	linked hand in hand, and all spun round together: then the ring broke,
ham	and in separate rings of two and four they turned and turned until they
spam	all stopped at once, began again, struck, clutched, and tore, and then
ham	reversed the spin, and all spun round another way. Suddenly they stopped
ham	again, paused, struck out the time afresh, formed into lines the width
ham	of the public way, and, with their heads low down and their hands high
spam	up, swooped screaming off. No fight could have been half so terrible
ham	as this dance. It was so emphatically a fallen sport--a something, once
spam	innocent, delivered over to all devilry--a healthy pastime changed into
spam	a means of angering the blood, bewildering the senses, and steeling the
ham	heart. Such grace as was visible in it, made it the uglier, showing how
ham	warped and perverted all things good by nature were become. The maidenly
ham	bosom bared to this, the pretty almost-child's head thus distracted, the
spam	delicate foot mincing in this slough of blood and dirt, were types of
spam	the disjointed time.
spam	This was the Carmagnole. As it passed, leaving Lucie frightened and
ham	bewildered in the doorway of the wood-sawyer's house, the feathery snow
spam	fell as quietly and lay as white and soft, as if it had never been.
ham	"O my father!" for he stood before her when she lifted up the eyes she
ham	had momentarily darkened with her hand; "such a cruel, bad sight."
ham	"I know, my dear, I know. I have seen it many times. Don't be
spam	frightened! Not one of them would harm you."
ham	"I am not frightened for myself, my father. But when I think of my
spam	husband, and the mercies of these people--"
spam	"We will set him above their mercies very soon. I left him climbing to
ham	the window, and I came to tell you. There is no one here to see. You may
ham	kiss your hand towards that highest shelving roof."
ham	"I do so, father, and I send him my Soul with it!"
ham	"You cannot see him, my poor dear?"
spam	"No, father," said Lucie, yearning and weeping as she kissed her hand,
ham	"no."
spam	A footstep in the snow. Madame Defarge. "I salute you, citizeness,"
ham	from the Doctor. "I salute you, citizen." This in passing. Nothing more.
ham	Madame Defarge gone, like a shadow over the white road.
spam	"Give me your arm, my love. Pass from here with an air of cheerfulness
spam	and courage, for his sake. That was well done;" they had left the spot;
ham	"it shall not be in vain. Charles is summoned for to-morrow."
spam	"For to-morrow!"
ham	"There is no time to lose. I am well prepared, but there are precautions
spam	to be taken, that could not be taken until he was actually summoned
spam	before the Tribunal. He has not received the notice yet, but I know
spam	that he will presently be summoned for to-morrow, and removed to the
spam	Conciergerie; I have timely information. You are not afraid?"
spam	She could scarcely answer, "I trust in you."
ham	"Do so, implicitly. Your suspense is nearly ended, my darling; he shall
ham	be restored to you within a few hours; I have encompassed him with every
ham	protection. I must see Lorry."
ham	He stopped. There was a heavy lumbering of wheels within hearing. They
spam	both knew too well what it meant. One. Two. Three. Three tumbrils faring
ham	away with their dread loads over the hushing snow.
ham	"I must see Lorry," the Doctor repeated, turning her another way.
ham	The staunch old gentleman was still in his trust; had never left it. He
spam	and his books were in frequent requisition as to property confiscated
ham	and made national. What he could save for the owners, he saved. No
ham	better man living to hold fast by what Tellson's had in keeping, and to
spam	hold his peace.
spam	A murky red and yellow sky, and a rising mist from the Seine, denoted
ham	the approach of darkness. It was almost dark when they arrived at the
ham	Bank. The stately residence of Monseigneur was altogether blighted and
spam	deserted. Above a heap of dust and ashes in the court, ran the letters:
spam	National Property. Republic One and Indivisible. Liberty, Equality,
spam	Fraternity, or Death!
spam	Who could that be with Mr. Lorry--the owner of the riding-coat upon the
spam	chair--who must not be seen? From whom newly arrived, did he come out,
spam	agitated and surprised, to take his favourite in his arms? To whom did
spam	he appear to repeat her faltering words, when, raising his voice and
ham	turning his head towards the door of the room from which he had issued,
ham	he said: "Removed to the Conciergerie, and summoned for to-morrow?"
spam	VI. Triumph
ham	The dread tribunal of five Judges, Public Prosecutor, and determined
spam	Jury, sat every day. Their lists went forth every evening, and were
ham	read out by the gaolers of the various prisons to their prisoners. The
spam	standard gaoler-joke was, "Come out and listen to the Evening Paper, you
spam	inside there!"
ham	"Charles Evremonde, called Darnay!"
ham	So at last began the Evening Paper at La Force.
ham	When a name was called, its owner stepped apart into a spot reserved
ham	for those who were announced as being thus fatally recorded. Charles
ham	Evremonde, called Darnay, had reason to know the usage; he had seen
ham	hundreds pass away so.
spam	His bloated gaoler, who wore spectacles to read with, glanced over them
spam	to assure himself that he had taken his place, and went through the
spam	list, making a similar short pause at each name. There were twenty-three
ham	names, but only twenty were responded to; for one of the prisoners so
spam	summoned had died in gaol and been forgotten, and two had already been
ham	guillotined and forgotten. The list was read, in the vaulted chamber
spam	where Darnay had seen the associated prisoners on the night of his
ham	arrival. Every one of those had perished in the massacre; every human
ham	creature he had since cared for and parted with, had died on the
spam	scaffold.
spam	There were hurried words of farewell and kindness, but the parting was
ham	soon over. It was the incident of every day, and the society of La Force
ham	were engaged in the preparation of some games of forfeits and a little
spam	concert, for that evening. They crowded to the grates and shed tears
spam	there; but, twenty places in the projected entertainments had to be
spam	refilled, and the time was, at best, short to the lock-up hour, when the
ham	common rooms and corridors would be delivered over to the great dogs
spam	who kept watch there through the night. The prisoners were far from
ham	insensible or unfeeling; their ways arose out of the condition of the
ham	time. Similarly, though with a subtle difference, a species of fervour
spam	or intoxication, known, without doubt, to have led some persons to
ham	brave the guillotine unnecessarily, and to die by it, was not mere
spam	boastfulness, but a wild infection of the wildly shaken public mind. In
spam	seasons of pestilence, some of us will have a secret attraction to the
spam	disease--a terrible passing inclination to die of it. And all of us have
spam	like wonders hidden in our breasts, only needing circumstances to evoke
spam	them.
spam	The passage to the Conciergerie was short and dark; the night in its
spam	vermin-haunted cells was long and cold. Next day, fifteen prisoners were
spam	put to the bar before Charles Darnay's name was called. All the fifteen
ham	were condemned, and the trials of the whole occupied an hour and a half.
spam	"Charles Evremonde, called Darnay," was at length arraigned.
spam	His judges sat upon the Bench in feathered hats; but the rough red cap
ham	and tricoloured cockade was the head-dress otherwise prevailing. Looking
spam	at the Jury and the turbulent audience, he might have thought that the
spam	usual order of things was reversed, and that the felons were trying the
ham	honest men. The lowest, cruelest, and worst populace of a city, never
ham	without its quantity of low, cruel, and bad, were the directing
spam	spirits of the scene: noisily commenting, applauding, disapproving,
spam	anticipating, and precipitating the result, without a check. Of the men,
ham	the greater part were armed in various ways; of the women, some wore
ham	knives, some daggers, some ate and drank as they looked on, many
ham	knitted. Among these last, was one, with a spare piece of knitting under
spam	her arm as she worked. She was in a front row, by the side of a man whom
spam	he had never seen since his arrival at the Barrier, but whom he directly
ham	remembered as Defarge. He noticed that she once or twice whispered in
spam	his ear, and that she seemed to be his wife; but, what he most noticed
ham	in the two figures was, that although they were posted as close to
spam	himself as they could be, they never looked towards him. They seemed to
spam	be waiting for something with a dogged determination, and they looked at
spam	the Jury, but at nothing else. Under the President sat Doctor Manette,
spam	in his usual quiet dress. As well as the prisoner could see, he and Mr.
spam	Lorry were the only men there, unconnected with the Tribunal, who
ham	wore their usual clothes, and had not assumed the coarse garb of the
ham	Carmagnole.
spam	Charles Evremonde, called Darnay, was accused by the public prosecutor
spam	as an emigrant, whose life was forfeit to the Republic, under the decree
spam	which banished all emigrants on pain of Death. It was nothing that the
spam	decree bore date since his return to France. There he was, and there was
ham	the decree; he had been taken in France, and his head was demanded.
spam	"Take off his head!" cried the audience. "An enemy to the Republic!"
ham	The President rang his bell to silence those cries, and asked the
spam	prisoner whether it was not true that he had lived many years in
ham	England?
spam	Undoubtedly it was.
ham	Was he not an emigrant then? What did he call himself?
spam	Not an emigrant, he hoped, within the sense and spirit of the law.
spam	Why not? the President desired to know.
spam	Because he had voluntarily relinquished a title that was distasteful
spam	to him, and a station that was distasteful to him, and had left
spam	his country--he submitted before the word emigrant in the present
ham	acceptation by the Tribunal was in use--to live by his own industry in
spam	England, rather than on the industry of the overladen people of France.
spam	What proof had he of this?
ham	He handed in the names of two witnesses; Theophile Gabelle, and
ham	Alexandre Manette.
ham	But he had married in England? the President reminded him.
spam	True, but not an English woman.
ham	A citizeness of France?
spam	Yes. By birth.
spam	Her name and family?
ham	"Lucie Manette, only daughter of Doctor Manette, the good physician who
ham	sits there."
ham	This answer had a happy effect upon the audience. Cries in exaltation
spam	of the well-known good physician rent the hall. So capriciously were
spam	the people moved, that tears immediately rolled down several ferocious
ham	countenances which had been glaring at the prisoner a moment before, as
spam	if with impatience to pluck him out into the streets and kill him.
ham	On these few steps of his dangerous way, Charles Darnay had set his foot
spam	according to Doctor Manette's reiterated instructions. The same cautious
spam	counsel directed every step that lay before him, and had prepared every
ham	inch of his road.
ham	The President asked, why had he returned to France when he did, and not
ham	sooner?
ham	He had not returned sooner, he replied, simply because he had no means
ham	of living in France, save those he had resigned; whereas, in England,
spam	he lived by giving instruction in the French language and literature.
spam	He had returned when he did, on the pressing and written entreaty of
spam	a French citizen, who represented that his life was endangered by his
spam	absence. He had come back, to save a citizen's life, and to bear his
spam	testimony, at whatever personal hazard, to the truth. Was that criminal
ham	in the eyes of the Republic?
spam	The populace cried enthusiastically, "No!" and the President rang his
ham	bell to quiet them. Which it did not, for they continued to cry "No!"
spam	until they left off, of their own will.
spam	The President required the name of that citizen. The accused explained
ham	that the citizen was his first witness. He also referred with confidence
spam	to the citizen's letter, which had been taken from him at the Barrier,
spam	but which he did not doubt would be found among the papers then before
ham	the President.
spam	The Doctor had taken care that it should be there--had assured him that
ham	it would be there--and at this stage of the proceedings it was produced
spam	and read. Citizen Gabelle was called to confirm it, and did so. Citizen
spam	Gabelle hinted, with infinite delicacy and politeness, that in the
ham	pressure of business imposed on the Tribunal by the multitude of
ham	enemies of the Republic with which it had to deal, he had been slightly
ham	overlooked in his prison of the Abbaye--in fact, had rather passed out
spam	of the Tribunal's patriotic remembrance--until three days ago; when he
spam	had been summoned before it, and had been set at liberty on the Jury's
spam	declaring themselves satisfied that the accusation against him was
ham	answered, as to himself, by the surrender of the citizen Evremonde,
spam	called Darnay.
spam	Doctor Manette was next questioned. His high personal popularity,
spam	and the clearness of his answers, made a great impression; but, as he
ham	proceeded, as he showed that the Accused was his first friend on his
spam	release from his long imprisonment; that, the accused had remained in
spam	England, always faithful and devoted to his daughter and himself in
ham	their exile; that, so far from being in favour with the Aristocrat
spam	government there, he had actually been tried for his life by it, as
spam	the foe of England and friend of the United States--as he brought these
ham	circumstances into view, with the greatest discretion and with the
ham	straightforward force of truth and earnestness, the Jury and the
spam	populace became one. At last, when he appealed by name to Monsieur
ham	Lorry, an English gentleman then and there present, who, like himself,
ham	had been a witness on that English trial and could corroborate his
spam	account of it, the Jury declared that they had heard enough, and that
ham	they were ready with their votes if the President were content to
spam	receive them.
spam	At every vote (the Jurymen voted aloud and individually), the populace
spam	set up a shout of applause. All the voices were in the prisoner's
ham	favour, and the President declared him free.
spam	Then, began one of those extraordinary scenes with which the populace
ham	sometimes gratified their fickleness, or their better impulses towards
ham	generosity and mercy, or which they regarded as some set-off against
spam	their swollen account of cruel rage. No man can decide now to which of
spam	these motives such extraordinary scenes were referable; it is probable,
ham	to a blending of all the three, with the second predominating. No sooner
spam	was the acquittal pronounced, than tears were shed as freely as blood
spam	at another time, and such fraternal embraces were bestowed upon the
spam	prisoner by as many of both sexes as could rush at him, that after
spam	his long and unwholesome confinement he was in danger of fainting from
ham	exhaustion; none the less because he knew very well, that the very same
ham	people, carried by another current, would have rushed at him with
spam	the very same intensity, to rend him to pieces and strew him over the
ham	streets.
spam	His removal, to make way for other accused persons who were to be tried,
ham	rescued him from these caresses for the moment. Five were to be tried
spam	together, next, as enemies of the Republic, forasmuch as they had not
spam	assisted it by word or deed. So quick was the Tribunal to compensate
spam	itself and the nation for a chance lost, that these five came down to
spam	him before he left the place, condemned to die within twenty-four
ham	hours. The first of them told him so, with the customary prison sign
ham	of Death--a raised finger--and they all added in words, "Long live the
ham	Republic!"
ham	The five had had, it is true, no audience to lengthen their proceedings,
spam	for when he and Doctor Manette emerged from the gate, there was a great
ham	crowd about it, in which there seemed to be every face he had seen in
ham	Court--except two, for which he looked in vain. On his coming out, the
ham	concourse made at him anew, weeping, embracing, and shouting, all by
spam	turns and all together, until the very tide of the river on the bank of
ham	which the mad scene was acted, seemed to run mad, like the people on the
spam	shore.
ham	They put him into a great chair they had among them, and which they had
ham	taken either out of the Court itself, or one of its rooms or passages.
spam	Over the chair they had thrown a red flag, and to the back of it they
ham	had bound a pike with a red cap on its top. In this car of triumph, not
ham	even the Doctor's entreaties could prevent his being carried to his home
ham	on men's shoulders, with a confused sea of red caps heaving about him,
ham	and casting up to sight from the stormy deep such wrecks of faces, that
spam	he more than once misdoubted his mind being in confusion, and that he
ham	was in the tumbril on his way to the Guillotine.
ham	In wild dreamlike procession, embracing whom they met and pointing
ham	him out, they carried him on. Reddening the snowy streets with the
ham	prevailing Republican colour, in winding and tramping through them, as
spam	they had reddened them below the snow with a deeper dye, they carried
spam	him thus into the courtyard of the building where he lived. Her father
ham	had gone on before, to prepare her, and when her husband stood upon his
spam	feet, she dropped insensible in his arms.
ham	As he held her to his heart and turned her beautiful head between his
spam	face and the brawling crowd, so that his tears and her lips might come
spam	together unseen, a few of the people fell to dancing. Instantly, all the
ham	rest fell to dancing, and the courtyard overflowed with the Carmagnole.
ham	Then, they elevated into the vacant chair a young woman from the
ham	crowd to be carried as the Goddess of Liberty, and then swelling and
spam	overflowing out into the adjacent streets, and along the river's bank,
ham	and over the bridge, the Carmagnole absorbed them every one and whirled
ham	them away.
ham	After grasping the Doctor's hand, as he stood victorious and proud
ham	before him; after grasping the hand of Mr. Lorry, who came panting in
ham	breathless from his struggle against the waterspout of the Carmagnole;
spam	after kissing little Lucie, who was lifted up to clasp her arms round
spam	his neck; and after embracing the ever zealous and faithful Pross who
ham	lifted her; he took his wife in his arms, and carried her up to their
ham	rooms.
spam	"Lucie! My own! I am safe."
spam	"O dearest Charles, let me thank God for this on my knees as I have
ham	prayed to Him."
ham	They all reverently bowed their heads and hearts. When she was again in
ham	his arms, he said to her:
ham	"And now speak to your father, dearest. No other man in all this France
ham	could have done what he has done for me."
spam	She laid her head upon her father's breast, as she had laid his poor
spam	head on her own breast, long, long ago. He was happy in the return he
spam	had made her, he was recompensed for his suffering, he was proud of his
ham	strength. "You must not be weak, my darling," he remonstrated; "don't
spam	tremble so. I have saved him."
spam	VII. A Knock at the Door
spam	"I have saved him." It was not another of the dreams in which he had
ham	often come back; he was really here. And yet his wife trembled, and a
spam	vague but heavy fear was upon her.
ham	All the air round was so thick and dark, the people were so passionately
ham	revengeful and fitful, the innocent were so constantly put to death on
spam	vague suspicion and black malice, it was so impossible to forget that
ham	many as blameless as her husband and as dear to others as he was to
ham	her, every day shared the fate from which he had been clutched, that her
spam	heart could not be as lightened of its load as she felt it ought to be.
ham	The shadows of the wintry afternoon were beginning to fall, and even now
ham	the dreadful carts were rolling through the streets. Her mind pursued
spam	them, looking for him among the Condemned; and then she clung closer to
spam	his real presence and trembled more.
spam	Her father, cheering her, showed a compassionate superiority to this
ham	woman's weakness, which was wonderful to see. No garret, no shoemaking,
ham	no One Hundred and Five, North Tower, now! He had accomplished the task
ham	he had set himself, his promise was redeemed, he had saved Charles. Let
spam	them all lean upon him.
spam	Their housekeeping was of a very frugal kind: not only because that was
ham	the safest way of life, involving the least offence to the people, but
spam	because they were not rich, and Charles, throughout his imprisonment,
ham	had had to pay heavily for his bad food, and for his guard, and towards
ham	the living of the poorer prisoners. Partly on this account, and
ham	partly to avoid a domestic spy, they kept no servant; the citizen and
ham	citizeness who acted as porters at the courtyard gate, rendered them
ham	occasional service; and Jerry (almost wholly transferred to them by
spam	Mr. Lorry) had become their daily retainer, and had his bed there every
spam	night.
spam	It was an ordinance of the Republic One and Indivisible of Liberty,
ham	Equality, Fraternity, or Death, that on the door or doorpost of every
ham	house, the name of every inmate must be legibly inscribed in letters
spam	of a certain size, at a certain convenient height from the ground. Mr.
spam	Jerry Cruncher's name, therefore, duly embellished the doorpost down
ham	below; and, as the afternoon shadows deepened, the owner of that name
spam	himself appeared, from overlooking a painter whom Doctor Manette had
ham	employed to add to the list the name of Charles Evremonde, called
spam	Darnay.
spam	In the universal fear and distrust that darkened the time, all the usual
ham	harmless ways of life were changed. In the Doctor's little household, as
spam	in very many others, the articles of daily consumption that were wanted
spam	were purchased every evening, in small quantities and at various small
ham	shops. To avoid attracting notice, and to give as little occasion as
spam	possible for talk and envy, was the general desire.
spam	For some months past, Miss Pross and Mr. Cruncher had discharged the
spam	office of purveyors; the former carrying the money; the latter, the
ham	basket. Every afternoon at about the time when the public lamps were
ham	lighted, they fared forth on this duty, and made and brought home
ham	such purchases as were needful. Although Miss Pross, through her long
ham	association with a French family, might have known as much of their
ham	language as of her own, if she had had a mind, she had no mind in that
spam	direction; consequently she knew no more of that "nonsense" (as she was
spam	pleased to call it) than Mr. Cruncher did. So her manner of marketing
spam	was to plump a noun-substantive at the head of a shopkeeper without any
spam	introduction in the nature of an article, and, if it happened not to be
ham	the name of the thing she wanted, to look round for that thing, lay hold
ham	of it, and hold on by it until the bargain was concluded. She always
ham	made a bargain for it, by holding up, as a statement of its just price,
spam	one finger less than the merchant held up, whatever his number might be.
spam	"Now, Mr. Cruncher," said Miss Pross, whose eyes were red with felicity;
spam	"if you are ready, I am."
spam	Jerry hoarsely professed himself at Miss Pross's service. He had worn
spam	all his rust off long ago, but nothing would file his spiky head down.
ham	"There's all manner of things wanted," said Miss Pross, "and we shall
ham	have a precious time of it. We want wine, among the rest. Nice toasts
spam	these Redheads will be drinking, wherever we buy it."
ham	"It will be much the same to your knowledge, miss, I should think,"
spam	retorted Jerry, "whether they drink your health or the Old Un's."
ham	"Who's he?" said Miss Pross.
ham	Mr. Cruncher, with some diffidence, explained himself as meaning "Old
spam	Nick's."
ham	"Ha!" said Miss Pross, "it doesn't need an interpreter to explain the
spam	meaning of these creatures. They have but one, and it's Midnight Murder,
ham	and Mischief."
ham	"Hush, dear! Pray, pray, be cautious!" cried Lucie.
ham	"Yes, yes, yes, I'll be cautious," said Miss Pross; "but I may say
ham	among ourselves, that I do hope there will be no oniony and tobaccoey
spam	smotherings in the form of embracings all round, going on in the
spam	streets. Now, Ladybird, never you stir from that fire till I come back!
spam	Take care of the dear husband you have recovered, and don't move your
spam	pretty head from his shoulder as you have it now, till you see me again!
spam	May I ask a question, Doctor Manette, before I go?"
spam	"I think you may take that liberty," the Doctor answered, smiling.
ham	"For gracious sake, don't talk about Liberty; we have quite enough of
ham	that," said Miss Pross.
ham	"Hush, dear! Again?" Lucie remonstrated.
ham	"Well, my sweet," said Miss Pross, nodding her head emphatically, "the
spam	short and the long of it is, that I am a subject of His Most Gracious
ham	Majesty King George the Third;" Miss Pross curtseyed at the name; "and
ham	as such, my maxim is, Confound their politics, Frustrate their knavish
ham	tricks, On him our hopes we fix, God save the King!"
spam	Mr. Cruncher, in an access of loyalty, growlingly repeated the words
ham	after Miss Pross, like somebody at church.
ham	"I am glad you have so much of the Englishman in you, though I wish you
spam	had never taken that cold in your voice," said Miss Pross, approvingly.
spam	"But the question, Doctor Manette. Is there"--it was the good creature's
spam	way to affect to make light of anything that was a great anxiety
spam	with them all, and to come at it in this chance manner--"is there any
spam	prospect yet, of our getting out of this place?"
ham	"I fear not yet. It would be dangerous for Charles yet."
spam	"Heigh-ho-hum!" said Miss Pross, cheerfully repressing a sigh as she
ham	glanced at her darling's golden hair in the light of the fire, "then we
spam	must have patience and wait: that's all. We must hold up our heads and
spam	fight low, as my brother Solomon used to say. Now, Mr. Cruncher!--Don't
ham	you move, Ladybird!"
ham	They went out, leaving Lucie, and her husband, her father, and the
ham	child, by a bright fire. Mr. Lorry was expected back presently from the
spam	Banking House. Miss Pross had lighted the lamp, but had put it aside in
ham	a corner, that they might enjoy the fire-light undisturbed. Little Lucie
ham	sat by her grandfather with her hands clasped through his arm: and he,
spam	in a tone not rising much above a whisper, began to tell her a story of
ham	a great and powerful Fairy who had opened a prison-wall and let out
ham	a captive who had once done the Fairy a service. All was subdued and
spam	quiet, and Lucie was more at ease than she had been.
ham	"What is that?" she cried, all at once.
ham	"My dear!" said her father, stopping in his story, and laying his hand
spam	on hers, "command yourself. What a disordered state you are in! The
spam	least thing--nothing--startles you! _You_, your father's daughter!"
spam	"I thought, my father," said Lucie, excusing herself, with a pale face
spam	and in a faltering voice, "that I heard strange feet upon the stairs."
spam	"My love, the staircase is as still as Death."
spam	As he said the word, a blow was struck upon the door.
spam	"Oh father, father. What can this be! Hide Charles. Save him!"
ham	"My child," said the Doctor, rising, and laying his hand upon her
spam	shoulder, "I _have_ saved him. What weakness is this, my dear! Let me go
ham	to the door."
ham	He took the lamp in his hand, crossed the two intervening outer rooms,
ham	and opened it. A rude clattering of feet over the floor, and four rough
ham	men in red caps, armed with sabres and pistols, entered the room.
ham	"The Citizen Evremonde, called Darnay," said the first.
ham	"Who seeks him?" answered Darnay.
ham	"I seek him. We seek him. I know you, Evremonde; I saw you before the
ham	Tribunal to-day. You are again the prisoner of the Republic."
ham	The four surrounded him, where he stood with his wife and child clinging
spam	to him.
spam	"Tell me how and why am I again a prisoner?"
ham	"It is enough that you return straight to the Conciergerie, and will
ham	know to-morrow. You are summoned for to-morrow."
