ham	Doctor Manette, whom this visitation had so turned into stone, that he
spam	stood with the lamp in his hand, as if he were a statue made to hold it,
spam	moved after these words were spoken, put the lamp down, and confronting
ham	the speaker, and taking him, not ungently, by the loose front of his red
ham	woollen shirt, said:
spam	"You know him, you have said. Do you know me?"
spam	"Yes, I know you, Citizen Doctor."
ham	"We all know you, Citizen Doctor," said the other three.
ham	He looked abstractedly from one to another, and said, in a lower voice,
ham	after a pause:
spam	"Will you answer his question to me then? How does this happen?"
ham	"Citizen Doctor," said the first, reluctantly, "he has been denounced to
ham	the Section of Saint Antoine. This citizen," pointing out the second who
ham	had entered, "is from Saint Antoine."
spam	The citizen here indicated nodded his head, and added:
spam	"He is accused by Saint Antoine."
spam	"Of what?" asked the Doctor.
spam	"Citizen Doctor," said the first, with his former reluctance, "ask no
spam	more. If the Republic demands sacrifices from you, without doubt you as
spam	a good patriot will be happy to make them. The Republic goes before all.
ham	The People is supreme. Evremonde, we are pressed."
ham	"One word," the Doctor entreated. "Will you tell me who denounced him?"
spam	"It is against rule," answered the first; "but you can ask Him of Saint
spam	Antoine here."
ham	The Doctor turned his eyes upon that man. Who moved uneasily on his
spam	feet, rubbed his beard a little, and at length said:
spam	"Well! Truly it is against rule. But he is denounced--and gravely--by
spam	the Citizen and Citizeness Defarge. And by one other."
ham	"What other?"
ham	"Do _you_ ask, Citizen Doctor?"
spam	"Yes."
spam	"Then," said he of Saint Antoine, with a strange look, "you will be
spam	answered to-morrow. Now, I am dumb!"
spam	VIII. A Hand at Cards
spam	Happily unconscious of the new calamity at home, Miss Pross threaded her
spam	way along the narrow streets and crossed the river by the bridge of the
spam	Pont-Neuf, reckoning in her mind the number of indispensable purchases
ham	she had to make. Mr. Cruncher, with the basket, walked at her side. They
ham	both looked to the right and to the left into most of the shops they
spam	passed, had a wary eye for all gregarious assemblages of people, and
ham	turned out of their road to avoid any very excited group of talkers. It
spam	was a raw evening, and the misty river, blurred to the eye with blazing
ham	lights and to the ear with harsh noises, showed where the barges were
spam	stationed in which the smiths worked, making guns for the Army of the
spam	Republic. Woe to the man who played tricks with _that_ Army, or got
ham	undeserved promotion in it! Better for him that his beard had never
ham	grown, for the National Razor shaved him close.
spam	Having purchased a few small articles of grocery, and a measure of oil
ham	for the lamp, Miss Pross bethought herself of the wine they wanted.
spam	After peeping into several wine-shops, she stopped at the sign of the
ham	Good Republican Brutus of Antiquity, not far from the National Palace,
spam	once (and twice) the Tuileries, where the aspect of things rather
spam	took her fancy. It had a quieter look than any other place of the same
spam	description they had passed, and, though red with patriotic caps, was
ham	not so red as the rest. Sounding Mr. Cruncher, and finding him of her
ham	opinion, Miss Pross resorted to the Good Republican Brutus of Antiquity,
ham	attended by her cavalier.
spam	Slightly observant of the smoky lights; of the people, pipe in mouth,
ham	playing with limp cards and yellow dominoes; of the one bare-breasted,
ham	bare-armed, soot-begrimed workman reading a journal aloud, and of
spam	the others listening to him; of the weapons worn, or laid aside to be
ham	resumed; of the two or three customers fallen forward asleep, who in the
ham	popular high-shouldered shaggy black spencer looked, in that attitude,
spam	like slumbering bears or dogs; the two outlandish customers approached
ham	the counter, and showed what they wanted.
spam	As their wine was measuring out, a man parted from another man in a
ham	corner, and rose to depart. In going, he had to face Miss Pross. No
spam	sooner did he face her, than Miss Pross uttered a scream, and clapped
ham	her hands.
spam	In a moment, the whole company were on their feet. That somebody was
spam	assassinated by somebody vindicating a difference of opinion was the
spam	likeliest occurrence. Everybody looked to see somebody fall, but only
spam	saw a man and a woman standing staring at each other; the man with all
spam	the outward aspect of a Frenchman and a thorough Republican; the woman,
ham	evidently English.
spam	What was said in this disappointing anti-climax, by the disciples of the
spam	Good Republican Brutus of Antiquity, except that it was something very
ham	voluble and loud, would have been as so much Hebrew or Chaldean to Miss
ham	Pross and her protector, though they had been all ears. But, they had no
ham	ears for anything in their surprise. For, it must be recorded, that
spam	not only was Miss Pross lost in amazement and agitation, but,
spam	Mr. Cruncher--though it seemed on his own separate and individual
spam	account--was in a state of the greatest wonder.
ham	"What is the matter?" said the man who had caused Miss Pross to scream;
spam	speaking in a vexed, abrupt voice (though in a low tone), and in
ham	English.
ham	"Oh, Solomon, dear Solomon!" cried Miss Pross, clapping her hands again.
ham	"After not setting eyes upon you or hearing of you for so long a time,
ham	do I find you here!"
spam	"Don't call me Solomon. Do you want to be the death of me?" asked the
spam	man, in a furtive, frightened way.
ham	"Brother, brother!" cried Miss Pross, bursting into tears. "Have I ever
ham	been so hard with you that you ask me such a cruel question?"
ham	"Then hold your meddlesome tongue," said Solomon, "and come out, if you
ham	want to speak to me. Pay for your wine, and come out. Who's this man?"
spam	Miss Pross, shaking her loving and dejected head at her by no means
ham	affectionate brother, said through her tears, "Mr. Cruncher."
ham	"Let him come out too," said Solomon. "Does he think me a ghost?"
ham	Apparently, Mr. Cruncher did, to judge from his looks. He said not a
ham	word, however, and Miss Pross, exploring the depths of her reticule
ham	through her tears with great difficulty paid for her wine. As she did
spam	so, Solomon turned to the followers of the Good Republican Brutus
ham	of Antiquity, and offered a few words of explanation in the French
spam	language, which caused them all to relapse into their former places and
ham	pursuits.
ham	"Now," said Solomon, stopping at the dark street corner, "what do you
spam	want?"
spam	"How dreadfully unkind in a brother nothing has ever turned my love away
ham	from!" cried Miss Pross, "to give me such a greeting, and show me no
spam	affection."
spam	"There. Confound it! There," said Solomon, making a dab at Miss Pross's
ham	lips with his own. "Now are you content?"
spam	Miss Pross only shook her head and wept in silence.
ham	"If you expect me to be surprised," said her brother Solomon, "I am not
ham	surprised; I knew you were here; I know of most people who are here. If
ham	you really don't want to endanger my existence--which I half believe you
ham	do--go your ways as soon as possible, and let me go mine. I am busy. I
ham	am an official."
spam	"My English brother Solomon," mourned Miss Pross, casting up her
ham	tear-fraught eyes, "that had the makings in him of one of the best and
ham	greatest of men in his native country, an official among foreigners, and
spam	such foreigners! I would almost sooner have seen the dear boy lying in
spam	his--"
spam	"I said so!" cried her brother, interrupting. "I knew it. You want to be
ham	the death of me. I shall be rendered Suspected, by my own sister. Just
ham	as I am getting on!"
spam	"The gracious and merciful Heavens forbid!" cried Miss Pross. "Far
ham	rather would I never see you again, dear Solomon, though I have ever
ham	loved you truly, and ever shall. Say but one affectionate word to me,
ham	and tell me there is nothing angry or estranged between us, and I will
spam	detain you no longer."
spam	Good Miss Pross! As if the estrangement between them had come of any
ham	culpability of hers. As if Mr. Lorry had not known it for a fact, years
spam	ago, in the quiet corner in Soho, that this precious brother had spent
ham	her money and left her!
ham	He was saying the affectionate word, however, with a far more grudging
ham	condescension and patronage than he could have shown if their relative
spam	merits and positions had been reversed (which is invariably the case,
spam	all the world over), when Mr. Cruncher, touching him on the shoulder,
spam	hoarsely and unexpectedly interposed with the following singular
spam	question:
spam	"I say! Might I ask the favour? As to whether your name is John Solomon,
ham	or Solomon John?"
ham	The official turned towards him with sudden distrust. He had not
spam	previously uttered a word.
spam	"Come!" said Mr. Cruncher. "Speak out, you know." (Which, by the way,
spam	was more than he could do himself.) "John Solomon, or Solomon John? She
ham	calls you Solomon, and she must know, being your sister. And _I_ know
ham	you're John, you know. Which of the two goes first? And regarding that
spam	name of Pross, likewise. That warn't your name over the water."
spam	"What do you mean?"
ham	"Well, I don't know all I mean, for I can't call to mind what your name
spam	was, over the water."
spam	"No?"
ham	"No. But I'll swear it was a name of two syllables."
ham	"Indeed?"
ham	"Yes. T'other one's was one syllable. I know you. You was a spy--witness
spam	at the Bailey. What, in the name of the Father of Lies, own father to
spam	yourself, was you called at that time?"
ham	"Barsad," said another voice, striking in.
spam	"That's the name for a thousand pound!" cried Jerry.
ham	The speaker who struck in, was Sydney Carton. He had his hands behind
ham	him under the skirts of his riding-coat, and he stood at Mr. Cruncher's
spam	elbow as negligently as he might have stood at the Old Bailey itself.
spam	"Don't be alarmed, my dear Miss Pross. I arrived at Mr. Lorry's, to his
ham	surprise, yesterday evening; we agreed that I would not present myself
spam	elsewhere until all was well, or unless I could be useful; I present
ham	myself here, to beg a little talk with your brother. I wish you had a
ham	better employed brother than Mr. Barsad. I wish for your sake Mr. Barsad
ham	was not a Sheep of the Prisons."
ham	Sheep was a cant word of the time for a spy, under the gaolers. The spy,
ham	who was pale, turned paler, and asked him how he dared--
spam	"I'll tell you," said Sydney. "I lighted on you, Mr. Barsad, coming out
spam	of the prison of the Conciergerie while I was contemplating the walls,
ham	an hour or more ago. You have a face to be remembered, and I remember
spam	faces well. Made curious by seeing you in that connection, and having
ham	a reason, to which you are no stranger, for associating you with
ham	the misfortunes of a friend now very unfortunate, I walked in your
ham	direction. I walked into the wine-shop here, close after you, and
spam	sat near you. I had no difficulty in deducing from your unreserved
spam	conversation, and the rumour openly going about among your admirers, the
spam	nature of your calling. And gradually, what I had done at random, seemed
spam	to shape itself into a purpose, Mr. Barsad."
spam	"What purpose?" the spy asked.
ham	"It would be troublesome, and might be dangerous, to explain in the
ham	street. Could you favour me, in confidence, with some minutes of your
ham	company--at the office of Tellson's Bank, for instance?"
spam	"Under a threat?"
spam	"Oh! Did I say that?"
spam	"Then, why should I go there?"
spam	"Really, Mr. Barsad, I can't say, if you can't."
spam	"Do you mean that you won't say, sir?" the spy irresolutely asked.
ham	"You apprehend me very clearly, Mr. Barsad. I won't."
ham	Carton's negligent recklessness of manner came powerfully in aid of his
spam	quickness and skill, in such a business as he had in his secret mind,
spam	and with such a man as he had to do with. His practised eye saw it, and
ham	made the most of it.
ham	"Now, I told you so," said the spy, casting a reproachful look at his
ham	sister; "if any trouble comes of this, it's your doing."
spam	"Come, come, Mr. Barsad!" exclaimed Sydney. "Don't be ungrateful.
ham	But for my great respect for your sister, I might not have led up so
spam	pleasantly to a little proposal that I wish to make for our mutual
ham	satisfaction. Do you go with me to the Bank?"
spam	"I'll hear what you have got to say. Yes, I'll go with you."
spam	"I propose that we first conduct your sister safely to the corner of her
spam	own street. Let me take your arm, Miss Pross. This is not a good city,
ham	at this time, for you to be out in, unprotected; and as your escort
spam	knows Mr. Barsad, I will invite him to Mr. Lorry's with us. Are we
ham	ready? Come then!"
ham	Miss Pross recalled soon afterwards, and to the end of her life
ham	remembered, that as she pressed her hands on Sydney's arm and looked up
spam	in his face, imploring him to do no hurt to Solomon, there was a braced
ham	purpose in the arm and a kind of inspiration in the eyes, which not only
spam	contradicted his light manner, but changed and raised the man. She was
ham	too much occupied then with fears for the brother who so little deserved
ham	her affection, and with Sydney's friendly reassurances, adequately to
ham	heed what she observed.
ham	They left her at the corner of the street, and Carton led the way to Mr.
spam	Lorry's, which was within a few minutes' walk. John Barsad, or Solomon
ham	Pross, walked at his side.
ham	Mr. Lorry had just finished his dinner, and was sitting before a cheery
ham	little log or two of fire--perhaps looking into their blaze for the
spam	picture of that younger elderly gentleman from Tellson's, who had looked
spam	into the red coals at the Royal George at Dover, now a good many years
ham	ago. He turned his head as they entered, and showed the surprise with
ham	which he saw a stranger.
spam	"Miss Pross's brother, sir," said Sydney. "Mr. Barsad."
ham	"Barsad?" repeated the old gentleman, "Barsad? I have an association
ham	with the name--and with the face."
ham	"I told you you had a remarkable face, Mr. Barsad," observed Carton,
spam	coolly. "Pray sit down."
spam	As he took a chair himself, he supplied the link that Mr. Lorry wanted,
ham	by saying to him with a frown, "Witness at that trial." Mr. Lorry
spam	immediately remembered, and regarded his new visitor with an undisguised
ham	look of abhorrence.
ham	"Mr. Barsad has been recognised by Miss Pross as the affectionate
ham	brother you have heard of," said Sydney, "and has acknowledged the
ham	relationship. I pass to worse news. Darnay has been arrested again."
spam	Struck with consternation, the old gentleman exclaimed, "What do you
spam	tell me! I left him safe and free within these two hours, and am about
ham	to return to him!"
spam	"Arrested for all that. When was it done, Mr. Barsad?"
ham	"Just now, if at all."
spam	"Mr. Barsad is the best authority possible, sir," said Sydney, "and I
ham	have it from Mr. Barsad's communication to a friend and brother Sheep
spam	over a bottle of wine, that the arrest has taken place. He left the
ham	messengers at the gate, and saw them admitted by the porter. There is no
ham	earthly doubt that he is retaken."
spam	Mr. Lorry's business eye read in the speaker's face that it was loss
ham	of time to dwell upon the point. Confused, but sensible that something
ham	might depend on his presence of mind, he commanded himself, and was
spam	silently attentive.
ham	"Now, I trust," said Sydney to him, "that the name and influence of
spam	Doctor Manette may stand him in as good stead to-morrow--you said he
spam	would be before the Tribunal again to-morrow, Mr. Barsad?--"
ham	"Yes; I believe so."
ham	"--In as good stead to-morrow as to-day. But it may not be so. I own
spam	to you, I am shaken, Mr. Lorry, by Doctor Manette's not having had the
ham	power to prevent this arrest."
ham	"He may not have known of it beforehand," said Mr. Lorry.
ham	"But that very circumstance would be alarming, when we remember how
spam	identified he is with his son-in-law."
spam	"That's true," Mr. Lorry acknowledged, with his troubled hand at his
ham	chin, and his troubled eyes on Carton.
spam	"In short," said Sydney, "this is a desperate time, when desperate games
ham	are played for desperate stakes. Let the Doctor play the winning game; I
spam	will play the losing one. No man's life here is worth purchase. Any one
ham	carried home by the people to-day, may be condemned tomorrow. Now, the
ham	stake I have resolved to play for, in case of the worst, is a friend
spam	in the Conciergerie. And the friend I purpose to myself to win, is Mr.
ham	Barsad."
ham	"You need have good cards, sir," said the spy.
spam	"I'll run them over. I'll see what I hold,--Mr. Lorry, you know what a
ham	brute I am; I wish you'd give me a little brandy."
ham	It was put before him, and he drank off a glassful--drank off another
ham	glassful--pushed the bottle thoughtfully away.
spam	"Mr. Barsad," he went on, in the tone of one who really was looking
ham	over a hand at cards: "Sheep of the prisons, emissary of Republican
spam	committees, now turnkey, now prisoner, always spy and secret informer,
ham	so much the more valuable here for being English that an Englishman
ham	is less open to suspicion of subornation in those characters than a
ham	Frenchman, represents himself to his employers under a false name.
ham	That's a very good card. Mr. Barsad, now in the employ of the republican
spam	French government, was formerly in the employ of the aristocratic
ham	English government, the enemy of France and freedom. That's an excellent
spam	card. Inference clear as day in this region of suspicion, that Mr.
spam	Barsad, still in the pay of the aristocratic English government, is the
spam	spy of Pitt, the treacherous foe of the Republic crouching in its bosom,
ham	the English traitor and agent of all mischief so much spoken of and so
spam	difficult to find. That's a card not to be beaten. Have you followed my
ham	hand, Mr. Barsad?"
spam	"Not to understand your play," returned the spy, somewhat uneasily.
spam	"I play my Ace, Denunciation of Mr. Barsad to the nearest Section
spam	Committee. Look over your hand, Mr. Barsad, and see what you have. Don't
spam	hurry."
spam	He drew the bottle near, poured out another glassful of brandy, and
ham	drank it off. He saw that the spy was fearful of his drinking himself
spam	into a fit state for the immediate denunciation of him. Seeing it, he
ham	poured out and drank another glassful.
ham	"Look over your hand carefully, Mr. Barsad. Take time."
ham	It was a poorer hand than he suspected. Mr. Barsad saw losing cards
spam	in it that Sydney Carton knew nothing of. Thrown out of his honourable
ham	employment in England, through too much unsuccessful hard swearing
ham	there--not because he was not wanted there; our English reasons for
ham	vaunting our superiority to secrecy and spies are of very modern
ham	date--he knew that he had crossed the Channel, and accepted service in
ham	France: first, as a tempter and an eavesdropper among his own countrymen
spam	there: gradually, as a tempter and an eavesdropper among the natives. He
ham	knew that under the overthrown government he had been a spy upon Saint
spam	Antoine and Defarge's wine-shop; had received from the watchful police
ham	such heads of information concerning Doctor Manette's imprisonment,
ham	release, and history, as should serve him for an introduction to
ham	familiar conversation with the Defarges; and tried them on Madame
ham	Defarge, and had broken down with them signally. He always remembered
spam	with fear and trembling, that that terrible woman had knitted when he
ham	talked with her, and had looked ominously at him as her fingers moved.
spam	He had since seen her, in the Section of Saint Antoine, over and over
ham	again produce her knitted registers, and denounce people whose lives the
spam	guillotine then surely swallowed up. He knew, as every one employed as
ham	he was did, that he was never safe; that flight was impossible; that
spam	he was tied fast under the shadow of the axe; and that in spite of
ham	his utmost tergiversation and treachery in furtherance of the reigning
ham	terror, a word might bring it down upon him. Once denounced, and on such
spam	grave grounds as had just now been suggested to his mind, he foresaw
ham	that the dreadful woman of whose unrelenting character he had seen many
ham	proofs, would produce against him that fatal register, and would quash
ham	his last chance of life. Besides that all secret men are men soon
spam	terrified, here were surely cards enough of one black suit, to justify
spam	the holder in growing rather livid as he turned them over.
spam	"You scarcely seem to like your hand," said Sydney, with the greatest
ham	composure. "Do you play?"
spam	"I think, sir," said the spy, in the meanest manner, as he turned to Mr.
ham	Lorry, "I may appeal to a gentleman of your years and benevolence, to
spam	put it to this other gentleman, so much your junior, whether he can
spam	under any circumstances reconcile it to his station to play that Ace
ham	of which he has spoken. I admit that _I_ am a spy, and that it is
ham	considered a discreditable station--though it must be filled by
spam	somebody; but this gentleman is no spy, and why should he so demean
ham	himself as to make himself one?"
ham	"I play my Ace, Mr. Barsad," said Carton, taking the answer on himself,
spam	and looking at his watch, "without any scruple, in a very few minutes."
ham	"I should have hoped, gentlemen both," said the spy, always striving to
ham	hook Mr. Lorry into the discussion, "that your respect for my sister--"
spam	"I could not better testify my respect for your sister than by finally
spam	relieving her of her brother," said Sydney Carton.
ham	"You think not, sir?"
ham	"I have thoroughly made up my mind about it."
spam	The smooth manner of the spy, curiously in dissonance with his
ham	ostentatiously rough dress, and probably with his usual demeanour,
spam	received such a check from the inscrutability of Carton,--who was a
ham	mystery to wiser and honester men than he,--that it faltered here and
ham	failed him. While he was at a loss, Carton said, resuming his former air
ham	of contemplating cards:
spam	"And indeed, now I think again, I have a strong impression that I
spam	have another good card here, not yet enumerated. That friend and
ham	fellow-Sheep, who spoke of himself as pasturing in the country prisons;
ham	who was he?"
spam	"French. You don't know him," said the spy, quickly.
spam	"French, eh?" repeated Carton, musing, and not appearing to notice him
spam	at all, though he echoed his word. "Well; he may be."
spam	"Is, I assure you," said the spy; "though it's not important."
spam	"Though it's not important," repeated Carton, in the same mechanical
spam	way--"though it's not important--No, it's not important. No. Yet I know
spam	the face."
spam	"I think not. I am sure not. It can't be," said the spy.
spam	"It-can't-be," muttered Sydney Carton, retrospectively, and idling his
ham	glass (which fortunately was a small one) again. "Can't-be. Spoke good
spam	French. Yet like a foreigner, I thought?"
spam	"Provincial," said the spy.
spam	"No. Foreign!" cried Carton, striking his open hand on the table, as a
spam	light broke clearly on his mind. "Cly! Disguised, but the same man. We
ham	had that man before us at the Old Bailey."
ham	"Now, there you are hasty, sir," said Barsad, with a smile that gave his
ham	aquiline nose an extra inclination to one side; "there you really give
spam	me an advantage over you. Cly (who I will unreservedly admit, at this
spam	distance of time, was a partner of mine) has been dead several years. I
spam	attended him in his last illness. He was buried in London, at the church
spam	of Saint Pancras-in-the-Fields. His unpopularity with the blackguard
ham	multitude at the moment prevented my following his remains, but I helped
ham	to lay him in his coffin."
ham	Here, Mr. Lorry became aware, from where he sat, of a most remarkable
spam	goblin shadow on the wall. Tracing it to its source, he discovered it
ham	to be caused by a sudden extraordinary rising and stiffening of all the
ham	risen and stiff hair on Mr. Cruncher's head.
spam	"Let us be reasonable," said the spy, "and let us be fair. To show you
spam	how mistaken you are, and what an unfounded assumption yours is, I will
spam	lay before you a certificate of Cly's burial, which I happened to have
spam	carried in my pocket-book," with a hurried hand he produced and opened
ham	it, "ever since. There it is. Oh, look at it, look at it! You may take
ham	it in your hand; it's no forgery."
ham	Here, Mr. Lorry perceived the reflection on the wall to elongate, and
spam	Mr. Cruncher rose and stepped forward. His hair could not have been more
spam	violently on end, if it had been that moment dressed by the Cow with the
ham	crumpled horn in the house that Jack built.
ham	Unseen by the spy, Mr. Cruncher stood at his side, and touched him on
ham	the shoulder like a ghostly bailiff.
spam	"That there Roger Cly, master," said Mr. Cruncher, with a taciturn and
ham	iron-bound visage. "So _you_ put him in his coffin?"
ham	"I did."
ham	"Who took him out of it?"
ham	Barsad leaned back in his chair, and stammered, "What do you mean?"
ham	"I mean," said Mr. Cruncher, "that he warn't never in it. No! Not he!
spam	I'll have my head took off, if he was ever in it."
spam	The spy looked round at the two gentlemen; they both looked in
spam	unspeakable astonishment at Jerry.
ham	"I tell you," said Jerry, "that you buried paving-stones and earth in
ham	that there coffin. Don't go and tell me that you buried Cly. It was a
spam	take in. Me and two more knows it."
ham	"How do you know it?"
ham	"What's that to you? Ecod!" growled Mr. Cruncher, "it's you I have got a
spam	old grudge again, is it, with your shameful impositions upon tradesmen!
spam	I'd catch hold of your throat and choke you for half a guinea."
spam	Sydney Carton, who, with Mr. Lorry, had been lost in amazement at
ham	this turn of the business, here requested Mr. Cruncher to moderate and
ham	explain himself.
spam	"At another time, sir," he returned, evasively, "the present time is
ham	ill-conwenient for explainin'. What I stand to, is, that he knows well
spam	wot that there Cly was never in that there coffin. Let him say he was,
spam	in so much as a word of one syllable, and I'll either catch hold of his
ham	throat and choke him for half a guinea;" Mr. Cruncher dwelt upon this as
ham	quite a liberal offer; "or I'll out and announce him."
ham	"Humph! I see one thing," said Carton. "I hold another card, Mr. Barsad.
spam	Impossible, here in raging Paris, with Suspicion filling the air, for
ham	you to outlive denunciation, when you are in communication with another
spam	aristocratic spy of the same antecedents as yourself, who, moreover, has
ham	the mystery about him of having feigned death and come to life again!
ham	A plot in the prisons, of the foreigner against the Republic. A strong
ham	card--a certain Guillotine card! Do you play?"
spam	"No!" returned the spy. "I throw up. I confess that we were so unpopular
ham	with the outrageous mob, that I only got away from England at the risk
ham	of being ducked to death, and that Cly was so ferreted up and down, that
spam	he never would have got away at all but for that sham. Though how this
ham	man knows it was a sham, is a wonder of wonders to me."
spam	"Never you trouble your head about this man," retorted the contentious
spam	Mr. Cruncher; "you'll have trouble enough with giving your attention to
ham	that gentleman. And look here! Once more!"--Mr. Cruncher could not
spam	be restrained from making rather an ostentatious parade of his
ham	liberality--"I'd catch hold of your throat and choke you for half a
spam	guinea."
spam	The Sheep of the prisons turned from him to Sydney Carton, and said,
spam	with more decision, "It has come to a point. I go on duty soon, and
ham	can't overstay my time. You told me you had a proposal; what is it?
ham	Now, it is of no use asking too much of me. Ask me to do anything in my
spam	office, putting my head in great extra danger, and I had better trust my
spam	life to the chances of a refusal than the chances of consent. In short,
ham	I should make that choice. You talk of desperation. We are all desperate
spam	here. Remember! I may denounce you if I think proper, and I can swear my
spam	way through stone walls, and so can others. Now, what do you want with
ham	me?"
ham	"Not very much. You are a turnkey at the Conciergerie?"
ham	"I tell you once for all, there is no such thing as an escape possible,"
ham	said the spy, firmly.
spam	"Why need you tell me what I have not asked? You are a turnkey at the
ham	Conciergerie?"
spam	"I am sometimes."
ham	"You can be when you choose?"
ham	"I can pass in and out when I choose."
spam	Sydney Carton filled another glass with brandy, poured it slowly out
spam	upon the hearth, and watched it as it dropped. It being all spent, he
ham	said, rising:
spam	"So far, we have spoken before these two, because it was as well that
ham	the merits of the cards should not rest solely between you and me. Come
ham	into the dark room here, and let us have one final word alone."
ham	IX. The Game Made
spam	While Sydney Carton and the Sheep of the prisons were in the adjoining
ham	dark room, speaking so low that not a sound was heard, Mr. Lorry looked
spam	at Jerry in considerable doubt and mistrust. That honest tradesman's
spam	manner of receiving the look, did not inspire confidence; he changed the
ham	leg on which he rested, as often as if he had fifty of those limbs,
ham	and were trying them all; he examined his finger-nails with a very
ham	questionable closeness of attention; and whenever Mr. Lorry's eye caught
spam	his, he was taken with that peculiar kind of short cough requiring the
ham	hollow of a hand before it, which is seldom, if ever, known to be an
spam	infirmity attendant on perfect openness of character.
ham	"Jerry," said Mr. Lorry. "Come here."
ham	Mr. Cruncher came forward sideways, with one of his shoulders in advance
spam	of him.
spam	"What have you been, besides a messenger?"
ham	After some cogitation, accompanied with an intent look at his patron,
ham	Mr. Cruncher conceived the luminous idea of replying, "Agicultooral
spam	character."
ham	"My mind misgives me much," said Mr. Lorry, angrily shaking a forefinger
ham	at him, "that you have used the respectable and great house of Tellson's
spam	as a blind, and that you have had an unlawful occupation of an infamous
spam	description. If you have, don't expect me to befriend you when you
ham	get back to England. If you have, don't expect me to keep your secret.
ham	Tellson's shall not be imposed upon."
spam	"I hope, sir," pleaded the abashed Mr. Cruncher, "that a gentleman like
ham	yourself wot I've had the honour of odd jobbing till I'm grey at it,
ham	would think twice about harming of me, even if it wos so--I don't say it
spam	is, but even if it wos. And which it is to be took into account that if
spam	it wos, it wouldn't, even then, be all o' one side. There'd be two sides
ham	to it. There might be medical doctors at the present hour, a picking
spam	up their guineas where a honest tradesman don't pick up his
ham	fardens--fardens! no, nor yet his half fardens--half fardens! no, nor
spam	yet his quarter--a banking away like smoke at Tellson's, and a cocking
spam	their medical eyes at that tradesman on the sly, a going in and going
spam	out to their own carriages--ah! equally like smoke, if not more so.
ham	Well, that 'ud be imposing, too, on Tellson's. For you cannot sarse the
ham	goose and not the gander. And here's Mrs. Cruncher, or leastways wos
ham	in the Old England times, and would be to-morrow, if cause given,
spam	a floppin' again the business to that degree as is ruinating--stark
spam	ruinating! Whereas them medical doctors' wives don't flop--catch 'em at
ham	it! Or, if they flop, their floppings goes in favour of more patients,
spam	and how can you rightly have one without t'other? Then, wot with
ham	undertakers, and wot with parish clerks, and wot with sextons, and wot
ham	with private watchmen (all awaricious and all in it), a man wouldn't get
ham	much by it, even if it wos so. And wot little a man did get, would never
ham	prosper with him, Mr. Lorry. He'd never have no good of it; he'd want
ham	all along to be out of the line, if he, could see his way out, being
ham	once in--even if it wos so."
spam	"Ugh!" cried Mr. Lorry, rather relenting, nevertheless, "I am shocked at
spam	the sight of you."
spam	"Now, what I would humbly offer to you, sir," pursued Mr. Cruncher,
spam	"even if it wos so, which I don't say it is--"
spam	"Don't prevaricate," said Mr. Lorry.
ham	"No, I will _not_, sir," returned Mr. Crunches as if nothing were
ham	further from his thoughts or practice--"which I don't say it is--wot I
ham	would humbly offer to you, sir, would be this. Upon that there stool, at
spam	that there Bar, sets that there boy of mine, brought up and growed up to
spam	be a man, wot will errand you, message you, general-light-job you, till
spam	your heels is where your head is, if such should be your wishes. If it
ham	wos so, which I still don't say it is (for I will not prewaricate to
ham	you, sir), let that there boy keep his father's place, and take care of
spam	his mother; don't blow upon that boy's father--do not do it, sir--and
spam	let that father go into the line of the reg'lar diggin', and make amends
ham	for what he would have undug--if it wos so--by diggin' of 'em in with
spam	a will, and with conwictions respectin' the futur' keepin' of 'em safe.
spam	That, Mr. Lorry," said Mr. Cruncher, wiping his forehead with his
spam	arm, as an announcement that he had arrived at the peroration of his
ham	discourse, "is wot I would respectfully offer to you, sir. A man don't
spam	see all this here a goin' on dreadful round him, in the way of Subjects
spam	without heads, dear me, plentiful enough fur to bring the price down
ham	to porterage and hardly that, without havin' his serious thoughts of
spam	things. And these here would be mine, if it wos so, entreatin' of you
spam	fur to bear in mind that wot I said just now, I up and said in the good
ham	cause when I might have kep' it back."
spam	"That at least is true," said Mr. Lorry. "Say no more now. It may be
spam	that I shall yet stand your friend, if you deserve it, and repent in
ham	action--not in words. I want no more words."
spam	Mr. Cruncher knuckled his forehead, as Sydney Carton and the spy
spam	returned from the dark room. "Adieu, Mr. Barsad," said the former; "our
spam	arrangement thus made, you have nothing to fear from me."
spam	He sat down in a chair on the hearth, over against Mr. Lorry. When they
spam	were alone, Mr. Lorry asked him what he had done?
ham	"Not much. If it should go ill with the prisoner, I have ensured access
spam	to him, once."
ham	Mr. Lorry's countenance fell.
spam	"It is all I could do," said Carton. "To propose too much, would be
ham	to put this man's head under the axe, and, as he himself said, nothing
ham	worse could happen to him if he were denounced. It was obviously the
ham	weakness of the position. There is no help for it."
spam	"But access to him," said Mr. Lorry, "if it should go ill before the
spam	Tribunal, will not save him."
spam	"I never said it would."
ham	Mr. Lorry's eyes gradually sought the fire; his sympathy with his
ham	darling, and the heavy disappointment of his second arrest, gradually
spam	weakened them; he was an old man now, overborne with anxiety of late,
ham	and his tears fell.
spam	"You are a good man and a true friend," said Carton, in an altered
spam	voice. "Forgive me if I notice that you are affected. I could not see my
ham	father weep, and sit by, careless. And I could not respect your
spam	sorrow more, if you were my father. You are free from that misfortune,
spam	however."
spam	Though he said the last words, with a slip into his usual manner, there
ham	was a true feeling and respect both in his tone and in his touch,
ham	that Mr. Lorry, who had never seen the better side of him, was wholly
ham	unprepared for. He gave him his hand, and Carton gently pressed it.
spam	"To return to poor Darnay," said Carton. "Don't tell Her of this
ham	interview, or this arrangement. It would not enable Her to go to see
spam	him. She might think it was contrived, in case of the worse, to convey
ham	to him the means of anticipating the sentence."
spam	Mr. Lorry had not thought of that, and he looked quickly at Carton to
ham	see if it were in his mind. It seemed to be; he returned the look, and
ham	evidently understood it.
spam	"She might think a thousand things," Carton said, "and any of them would
ham	only add to her trouble. Don't speak of me to her. As I said to you when
ham	I first came, I had better not see her. I can put my hand out, to do any
ham	little helpful work for her that my hand can find to do, without that.
spam	You are going to her, I hope? She must be very desolate to-night."
spam	"I am going now, directly."
spam	"I am glad of that. She has such a strong attachment to you and reliance
ham	on you. How does she look?"
ham	"Anxious and unhappy, but very beautiful."
ham	"Ah!"
ham	It was a long, grieving sound, like a sigh--almost like a sob. It
spam	attracted Mr. Lorry's eyes to Carton's face, which was turned to the
ham	fire. A light, or a shade (the old gentleman could not have said which),
spam	passed from it as swiftly as a change will sweep over a hill-side on a
ham	wild bright day, and he lifted his foot to put back one of the little
spam	flaming logs, which was tumbling forward. He wore the white riding-coat
ham	and top-boots, then in vogue, and the light of the fire touching their
ham	light surfaces made him look very pale, with his long brown hair,
spam	all untrimmed, hanging loose about him. His indifference to fire was
ham	sufficiently remarkable to elicit a word of remonstrance from Mr. Lorry;
ham	his boot was still upon the hot embers of the flaming log, when it had
spam	broken under the weight of his foot.
ham	"I forgot it," he said.
ham	Mr. Lorry's eyes were again attracted to his face. Taking note of the
ham	wasted air which clouded the naturally handsome features, and having
ham	the expression of prisoners' faces fresh in his mind, he was strongly
ham	reminded of that expression.
ham	"And your duties here have drawn to an end, sir?" said Carton, turning
ham	to him.
ham	"Yes. As I was telling you last night when Lucie came in so
spam	unexpectedly, I have at length done all that I can do here. I hoped to
ham	have left them in perfect safety, and then to have quitted Paris. I have
spam	my Leave to Pass. I was ready to go."
spam	They were both silent.
spam	"Yours is a long life to look back upon, sir?" said Carton, wistfully.
spam	"I am in my seventy-eighth year."
spam	"You have been useful all your life; steadily and constantly occupied;
ham	trusted, respected, and looked up to?"
spam	"I have been a man of business, ever since I have been a man. Indeed, I
spam	may say that I was a man of business when a boy."
ham	"See what a place you fill at seventy-eight. How many people will miss
ham	you when you leave it empty!"
spam	"A solitary old bachelor," answered Mr. Lorry, shaking his head. "There
ham	is nobody to weep for me."
ham	"How can you say that? Wouldn't She weep for you? Wouldn't her child?"
spam	"Yes, yes, thank God. I didn't quite mean what I said."
spam	"It _is_ a thing to thank God for; is it not?"
spam	"Surely, surely."
ham	"If you could say, with truth, to your own solitary heart, to-night,
ham	'I have secured to myself the love and attachment, the gratitude or
spam	respect, of no human creature; I have won myself a tender place in no
ham	regard; I have done nothing good or serviceable to be remembered by!'
ham	your seventy-eight years would be seventy-eight heavy curses; would they
spam	not?"
ham	"You say truly, Mr. Carton; I think they would be."
ham	Sydney turned his eyes again upon the fire, and, after a silence of a
ham	few moments, said:
ham	"I should like to ask you:--Does your childhood seem far off? Do the
spam	days when you sat at your mother's knee, seem days of very long ago?"
ham	Responding to his softened manner, Mr. Lorry answered:
ham	"Twenty years back, yes; at this time of my life, no. For, as I draw
spam	closer and closer to the end, I travel in the circle, nearer and
spam	nearer to the beginning. It seems to be one of the kind smoothings and
spam	preparings of the way. My heart is touched now, by many remembrances
ham	that had long fallen asleep, of my pretty young mother (and I so old!),
ham	and by many associations of the days when what we call the World was not
ham	so real with me, and my faults were not confirmed in me."
spam	"I understand the feeling!" exclaimed Carton, with a bright flush. "And
spam	you are the better for it?"
spam	"I hope so."
ham	Carton terminated the conversation here, by rising to help him on with
spam	his outer coat; "But you," said Mr. Lorry, reverting to the theme, "you
spam	are young."
spam	"Yes," said Carton. "I am not old, but my young way was never the way to
spam	age. Enough of me."
spam	"And of me, I am sure," said Mr. Lorry. "Are you going out?"
ham	"I'll walk with you to her gate. You know my vagabond and restless
ham	habits. If I should prowl about the streets a long time, don't be
spam	uneasy; I shall reappear in the morning. You go to the Court to-morrow?"
spam	"Yes, unhappily."
spam	"I shall be there, but only as one of the crowd. My Spy will find a
spam	place for me. Take my arm, sir."
ham	Mr. Lorry did so, and they went down-stairs and out in the streets. A
spam	few minutes brought them to Mr. Lorry's destination. Carton left him
ham	there; but lingered at a little distance, and turned back to the gate
ham	again when it was shut, and touched it. He had heard of her going to
spam	the prison every day. "She came out here," he said, looking about him,
ham	"turned this way, must have trod on these stones often. Let me follow in
ham	her steps."
spam	It was ten o'clock at night when he stood before the prison of La Force,
spam	where she had stood hundreds of times. A little wood-sawyer, having
ham	closed his shop, was smoking his pipe at his shop-door.
ham	"Good night, citizen," said Sydney Carton, pausing in going by; for, the
spam	man eyed him inquisitively.
spam	"Good night, citizen."
ham	"How goes the Republic?"
ham	"You mean the Guillotine. Not ill. Sixty-three to-day. We shall mount
ham	to a hundred soon. Samson and his men complain sometimes, of being
spam	exhausted. Ha, ha, ha! He is so droll, that Samson. Such a Barber!"
ham	"Do you often go to see him--"
spam	"Shave? Always. Every day. What a barber! You have seen him at work?"
ham	"Never."
ham	"Go and see him when he has a good batch. Figure this to yourself,
spam	citizen; he shaved the sixty-three to-day, in less than two pipes! Less
ham	than two pipes. Word of honour!"
spam	As the grinning little man held out the pipe he was smoking, to explain
ham	how he timed the executioner, Carton was so sensible of a rising desire
ham	to strike the life out of him, that he turned away.
spam	"But you are not English," said the wood-sawyer, "though you wear
spam	English dress?"
spam	"Yes," said Carton, pausing again, and answering over his shoulder.
ham	"You speak like a Frenchman."
spam	"I am an old student here."
spam	"Aha, a perfect Frenchman! Good night, Englishman."
ham	"Good night, citizen."
ham	"But go and see that droll dog," the little man persisted, calling after
spam	him. "And take a pipe with you!"
ham	Sydney had not gone far out of sight, when he stopped in the middle of
spam	the street under a glimmering lamp, and wrote with his pencil on a scrap
spam	of paper. Then, traversing with the decided step of one who remembered
spam	the way well, several dark and dirty streets--much dirtier than usual,
ham	for the best public thoroughfares remained uncleansed in those times of
spam	terror--he stopped at a chemist's shop, which the owner was closing with
ham	his own hands. A small, dim, crooked shop, kept in a tortuous, up-hill
ham	thoroughfare, by a small, dim, crooked man.
spam	Giving this citizen, too, good night, as he confronted him at his
spam	counter, he laid the scrap of paper before him. "Whew!" the chemist
spam	whistled softly, as he read it. "Hi! hi! hi!"
ham	Sydney Carton took no heed, and the chemist said:
spam	"For you, citizen?"
spam	"For me."
spam	"You will be careful to keep them separate, citizen? You know the
ham	consequences of mixing them?"
ham	"Perfectly."
spam	Certain small packets were made and given to him. He put them, one by
ham	one, in the breast of his inner coat, counted out the money for them,
spam	and deliberately left the shop. "There is nothing more to do," said he,
spam	glancing upward at the moon, "until to-morrow. I can't sleep."
spam	It was not a reckless manner, the manner in which he said these words
ham	aloud under the fast-sailing clouds, nor was it more expressive of
ham	negligence than defiance. It was the settled manner of a tired man, who
spam	had wandered and struggled and got lost, but who at length struck into
spam	his road and saw its end.
spam	Long ago, when he had been famous among his earliest competitors as a
ham	youth of great promise, he had followed his father to the grave. His
ham	mother had died, years before. These solemn words, which had been
spam	read at his father's grave, arose in his mind as he went down the dark
ham	streets, among the heavy shadows, with the moon and the clouds sailing
ham	on high above him. "I am the resurrection and the life, saith the Lord:
ham	he that believeth in me, though he were dead, yet shall he live: and
spam	whosoever liveth and believeth in me, shall never die."
ham	In a city dominated by the axe, alone at night, with natural sorrow
ham	rising in him for the sixty-three who had been that day put to death,
spam	and for to-morrow's victims then awaiting their doom in the prisons,
ham	and still of to-morrow's and to-morrow's, the chain of association that
spam	brought the words home, like a rusty old ship's anchor from the deep,
ham	might have been easily found. He did not seek it, but repeated them and
spam	went on.
ham	With a solemn interest in the lighted windows where the people were
spam	going to rest, forgetful through a few calm hours of the horrors
ham	surrounding them; in the towers of the churches, where no prayers
spam	were said, for the popular revulsion had even travelled that length
spam	of self-destruction from years of priestly impostors, plunderers, and
spam	profligates; in the distant burial-places, reserved, as they wrote upon
spam	the gates, for Eternal Sleep; in the abounding gaols; and in the streets
ham	along which the sixties rolled to a death which had become so common and
ham	material, that no sorrowful story of a haunting Spirit ever arose among
spam	the people out of all the working of the Guillotine; with a solemn
ham	interest in the whole life and death of the city settling down to its
ham	short nightly pause in fury; Sydney Carton crossed the Seine again for
spam	the lighter streets.
spam	Few coaches were abroad, for riders in coaches were liable to be
spam	suspected, and gentility hid its head in red nightcaps, and put on heavy
ham	shoes, and trudged. But, the theatres were all well filled, and the
ham	people poured cheerfully out as he passed, and went chatting home. At
ham	one of the theatre doors, there was a little girl with a mother, looking
spam	for a way across the street through the mud. He carried the child over,
ham	and before the timid arm was loosed from his neck asked her for a kiss.
ham	"I am the resurrection and the life, saith the Lord: he that believeth
ham	in me, though he were dead, yet shall he live: and whosoever liveth and
ham	believeth in me, shall never die."
spam	Now, that the streets were quiet, and the night wore on, the words
ham	were in the echoes of his feet, and were in the air. Perfectly calm
spam	and steady, he sometimes repeated them to himself as he walked; but, he
ham	heard them always.
spam	The night wore out, and, as he stood upon the bridge listening to the
spam	water as it splashed the river-walls of the Island of Paris, where the
ham	picturesque confusion of houses and cathedral shone bright in the light
spam	of the moon, the day came coldly, looking like a dead face out of the
ham	sky. Then, the night, with the moon and the stars, turned pale and died,
ham	and for a little while it seemed as if Creation were delivered over to
spam	Death's dominion.
ham	But, the glorious sun, rising, seemed to strike those words, that burden
ham	of the night, straight and warm to his heart in its long bright rays.
ham	And looking along them, with reverently shaded eyes, a bridge of light
ham	appeared to span the air between him and the sun, while the river
spam	sparkled under it.
spam	The strong tide, so swift, so deep, and certain, was like a congenial
ham	friend, in the morning stillness. He walked by the stream, far from the
ham	houses, and in the light and warmth of the sun fell asleep on the
ham	bank. When he awoke and was afoot again, he lingered there yet a little
spam	longer, watching an eddy that turned and turned purposeless, until the
ham	stream absorbed it, and carried it on to the sea.--"Like me."
ham	A trading-boat, with a sail of the softened colour of a dead leaf, then
ham	glided into his view, floated by him, and died away. As its silent track
spam	in the water disappeared, the prayer that had broken up out of his heart
ham	for a merciful consideration of all his poor blindnesses and errors,
ham	ended in the words, "I am the resurrection and the life."
spam	Mr. Lorry was already out when he got back, and it was easy to surmise
spam	where the good old man was gone. Sydney Carton drank nothing but a
spam	little coffee, ate some bread, and, having washed and changed to refresh
spam	himself, went out to the place of trial.
ham	The court was all astir and a-buzz, when the black sheep--whom many fell
spam	away from in dread--pressed him into an obscure corner among the crowd.
spam	Mr. Lorry was there, and Doctor Manette was there. She was there,
spam	sitting beside her father.
spam	When her husband was brought in, she turned a look upon him, so
spam	sustaining, so encouraging, so full of admiring love and pitying
ham	tenderness, yet so courageous for his sake, that it called the healthy
ham	blood into his face, brightened his glance, and animated his heart. If
ham	there had been any eyes to notice the influence of her look, on Sydney
spam	Carton, it would have been seen to be the same influence exactly.
ham	Before that unjust Tribunal, there was little or no order of procedure,
spam	ensuring to any accused person any reasonable hearing. There could have
ham	been no such Revolution, if all laws, forms, and ceremonies, had not
ham	first been so monstrously abused, that the suicidal vengeance of the
spam	Revolution was to scatter them all to the winds.
spam	Every eye was turned to the jury. The same determined patriots and good
ham	republicans as yesterday and the day before, and to-morrow and the day
ham	after. Eager and prominent among them, one man with a craving face, and
ham	his fingers perpetually hovering about his lips, whose appearance
spam	gave great satisfaction to the spectators. A life-thirsting,
ham	cannibal-looking, bloody-minded juryman, the Jacques Three of St.
ham	Antoine. The whole jury, as a jury of dogs empannelled to try the deer.
spam	Every eye then turned to the five judges and the public prosecutor.
spam	No favourable leaning in that quarter to-day. A fell, uncompromising,
ham	murderous business-meaning there. Every eye then sought some other eye
spam	in the crowd, and gleamed at it approvingly; and heads nodded at one
ham	another, before bending forward with a strained attention.
spam	Charles Evremonde, called Darnay. Released yesterday. Reaccused and
spam	retaken yesterday. Indictment delivered to him last night. Suspected and
ham	Denounced enemy of the Republic, Aristocrat, one of a family of tyrants,
ham	one of a race proscribed, for that they had used their abolished
ham	privileges to the infamous oppression of the people. Charles Evremonde,
ham	called Darnay, in right of such proscription, absolutely Dead in Law.
spam	To this effect, in as few or fewer words, the Public Prosecutor.
spam	The President asked, was the Accused openly denounced or secretly?
spam	"Openly, President."
spam	"By whom?"
spam	"Three voices. Ernest Defarge, wine-vendor of St. Antoine."
spam	"Good."
ham	"Therese Defarge, his wife."
spam	"Good."
ham	"Alexandre Manette, physician."
ham	A great uproar took place in the court, and in the midst of it, Doctor
ham	Manette was seen, pale and trembling, standing where he had been seated.
spam	"President, I indignantly protest to you that this is a forgery and
spam	a fraud. You know the accused to be the husband of my daughter. My
ham	daughter, and those dear to her, are far dearer to me than my life. Who
spam	and where is the false conspirator who says that I denounce the husband
spam	of my child!"
ham	"Citizen Manette, be tranquil. To fail in submission to the authority of
ham	the Tribunal would be to put yourself out of Law. As to what is dearer
ham	to you than life, nothing can be so dear to a good citizen as the
spam	Republic."
spam	Loud acclamations hailed this rebuke. The President rang his bell, and
spam	with warmth resumed.
ham	"If the Republic should demand of you the sacrifice of your child
spam	herself, you would have no duty but to sacrifice her. Listen to what is
spam	to follow. In the meanwhile, be silent!"
ham	Frantic acclamations were again raised. Doctor Manette sat down, with
spam	his eyes looking around, and his lips trembling; his daughter drew
ham	closer to him. The craving man on the jury rubbed his hands together,
spam	and restored the usual hand to his mouth.
spam	Defarge was produced, when the court was quiet enough to admit of his
spam	being heard, and rapidly expounded the story of the imprisonment, and of
ham	his having been a mere boy in the Doctor's service, and of the release,
ham	and of the state of the prisoner when released and delivered to him.
spam	This short examination followed, for the court was quick with its work.
ham	"You did good service at the taking of the Bastille, citizen?"
spam	"I believe so."
spam	Here, an excited woman screeched from the crowd: "You were one of the
ham	best patriots there. Why not say so? You were a cannonier that day
spam	there, and you were among the first to enter the accursed fortress when
spam	it fell. Patriots, I speak the truth!"
ham	It was The Vengeance who, amidst the warm commendations of the audience,
ham	thus assisted the proceedings. The President rang his bell; but, The
spam	Vengeance, warming with encouragement, shrieked, "I defy that bell!"
spam	wherein she was likewise much commended.
ham	"Inform the Tribunal of what you did that day within the Bastille,
ham	citizen."
ham	"I knew," said Defarge, looking down at his wife, who stood at the
ham	bottom of the steps on which he was raised, looking steadily up at him;
spam	"I knew that this prisoner, of whom I speak, had been confined in a cell
ham	known as One Hundred and Five, North Tower. I knew it from himself. He
spam	knew himself by no other name than One Hundred and Five, North Tower,
spam	when he made shoes under my care. As I serve my gun that day, I resolve,
ham	when the place shall fall, to examine that cell. It falls. I mount to
ham	the cell, with a fellow-citizen who is one of the Jury, directed by a
ham	gaoler. I examine it, very closely. In a hole in the chimney, where a
ham	stone has been worked out and replaced, I find a written paper. This is
spam	that written paper. I have made it my business to examine some specimens
ham	of the writing of Doctor Manette. This is the writing of Doctor Manette.
spam	I confide this paper, in the writing of Doctor Manette, to the hands of
spam	the President."
spam	"Let it be read."
ham	In a dead silence and stillness--the prisoner under trial looking
ham	lovingly at his wife, his wife only looking from him to look with
spam	solicitude at her father, Doctor Manette keeping his eyes fixed on the
ham	reader, Madame Defarge never taking hers from the prisoner, Defarge
spam	never taking his from his feasting wife, and all the other eyes there
ham	intent upon the Doctor, who saw none of them--the paper was read, as
spam	follows.
spam	X. The Substance of the Shadow
ham	"I, Alexandre Manette, unfortunate physician, native of Beauvais, and
spam	afterwards resident in Paris, write this melancholy paper in my doleful
spam	cell in the Bastille, during the last month of the year, 1767. I write
spam	it at stolen intervals, under every difficulty. I design to secrete it
spam	in the wall of the chimney, where I have slowly and laboriously made a
ham	place of concealment for it. Some pitying hand may find it there, when I
ham	and my sorrows are dust.
ham	"These words are formed by the rusty iron point with which I write with
ham	difficulty in scrapings of soot and charcoal from the chimney, mixed
ham	with blood, in the last month of the tenth year of my captivity. Hope
spam	has quite departed from my breast. I know from terrible warnings I have
spam	noted in myself that my reason will not long remain unimpaired, but I
ham	solemnly declare that I am at this time in the possession of my right
ham	mind--that my memory is exact and circumstantial--and that I write the
ham	truth as I shall answer for these my last recorded words, whether they
ham	be ever read by men or not, at the Eternal Judgment-seat.
spam	"One cloudy moonlight night, in the third week of December (I think the
ham	twenty-second of the month) in the year 1757, I was walking on a retired
spam	part of the quay by the Seine for the refreshment of the frosty air,
ham	at an hour's distance from my place of residence in the Street of the
spam	School of Medicine, when a carriage came along behind me, driven very
spam	fast. As I stood aside to let that carriage pass, apprehensive that it
spam	might otherwise run me down, a head was put out at the window, and a
ham	voice called to the driver to stop.
ham	"The carriage stopped as soon as the driver could rein in his horses,
spam	and the same voice called to me by my name. I answered. The carriage
spam	was then so far in advance of me that two gentlemen had time to open the
ham	door and alight before I came up with it.
ham	"I observed that they were both wrapped in cloaks, and appeared to
ham	conceal themselves. As they stood side by side near the carriage door,
spam	I also observed that they both looked of about my own age, or rather
ham	younger, and that they were greatly alike, in stature, manner, voice,
ham	and (as far as I could see) face too.
spam	"'You are Doctor Manette?' said one.
ham	"I am."
ham	"'Doctor Manette, formerly of Beauvais,' said the other; 'the young
spam	physician, originally an expert surgeon, who within the last year or two
spam	has made a rising reputation in Paris?'
spam	"'Gentlemen,' I returned, 'I am that Doctor Manette of whom you speak so
ham	graciously.'
ham	"'We have been to your residence,' said the first, 'and not being
ham	so fortunate as to find you there, and being informed that you were
ham	probably walking in this direction, we followed, in the hope of
spam	overtaking you. Will you please to enter the carriage?'
ham	"The manner of both was imperious, and they both moved, as these words
ham	were spoken, so as to place me between themselves and the carriage door.
spam	They were armed. I was not.
spam	"'Gentlemen,' said I, 'pardon me; but I usually inquire who does me
spam	the honour to seek my assistance, and what is the nature of the case to
ham	which I am summoned.'
ham	"The reply to this was made by him who had spoken second. 'Doctor,
ham	your clients are people of condition. As to the nature of the case,
spam	our confidence in your skill assures us that you will ascertain it for
ham	yourself better than we can describe it. Enough. Will you please to
ham	enter the carriage?'
ham	"I could do nothing but comply, and I entered it in silence. They both
ham	entered after me--the last springing in, after putting up the steps. The
spam	carriage turned about, and drove on at its former speed.
ham	"I repeat this conversation exactly as it occurred. I have no doubt that
ham	it is, word for word, the same. I describe everything exactly as it took
ham	place, constraining my mind not to wander from the task. Where I make
ham	the broken marks that follow here, I leave off for the time, and put my
ham	paper in its hiding-place.
spam	        *****
ham	"The carriage left the streets behind, passed the North Barrier, and
spam	emerged upon the country road. At two-thirds of a league from the
ham	Barrier--I did not estimate the distance at that time, but afterwards
spam	when I traversed it--it struck out of the main avenue, and presently
spam	stopped at a solitary house, We all three alighted, and walked, by
spam	a damp soft footpath in a garden where a neglected fountain had
spam	overflowed, to the door of the house. It was not opened immediately, in
ham	answer to the ringing of the bell, and one of my two conductors struck
ham	the man who opened it, with his heavy riding glove, across the face.
ham	"There was nothing in this action to attract my particular attention,
ham	for I had seen common people struck more commonly than dogs. But, the
ham	other of the two, being angry likewise, struck the man in like manner
spam	with his arm; the look and bearing of the brothers were then so exactly
ham	alike, that I then first perceived them to be twin brothers.
spam	"From the time of our alighting at the outer gate (which we found
ham	locked, and which one of the brothers had opened to admit us, and had
ham	relocked), I had heard cries proceeding from an upper chamber. I was
ham	conducted to this chamber straight, the cries growing louder as we
spam	ascended the stairs, and I found a patient in a high fever of the brain,
ham	lying on a bed.
ham	"The patient was a woman of great beauty, and young; assuredly not much
ham	past twenty. Her hair was torn and ragged, and her arms were bound to
spam	her sides with sashes and handkerchiefs. I noticed that these bonds were
ham	all portions of a gentleman's dress. On one of them, which was a fringed
ham	scarf for a dress of ceremony, I saw the armorial bearings of a Noble,
ham	and the letter E.
ham	"I saw this, within the first minute of my contemplation of the patient;
ham	for, in her restless strivings she had turned over on her face on the
spam	edge of the bed, had drawn the end of the scarf into her mouth, and was
ham	in danger of suffocation. My first act was to put out my hand to relieve
ham	her breathing; and in moving the scarf aside, the embroidery in the
ham	corner caught my sight.
spam	"I turned her gently over, placed my hands upon her breast to calm her
spam	and keep her down, and looked into her face. Her eyes were dilated and
spam	wild, and she constantly uttered piercing shrieks, and repeated the
spam	words, 'My husband, my father, and my brother!' and then counted up to
ham	twelve, and said, 'Hush!' For an instant, and no more, she would pause
ham	to listen, and then the piercing shrieks would begin again, and she
ham	would repeat the cry, 'My husband, my father, and my brother!' and
spam	would count up to twelve, and say, 'Hush!' There was no variation in the
ham	order, or the manner. There was no cessation, but the regular moment's
spam	pause, in the utterance of these sounds.
spam	"'How long,' I asked, 'has this lasted?'
ham	"To distinguish the brothers, I will call them the elder and the
ham	younger; by the elder, I mean him who exercised the most authority. It
spam	was the elder who replied, 'Since about this hour last night.'
ham	"'She has a husband, a father, and a brother?'
spam	"'A brother.'
spam	"'I do not address her brother?'
spam	"He answered with great contempt, 'No.'
ham	"'She has some recent association with the number twelve?'
spam	"The younger brother impatiently rejoined, 'With twelve o'clock?'
ham	"'See, gentlemen,' said I, still keeping my hands upon her breast, 'how
ham	useless I am, as you have brought me! If I had known what I was coming
ham	to see, I could have come provided. As it is, time must be lost. There
ham	are no medicines to be obtained in this lonely place.'
spam	"The elder brother looked to the younger, who said haughtily, 'There is
spam	a case of medicines here;' and brought it from a closet, and put it on
ham	the table.
ham	        *****
ham	"I opened some of the bottles, smelt them, and put the stoppers to my
ham	lips. If I had wanted to use anything save narcotic medicines that were
spam	poisons in themselves, I would not have administered any of those.
ham	"'Do you doubt them?' asked the younger brother.
ham	"'You see, monsieur, I am going to use them,' I replied, and said no
spam	more.
spam	"I made the patient swallow, with great difficulty, and after many
spam	efforts, the dose that I desired to give. As I intended to repeat it
ham	after a while, and as it was necessary to watch its influence, I then
spam	sat down by the side of the bed. There was a timid and suppressed woman
spam	in attendance (wife of the man down-stairs), who had retreated into
spam	a corner. The house was damp and decayed, indifferently
spam	furnished--evidently, recently occupied and temporarily used. Some thick
ham	old hangings had been nailed up before the windows, to deaden the
ham	sound of the shrieks. They continued to be uttered in their regular
spam	succession, with the cry, 'My husband, my father, and my brother!' the
ham	counting up to twelve, and 'Hush!' The frenzy was so violent, that I had
spam	not unfastened the bandages restraining the arms; but, I had looked to
spam	them, to see that they were not painful. The only spark of encouragement
spam	in the case, was, that my hand upon the sufferer's breast had this much
spam	soothing influence, that for minutes at a time it tranquillised the
ham	figure. It had no effect upon the cries; no pendulum could be more
ham	regular.
ham	"For the reason that my hand had this effect (I assume), I had sat by
spam	the side of the bed for half an hour, with the two brothers looking on,
ham	before the elder said:
ham	"'There is another patient.'
ham	"I was startled, and asked, 'Is it a pressing case?'
spam	"'You had better see,' he carelessly answered; and took up a light.
spam	        *****
ham	"The other patient lay in a back room across a second staircase, which
ham	was a species of loft over a stable. There was a low plastered ceiling
ham	to a part of it; the rest was open, to the ridge of the tiled roof, and
spam	there were beams across. Hay and straw were stored in that portion of
ham	the place, fagots for firing, and a heap of apples in sand. I had to
spam	pass through that part, to get at the other. My memory is circumstantial
spam	and unshaken. I try it with these details, and I see them all, in
spam	this my cell in the Bastille, near the close of the tenth year of my
ham	captivity, as I saw them all that night.
spam	"On some hay on the ground, with a cushion thrown under his head, lay a
spam	handsome peasant boy--a boy of not more than seventeen at the most.
ham	He lay on his back, with his teeth set, his right hand clenched on his
spam	breast, and his glaring eyes looking straight upward. I could not see
ham	where his wound was, as I kneeled on one knee over him; but, I could see
spam	that he was dying of a wound from a sharp point.
spam	"'I am a doctor, my poor fellow,' said I. 'Let me examine it.'
ham	"'I do not want it examined,' he answered; 'let it be.'
spam	"It was under his hand, and I soothed him to let me move his hand away.
ham	The wound was a sword-thrust, received from twenty to twenty-four hours
spam	before, but no skill could have saved him if it had been looked to
ham	without delay. He was then dying fast. As I turned my eyes to the elder
spam	brother, I saw him looking down at this handsome boy whose life was
spam	ebbing out, as if he were a wounded bird, or hare, or rabbit; not at all
spam	as if he were a fellow-creature.
ham	"'How has this been done, monsieur?' said I.
spam	"'A crazed young common dog! A serf! Forced my brother to draw upon him,
ham	and has fallen by my brother's sword--like a gentleman.'
ham	"There was no touch of pity, sorrow, or kindred humanity, in this
spam	answer. The speaker seemed to acknowledge that it was inconvenient to
spam	have that different order of creature dying there, and that it would
ham	have been better if he had died in the usual obscure routine of his
spam	vermin kind. He was quite incapable of any compassionate feeling about
ham	the boy, or about his fate.
spam	"The boy's eyes had slowly moved to him as he had spoken, and they now
spam	slowly moved to me.
ham	"'Doctor, they are very proud, these Nobles; but we common dogs are
ham	proud too, sometimes. They plunder us, outrage us, beat us, kill us; but
spam	we have a little pride left, sometimes. She--have you seen her, Doctor?'
spam	"The shrieks and the cries were audible there, though subdued by the
ham	distance. He referred to them, as if she were lying in our presence.
spam	"I said, 'I have seen her.'
spam	"'She is my sister, Doctor. They have had their shameful rights, these
ham	Nobles, in the modesty and virtue of our sisters, many years, but we
ham	have had good girls among us. I know it, and have heard my father say
ham	so. She was a good girl. She was betrothed to a good young man, too: a
ham	tenant of his. We were all tenants of his--that man's who stands there.
spam	The other is his brother, the worst of a bad race.'
ham	"It was with the greatest difficulty that the boy gathered bodily force
spam	to speak; but, his spirit spoke with a dreadful emphasis.
spam	"'We were so robbed by that man who stands there, as all we common dogs
spam	are by those superior Beings--taxed by him without mercy, obliged to
spam	work for him without pay, obliged to grind our corn at his mill, obliged
ham	to feed scores of his tame birds on our wretched crops, and forbidden
ham	for our lives to keep a single tame bird of our own, pillaged and
ham	plundered to that degree that when we chanced to have a bit of meat, we
ham	ate it in fear, with the door barred and the shutters closed, that his
spam	people should not see it and take it from us--I say, we were so robbed,
ham	and hunted, and were made so poor, that our father told us it was a
spam	dreadful thing to bring a child into the world, and that what we should
ham	most pray for, was, that our women might be barren and our miserable
ham	race die out!'
ham	"I had never before seen the sense of being oppressed, bursting forth
ham	like a fire. I had supposed that it must be latent in the people
ham	somewhere; but, I had never seen it break out, until I saw it in the
ham	dying boy.
ham	"'Nevertheless, Doctor, my sister married. He was ailing at that time,
spam	poor fellow, and she married her lover, that she might tend and comfort
spam	him in our cottage--our dog-hut, as that man would call it. She had not
ham	been married many weeks, when that man's brother saw her and admired
ham	her, and asked that man to lend her to him--for what are husbands among
spam	us! He was willing enough, but my sister was good and virtuous, and
spam	hated his brother with a hatred as strong as mine. What did the two
spam	then, to persuade her husband to use his influence with her, to make her
ham	willing?'
spam	"The boy's eyes, which had been fixed on mine, slowly turned to the
spam	looker-on, and I saw in the two faces that all he said was true. The two
spam	opposing kinds of pride confronting one another, I can see, even in this
spam	Bastille; the gentleman's, all negligent indifference; the peasant's, all
spam	trodden-down sentiment, and passionate revenge.
ham	"'You know, Doctor, that it is among the Rights of these Nobles to
ham	harness us common dogs to carts, and drive us. They so harnessed him and
spam	drove him. You know that it is among their Rights to keep us in their
ham	grounds all night, quieting the frogs, in order that their noble sleep
spam	may not be disturbed. They kept him out in the unwholesome mists at
ham	night, and ordered him back into his harness in the day. But he was
ham	not persuaded. No! Taken out of harness one day at noon, to feed--if he
spam	could find food--he sobbed twelve times, once for every stroke of the
ham	bell, and died on her bosom.'
ham	"Nothing human could have held life in the boy but his determination to
spam	tell all his wrong. He forced back the gathering shadows of death, as
spam	he forced his clenched right hand to remain clenched, and to cover his
spam	wound.
ham	"'Then, with that man's permission and even with his aid, his
ham	brother took her away; in spite of what I know she must have told his
ham	brother--and what that is, will not be long unknown to you, Doctor, if
ham	it is now--his brother took her away--for his pleasure and diversion,
spam	for a little while. I saw her pass me on the road. When I took the
ham	tidings home, our father's heart burst; he never spoke one of the words
spam	that filled it. I took my young sister (for I have another) to a place
spam	beyond the reach of this man, and where, at least, she will never be
ham	_his_ vassal. Then, I tracked the brother here, and last night climbed
ham	in--a common dog, but sword in hand.--Where is the loft window? It was
spam	somewhere here?'
ham	"The room was darkening to his sight; the world was narrowing around
ham	him. I glanced about me, and saw that the hay and straw were trampled
ham	over the floor, as if there had been a struggle.
ham	"'She heard me, and ran in. I told her not to come near us till he was
ham	dead. He came in and first tossed me some pieces of money; then struck
ham	at me with a whip. But I, though a common dog, so struck at him as to
spam	make him draw. Let him break into as many pieces as he will, the sword
ham	that he stained with my common blood; he drew to defend himself--thrust
spam	at me with all his skill for his life.'
spam	"My glance had fallen, but a few moments before, on the fragments of
spam	a broken sword, lying among the hay. That weapon was a gentleman's. In
ham	another place, lay an old sword that seemed to have been a soldier's.
ham	"'Now, lift me up, Doctor; lift me up. Where is he?'
spam	"'He is not here,' I said, supporting the boy, and thinking that he
ham	referred to the brother.
ham	"'He! Proud as these nobles are, he is afraid to see me. Where is the
spam	man who was here? Turn my face to him.'
spam	"I did so, raising the boy's head against my knee. But, invested for the
spam	moment with extraordinary power, he raised himself completely: obliging
ham	me to rise too, or I could not have still supported him.
ham	"'Marquis,' said the boy, turned to him with his eyes opened wide, and
ham	his right hand raised, 'in the days when all these things are to be
ham	answered for, I summon you and yours, to the last of your bad race, to
ham	answer for them. I mark this cross of blood upon you, as a sign that
ham	I do it. In the days when all these things are to be answered for,
ham	I summon your brother, the worst of the bad race, to answer for them
ham	separately. I mark this cross of blood upon him, as a sign that I do
spam	it.'
spam	"Twice, he put his hand to the wound in his breast, and with his
spam	forefinger drew a cross in the air. He stood for an instant with the
spam	finger yet raised, and as it dropped, he dropped with it, and I laid him
ham	down dead.
ham	        *****
spam	"When I returned to the bedside of the young woman, I found her raving
spam	in precisely the same order of continuity. I knew that this might last
spam	for many hours, and that it would probably end in the silence of the
ham	grave.
spam	"I repeated the medicines I had given her, and I sat at the side of
ham	the bed until the night was far advanced. She never abated the piercing
spam	quality of her shrieks, never stumbled in the distinctness or the order
ham	of her words. They were always 'My husband, my father, and my brother!
spam	One, two, three, four, five, six, seven, eight, nine, ten, eleven,
ham	twelve. Hush!'
ham	"This lasted twenty-six hours from the time when I first saw her. I had
spam	come and gone twice, and was again sitting by her, when she began to
ham	falter. I did what little could be done to assist that opportunity, and
spam	by-and-bye she sank into a lethargy, and lay like the dead.
ham	"It was as if the wind and rain had lulled at last, after a long and
spam	fearful storm. I released her arms, and called the woman to assist me to
ham	compose her figure and the dress she had torn. It was then that I knew
spam	her condition to be that of one in whom the first expectations of being
spam	a mother have arisen; and it was then that I lost the little hope I had
ham	had of her.
spam	"'Is she dead?' asked the Marquis, whom I will still describe as the
ham	elder brother, coming booted into the room from his horse.
ham	"'Not dead,' said I; 'but like to die.'
spam	"'What strength there is in these common bodies!' he said, looking down
ham	at her with some curiosity.
spam	"'There is prodigious strength,' I answered him, 'in sorrow and
ham	despair.'
ham	"He first laughed at my words, and then frowned at them. He moved a
spam	chair with his foot near to mine, ordered the woman away, and said in a
ham	subdued voice,
ham	"'Doctor, finding my brother in this difficulty with these hinds, I
ham	recommended that your aid should be invited. Your reputation is high,
ham	and, as a young man with your fortune to make, you are probably mindful
spam	of your interest. The things that you see here, are things to be seen,
spam	and not spoken of.'
ham	"I listened to the patient's breathing, and avoided answering.
spam	"'Do you honour me with your attention, Doctor?'
spam	"'Monsieur,' said I, 'in my profession, the communications of patients
spam	are always received in confidence.' I was guarded in my answer, for I
spam	was troubled in my mind with what I had heard and seen.
spam	"Her breathing was so difficult to trace, that I carefully tried the
spam	pulse and the heart. There was life, and no more. Looking round as I
ham	resumed my seat, I found both the brothers intent upon me.
spam	        *****
ham	"I write with so much difficulty, the cold is so severe, I am so
ham	fearful of being detected and consigned to an underground cell and total
ham	darkness, that I must abridge this narrative. There is no confusion or
spam	failure in my memory; it can recall, and could detail, every word that
spam	was ever spoken between me and those brothers.
spam	"She lingered for a week. Towards the last, I could understand some few
spam	syllables that she said to me, by placing my ear close to her lips. She
spam	asked me where she was, and I told her; who I was, and I told her. It
ham	was in vain that I asked her for her family name. She faintly shook her
ham	head upon the pillow, and kept her secret, as the boy had done.
spam	"I had no opportunity of asking her any question, until I had told the
ham	brothers she was sinking fast, and could not live another day. Until
spam	then, though no one was ever presented to her consciousness save the
