spam	woman and myself, one or other of them had always jealously sat behind
ham	the curtain at the head of the bed when I was there. But when it came to
ham	that, they seemed careless what communication I might hold with her; as
spam	if--the thought passed through my mind--I were dying too.
ham	"I always observed that their pride bitterly resented the younger
ham	brother's (as I call him) having crossed swords with a peasant, and that
spam	peasant a boy. The only consideration that appeared to affect the mind
spam	of either of them was the consideration that this was highly degrading
ham	to the family, and was ridiculous. As often as I caught the younger
spam	brother's eyes, their expression reminded me that he disliked me deeply,
ham	for knowing what I knew from the boy. He was smoother and more polite to
spam	me than the elder; but I saw this. I also saw that I was an incumbrance
ham	in the mind of the elder, too.
ham	"My patient died, two hours before midnight--at a time, by my watch,
spam	answering almost to the minute when I had first seen her. I was alone
ham	with her, when her forlorn young head drooped gently on one side, and
spam	all her earthly wrongs and sorrows ended.
spam	"The brothers were waiting in a room down-stairs, impatient to ride
spam	away. I had heard them, alone at the bedside, striking their boots with
ham	their riding-whips, and loitering up and down.
spam	"'At last she is dead?' said the elder, when I went in.
ham	"'She is dead,' said I.
ham	"'I congratulate you, my brother,' were his words as he turned round.
spam	"He had before offered me money, which I had postponed taking. He now
spam	gave me a rouleau of gold. I took it from his hand, but laid it on
ham	the table. I had considered the question, and had resolved to accept
ham	nothing.
spam	"'Pray excuse me,' said I. 'Under the circumstances, no.'
spam	"They exchanged looks, but bent their heads to me as I bent mine to
spam	them, and we parted without another word on either side.
ham	        *****
ham	"I am weary, weary, weary--worn down by misery. I cannot read what I
spam	have written with this gaunt hand.
spam	"Early in the morning, the rouleau of gold was left at my door in a
ham	little box, with my name on the outside. From the first, I had anxiously
ham	considered what I ought to do. I decided, that day, to write privately
spam	to the Minister, stating the nature of the two cases to which I had been
ham	summoned, and the place to which I had gone: in effect, stating all the
ham	circumstances. I knew what Court influence was, and what the immunities
ham	of the Nobles were, and I expected that the matter would never be
ham	heard of; but, I wished to relieve my own mind. I had kept the matter a
ham	profound secret, even from my wife; and this, too, I resolved to state
spam	in my letter. I had no apprehension whatever of my real danger; but
spam	I was conscious that there might be danger for others, if others were
spam	compromised by possessing the knowledge that I possessed.
spam	"I was much engaged that day, and could not complete my letter that
ham	night. I rose long before my usual time next morning to finish it.
spam	It was the last day of the year. The letter was lying before me just
ham	completed, when I was told that a lady waited, who wished to see me.
spam	        *****
ham	"I am growing more and more unequal to the task I have set myself. It is
spam	so cold, so dark, my senses are so benumbed, and the gloom upon me is so
spam	dreadful.
spam	"The lady was young, engaging, and handsome, but not marked for long
ham	life. She was in great agitation. She presented herself to me as the
spam	wife of the Marquis St. Evremonde. I connected the title by which the
ham	boy had addressed the elder brother, with the initial letter embroidered
ham	on the scarf, and had no difficulty in arriving at the conclusion that I
ham	had seen that nobleman very lately.
spam	"My memory is still accurate, but I cannot write the words of our
ham	conversation. I suspect that I am watched more closely than I was, and I
ham	know not at what times I may be watched. She had in part suspected, and
spam	in part discovered, the main facts of the cruel story, of her husband's
ham	share in it, and my being resorted to. She did not know that the girl
ham	was dead. Her hope had been, she said in great distress, to show her,
spam	in secret, a woman's sympathy. Her hope had been to avert the wrath of
spam	Heaven from a House that had long been hateful to the suffering many.
ham	"She had reasons for believing that there was a young sister living, and
ham	her greatest desire was, to help that sister. I could tell her nothing
spam	but that there was such a sister; beyond that, I knew nothing. Her
spam	inducement to come to me, relying on my confidence, had been the hope
ham	that I could tell her the name and place of abode. Whereas, to this
ham	wretched hour I am ignorant of both.
spam	        *****
ham	"These scraps of paper fail me. One was taken from me, with a warning,
spam	yesterday. I must finish my record to-day.
ham	"She was a good, compassionate lady, and not happy in her marriage. How
spam	could she be! The brother distrusted and disliked her, and his influence
spam	was all opposed to her; she stood in dread of him, and in dread of her
spam	husband too. When I handed her down to the door, there was a child, a
spam	pretty boy from two to three years old, in her carriage.
ham	"'For his sake, Doctor,' she said, pointing to him in tears, 'I would do
spam	all I can to make what poor amends I can. He will never prosper in his
spam	inheritance otherwise. I have a presentiment that if no other innocent
spam	atonement is made for this, it will one day be required of him. What
spam	I have left to call my own--it is little beyond the worth of a few
spam	jewels--I will make it the first charge of his life to bestow, with the
ham	compassion and lamenting of his dead mother, on this injured family, if
ham	the sister can be discovered.'
ham	"She kissed the boy, and said, caressing him, 'It is for thine own dear
ham	sake. Thou wilt be faithful, little Charles?' The child answered her
spam	bravely, 'Yes!' I kissed her hand, and she took him in her arms, and
spam	went away caressing him. I never saw her more.
spam	"As she had mentioned her husband's name in the faith that I knew it,
spam	I added no mention of it to my letter. I sealed my letter, and, not
spam	trusting it out of my own hands, delivered it myself that day.
spam	"That night, the last night of the year, towards nine o'clock, a man in
ham	a black dress rang at my gate, demanded to see me, and softly followed
spam	my servant, Ernest Defarge, a youth, up-stairs. When my servant came
ham	into the room where I sat with my wife--O my wife, beloved of my heart!
spam	My fair young English wife!--we saw the man, who was supposed to be at
ham	the gate, standing silent behind him.
ham	"An urgent case in the Rue St. Honore, he said. It would not detain me,
spam	he had a coach in waiting.
spam	"It brought me here, it brought me to my grave. When I was clear of the
ham	house, a black muffler was drawn tightly over my mouth from behind, and
spam	my arms were pinioned. The two brothers crossed the road from a dark
spam	corner, and identified me with a single gesture. The Marquis took from
ham	his pocket the letter I had written, showed it me, burnt it in the light
spam	of a lantern that was held, and extinguished the ashes with his foot.
ham	Not a word was spoken. I was brought here, I was brought to my living
spam	grave.
spam	"If it had pleased _God_ to put it in the hard heart of either of the
spam	brothers, in all these frightful years, to grant me any tidings of
ham	my dearest wife--so much as to let me know by a word whether alive or
spam	dead--I might have thought that He had not quite abandoned them. But,
spam	now I believe that the mark of the red cross is fatal to them, and that
ham	they have no part in His mercies. And them and their descendants, to the
ham	last of their race, I, Alexandre Manette, unhappy prisoner, do this last
ham	night of the year 1767, in my unbearable agony, denounce to the times
spam	when all these things shall be answered for. I denounce them to Heaven
spam	and to earth."
spam	A terrible sound arose when the reading of this document was done. A
ham	sound of craving and eagerness that had nothing articulate in it but
spam	blood. The narrative called up the most revengeful passions of the time,
ham	and there was not a head in the nation but must have dropped before it.
spam	Little need, in presence of that tribunal and that auditory, to show
spam	how the Defarges had not made the paper public, with the other captured
spam	Bastille memorials borne in procession, and had kept it, biding their
ham	time. Little need to show that this detested family name had long been
spam	anathematised by Saint Antoine, and was wrought into the fatal register.
ham	The man never trod ground whose virtues and services would have
spam	sustained him in that place that day, against such denunciation.
ham	And all the worse for the doomed man, that the denouncer was a
ham	well-known citizen, his own attached friend, the father of his wife. One
ham	of the frenzied aspirations of the populace was, for imitations of
ham	the questionable public virtues of antiquity, and for sacrifices and
spam	self-immolations on the people's altar. Therefore when the President
spam	said (else had his own head quivered on his shoulders), that the good
ham	physician of the Republic would deserve better still of the Republic by
spam	rooting out an obnoxious family of Aristocrats, and would doubtless feel
spam	a sacred glow and joy in making his daughter a widow and her child an
ham	orphan, there was wild excitement, patriotic fervour, not a touch of
ham	human sympathy.
spam	"Much influence around him, has that Doctor?" murmured Madame Defarge,
spam	smiling to The Vengeance. "Save him now, my Doctor, save him!"
spam	At every juryman's vote, there was a roar. Another and another. Roar and
spam	roar.
spam	Unanimously voted. At heart and by descent an Aristocrat, an enemy
spam	of the Republic, a notorious oppressor of the People. Back to the
spam	Conciergerie, and Death within four-and-twenty hours!
spam	XI. Dusk
ham	The wretched wife of the innocent man thus doomed to die, fell under
ham	the sentence, as if she had been mortally stricken. But, she uttered no
spam	sound; and so strong was the voice within her, representing that it was
spam	she of all the world who must uphold him in his misery and not augment
ham	it, that it quickly raised her, even from that shock.
spam	The Judges having to take part in a public demonstration out of doors,
spam	the Tribunal adjourned. The quick noise and movement of the court's
spam	emptying itself by many passages had not ceased, when Lucie stood
spam	stretching out her arms towards her husband, with nothing in her face
spam	but love and consolation.
ham	"If I might touch him! If I might embrace him once! O, good citizens, if
ham	you would have so much compassion for us!"
ham	There was but a gaoler left, along with two of the four men who had
spam	taken him last night, and Barsad. The people had all poured out to the
ham	show in the streets. Barsad proposed to the rest, "Let her embrace
ham	him then; it is but a moment." It was silently acquiesced in, and they
spam	passed her over the seats in the hall to a raised place, where he, by
ham	leaning over the dock, could fold her in his arms.
spam	"Farewell, dear darling of my soul. My parting blessing on my love. We
ham	shall meet again, where the weary are at rest!"
ham	They were her husband's words, as he held her to his bosom.
spam	"I can bear it, dear Charles. I am supported from above: don't suffer
spam	for me. A parting blessing for our child."
ham	"I send it to her by you. I kiss her by you. I say farewell to her by
spam	you."
spam	"My husband. No! A moment!" He was tearing himself apart from her.
ham	"We shall not be separated long. I feel that this will break my heart
ham	by-and-bye; but I will do my duty while I can, and when I leave her, God
ham	will raise up friends for her, as He did for me."
spam	Her father had followed her, and would have fallen on his knees to both
spam	of them, but that Darnay put out a hand and seized him, crying:
ham	"No, no! What have you done, what have you done, that you should kneel
ham	to us! We know now, what a struggle you made of old. We know, now what
spam	you underwent when you suspected my descent, and when you knew it. We
ham	know now, the natural antipathy you strove against, and conquered, for
spam	her dear sake. We thank you with all our hearts, and all our love and
spam	duty. Heaven be with you!"
ham	Her father's only answer was to draw his hands through his white hair,
ham	and wring them with a shriek of anguish.
ham	"It could not be otherwise," said the prisoner. "All things have worked
spam	together as they have fallen out. It was the always-vain endeavour to
ham	discharge my poor mother's trust that first brought my fatal presence
ham	near you. Good could never come of such evil, a happier end was not in
spam	nature to so unhappy a beginning. Be comforted, and forgive me. Heaven
spam	bless you!"
ham	As he was drawn away, his wife released him, and stood looking after him
spam	with her hands touching one another in the attitude of prayer, and
spam	with a radiant look upon her face, in which there was even a comforting
spam	smile. As he went out at the prisoners' door, she turned, laid her head
ham	lovingly on her father's breast, tried to speak to him, and fell at his
ham	feet.
ham	Then, issuing from the obscure corner from which he had never moved,
ham	Sydney Carton came and took her up. Only her father and Mr. Lorry were
spam	with her. His arm trembled as it raised her, and supported her head.
spam	Yet, there was an air about him that was not all of pity--that had a
ham	flush of pride in it.
spam	"Shall I take her to a coach? I shall never feel her weight."
ham	He carried her lightly to the door, and laid her tenderly down in a
spam	coach. Her father and their old friend got into it, and he took his seat
spam	beside the driver.
ham	When they arrived at the gateway where he had paused in the dark not
spam	many hours before, to picture to himself on which of the rough stones of
ham	the street her feet had trodden, he lifted her again, and carried her up
ham	the staircase to their rooms. There, he laid her down on a couch, where
ham	her child and Miss Pross wept over her.
ham	"Don't recall her to herself," he said, softly, to the latter, "she is
ham	better so. Don't revive her to consciousness, while she only faints."
spam	"Oh, Carton, Carton, dear Carton!" cried little Lucie, springing up and
ham	throwing her arms passionately round him, in a burst of grief. "Now that
spam	you have come, I think you will do something to help mamma, something to
spam	save papa! O, look at her, dear Carton! Can you, of all the people who
ham	love her, bear to see her so?"
spam	He bent over the child, and laid her blooming cheek against his face. He
ham	put her gently from him, and looked at her unconscious mother.
spam	"Before I go," he said, and paused--"I may kiss her?"
ham	It was remembered afterwards that when he bent down and touched her face
spam	with his lips, he murmured some words. The child, who was nearest to
spam	him, told them afterwards, and told her grandchildren when she was a
ham	handsome old lady, that she heard him say, "A life you love."
ham	When he had gone out into the next room, he turned suddenly on Mr. Lorry
ham	and her father, who were following, and said to the latter:
ham	"You had great influence but yesterday, Doctor Manette; let it at least
spam	be tried. These judges, and all the men in power, are very friendly to
ham	you, and very recognisant of your services; are they not?"
spam	"Nothing connected with Charles was concealed from me. I had the
ham	strongest assurances that I should save him; and I did." He returned the
spam	answer in great trouble, and very slowly.
ham	"Try them again. The hours between this and to-morrow afternoon are few
ham	and short, but try."
ham	"I intend to try. I will not rest a moment."
spam	"That's well. I have known such energy as yours do great things before
spam	now--though never," he added, with a smile and a sigh together, "such
spam	great things as this. But try! Of little worth as life is when we misuse
spam	it, it is worth that effort. It would cost nothing to lay down if it
ham	were not."
spam	"I will go," said Doctor Manette, "to the Prosecutor and the President
ham	straight, and I will go to others whom it is better not to name. I will
spam	write too, and--But stay! There is a Celebration in the streets, and no
spam	one will be accessible until dark."
spam	"That's true. Well! It is a forlorn hope at the best, and not much the
ham	forlorner for being delayed till dark. I should like to know how you
spam	speed; though, mind! I expect nothing! When are you likely to have seen
ham	these dread powers, Doctor Manette?"
ham	"Immediately after dark, I should hope. Within an hour or two from
ham	this."
spam	"It will be dark soon after four. Let us stretch the hour or two. If I
ham	go to Mr. Lorry's at nine, shall I hear what you have done, either from
ham	our friend or from yourself?"
ham	"Yes."
ham	"May you prosper!"
spam	Mr. Lorry followed Sydney to the outer door, and, touching him on the
spam	shoulder as he was going away, caused him to turn.
ham	"I have no hope," said Mr. Lorry, in a low and sorrowful whisper.
spam	"Nor have I."
ham	"If any one of these men, or all of these men, were disposed to spare
ham	him--which is a large supposition; for what is his life, or any man's
ham	to them!--I doubt if they durst spare him after the demonstration in the
ham	court."
ham	"And so do I. I heard the fall of the axe in that sound."
ham	Mr. Lorry leaned his arm upon the door-post, and bowed his face upon it.
ham	"Don't despond," said Carton, very gently; "don't grieve. I encouraged
spam	Doctor Manette in this idea, because I felt that it might one day be
spam	consolatory to her. Otherwise, she might think 'his life was wantonly
ham	thrown away or wasted,' and that might trouble her."
ham	"Yes, yes, yes," returned Mr. Lorry, drying his eyes, "you are right.
ham	But he will perish; there is no real hope."
spam	"Yes. He will perish: there is no real hope," echoed Carton.
ham	And walked with a settled step, down-stairs.
ham	XII. Darkness
ham	Sydney Carton paused in the street, not quite decided where to go. "At
spam	Tellson's banking-house at nine," he said, with a musing face. "Shall I
spam	do well, in the mean time, to show myself? I think so. It is best that
spam	these people should know there is such a man as I here; it is a sound
spam	precaution, and may be a necessary preparation. But care, care, care!
spam	Let me think it out!"
ham	Checking his steps which had begun to tend towards an object, he took a
spam	turn or two in the already darkening street, and traced the thought
ham	in his mind to its possible consequences. His first impression was
ham	confirmed. "It is best," he said, finally resolved, "that these people
ham	should know there is such a man as I here." And he turned his face
ham	towards Saint Antoine.
spam	Defarge had described himself, that day, as the keeper of a wine-shop in
ham	the Saint Antoine suburb. It was not difficult for one who knew the city
ham	well, to find his house without asking any question. Having ascertained
ham	its situation, Carton came out of those closer streets again, and dined
spam	at a place of refreshment and fell sound asleep after dinner. For the
spam	first time in many years, he had no strong drink. Since last night he
spam	had taken nothing but a little light thin wine, and last night he had
spam	dropped the brandy slowly down on Mr. Lorry's hearth like a man who had
spam	done with it.
ham	It was as late as seven o'clock when he awoke refreshed, and went out
spam	into the streets again. As he passed along towards Saint Antoine, he
spam	stopped at a shop-window where there was a mirror, and slightly altered
spam	the disordered arrangement of his loose cravat, and his coat-collar, and
ham	his wild hair. This done, he went on direct to Defarge's, and went in.
ham	There happened to be no customer in the shop but Jacques Three, of the
ham	restless fingers and the croaking voice. This man, whom he had seen upon
spam	the Jury, stood drinking at the little counter, in conversation with the
spam	Defarges, man and wife. The Vengeance assisted in the conversation, like
ham	a regular member of the establishment.
spam	As Carton walked in, took his seat and asked (in very indifferent
spam	French) for a small measure of wine, Madame Defarge cast a careless
ham	glance at him, and then a keener, and then a keener, and then advanced
ham	to him herself, and asked him what it was he had ordered.
spam	He repeated what he had already said.
ham	"English?" asked Madame Defarge, inquisitively raising her dark
spam	eyebrows.
spam	After looking at her, as if the sound of even a single French word were
spam	slow to express itself to him, he answered, in his former strong foreign
ham	accent. "Yes, madame, yes. I am English!"
ham	Madame Defarge returned to her counter to get the wine, and, as he
spam	took up a Jacobin journal and feigned to pore over it puzzling out its
ham	meaning, he heard her say, "I swear to you, like Evremonde!"
ham	Defarge brought him the wine, and gave him Good Evening.
ham	"How?"
spam	"Good evening."
spam	"Oh! Good evening, citizen," filling his glass. "Ah! and good wine. I
ham	drink to the Republic."
ham	Defarge went back to the counter, and said, "Certainly, a little like."
ham	Madame sternly retorted, "I tell you a good deal like." Jacques Three
ham	pacifically remarked, "He is so much in your mind, see you, madame."
ham	The amiable Vengeance added, with a laugh, "Yes, my faith! And you
ham	are looking forward with so much pleasure to seeing him once more
ham	to-morrow!"
spam	Carton followed the lines and words of his paper, with a slow
spam	forefinger, and with a studious and absorbed face. They were all leaning
spam	their arms on the counter close together, speaking low. After a silence
spam	of a few moments, during which they all looked towards him without
spam	disturbing his outward attention from the Jacobin editor, they resumed
ham	their conversation.
spam	"It is true what madame says," observed Jacques Three. "Why stop? There
spam	is great force in that. Why stop?"
spam	"Well, well," reasoned Defarge, "but one must stop somewhere. After all,
spam	the question is still where?"
ham	"At extermination," said madame.
spam	"Magnificent!" croaked Jacques Three. The Vengeance, also, highly
spam	approved.
ham	"Extermination is good doctrine, my wife," said Defarge, rather
spam	troubled; "in general, I say nothing against it. But this Doctor has
spam	suffered much; you have seen him to-day; you have observed his face when
spam	the paper was read."
ham	"I have observed his face!" repeated madame, contemptuously and angrily.
ham	"Yes. I have observed his face. I have observed his face to be not the
spam	face of a true friend of the Republic. Let him take care of his face!"
spam	"And you have observed, my wife," said Defarge, in a deprecatory manner,
ham	"the anguish of his daughter, which must be a dreadful anguish to him!"
spam	"I have observed his daughter," repeated madame; "yes, I have observed
spam	his daughter, more times than one. I have observed her to-day, and I
spam	have observed her other days. I have observed her in the court, and
ham	I have observed her in the street by the prison. Let me but lift my
ham	finger--!" She seemed to raise it (the listener's eyes were always on
spam	his paper), and to let it fall with a rattle on the ledge before her, as
ham	if the axe had dropped.
ham	"The citizeness is superb!" croaked the Juryman.
spam	"She is an Angel!" said The Vengeance, and embraced her.
spam	"As to thee," pursued madame, implacably, addressing her husband, "if it
spam	depended on thee--which, happily, it does not--thou wouldst rescue this
ham	man even now."
ham	"No!" protested Defarge. "Not if to lift this glass would do it! But I
spam	would leave the matter there. I say, stop there."
spam	"See you then, Jacques," said Madame Defarge, wrathfully; "and see you,
spam	too, my little Vengeance; see you both! Listen! For other crimes as
spam	tyrants and oppressors, I have this race a long time on my register,
spam	doomed to destruction and extermination. Ask my husband, is that so."
spam	"It is so," assented Defarge, without being asked.
spam	"In the beginning of the great days, when the Bastille falls, he finds
ham	this paper of to-day, and he brings it home, and in the middle of the
spam	night when this place is clear and shut, we read it, here on this spot,
spam	by the light of this lamp. Ask him, is that so."
spam	"It is so," assented Defarge.
ham	"That night, I tell him, when the paper is read through, and the lamp is
ham	burnt out, and the day is gleaming in above those shutters and between
ham	those iron bars, that I have now a secret to communicate. Ask him, is
ham	that so."
spam	"It is so," assented Defarge again.
spam	"I communicate to him that secret. I smite this bosom with these two
ham	hands as I smite it now, and I tell him, 'Defarge, I was brought up
spam	among the fishermen of the sea-shore, and that peasant family so injured
ham	by the two Evremonde brothers, as that Bastille paper describes, is my
spam	family. Defarge, that sister of the mortally wounded boy upon the ground
ham	was my sister, that husband was my sister's husband, that unborn child
spam	was their child, that brother was my brother, that father was my father,
ham	those dead are my dead, and that summons to answer for those things
spam	descends to me!' Ask him, is that so."
ham	"It is so," assented Defarge once more.
spam	"Then tell Wind and Fire where to stop," returned madame; "but don't
ham	tell me."
ham	Both her hearers derived a horrible enjoyment from the deadly nature
ham	of her wrath--the listener could feel how white she was, without seeing
spam	her--and both highly commended it. Defarge, a weak minority, interposed
spam	a few words for the memory of the compassionate wife of the Marquis; but
ham	only elicited from his own wife a repetition of her last reply. "Tell
spam	the Wind and the Fire where to stop; not me!"
ham	Customers entered, and the group was broken up. The English customer
spam	paid for what he had had, perplexedly counted his change, and asked, as
ham	a stranger, to be directed towards the National Palace. Madame Defarge
spam	took him to the door, and put her arm on his, in pointing out the road.
spam	The English customer was not without his reflections then, that it might
spam	be a good deed to seize that arm, lift it, and strike under it sharp and
ham	deep.
spam	But, he went his way, and was soon swallowed up in the shadow of the
ham	prison wall. At the appointed hour, he emerged from it to present
ham	himself in Mr. Lorry's room again, where he found the old gentleman
ham	walking to and fro in restless anxiety. He said he had been with Lucie
spam	until just now, and had only left her for a few minutes, to come and
ham	keep his appointment. Her father had not been seen, since he quitted the
ham	banking-house towards four o'clock. She had some faint hopes that his
spam	mediation might save Charles, but they were very slight. He had been
ham	more than five hours gone: where could he be?
ham	Mr. Lorry waited until ten; but, Doctor Manette not returning, and
spam	he being unwilling to leave Lucie any longer, it was arranged that he
spam	should go back to her, and come to the banking-house again at midnight.
ham	In the meanwhile, Carton would wait alone by the fire for the Doctor.
spam	He waited and waited, and the clock struck twelve; but Doctor Manette
ham	did not come back. Mr. Lorry returned, and found no tidings of him, and
spam	brought none. Where could he be?
ham	They were discussing this question, and were almost building up some
spam	weak structure of hope on his prolonged absence, when they heard him on
ham	the stairs. The instant he entered the room, it was plain that all was
ham	lost.
ham	Whether he had really been to any one, or whether he had been all that
spam	time traversing the streets, was never known. As he stood staring at
ham	them, they asked him no question, for his face told them everything.
ham	"I cannot find it," said he, "and I must have it. Where is it?"
ham	His head and throat were bare, and, as he spoke with a helpless look
ham	straying all around, he took his coat off, and let it drop on the floor.
spam	"Where is my bench? I have been looking everywhere for my bench, and I
spam	can't find it. What have they done with my work? Time presses: I must
spam	finish those shoes."
spam	They looked at one another, and their hearts died within them.
spam	"Come, come!" said he, in a whimpering miserable way; "let me get to
ham	work. Give me my work."
ham	Receiving no answer, he tore his hair, and beat his feet upon the
spam	ground, like a distracted child.
ham	"Don't torture a poor forlorn wretch," he implored them, with a dreadful
ham	cry; "but give me my work! What is to become of us, if those shoes are
spam	not done to-night?"
spam	Lost, utterly lost!
spam	It was so clearly beyond hope to reason with him, or try to restore him,
spam	that--as if by agreement--they each put a hand upon his shoulder, and
ham	soothed him to sit down before the fire, with a promise that he should
ham	have his work presently. He sank into the chair, and brooded over the
ham	embers, and shed tears. As if all that had happened since the garret
ham	time were a momentary fancy, or a dream, Mr. Lorry saw him shrink into
ham	the exact figure that Defarge had had in keeping.
spam	Affected, and impressed with terror as they both were, by this spectacle
spam	of ruin, it was not a time to yield to such emotions. His lonely
ham	daughter, bereft of her final hope and reliance, appealed to them both
ham	too strongly. Again, as if by agreement, they looked at one another with
ham	one meaning in their faces. Carton was the first to speak:
spam	"The last chance is gone: it was not much. Yes; he had better be taken
ham	to her. But, before you go, will you, for a moment, steadily attend to
ham	me? Don't ask me why I make the stipulations I am going to make, and
ham	exact the promise I am going to exact; I have a reason--a good one."
ham	"I do not doubt it," answered Mr. Lorry. "Say on."
ham	The figure in the chair between them, was all the time monotonously
spam	rocking itself to and fro, and moaning. They spoke in such a tone as
spam	they would have used if they had been watching by a sick-bed in the
spam	night.
spam	Carton stooped to pick up the coat, which lay almost entangling his
spam	feet. As he did so, a small case in which the Doctor was accustomed to
ham	carry the lists of his day's duties, fell lightly on the floor. Carton
spam	took it up, and there was a folded paper in it. "We should look
spam	at this!" he said. Mr. Lorry nodded his consent. He opened it, and
spam	exclaimed, "Thank _God!_"
ham	"What is it?" asked Mr. Lorry, eagerly.
spam	"A moment! Let me speak of it in its place. First," he put his hand in
ham	his coat, and took another paper from it, "that is the certificate which
ham	enables me to pass out of this city. Look at it. You see--Sydney Carton,
ham	an Englishman?"
ham	Mr. Lorry held it open in his hand, gazing in his earnest face.
spam	"Keep it for me until to-morrow. I shall see him to-morrow, you
spam	remember, and I had better not take it into the prison."
spam	"Why not?"
spam	"I don't know; I prefer not to do so. Now, take this paper that Doctor
ham	Manette has carried about him. It is a similar certificate, enabling him
spam	and his daughter and her child, at any time, to pass the barrier and the
ham	frontier! You see?"
ham	"Yes!"
ham	"Perhaps he obtained it as his last and utmost precaution against evil,
ham	yesterday. When is it dated? But no matter; don't stay to look; put it
ham	up carefully with mine and your own. Now, observe! I never doubted until
spam	within this hour or two, that he had, or could have such a paper. It is
ham	good, until recalled. But it may be soon recalled, and, I have reason to
spam	think, will be."
ham	"They are not in danger?"
spam	"They are in great danger. They are in danger of denunciation by Madame
ham	Defarge. I know it from her own lips. I have overheard words of that
ham	woman's, to-night, which have presented their danger to me in strong
ham	colours. I have lost no time, and since then, I have seen the spy. He
ham	confirms me. He knows that a wood-sawyer, living by the prison wall,
spam	is under the control of the Defarges, and has been rehearsed by
ham	Madame Defarge as to his having seen Her"--he never mentioned Lucie's
spam	name--"making signs and signals to prisoners. It is easy to foresee that
ham	the pretence will be the common one, a prison plot, and that it will
ham	involve her life--and perhaps her child's--and perhaps her father's--for
ham	both have been seen with her at that place. Don't look so horrified. You
spam	will save them all."
ham	"Heaven grant I may, Carton! But how?"
ham	"I am going to tell you how. It will depend on you, and it could depend
ham	on no better man. This new denunciation will certainly not take place
spam	until after to-morrow; probably not until two or three days afterwards;
ham	more probably a week afterwards. You know it is a capital crime, to
ham	mourn for, or sympathise with, a victim of the Guillotine. She and her
ham	father would unquestionably be guilty of this crime, and this woman (the
spam	inveteracy of whose pursuit cannot be described) would wait to add that
spam	strength to her case, and make herself doubly sure. You follow me?"
spam	"So attentively, and with so much confidence in what you say, that for
ham	the moment I lose sight," touching the back of the Doctor's chair, "even
ham	of this distress."
spam	"You have money, and can buy the means of travelling to the seacoast
spam	as quickly as the journey can be made. Your preparations have been
spam	completed for some days, to return to England. Early to-morrow have your
spam	horses ready, so that they may be in starting trim at two o'clock in the
spam	afternoon."
ham	"It shall be done!"
ham	His manner was so fervent and inspiring, that Mr. Lorry caught the
spam	flame, and was as quick as youth.
ham	"You are a noble heart. Did I say we could depend upon no better man?
ham	Tell her, to-night, what you know of her danger as involving her child
ham	and her father. Dwell upon that, for she would lay her own fair head
ham	beside her husband's cheerfully." He faltered for an instant; then went
spam	on as before. "For the sake of her child and her father, press upon her
ham	the necessity of leaving Paris, with them and you, at that hour. Tell
ham	her that it was her husband's last arrangement. Tell her that more
spam	depends upon it than she dare believe, or hope. You think that her
spam	father, even in this sad state, will submit himself to her; do you not?"
spam	"I am sure of it."
ham	"I thought so. Quietly and steadily have all these arrangements made in
spam	the courtyard here, even to the taking of your own seat in the carriage.
spam	The moment I come to you, take me in, and drive away."
ham	"I understand that I wait for you under all circumstances?"
ham	"You have my certificate in your hand with the rest, you know, and will
ham	reserve my place. Wait for nothing but to have my place occupied, and
spam	then for England!"
ham	"Why, then," said Mr. Lorry, grasping his eager but so firm and steady
spam	hand, "it does not all depend on one old man, but I shall have a young
ham	and ardent man at my side."
spam	"By the help of Heaven you shall! Promise me solemnly that nothing will
ham	influence you to alter the course on which we now stand pledged to one
spam	another."
spam	"Nothing, Carton."
ham	"Remember these words to-morrow: change the course, or delay in it--for
ham	any reason--and no life can possibly be saved, and many lives must
spam	inevitably be sacrificed."
ham	"I will remember them. I hope to do my part faithfully."
ham	"And I hope to do mine. Now, good bye!"
ham	Though he said it with a grave smile of earnestness, and though he even
spam	put the old man's hand to his lips, he did not part from him then. He
spam	helped him so far to arouse the rocking figure before the dying embers,
spam	as to get a cloak and hat put upon it, and to tempt it forth to find
ham	where the bench and work were hidden that it still moaningly besought
spam	to have. He walked on the other side of it and protected it to the
spam	courtyard of the house where the afflicted heart--so happy in
spam	the memorable time when he had revealed his own desolate heart to
spam	it--outwatched the awful night. He entered the courtyard and remained
spam	there for a few moments alone, looking up at the light in the window of
spam	her room. Before he went away, he breathed a blessing towards it, and a
ham	Farewell.
ham	XIII. Fifty-two
spam	In the black prison of the Conciergerie, the doomed of the day awaited
spam	their fate. They were in number as the weeks of the year. Fifty-two were
spam	to roll that afternoon on the life-tide of the city to the boundless
spam	everlasting sea. Before their cells were quit of them, new occupants
spam	were appointed; before their blood ran into the blood spilled yesterday,
spam	the blood that was to mingle with theirs to-morrow was already set
spam	apart.
ham	Two score and twelve were told off. From the farmer-general of seventy,
spam	whose riches could not buy his life, to the seamstress of twenty, whose
ham	poverty and obscurity could not save her. Physical diseases, engendered
spam	in the vices and neglects of men, will seize on victims of all degrees;
ham	and the frightful moral disorder, born of unspeakable suffering,
ham	intolerable oppression, and heartless indifference, smote equally
ham	without distinction.
ham	Charles Darnay, alone in a cell, had sustained himself with no
spam	flattering delusion since he came to it from the Tribunal. In every line
ham	of the narrative he had heard, he had heard his condemnation. He had
spam	fully comprehended that no personal influence could possibly save him,
spam	that he was virtually sentenced by the millions, and that units could
ham	avail him nothing.
spam	Nevertheless, it was not easy, with the face of his beloved wife fresh
spam	before him, to compose his mind to what it must bear. His hold on life
ham	was strong, and it was very, very hard, to loosen; by gradual efforts
spam	and degrees unclosed a little here, it clenched the tighter there; and
spam	when he brought his strength to bear on that hand and it yielded,
spam	this was closed again. There was a hurry, too, in all his thoughts,
spam	a turbulent and heated working of his heart, that contended against
spam	resignation. If, for a moment, he did feel resigned, then his wife and
spam	child who had to live after him, seemed to protest and to make it a
spam	selfish thing.
ham	But, all this was at first. Before long, the consideration that there
ham	was no disgrace in the fate he must meet, and that numbers went the same
ham	road wrongfully, and trod it firmly every day, sprang up to stimulate
spam	him. Next followed the thought that much of the future peace of mind
spam	enjoyable by the dear ones, depended on his quiet fortitude. So,
spam	by degrees he calmed into the better state, when he could raise his
ham	thoughts much higher, and draw comfort down.
spam	Before it had set in dark on the night of his condemnation, he had
ham	travelled thus far on his last way. Being allowed to purchase the means
spam	of writing, and a light, he sat down to write until such time as the
ham	prison lamps should be extinguished.
spam	He wrote a long letter to Lucie, showing her that he had known nothing
ham	of her father's imprisonment, until he had heard of it from herself,
spam	and that he had been as ignorant as she of his father's and uncle's
ham	responsibility for that misery, until the paper had been read. He had
spam	already explained to her that his concealment from herself of the name
ham	he had relinquished, was the one condition--fully intelligible now--that
ham	her father had attached to their betrothal, and was the one promise he
spam	had still exacted on the morning of their marriage. He entreated her,
spam	for her father's sake, never to seek to know whether her father had
spam	become oblivious of the existence of the paper, or had had it recalled
ham	to him (for the moment, or for good), by the story of the Tower, on
ham	that old Sunday under the dear old plane-tree in the garden. If he had
spam	preserved any definite remembrance of it, there could be no doubt that
ham	he had supposed it destroyed with the Bastille, when he had found no
spam	mention of it among the relics of prisoners which the populace had
ham	discovered there, and which had been described to all the world. He
spam	besought her--though he added that he knew it was needless--to console
ham	her father, by impressing him through every tender means she could think
ham	of, with the truth that he had done nothing for which he could justly
ham	reproach himself, but had uniformly forgotten himself for their joint
ham	sakes. Next to her preservation of his own last grateful love and
spam	blessing, and her overcoming of her sorrow, to devote herself to their
spam	dear child, he adjured her, as they would meet in Heaven, to comfort her
ham	father.
ham	To her father himself, he wrote in the same strain; but, he told her
spam	father that he expressly confided his wife and child to his care. And
spam	he told him this, very strongly, with the hope of rousing him from any
spam	despondency or dangerous retrospect towards which he foresaw he might be
ham	tending.
spam	To Mr. Lorry, he commended them all, and explained his worldly affairs.
spam	That done, with many added sentences of grateful friendship and warm
spam	attachment, all was done. He never thought of Carton. His mind was so
spam	full of the others, that he never once thought of him.
spam	He had time to finish these letters before the lights were put out. When
spam	he lay down on his straw bed, he thought he had done with this world.
ham	But, it beckoned him back in his sleep, and showed itself in shining
ham	forms. Free and happy, back in the old house in Soho (though it had
ham	nothing in it like the real house), unaccountably released and light of
ham	heart, he was with Lucie again, and she told him it was all a dream, and
ham	he had never gone away. A pause of forgetfulness, and then he had even
ham	suffered, and had come back to her, dead and at peace, and yet there
ham	was no difference in him. Another pause of oblivion, and he awoke in the
spam	sombre morning, unconscious where he was or what had happened, until it
spam	flashed upon his mind, "this is the day of my death!"
spam	Thus, had he come through the hours, to the day when the fifty-two heads
ham	were to fall. And now, while he was composed, and hoped that he could
spam	meet the end with quiet heroism, a new action began in his waking
ham	thoughts, which was very difficult to master.
ham	He had never seen the instrument that was to terminate his life. How
ham	high it was from the ground, how many steps it had, where he would be
ham	stood, how he would be touched, whether the touching hands would be dyed
ham	red, which way his face would be turned, whether he would be the first,
ham	or might be the last: these and many similar questions, in nowise
spam	directed by his will, obtruded themselves over and over again, countless
ham	times. Neither were they connected with fear: he was conscious of no
ham	fear. Rather, they originated in a strange besetting desire to know what
ham	to do when the time came; a desire gigantically disproportionate to the
spam	few swift moments to which it referred; a wondering that was more like
spam	the wondering of some other spirit within his, than his own.
ham	The hours went on as he walked to and fro, and the clocks struck the
ham	numbers he would never hear again. Nine gone for ever, ten gone for
ham	ever, eleven gone for ever, twelve coming on to pass away. After a hard
spam	contest with that eccentric action of thought which had last perplexed
ham	him, he had got the better of it. He walked up and down, softly
ham	repeating their names to himself. The worst of the strife was over.
spam	He could walk up and down, free from distracting fancies, praying for
spam	himself and for them.
ham	Twelve gone for ever.
spam	He had been apprised that the final hour was Three, and he knew he would
spam	be summoned some time earlier, inasmuch as the tumbrils jolted heavily
spam	and slowly through the streets. Therefore, he resolved to keep Two
spam	before his mind, as the hour, and so to strengthen himself in the
spam	interval that he might be able, after that time, to strengthen others.
spam	Walking regularly to and fro with his arms folded on his breast, a very
spam	different man from the prisoner, who had walked to and fro at La Force,
spam	he heard One struck away from him, without surprise. The hour had
ham	measured like most other hours. Devoutly thankful to Heaven for his
spam	recovered self-possession, he thought, "There is but another now," and
spam	turned to walk again.
spam	Footsteps in the stone passage outside the door. He stopped.
spam	The key was put in the lock, and turned. Before the door was opened, or
spam	as it opened, a man said in a low voice, in English: "He has never seen
ham	me here; I have kept out of his way. Go you in alone; I wait near. Lose
ham	no time!"
spam	The door was quickly opened and closed, and there stood before him
ham	face to face, quiet, intent upon him, with the light of a smile on his
spam	features, and a cautionary finger on his lip, Sydney Carton.
spam	There was something so bright and remarkable in his look, that, for the
ham	first moment, the prisoner misdoubted him to be an apparition of his own
spam	imagining. But, he spoke, and it was his voice; he took the prisoner's
spam	hand, and it was his real grasp.
spam	"Of all the people upon earth, you least expected to see me?" he said.
ham	"I could not believe it to be you. I can scarcely believe it now. You
spam	are not"--the apprehension came suddenly into his mind--"a prisoner?"
ham	"No. I am accidentally possessed of a power over one of the keepers
ham	here, and in virtue of it I stand before you. I come from her--your
ham	wife, dear Darnay."
spam	The prisoner wrung his hand.
ham	"I bring you a request from her."
ham	"What is it?"
spam	"A most earnest, pressing, and emphatic entreaty, addressed to you
ham	in the most pathetic tones of the voice so dear to you, that you well
ham	remember."
spam	The prisoner turned his face partly aside.
spam	"You have no time to ask me why I bring it, or what it means; I have
ham	no time to tell you. You must comply with it--take off those boots you
ham	wear, and draw on these of mine."
spam	There was a chair against the wall of the cell, behind the prisoner.
ham	Carton, pressing forward, had already, with the speed of lightning, got
ham	him down into it, and stood over him, barefoot.
spam	"Draw on these boots of mine. Put your hands to them; put your will to
ham	them. Quick!"
spam	"Carton, there is no escaping from this place; it never can be done. You
spam	will only die with me. It is madness."
spam	"It would be madness if I asked you to escape; but do I? When I ask you
ham	to pass out at that door, tell me it is madness and remain here. Change
spam	that cravat for this of mine, that coat for this of mine. While you do
ham	it, let me take this ribbon from your hair, and shake out your hair like
spam	this of mine!"
ham	With wonderful quickness, and with a strength both of will and action,
spam	that appeared quite supernatural, he forced all these changes upon him.
spam	The prisoner was like a young child in his hands.
spam	"Carton! Dear Carton! It is madness. It cannot be accomplished, it never
spam	can be done, it has been attempted, and has always failed. I implore you
ham	not to add your death to the bitterness of mine."
spam	"Do I ask you, my dear Darnay, to pass the door? When I ask that,
ham	refuse. There are pen and ink and paper on this table. Is your hand
spam	steady enough to write?"
spam	"It was when you came in."
ham	"Steady it again, and write what I shall dictate. Quick, friend, quick!"
ham	Pressing his hand to his bewildered head, Darnay sat down at the table.
ham	Carton, with his right hand in his breast, stood close beside him.
ham	"Write exactly as I speak."
spam	"To whom do I address it?"
ham	"To no one." Carton still had his hand in his breast.
ham	"Do I date it?"
spam	"No."
ham	The prisoner looked up, at each question. Carton, standing over him with
spam	his hand in his breast, looked down.
spam	"'If you remember,'" said Carton, dictating, "'the words that passed
spam	between us, long ago, you will readily comprehend this when you see it.
spam	You do remember them, I know. It is not in your nature to forget them.'"
ham	He was drawing his hand from his breast; the prisoner chancing to look
spam	up in his hurried wonder as he wrote, the hand stopped, closing upon
spam	something.
ham	"Have you written 'forget them'?" Carton asked.
ham	"I have. Is that a weapon in your hand?"
ham	"No; I am not armed."
ham	"What is it in your hand?"
ham	"You shall know directly. Write on; there are but a few words more." He
spam	dictated again. "'I am thankful that the time has come, when I can prove
ham	them. That I do so is no subject for regret or grief.'" As he said these
spam	words with his eyes fixed on the writer, his hand slowly and softly
spam	moved down close to the writer's face.
spam	The pen dropped from Darnay's fingers on the table, and he looked about
spam	him vacantly.
ham	"What vapour is that?" he asked.
ham	"Vapour?"
ham	"Something that crossed me?"
ham	"I am conscious of nothing; there can be nothing here. Take up the pen
spam	and finish. Hurry, hurry!"
spam	As if his memory were impaired, or his faculties disordered, the
ham	prisoner made an effort to rally his attention. As he looked at Carton
ham	with clouded eyes and with an altered manner of breathing, Carton--his
ham	hand again in his breast--looked steadily at him.
ham	"Hurry, hurry!"
ham	The prisoner bent over the paper, once more.
spam	"'If it had been otherwise;'" Carton's hand was again watchfully and
spam	softly stealing down; "'I never should have used the longer opportunity.
spam	If it had been otherwise;'" the hand was at the prisoner's face; "'I
ham	should but have had so much the more to answer for. If it had been
spam	otherwise--'" Carton looked at the pen and saw it was trailing off into
spam	unintelligible signs.
ham	Carton's hand moved back to his breast no more. The prisoner sprang up
spam	with a reproachful look, but Carton's hand was close and firm at his
ham	nostrils, and Carton's left arm caught him round the waist. For a few
spam	seconds he faintly struggled with the man who had come to lay down his
spam	life for him; but, within a minute or so, he was stretched insensible on
ham	the ground.
ham	Quickly, but with hands as true to the purpose as his heart was, Carton
ham	dressed himself in the clothes the prisoner had laid aside, combed back
spam	his hair, and tied it with the ribbon the prisoner had worn. Then, he
spam	softly called, "Enter there! Come in!" and the Spy presented himself.
ham	"You see?" said Carton, looking up, as he kneeled on one knee beside the
spam	insensible figure, putting the paper in the breast: "is your hazard very
spam	great?"
spam	"Mr. Carton," the Spy answered, with a timid snap of his fingers, "my
ham	hazard is not _that_, in the thick of business here, if you are true to
ham	the whole of your bargain."
ham	"Don't fear me. I will be true to the death."
spam	"You must be, Mr. Carton, if the tale of fifty-two is to be right. Being
spam	made right by you in that dress, I shall have no fear."
ham	"Have no fear! I shall soon be out of the way of harming you, and the
spam	rest will soon be far from here, please God! Now, get assistance and
ham	take me to the coach."
ham	"You?" said the Spy nervously.
spam	"Him, man, with whom I have exchanged. You go out at the gate by which
ham	you brought me in?"
ham	"Of course."
spam	"I was weak and faint when you brought me in, and I am fainter now you
ham	take me out. The parting interview has overpowered me. Such a thing has
spam	happened here, often, and too often. Your life is in your own hands.
ham	Quick! Call assistance!"
ham	"You swear not to betray me?" said the trembling Spy, as he paused for a
spam	last moment.
ham	"Man, man!" returned Carton, stamping his foot; "have I sworn by no
spam	solemn vow already, to go through with this, that you waste the precious
spam	moments now? Take him yourself to the courtyard you know of, place
spam	him yourself in the carriage, show him yourself to Mr. Lorry, tell him
spam	yourself to give him no restorative but air, and to remember my words of
spam	last night, and his promise of last night, and drive away!"
spam	The Spy withdrew, and Carton seated himself at the table, resting his
spam	forehead on his hands. The Spy returned immediately, with two men.
ham	"How, then?" said one of them, contemplating the fallen figure. "So
spam	afflicted to find that his friend has drawn a prize in the lottery of
spam	Sainte Guillotine?"
ham	"A good patriot," said the other, "could hardly have been more afflicted
ham	if the Aristocrat had drawn a blank."
ham	They raised the unconscious figure, placed it on a litter they had
spam	brought to the door, and bent to carry it away.
spam	"The time is short, Evremonde," said the Spy, in a warning voice.
ham	"I know it well," answered Carton. "Be careful of my friend, I entreat
ham	you, and leave me."
ham	"Come, then, my children," said Barsad. "Lift him, and come away!"
ham	The door closed, and Carton was left alone. Straining his powers of
spam	listening to the utmost, he listened for any sound that might denote
spam	suspicion or alarm. There was none. Keys turned, doors clashed,
spam	footsteps passed along distant passages: no cry was raised, or hurry
ham	made, that seemed unusual. Breathing more freely in a little while, he
spam	sat down at the table, and listened again until the clock struck Two.
spam	Sounds that he was not afraid of, for he divined their meaning, then
ham	began to be audible. Several doors were opened in succession, and
ham	finally his own. A gaoler, with a list in his hand, looked in, merely
spam	saying, "Follow me, Evremonde!" and he followed into a large dark room,
spam	at a distance. It was a dark winter day, and what with the shadows
ham	within, and what with the shadows without, he could but dimly discern
spam	the others who were brought there to have their arms bound. Some were
ham	standing; some seated. Some were lamenting, and in restless motion;
spam	but, these were few. The great majority were silent and still, looking
ham	fixedly at the ground.
ham	As he stood by the wall in a dim corner, while some of the fifty-two
spam	were brought in after him, one man stopped in passing, to embrace him,
ham	as having a knowledge of him. It thrilled him with a great dread of
spam	discovery; but the man went on. A very few moments after that, a young
ham	woman, with a slight girlish form, a sweet spare face in which there was
ham	no vestige of colour, and large widely opened patient eyes, rose from
ham	the seat where he had observed her sitting, and came to speak to him.
ham	"Citizen Evremonde," she said, touching him with her cold hand. "I am a
ham	poor little seamstress, who was with you in La Force."
spam	He murmured for answer: "True. I forget what you were accused of?"
spam	"Plots. Though the just Heaven knows that I am innocent of any. Is it
ham	likely? Who would think of plotting with a poor little weak creature
spam	like me?"
spam	The forlorn smile with which she said it, so touched him, that tears
ham	started from his eyes.
spam	"I am not afraid to die, Citizen Evremonde, but I have done nothing. I
spam	am not unwilling to die, if the Republic which is to do so much good
spam	to us poor, will profit by my death; but I do not know how that can be,
ham	Citizen Evremonde. Such a poor weak little creature!"
spam	As the last thing on earth that his heart was to warm and soften to, it
ham	warmed and softened to this pitiable girl.
spam	"I heard you were released, Citizen Evremonde. I hoped it was true?"
ham	"It was. But, I was again taken and condemned."
ham	"If I may ride with you, Citizen Evremonde, will you let me hold your
ham	hand? I am not afraid, but I am little and weak, and it will give me
spam	more courage."
spam	As the patient eyes were lifted to his face, he saw a sudden doubt in
ham	them, and then astonishment. He pressed the work-worn, hunger-worn young
spam	fingers, and touched his lips.
spam	"Are you dying for him?" she whispered.
ham	"And his wife and child. Hush! Yes."
ham	"O you will let me hold your brave hand, stranger?"
ham	"Hush! Yes, my poor sister; to the last."
ham	        *****
spam	The same shadows that are falling on the prison, are falling, in that
ham	same hour of the early afternoon, on the Barrier with the crowd about
ham	it, when a coach going out of Paris drives up to be examined.
ham	"Who goes here? Whom have we within? Papers!"
ham	The papers are handed out, and read.
ham	"Alexandre Manette. Physician. French. Which is he?"
spam	This is he; this helpless, inarticulately murmuring, wandering old man
ham	pointed out.
ham	"Apparently the Citizen-Doctor is not in his right mind? The
ham	Revolution-fever will have been too much for him?"
spam	Greatly too much for him.
ham	"Hah! Many suffer with it. Lucie. His daughter. French. Which is she?"
spam	This is she.
spam	"Apparently it must be. Lucie, the wife of Evremonde; is it not?"
ham	It is.
ham	"Hah! Evremonde has an assignation elsewhere. Lucie, her child. English.
spam	This is she?"
spam	She and no other.
ham	"Kiss me, child of Evremonde. Now, thou hast kissed a good Republican;
spam	something new in thy family; remember it! Sydney Carton. Advocate.
ham	English. Which is he?"
ham	He lies here, in this corner of the carriage. He, too, is pointed out.
ham	"Apparently the English advocate is in a swoon?"
ham	It is hoped he will recover in the fresher air. It is represented that
ham	he is not in strong health, and has separated sadly from a friend who is
spam	under the displeasure of the Republic.
ham	"Is that all? It is not a great deal, that! Many are under the
spam	displeasure of the Republic, and must look out at the little window.
ham	Jarvis Lorry. Banker. English. Which is he?"
ham	"I am he. Necessarily, being the last."
spam	It is Jarvis Lorry who has replied to all the previous questions. It
spam	is Jarvis Lorry who has alighted and stands with his hand on the coach
ham	door, replying to a group of officials. They leisurely walk round the
ham	carriage and leisurely mount the box, to look at what little luggage it
spam	carries on the roof; the country-people hanging about, press nearer to
ham	the coach doors and greedily stare in; a little child, carried by its
ham	mother, has its short arm held out for it, that it may touch the wife of
spam	an aristocrat who has gone to the Guillotine.
ham	"Behold your papers, Jarvis Lorry, countersigned."
ham	"One can depart, citizen?"
ham	"One can depart. Forward, my postilions! A good journey!"
spam	"I salute you, citizens.--And the first danger passed!"
spam	These are again the words of Jarvis Lorry, as he clasps his hands, and
ham	looks upward. There is terror in the carriage, there is weeping, there
spam	is the heavy breathing of the insensible traveller.
spam	"Are we not going too slowly? Can they not be induced to go faster?"
spam	asks Lucie, clinging to the old man.
spam	"It would seem like flight, my darling. I must not urge them too much;
ham	it would rouse suspicion."
ham	"Look back, look back, and see if we are pursued!"
ham	"The road is clear, my dearest. So far, we are not pursued."
ham	Houses in twos and threes pass by us, solitary farms, ruinous buildings,
spam	dye-works, tanneries, and the like, open country, avenues of leafless
ham	trees. The hard uneven pavement is under us, the soft deep mud is on
spam	either side. Sometimes, we strike into the skirting mud, to avoid the
ham	stones that clatter us and shake us; sometimes, we stick in ruts and
ham	sloughs there. The agony of our impatience is then so great, that in our
ham	wild alarm and hurry we are for getting out and running--hiding--doing
spam	anything but stopping.
spam	Out of the open country, in again among ruinous buildings, solitary
ham	farms, dye-works, tanneries, and the like, cottages in twos and threes,
spam	avenues of leafless trees. Have these men deceived us, and taken us back
ham	by another road? Is not this the same place twice over? Thank Heaven,
ham	no. A village. Look back, look back, and see if we are pursued! Hush!
ham	the posting-house.
ham	Leisurely, our four horses are taken out; leisurely, the coach stands in
ham	the little street, bereft of horses, and with no likelihood upon it
ham	of ever moving again; leisurely, the new horses come into visible
ham	existence, one by one; leisurely, the new postilions follow, sucking and
ham	plaiting the lashes of their whips; leisurely, the old postilions count
ham	their money, make wrong additions, and arrive at dissatisfied results.
spam	All the time, our overfraught hearts are beating at a rate that would
ham	far outstrip the fastest gallop of the fastest horses ever foaled.
ham	At length the new postilions are in their saddles, and the old are left
spam	behind. We are through the village, up the hill, and down the hill, and
ham	on the low watery grounds. Suddenly, the postilions exchange speech with
ham	animated gesticulation, and the horses are pulled up, almost on their
spam	haunches. We are pursued?
ham	"Ho! Within the carriage there. Speak then!"
spam	"What is it?" asks Mr. Lorry, looking out at window.
spam	"How many did they say?"
spam	"I do not understand you."
ham	"--At the last post. How many to the Guillotine to-day?"
ham	"Fifty-two."
ham	"I said so! A brave number! My fellow-citizen here would have it
ham	forty-two; ten more heads are worth having. The Guillotine goes
spam	handsomely. I love it. Hi forward. Whoop!"
ham	The night comes on dark. He moves more; he is beginning to revive, and
spam	to speak intelligibly; he thinks they are still together; he asks him,
spam	by his name, what he has in his hand. O pity us, kind Heaven, and help
spam	us! Look out, look out, and see if we are pursued.
ham	The wind is rushing after us, and the clouds are flying after us, and
ham	the moon is plunging after us, and the whole wild night is in pursuit of
ham	us; but, so far, we are pursued by nothing else.
ham	XIV. The Knitting Done
spam	In that same juncture of time when the Fifty-Two awaited their fate
ham	Madame Defarge held darkly ominous council with The Vengeance and
ham	Jacques Three of the Revolutionary Jury. Not in the wine-shop did Madame
spam	Defarge confer with these ministers, but in the shed of the wood-sawyer,
ham	erst a mender of roads. The sawyer himself did not participate in the
ham	conference, but abided at a little distance, like an outer satellite who
spam	was not to speak until required, or to offer an opinion until invited.
ham	"But our Defarge," said Jacques Three, "is undoubtedly a good
ham	Republican? Eh?"
spam	"There is no better," the voluble Vengeance protested in her shrill
ham	notes, "in France."
spam	"Peace, little Vengeance," said Madame Defarge, laying her hand with
spam	a slight frown on her lieutenant's lips, "hear me speak. My husband,
spam	fellow-citizen, is a good Republican and a bold man; he has deserved
spam	well of the Republic, and possesses its confidence. But my husband has
spam	his weaknesses, and he is so weak as to relent towards this Doctor."
spam	"It is a great pity," croaked Jacques Three, dubiously shaking his head,
ham	with his cruel fingers at his hungry mouth; "it is not quite like a good
spam	citizen; it is a thing to regret."
ham	"See you," said madame, "I care nothing for this Doctor, I. He may wear
spam	his head or lose it, for any interest I have in him; it is all one to
ham	me. But, the Evremonde people are to be exterminated, and the wife and
ham	child must follow the husband and father."
spam	"She has a fine head for it," croaked Jacques Three. "I have seen blue
ham	eyes and golden hair there, and they looked charming when Samson held
ham	them up." Ogre that he was, he spoke like an epicure.
ham	Madame Defarge cast down her eyes, and reflected a little.
ham	"The child also," observed Jacques Three, with a meditative enjoyment
ham	of his words, "has golden hair and blue eyes. And we seldom have a child
ham	there. It is a pretty sight!"
ham	"In a word," said Madame Defarge, coming out of her short abstraction,
ham	"I cannot trust my husband in this matter. Not only do I feel, since
spam	last night, that I dare not confide to him the details of my projects;
ham	but also I feel that if I delay, there is danger of his giving warning,
spam	and then they might escape."
ham	"That must never be," croaked Jacques Three; "no one must escape. We
ham	have not half enough as it is. We ought to have six score a day."
spam	"In a word," Madame Defarge went on, "my husband has not my reason for
spam	pursuing this family to annihilation, and I have not his reason for
spam	regarding this Doctor with any sensibility. I must act for myself,
ham	therefore. Come hither, little citizen."
ham	The wood-sawyer, who held her in the respect, and himself in the
spam	submission, of mortal fear, advanced with his hand to his red cap.
spam	"Touching those signals, little citizen," said Madame Defarge, sternly,
ham	"that she made to the prisoners; you are ready to bear witness to them
ham	this very day?"
ham	"Ay, ay, why not!" cried the sawyer. "Every day, in all weathers, from
spam	two to four, always signalling, sometimes with the little one, sometimes
spam	without. I know what I know. I have seen with my eyes."
spam	He made all manner of gestures while he spoke, as if in incidental
spam	imitation of some few of the great diversity of signals that he had
ham	never seen.
ham	"Clearly plots," said Jacques Three. "Transparently!"
spam	"There is no doubt of the Jury?" inquired Madame Defarge, letting her
ham	eyes turn to him with a gloomy smile.
spam	"Rely upon the patriotic Jury, dear citizeness. I answer for my
spam	fellow-Jurymen."
ham	"Now, let me see," said Madame Defarge, pondering again. "Yet once more!
ham	Can I spare this Doctor to my husband? I have no feeling either way. Can
spam	I spare him?"
spam	"He would count as one head," observed Jacques Three, in a low voice.
ham	"We really have not heads enough; it would be a pity, I think."
spam	"He was signalling with her when I saw her," argued Madame Defarge; "I
spam	cannot speak of one without the other; and I must not be silent, and
ham	trust the case wholly to him, this little citizen here. For, I am not a
spam	bad witness."
spam	The Vengeance and Jacques Three vied with each other in their fervent
ham	protestations that she was the most admirable and marvellous of
spam	witnesses. The little citizen, not to be outdone, declared her to be a
spam	celestial witness.
spam	"He must take his chance," said Madame Defarge. "No, I cannot spare
ham	him! You are engaged at three o'clock; you are going to see the batch of
spam	to-day executed.--You?"
spam	The question was addressed to the wood-sawyer, who hurriedly replied in
spam	the affirmative: seizing the occasion to add that he was the most ardent
ham	of Republicans, and that he would be in effect the most desolate of
spam	Republicans, if anything prevented him from enjoying the pleasure of
spam	smoking his afternoon pipe in the contemplation of the droll national
ham	barber. He was so very demonstrative herein, that he might have been
spam	suspected (perhaps was, by the dark eyes that looked contemptuously at
ham	him out of Madame Defarge's head) of having his small individual fears
spam	for his own personal safety, every hour in the day.
spam	"I," said madame, "am equally engaged at the same place. After it is
ham	over--say at eight to-night--come you to me, in Saint Antoine, and we
spam	will give information against these people at my Section."
ham	The wood-sawyer said he would be proud and flattered to attend the
ham	citizeness. The citizeness looking at him, he became embarrassed, evaded
spam	her glance as a small dog would have done, retreated among his wood, and
spam	hid his confusion over the handle of his saw.
ham	Madame Defarge beckoned the Juryman and The Vengeance a little nearer to
ham	the door, and there expounded her further views to them thus:
ham	"She will now be at home, awaiting the moment of his death. She will
spam	be mourning and grieving. She will be in a state of mind to impeach the
spam	justice of the Republic. She will be full of sympathy with its enemies.
ham	I will go to her."
ham	"What an admirable woman; what an adorable woman!" exclaimed Jacques
ham	Three, rapturously. "Ah, my cherished!" cried The Vengeance; and
spam	embraced her.
ham	"Take you my knitting," said Madame Defarge, placing it in her
spam	lieutenant's hands, "and have it ready for me in my usual seat. Keep
spam	me my usual chair. Go you there, straight, for there will probably be a
ham	greater concourse than usual, to-day."
ham	"I willingly obey the orders of my Chief," said The Vengeance with
spam	alacrity, and kissing her cheek. "You will not be late?"
ham	"I shall be there before the commencement."
ham	"And before the tumbrils arrive. Be sure you are there, my soul," said
ham	The Vengeance, calling after her, for she had already turned into the
ham	street, "before the tumbrils arrive!"
ham	Madame Defarge slightly waved her hand, to imply that she heard, and
spam	might be relied upon to arrive in good time, and so went through the
spam	mud, and round the corner of the prison wall. The Vengeance and the
ham	Juryman, looking after her as she walked away, were highly appreciative
spam	of her fine figure, and her superb moral endowments.
spam	There were many women at that time, upon whom the time laid a dreadfully
spam	disfiguring hand; but, there was not one among them more to be dreaded
spam	than this ruthless woman, now taking her way along the streets. Of a
ham	strong and fearless character, of shrewd sense and readiness, of great
ham	determination, of that kind of beauty which not only seems to impart
ham	to its possessor firmness and animosity, but to strike into others an
ham	instinctive recognition of those qualities; the troubled time would have
ham	heaved her up, under any circumstances. But, imbued from her childhood
spam	with a brooding sense of wrong, and an inveterate hatred of a class,
spam	opportunity had developed her into a tigress. She was absolutely without
ham	pity. If she had ever had the virtue in her, it had quite gone out of
spam	her.
ham	It was nothing to her, that an innocent man was to die for the sins of
ham	his forefathers; she saw, not him, but them. It was nothing to her, that
ham	his wife was to be made a widow and his daughter an orphan; that was
ham	insufficient punishment, because they were her natural enemies and
spam	her prey, and as such had no right to live. To appeal to her, was made
spam	hopeless by her having no sense of pity, even for herself. If she had
ham	been laid low in the streets, in any of the many encounters in which
ham	she had been engaged, she would not have pitied herself; nor, if she had
spam	been ordered to the axe to-morrow, would she have gone to it with any
spam	softer feeling than a fierce desire to change places with the man who
spam	sent her there.
spam	Such a heart Madame Defarge carried under her rough robe. Carelessly
spam	worn, it was a becoming robe enough, in a certain weird way, and her
spam	dark hair looked rich under her coarse red cap. Lying hidden in her
spam	bosom, was a loaded pistol. Lying hidden at her waist, was a sharpened
ham	dagger. Thus accoutred, and walking with the confident tread of such
ham	a character, and with the supple freedom of a woman who had habitually
ham	walked in her girlhood, bare-foot and bare-legged, on the brown
ham	sea-sand, Madame Defarge took her way along the streets.
spam	Now, when the journey of the travelling coach, at that very moment
ham	waiting for the completion of its load, had been planned out last night,
ham	the difficulty of taking Miss Pross in it had much engaged Mr. Lorry's
ham	attention. It was not merely desirable to avoid overloading the coach,
ham	but it was of the highest importance that the time occupied in examining
spam	it and its passengers, should be reduced to the utmost; since their
ham	escape might depend on the saving of only a few seconds here and there.
ham	Finally, he had proposed, after anxious consideration, that Miss Pross
spam	and Jerry, who were at liberty to leave the city, should leave it at
ham	three o'clock in the lightest-wheeled conveyance known to that period.
spam	Unencumbered with luggage, they would soon overtake the coach, and,
spam	passing it and preceding it on the road, would order its horses in
spam	advance, and greatly facilitate its progress during the precious hours
ham	of the night, when delay was the most to be dreaded.
spam	Seeing in this arrangement the hope of rendering real service in that
spam	pressing emergency, Miss Pross hailed it with joy. She and Jerry had
spam	beheld the coach start, had known who it was that Solomon brought, had
spam	passed some ten minutes in tortures of suspense, and were now concluding
ham	their arrangements to follow the coach, even as Madame Defarge,
ham	taking her way through the streets, now drew nearer and nearer to the
ham	else-deserted lodging in which they held their consultation.
spam	"Now what do you think, Mr. Cruncher," said Miss Pross, whose agitation
ham	was so great that she could hardly speak, or stand, or move, or live:
ham	"what do you think of our not starting from this courtyard? Another
spam	carriage having already gone from here to-day, it might awaken
spam	suspicion."
ham	"My opinion, miss," returned Mr. Cruncher, "is as you're right. Likewise
spam	wot I'll stand by you, right or wrong."
spam	"I am so distracted with fear and hope for our precious creatures," said
ham	Miss Pross, wildly crying, "that I am incapable of forming any plan. Are
spam	_you_ capable of forming any plan, my dear good Mr. Cruncher?"
spam	"Respectin' a future spear o' life, miss," returned Mr. Cruncher, "I
ham	hope so. Respectin' any present use o' this here blessed old head o'
ham	mine, I think not. Would you do me the favour, miss, to take notice o'
spam	two promises and wows wot it is my wishes fur to record in this here
spam	crisis?"
spam	"Oh, for gracious sake!" cried Miss Pross, still wildly crying, "record
ham	them at once, and get them out of the way, like an excellent man."
ham	"First," said Mr. Cruncher, who was all in a tremble, and who spoke with
spam	an ashy and solemn visage, "them poor things well out o' this, never no
ham	more will I do it, never no more!"
spam	"I am quite sure, Mr. Cruncher," returned Miss Pross, "that you
spam	never will do it again, whatever it is, and I beg you not to think it
spam	necessary to mention more particularly what it is."
spam	"No, miss," returned Jerry, "it shall not be named to you. Second: them
spam	poor things well out o' this, and never no more will I interfere with
ham	Mrs. Cruncher's flopping, never no more!"
ham	"Whatever housekeeping arrangement that may be," said Miss Pross,
ham	striving to dry her eyes and compose herself, "I have no doubt it
ham	is best that Mrs. Cruncher should have it entirely under her own
ham	superintendence.--O my poor darlings!"
spam	"I go so far as to say, miss, moreover," proceeded Mr. Cruncher, with a
spam	most alarming tendency to hold forth as from a pulpit--"and let my words
spam	be took down and took to Mrs. Cruncher through yourself--that wot my
spam	opinions respectin' flopping has undergone a change, and that wot I only
ham	hope with all my heart as Mrs. Cruncher may be a flopping at the present
ham	time."
spam	"There, there, there! I hope she is, my dear man," cried the distracted
spam	Miss Pross, "and I hope she finds it answering her expectations."
ham	"Forbid it," proceeded Mr. Cruncher, with additional solemnity,
spam	additional slowness, and additional tendency to hold forth and hold
spam	out, "as anything wot I have ever said or done should be wisited on my
spam	earnest wishes for them poor creeturs now! Forbid it as we shouldn't all
ham	flop (if it was anyways conwenient) to get 'em out o' this here dismal
ham	risk! Forbid it, miss! Wot I say, for-_bid_ it!" This was Mr. Cruncher's
ham	conclusion after a protracted but vain endeavour to find a better one.
ham	And still Madame Defarge, pursuing her way along the streets, came
ham	nearer and nearer.
ham	"If we ever get back to our native land," said Miss Pross, "you may rely
spam	upon my telling Mrs. Cruncher as much as I may be able to remember and
spam	understand of what you have so impressively said; and at all events
ham	you may be sure that I shall bear witness to your being thoroughly in
ham	earnest at this dreadful time. Now, pray let us think! My esteemed Mr.
spam	Cruncher, let us think!"
ham	Still, Madame Defarge, pursuing her way along the streets, came nearer
spam	and nearer.
ham	"If you were to go before," said Miss Pross, "and stop the vehicle and
spam	horses from coming here, and were to wait somewhere for me; wouldn't
ham	that be best?"
ham	Mr. Cruncher thought it might be best.
spam	"Where could you wait for me?" asked Miss Pross.
ham	Mr. Cruncher was so bewildered that he could think of no locality but
spam	Temple Bar. Alas! Temple Bar was hundreds of miles away, and Madame
ham	Defarge was drawing very near indeed.
ham	"By the cathedral door," said Miss Pross. "Would it be much out of
ham	the way, to take me in, near the great cathedral door between the two
ham	towers?"
ham	"No, miss," answered Mr. Cruncher.
spam	"Then, like the best of men," said Miss Pross, "go to the posting-house
ham	straight, and make that change."
spam	"I am doubtful," said Mr. Cruncher, hesitating and shaking his head,
ham	"about leaving of you, you see. We don't know what may happen."
spam	"Heaven knows we don't," returned Miss Pross, "but have no fear for me.
spam	Take me in at the cathedral, at Three o'Clock, or as near it as you can,
ham	and I am sure it will be better than our going from here. I feel certain
spam	of it. There! Bless you, Mr. Cruncher! Think-not of me, but of the lives
ham	that may depend on both of us!"
spam	This exordium, and Miss Pross's two hands in quite agonised entreaty
spam	clasping his, decided Mr. Cruncher. With an encouraging nod or two, he
ham	immediately went out to alter the arrangements, and left her by herself
ham	to follow as she had proposed.
spam	The having originated a precaution which was already in course of
ham	execution, was a great relief to Miss Pross. The necessity of composing
spam	her appearance so that it should attract no special notice in the
spam	streets, was another relief. She looked at her watch, and it was twenty
spam	minutes past two. She had no time to lose, but must get ready at once.
ham	Afraid, in her extreme perturbation, of the loneliness of the deserted
spam	rooms, and of half-imagined faces peeping from behind every open door
