spam	in them, Miss Pross got a basin of cold water and began laving her eyes,
spam	which were swollen and red. Haunted by her feverish apprehensions, she
spam	could not bear to have her sight obscured for a minute at a time by the
ham	dripping water, but constantly paused and looked round to see that there
ham	was no one watching her. In one of those pauses she recoiled and cried
ham	out, for she saw a figure standing in the room.
ham	The basin fell to the ground broken, and the water flowed to the feet of
ham	Madame Defarge. By strange stern ways, and through much staining blood,
ham	those feet had come to meet that water.
spam	Madame Defarge looked coldly at her, and said, "The wife of Evremonde;
spam	where is she?"
ham	It flashed upon Miss Pross's mind that the doors were all standing open,
spam	and would suggest the flight. Her first act was to shut them. There were
ham	four in the room, and she shut them all. She then placed herself before
ham	the door of the chamber which Lucie had occupied.
spam	Madame Defarge's dark eyes followed her through this rapid movement,
spam	and rested on her when it was finished. Miss Pross had nothing beautiful
ham	about her; years had not tamed the wildness, or softened the grimness,
ham	of her appearance; but, she too was a determined woman in her different
ham	way, and she measured Madame Defarge with her eyes, every inch.
ham	"You might, from your appearance, be the wife of Lucifer," said Miss
spam	Pross, in her breathing. "Nevertheless, you shall not get the better of
ham	me. I am an Englishwoman."
ham	Madame Defarge looked at her scornfully, but still with something of
spam	Miss Pross's own perception that they two were at bay. She saw a tight,
ham	hard, wiry woman before her, as Mr. Lorry had seen in the same figure a
spam	woman with a strong hand, in the years gone by. She knew full well that
spam	Miss Pross was the family's devoted friend; Miss Pross knew full well
spam	that Madame Defarge was the family's malevolent enemy.
ham	"On my way yonder," said Madame Defarge, with a slight movement of
spam	her hand towards the fatal spot, "where they reserve my chair and my
spam	knitting for me, I am come to make my compliments to her in passing. I
ham	wish to see her."
spam	"I know that your intentions are evil," said Miss Pross, "and you may
ham	depend upon it, I'll hold my own against them."
spam	Each spoke in her own language; neither understood the other's words;
spam	both were very watchful, and intent to deduce from look and manner, what
ham	the unintelligible words meant.
ham	"It will do her no good to keep herself concealed from me at this
spam	moment," said Madame Defarge. "Good patriots will know what that means.
ham	Let me see her. Go tell her that I wish to see her. Do you hear?"
ham	"If those eyes of yours were bed-winches," returned Miss Pross, "and I
spam	was an English four-poster, they shouldn't loose a splinter of me. No,
ham	you wicked foreign woman; I am your match."
spam	Madame Defarge was not likely to follow these idiomatic remarks in
spam	detail; but, she so far understood them as to perceive that she was set
spam	at naught.
spam	"Woman imbecile and pig-like!" said Madame Defarge, frowning. "I take no
ham	answer from you. I demand to see her. Either tell her that I demand
spam	to see her, or stand out of the way of the door and let me go to her!"
ham	This, with an angry explanatory wave of her right arm.
spam	"I little thought," said Miss Pross, "that I should ever want to
spam	understand your nonsensical language; but I would give all I have,
ham	except the clothes I wear, to know whether you suspect the truth, or any
spam	part of it."
ham	Neither of them for a single moment released the other's eyes. Madame
ham	Defarge had not moved from the spot where she stood when Miss Pross
ham	first became aware of her; but, she now advanced one step.
ham	"I am a Briton," said Miss Pross, "I am desperate. I don't care an
spam	English Twopence for myself. I know that the longer I keep you here, the
ham	greater hope there is for my Ladybird. I'll not leave a handful of that
spam	dark hair upon your head, if you lay a finger on me!"
spam	Thus Miss Pross, with a shake of her head and a flash of her eyes
ham	between every rapid sentence, and every rapid sentence a whole breath.
ham	Thus Miss Pross, who had never struck a blow in her life.
ham	But, her courage was of that emotional nature that it brought the
spam	irrepressible tears into her eyes. This was a courage that Madame
ham	Defarge so little comprehended as to mistake for weakness. "Ha, ha!" she
spam	laughed, "you poor wretch! What are you worth! I address myself to that
ham	Doctor." Then she raised her voice and called out, "Citizen Doctor! Wife
ham	of Evremonde! Child of Evremonde! Any person but this miserable fool,
spam	answer the Citizeness Defarge!"
spam	Perhaps the following silence, perhaps some latent disclosure in the
spam	expression of Miss Pross's face, perhaps a sudden misgiving apart from
spam	either suggestion, whispered to Madame Defarge that they were gone.
spam	Three of the doors she opened swiftly, and looked in.
spam	"Those rooms are all in disorder, there has been hurried packing, there
ham	are odds and ends upon the ground. There is no one in that room behind
ham	you! Let me look."
spam	"Never!" said Miss Pross, who understood the request as perfectly as
spam	Madame Defarge understood the answer.
ham	"If they are not in that room, they are gone, and can be pursued and
spam	brought back," said Madame Defarge to herself.
ham	"As long as you don't know whether they are in that room or not, you are
spam	uncertain what to do," said Miss Pross to herself; "and you shall not
spam	know that, if I can prevent your knowing it; and know that, or not know
ham	that, you shall not leave here while I can hold you."
spam	"I have been in the streets from the first, nothing has stopped me,
ham	I will tear you to pieces, but I will have you from that door," said
spam	Madame Defarge.
ham	"We are alone at the top of a high house in a solitary courtyard, we are
ham	not likely to be heard, and I pray for bodily strength to keep you here,
spam	while every minute you are here is worth a hundred thousand guineas to
spam	my darling," said Miss Pross.
ham	Madame Defarge made at the door. Miss Pross, on the instinct of the
ham	moment, seized her round the waist in both her arms, and held her tight.
ham	It was in vain for Madame Defarge to struggle and to strike; Miss Pross,
spam	with the vigorous tenacity of love, always so much stronger than hate,
ham	clasped her tight, and even lifted her from the floor in the struggle
spam	that they had. The two hands of Madame Defarge buffeted and tore her
ham	face; but, Miss Pross, with her head down, held her round the waist, and
ham	clung to her with more than the hold of a drowning woman.
ham	Soon, Madame Defarge's hands ceased to strike, and felt at her encircled
ham	waist. "It is under my arm," said Miss Pross, in smothered tones, "you
ham	shall not draw it. I am stronger than you, I bless Heaven for it. I hold
spam	you till one or other of us faints or dies!"
spam	Madame Defarge's hands were at her bosom. Miss Pross looked up, saw
spam	what it was, struck at it, struck out a flash and a crash, and stood
spam	alone--blinded with smoke.
ham	All this was in a second. As the smoke cleared, leaving an awful
ham	stillness, it passed out on the air, like the soul of the furious woman
ham	whose body lay lifeless on the ground.
ham	In the first fright and horror of her situation, Miss Pross passed the
spam	body as far from it as she could, and ran down the stairs to call for
spam	fruitless help. Happily, she bethought herself of the consequences of
ham	what she did, in time to check herself and go back. It was dreadful to
spam	go in at the door again; but, she did go in, and even went near it, to
spam	get the bonnet and other things that she must wear. These she put on,
spam	out on the staircase, first shutting and locking the door and taking
spam	away the key. She then sat down on the stairs a few moments to breathe
ham	and to cry, and then got up and hurried away.
spam	By good fortune she had a veil on her bonnet, or she could hardly have
spam	gone along the streets without being stopped. By good fortune, too, she
spam	was naturally so peculiar in appearance as not to show disfigurement
ham	like any other woman. She needed both advantages, for the marks of
ham	gripping fingers were deep in her face, and her hair was torn, and her
ham	dress (hastily composed with unsteady hands) was clutched and dragged a
ham	hundred ways.
ham	In crossing the bridge, she dropped the door key in the river. Arriving
spam	at the cathedral some few minutes before her escort, and waiting there,
spam	she thought, what if the key were already taken in a net, what if
ham	it were identified, what if the door were opened and the remains
ham	discovered, what if she were stopped at the gate, sent to prison, and
spam	charged with murder! In the midst of these fluttering thoughts, the
ham	escort appeared, took her in, and took her away.
ham	"Is there any noise in the streets?" she asked him.
ham	"The usual noises," Mr. Cruncher replied; and looked surprised by the
spam	question and by her aspect.
ham	"I don't hear you," said Miss Pross. "What do you say?"
spam	It was in vain for Mr. Cruncher to repeat what he said; Miss Pross could
spam	not hear him. "So I'll nod my head," thought Mr. Cruncher, amazed, "at
ham	all events she'll see that." And she did.
spam	"Is there any noise in the streets now?" asked Miss Pross again,
spam	presently.
ham	Again Mr. Cruncher nodded his head.
ham	"I don't hear it."
ham	"Gone deaf in an hour?" said Mr. Cruncher, ruminating, with his mind
ham	much disturbed; "wot's come to her?"
spam	"I feel," said Miss Pross, "as if there had been a flash and a crash,
ham	and that crash was the last thing I should ever hear in this life."
spam	"Blest if she ain't in a queer condition!" said Mr. Cruncher, more and
ham	more disturbed. "Wot can she have been a takin', to keep her courage up?
spam	Hark! There's the roll of them dreadful carts! You can hear that, miss?"
ham	"I can hear," said Miss Pross, seeing that he spoke to her, "nothing. O,
ham	my good man, there was first a great crash, and then a great stillness,
spam	and that stillness seems to be fixed and unchangeable, never to be
spam	broken any more as long as my life lasts."
spam	"If she don't hear the roll of those dreadful carts, now very nigh their
ham	journey's end," said Mr. Cruncher, glancing over his shoulder, "it's my
ham	opinion that indeed she never will hear anything else in this world."
ham	And indeed she never did.
ham	XV. The Footsteps Die Out For Ever
spam	Along the Paris streets, the death-carts rumble, hollow and harsh. Six
spam	tumbrils carry the day's wine to La Guillotine. All the devouring and
spam	insatiate Monsters imagined since imagination could record itself,
ham	are fused in the one realisation, Guillotine. And yet there is not in
spam	France, with its rich variety of soil and climate, a blade, a leaf,
spam	a root, a sprig, a peppercorn, which will grow to maturity under
spam	conditions more certain than those that have produced this horror. Crush
ham	humanity out of shape once more, under similar hammers, and it will
ham	twist itself into the same tortured forms. Sow the same seed of
spam	rapacious license and oppression over again, and it will surely yield
ham	the same fruit according to its kind.
ham	Six tumbrils roll along the streets. Change these back again to what
spam	they were, thou powerful enchanter, Time, and they shall be seen to be
ham	the carriages of absolute monarchs, the equipages of feudal nobles, the
ham	toilettes of flaring Jezebels, the churches that are not my father's
ham	house but dens of thieves, the huts of millions of starving peasants!
ham	No; the great magician who majestically works out the appointed order
ham	of the Creator, never reverses his transformations. "If thou be changed
spam	into this shape by the will of God," say the seers to the enchanted, in
spam	the wise Arabian stories, "then remain so! But, if thou wear this
spam	form through mere passing conjuration, then resume thy former aspect!"
ham	Changeless and hopeless, the tumbrils roll along.
spam	As the sombre wheels of the six carts go round, they seem to plough up
spam	a long crooked furrow among the populace in the streets. Ridges of faces
ham	are thrown to this side and to that, and the ploughs go steadily onward.
spam	So used are the regular inhabitants of the houses to the spectacle, that
ham	in many windows there are no people, and in some the occupation of the
spam	hands is not so much as suspended, while the eyes survey the faces in
spam	the tumbrils. Here and there, the inmate has visitors to see the sight;
ham	then he points his finger, with something of the complacency of a
spam	curator or authorised exponent, to this cart and to this, and seems to
spam	tell who sat here yesterday, and who there the day before.
ham	Of the riders in the tumbrils, some observe these things, and all
ham	things on their last roadside, with an impassive stare; others, with
ham	a lingering interest in the ways of life and men. Some, seated with
ham	drooping heads, are sunk in silent despair; again, there are some so
spam	heedful of their looks that they cast upon the multitude such glances as
spam	they have seen in theatres, and in pictures. Several close their eyes,
spam	and think, or try to get their straying thoughts together. Only one, and
ham	he a miserable creature, of a crazed aspect, is so shattered and made
ham	drunk by horror, that he sings, and tries to dance. Not one of the whole
ham	number appeals by look or gesture, to the pity of the people.
ham	There is a guard of sundry horsemen riding abreast of the tumbrils,
ham	and faces are often turned up to some of them, and they are asked some
spam	question. It would seem to be always the same question, for, it is
ham	always followed by a press of people towards the third cart. The
spam	horsemen abreast of that cart, frequently point out one man in it with
ham	their swords. The leading curiosity is, to know which is he; he stands
spam	at the back of the tumbril with his head bent down, to converse with a
spam	mere girl who sits on the side of the cart, and holds his hand. He has
ham	no curiosity or care for the scene about him, and always speaks to the
spam	girl. Here and there in the long street of St. Honore, cries are raised
spam	against him. If they move him at all, it is only to a quiet smile, as he
spam	shakes his hair a little more loosely about his face. He cannot easily
spam	touch his face, his arms being bound.
spam	On the steps of a church, awaiting the coming-up of the tumbrils, stands
ham	the Spy and prison-sheep. He looks into the first of them: not there.
ham	He looks into the second: not there. He already asks himself, "Has he
ham	sacrificed me?" when his face clears, as he looks into the third.
ham	"Which is Evremonde?" says a man behind him.
ham	"That. At the back there."
spam	"With his hand in the girl's?"
ham	"Yes."
ham	The man cries, "Down, Evremonde! To the Guillotine all aristocrats!
ham	Down, Evremonde!"
ham	"Hush, hush!" the Spy entreats him, timidly.
spam	"And why not, citizen?"
ham	"He is going to pay the forfeit: it will be paid in five minutes more.
spam	Let him be at peace."
ham	But the man continuing to exclaim, "Down, Evremonde!" the face of
spam	Evremonde is for a moment turned towards him. Evremonde then sees the
spam	Spy, and looks attentively at him, and goes his way.
ham	The clocks are on the stroke of three, and the furrow ploughed among the
spam	populace is turning round, to come on into the place of execution, and
ham	end. The ridges thrown to this side and to that, now crumble in and
spam	close behind the last plough as it passes on, for all are following
ham	to the Guillotine. In front of it, seated in chairs, as in a garden of
ham	public diversion, are a number of women, busily knitting. On one of the
spam	fore-most chairs, stands The Vengeance, looking about for her friend.
ham	"Therese!" she cries, in her shrill tones. "Who has seen her? Therese
spam	Defarge!"
ham	"She never missed before," says a knitting-woman of the sisterhood.
spam	"No; nor will she miss now," cries The Vengeance, petulantly. "Therese."
ham	"Louder," the woman recommends.
spam	Ay! Louder, Vengeance, much louder, and still she will scarcely hear
ham	thee. Louder yet, Vengeance, with a little oath or so added, and yet
ham	it will hardly bring her. Send other women up and down to seek her,
spam	lingering somewhere; and yet, although the messengers have done dread
spam	deeds, it is questionable whether of their own wills they will go far
spam	enough to find her!
spam	"Bad Fortune!" cries The Vengeance, stamping her foot in the chair, "and
ham	here are the tumbrils! And Evremonde will be despatched in a wink, and
spam	she not here! See her knitting in my hand, and her empty chair ready for
spam	her. I cry with vexation and disappointment!"
spam	As The Vengeance descends from her elevation to do it, the tumbrils
spam	begin to discharge their loads. The ministers of Sainte Guillotine are
ham	robed and ready. Crash!--A head is held up, and the knitting-women who
ham	scarcely lifted their eyes to look at it a moment ago when it could
ham	think and speak, count One.
spam	The second tumbril empties and moves on; the third comes up. Crash!--And
ham	the knitting-women, never faltering or pausing in their Work, count Two.
spam	The supposed Evremonde descends, and the seamstress is lifted out next
spam	after him. He has not relinquished her patient hand in getting out, but
spam	still holds it as he promised. He gently places her with her back to the
ham	crashing engine that constantly whirrs up and falls, and she looks into
spam	his face and thanks him.
spam	"But for you, dear stranger, I should not be so composed, for I am
spam	naturally a poor little thing, faint of heart; nor should I have been
ham	able to raise my thoughts to Him who was put to death, that we might
spam	have hope and comfort here to-day. I think you were sent to me by
ham	Heaven."
ham	"Or you to me," says Sydney Carton. "Keep your eyes upon me, dear child,
ham	and mind no other object."
ham	"I mind nothing while I hold your hand. I shall mind nothing when I let
spam	it go, if they are rapid."
spam	"They will be rapid. Fear not!"
spam	The two stand in the fast-thinning throng of victims, but they speak as
ham	if they were alone. Eye to eye, voice to voice, hand to hand, heart to
spam	heart, these two children of the Universal Mother, else so wide apart
ham	and differing, have come together on the dark highway, to repair home
spam	together, and to rest in her bosom.
spam	"Brave and generous friend, will you let me ask you one last question? I
spam	am very ignorant, and it troubles me--just a little."
spam	"Tell me what it is."
ham	"I have a cousin, an only relative and an orphan, like myself, whom I
spam	love very dearly. She is five years younger than I, and she lives in a
spam	farmer's house in the south country. Poverty parted us, and she knows
ham	nothing of my fate--for I cannot write--and if I could, how should I
spam	tell her! It is better as it is."
ham	"Yes, yes: better as it is."
spam	"What I have been thinking as we came along, and what I am still
spam	thinking now, as I look into your kind strong face which gives me so
spam	much support, is this:--If the Republic really does good to the poor,
spam	and they come to be less hungry, and in all ways to suffer less, she may
ham	live a long time: she may even live to be old."
ham	"What then, my gentle sister?"
spam	"Do you think:" the uncomplaining eyes in which there is so much
ham	endurance, fill with tears, and the lips part a little more and tremble:
ham	"that it will seem long to me, while I wait for her in the better land
spam	where I trust both you and I will be mercifully sheltered?"
ham	"It cannot be, my child; there is no Time there, and no trouble there."
ham	"You comfort me so much! I am so ignorant. Am I to kiss you now? Is the
ham	moment come?"
ham	"Yes."
spam	She kisses his lips; he kisses hers; they solemnly bless each other.
spam	The spare hand does not tremble as he releases it; nothing worse than
ham	a sweet, bright constancy is in the patient face. She goes next before
ham	him--is gone; the knitting-women count Twenty-Two.
spam	"I am the Resurrection and the Life, saith the Lord: he that believeth
ham	in me, though he were dead, yet shall he live: and whosoever liveth and
spam	believeth in me shall never die."
spam	The murmuring of many voices, the upturning of many faces, the pressing
ham	on of many footsteps in the outskirts of the crowd, so that it swells
spam	forward in a mass, like one great heave of water, all flashes away.
spam	Twenty-Three.
ham	        *****
ham	They said of him, about the city that night, that it was the
spam	peacefullest man's face ever beheld there. Many added that he looked
ham	sublime and prophetic.
spam	One of the most remarkable sufferers by the same axe--a woman--had asked
ham	at the foot of the same scaffold, not long before, to be allowed to
ham	write down the thoughts that were inspiring her. If he had given any
ham	utterance to his, and they were prophetic, they would have been these:
spam	"I see Barsad, and Cly, Defarge, The Vengeance, the Juryman, the Judge,
spam	long ranks of the new oppressors who have risen on the destruction of
spam	the old, perishing by this retributive instrument, before it shall cease
spam	out of its present use. I see a beautiful city and a brilliant people
ham	rising from this abyss, and, in their struggles to be truly free, in
spam	their triumphs and defeats, through long years to come, I see the evil
spam	of this time and of the previous time of which this is the natural
spam	birth, gradually making expiation for itself and wearing out.
ham	"I see the lives for which I lay down my life, peaceful, useful,
ham	prosperous and happy, in that England which I shall see no more. I see
ham	Her with a child upon her bosom, who bears my name. I see her father,
spam	aged and bent, but otherwise restored, and faithful to all men in his
spam	healing office, and at peace. I see the good old man, so long their
ham	friend, in ten years' time enriching them with all he has, and passing
spam	tranquilly to his reward.
spam	"I see that I hold a sanctuary in their hearts, and in the hearts of
spam	their descendants, generations hence. I see her, an old woman, weeping
ham	for me on the anniversary of this day. I see her and her husband, their
spam	course done, lying side by side in their last earthly bed, and I know
spam	that each was not more honoured and held sacred in the other's soul,
ham	than I was in the souls of both.
ham	"I see that child who lay upon her bosom and who bore my name, a man
spam	winning his way up in that path of life which once was mine. I see him
ham	winning it so well, that my name is made illustrious there by the
ham	light of his. I see the blots I threw upon it, faded away. I see him,
spam	fore-most of just judges and honoured men, bringing a boy of my name,
spam	with a forehead that I know and golden hair, to this place--then fair to
ham	look upon, with not a trace of this day's disfigurement--and I hear him
ham	tell the child my story, with a tender and a faltering voice.
spam	"It is a far, far better thing that I do, than I have ever done; it is a
spam	far, far better rest that I go to than I have ever known."
